# Weak / absent knockback at close range — raw pathway findings

Date: 2026-07-09. Workflow run `wf_cdd6e07e-8be` (10 parallel pathway investigators;
this doc is the RAW pre-verification output — the adversarial verify stage runs after
the merge, and some findings below are expected to be refuted or reclassified there).

## The report under investigation

> ever since versions as far back as I can remember, there is this issue where some
> hits truly just have little to no knockback (the victim just doesnt really move back)
> this happens especially when two players are quite close together and hitting eachother
> (even if one is w-tapping or blockhitting, it seems like the knockback is the
> non-sprinting knockback). I think the bug also occurs with sprint hits where they
> sometimes have less knockback than they should. overall the bug is very subtle and
> hard to reproduce, more like a "feeling" thing than something I can concretely pin
> to a certain scenario.

Classification vocabulary: `bug` (violates its own design contract) /
`divergence-from-era` (as written, but differs from the compendium ground truth) /
`era-real` (authentic era behavior that feels like weak KB) / `config-dependent`.

## Finder: `engine-math` — KnockbackEngine math — direction, taper, extras, every horizontal-shaving step

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

KnockbackEngine (kernel, pure math, thread-agnostic) is called with immutable EntityState captures from BOTH sites: the netty pre-send (D1, frozen PlayerViews) and the region-thread authoritative pass (D2) — same formula bit-for-bit. computePaced order: (1) LEGACY resistance roll (all-or-nothing cancel; legacy-1.8 only among presets). (2) pace = PaceScale.factor(attacker walk-normalized move-speed attr) — signature preset only, else exactly 1.0; taper = rangeReduction.reductionAt(3D distance) — disabled on every preset, and 0 within 3.0 blocks even when enabled. (3) servo sigma — only when the caller passes an active PocketServoConfig ('this attacker holds the victim's active combo', modules.combo-hold, default OFF); sigma = clamped [0.93,1.35] inverse-solve steering the victim to the answer-denial pocket; declines to 1.0 whenever freshEra (the fresh knock projected on the away-axis) <= 1e-9, air-time < 3 ticks, ice landing, or collapsed window. freshFactor = pace*sigma multiplies ONLY the fresh horizontal: the base directional push and the sprint/enchant extras — never the residual, never the vertical. (4) base(): dir = normalize(attackerPos - victimPos); if separation < 0.01 blocks the direction is randomized ONCE (deterministic 0.01 fallback) and the FULL push magnitude still ships (vanilla used a while-loop — equivalent). x = victimVx*friction.x - dirX*max(0, push-taper)*freshFactor (same z); y = vy*friction.y + base.vertical (ADD) or assigned (SET); optional horizontal cap rescales base pre-extras (disabled everywhere); vertical cap clamps base y only (0.4/0.36). victimMotion is the MotionLedger residual — world-fixed, stamped by previous knocks; combos:false presets (legacy-1.8, mmc, lunar, velt, signature) never carry melee residual. (5) extras: sprintLevels = attacker.sprinting() ? sprintFactor : 0 (the ONLY sprint gate — the caller's SprintVerdict decides), plus enchant levels; horizontal = levels * extra.h (wtapExtra never differs on any preset — enabled=false, same values) along attacker YAW (-sin/+cos), times freshFactor; flat vertical extra added once. (6) finish(): airborne victims scale whole vector by air multipliers (signature 0.92h/0.98v, else 1.0); sign-matched add offsets (0 everywhere); verticalMin floor (0.0 on all presets except velt/signature -3.9, since 2.4.7/2.4.8); SCALING resistance scales horizontal (no preset uses it); +/-3.9 per-axis clamp. Key structural fact: base push is POSITIONAL, extras are YAW-directed — their opposition at past/side geometry, and the world-fixed residual re-projected onto a rotated axis, are the two era-faithful ways close-range horizontal collapses toward zero.

### Findings (8)

#### `trade-opener-opposition-era-real` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Base push is positional (away from attacker position, normalized), sprint/enchant extras are yaw-directed. Net sprint horizontal = sqrt(push^2 + extra^2 + 2*push*extra*cos(theta)) where theta = angle between the away-axis and attacker yaw. legacy-1.7 (push 0.4, extra 0.5), grounded victim, zero residual: victim dead ahead = 0.90h; at the attacker's side (theta 90) = 0.64h; theta 135 = 0.357h; victim slightly PAST the attacker (theta 180) = 0.10h. A SPRINT hit is weaker than a PLAIN hit (0.4h, geometry-independent) whenever theta > ~129 deg. signature (push 0.325, extra 0.5): ahead 0.825, side 0.596, past 0.175 vs plain 0.325 (airborne victims additionally x0.92). Separation distance (0.01–3.0 blocks) does not change magnitude at all — direction is normalized and no taper is enabled on any preset. This is byte-identical to vanilla 1.7.10/1.8.9 (knockBack subtracts dir*0.4 from position, attack() adds yaw-directed addVelocity extras) — the exact formula, so no worse and no more frequent than era, given the same input positions.

**Trigger:** Two players inside ~1 block trading: the victim's center drifts beside/past the attacker's center (hitboxes are 0.6 wide, so 'past' happens constantly in face-hug trades) while the attacker's crosshair still lands the hit. The sprint extra then opposes the base push and the net horizontal collapses to 0.1–0.36h — reads as 'non-sprinting or no knockback even though I'm w-tapping'.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:212 (base push away from position), :224-227 (extras along attacker yaw, -sin/+cos), :487-501 (dir normalized, magnitude preserved); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:56-64 and :95-100 (era code: positional dir, yaw-directed addVelocity extras); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:119-121 ('victim past the attacker gets ~0.05h — era-real, identical on actual 1.7.10').

**Maps to the report:** This is the strongest kernel-math match for the report: 'especially when two players are quite close together... even if one is w-tapping... seems like the non-sprinting knockback'. It is authentic era behavior, identical formula to vanilla; if it feels MORE frequent than era, the cause must be upstream position capture (frozen views / latency), not this math.

#### `degenerate-direction-full-magnitude-random` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** When attacker/victim horizontal positions coincide within 0.01 blocks (dx^2+dz^2 < 1e-4), base() redraws a tiny random direction ((rand-rand)*0.01 per axis) once, with a deterministic dx=0.01 fallback if the redraw is still degenerate, then NORMALIZES — the full push magnitude ships in a RANDOM direction (unit-pinned: hypot(x,z)==0.4 at zero distance). Vanilla used a while-loop redraw (compendium: 'coincident-position re-roll being a while loop'); Mental's one-redraw+fallback is behaviorally equivalent (redraw failure probability ~0). No NaN, no zeroing, no shrink. Consequence: at true face-hug the base 0.4 points anywhere, so a sprint hit's net is uniformly random in [extra-push, extra+push] = [0.1, 0.9] for legacy-1.7 — some coincident-position sprint hits randomly ship ~0.1h.

**Trigger:** Players' centers within 1cm horizontally (standing inside each other — common in spam trades against a wall or during collision pushes). The knock direction is random; roughly half the time it partially opposes the sprint extra.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:474-481; kernel/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngineTest.java:184-195 (zeroDistanceHitStaysFiniteWithBaseMagnitude) and :240-257; docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:59-62 (vanilla while-loop re-roll).

**Maps to the report:** Contributes the 'random, hard to reproduce, feeling thing' character: identical-looking face-hug hits ship anywhere from 0.1h to 0.9h purely by RNG — era-authentic randomness, not a Mental defect.

#### `toward-attacker-residual-cancellation` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Step 4 base = victimMotion*friction - dir*push. The victim's ledger residual is world-fixed (stamped by the PREVIOUS knock's direction) while the push axis is recomputed per hit from current positions. If the geometry rotates between hits (close-range circling, players crossing through each other, or a mutual trade where the roles/axis flip), the residual's dot with the new away-axis goes NEGATIVE and residual*friction cancels the push: e.g. a decayed 0.7 residual x0.5 friction pointing at the attacker eats 0.35 of a 0.4 push, leaving ~0.05 base horizontal before extras. In a mutual trade at <1.5 blocks each fighter's residual points away from their OPPONENT, so for hits along the original axis it ADDS (combo compounding); the cancellation appears exactly when positions cross or the attacker rounds the victim — which at face-hug range takes one tick of movement. Only combos:true presets carry melee residual (legacy-1.7, kohi, minehq, badlion); combos:false presets (legacy-1.8, mmc, lunar, velt, signature) never record melee into the ledger, so their residual term is ~0 and they are immune. Era 1.7.10 server fields behaved identically (never restored, signs included).

**Trigger:** combos:true preset; hit N knocks victim east; within the residual's decay window the pair rotates/crosses so the attacker is now east of the victim; hit N+1's push (westward) is cancelled by the surviving eastward residual — near-zero horizontal ships.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:497-501 (x = vx*friction - pushX; sign structure); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java (combos flags: LEGACY_17:149 true, KOHI:80 true, MINEHQ:154 true, BADLION:180 true; LEGACY_18:43 false, MMC:107 false, LUNAR:133 false, VELT:206 false, SIGNATURE:236 false); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:117-120 (1.7.10 no restore, fields persist & decay).

**Maps to the report:** Directly produces 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback... when two players are quite close together and hitting each other' on the 1.7-lineage presets — era-authentic (vanilla 1.7 fields did the same), but any ledger-vs-reality horizontal divergence upstream (the known ledger-vy divergence family) would make it fire on geometries where era would not; the kernel math itself is faithful.

#### `pocket-servo-min-clamp-sprint-shave` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** With modules.combo-hold ON, every melee hit whose attacker holds the victim's active combo gets sigma = clamp(0.93, 1.35, blended sigma*) multiplying the FRESH horizontal (post-taper base push AND sprint/wtap/enchant extras; never residual, never vertical). A full sprint hit mid-combo naturally flies ~4.95 blocks vs the ~2.85 answer-denial target, so sigma* routinely solves well below the min clamp (e.g. d0 1.5, window 10, grounded dragSum ~5.3, chase floor ~1.96: sigma* ~0.7) and the hit rides the 0.93 floor — a systematic ~7% shave on mid-combo sprint hits. Degenerate paths are safe: freshEra <= 1e-9 (including past-attacker geometry where extras project negative onto the away-axis, and exact coincidence where ux=uz=0) DECLINES to sigma=1; ice landings, <3 air ticks, and collapsed windows decline too. Minor quirk: for separations in (1e-9, 0.01) servoFactor prices the true micro-axis while base() ships a RANDOMIZED direction, so sigma scales a push in a different direction than priced — bounded by the clamps, negligible. Module defaults false.

**Trigger:** modules.combo-hold: true (default false; the owner's 'Combo Solver' feature) + an attacker with >= min-hits (2) unanswered hits on the victim; the follow-up sprint knocks ship 0.93x fresh horizontal whenever the solve predicts pocket overshoot (the common case for full sprint stamps).

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:206-231 (sigma folds into freshFactor = pace*combo, applied to base push :489-492 and extras :221-222); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:331-342 (decline gates + clamp), :450-456 (dragSum), :535-541 (chase floor); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/ComboSettings.java:61 (min 0.93 max 1.35); core/src/main/resources/config.yml:273 (combo-hold: false default); kernel/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngineServoTest.java:60-113 (sigma scales fresh only, journaled).

**Maps to the report:** A plausible contributor to 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' IF the owner runs combo-hold on his server — but the shave is bounded at 7% and only mid-combo, so it cannot explain 'little to no knockback' by itself.

#### `legacy18-resistance-random-full-cancel` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** resistanceCancels() rolls all-or-nothing when profile.resistance()==LEGACY and victim.knockbackResistance()>0: random.nextDouble() < resistance cancels the ENTIRE knock (compute returns null). Only the legacy-1.8 preset ships ResistancePolicy.LEGACY (every other preset is NONE; velt/signature/forks deliberately NONE because 'era pools couldn't trigger the roll; legacy randomizes zero-knocks on modern gear'). On a modern server a full netherite set gives 0.4 knockback resistance — 40% of ALL hits (sprint or plain) ship ZERO knockback, at random. Era-authentic mechanic (1.8.9 rolled the same), but era PvP had no resistance items so it never fired; on modern gear it manifests as unreproducible dead hits. The pre-send path also suppresses the velocity burst pending the roll, so nothing ships at all.

**Trigger:** knockback profile = legacy-1.8 (or a custom profile with resistance: legacy) AND victims wearing netherite (0.1/piece) or any knockback-resistance attribute gear; ~resistance-fraction of hits produce literally no victim movement.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:192-193, :448-453; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java:46 (LEGACY_18 ResistancePolicy.LEGACY, pinned by PresetsTest:35); .claude/skills/knockback-profiles/SKILL.md:82-84 (fork presets ship none for exactly this reason); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:36-38.

**Maps to the report:** If the deployed profile is legacy-1.8 and players wear netherite, this alone IS 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback', random and unpinnable. Mechanism certain; relevance depends on the owner's deployed preset/gear.

#### `wtap-freshness-is-valueless-in-every-preset` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The engine's only freshness use is selecting wtapExtra vs extra (KnockbackEngine :217-219, :227), and ALL ten presets ship WtapExtra(enabled=false, h==extra.h, v==extra.v) — so freshSprint changes NOTHING on any bundled preset (unit-pinned: 'Disabled knob: freshness changes nothing — the era default'). Sprinting-but-not-fresh and fresh ship identical extras. The ONLY engine gate on the sprint bonus is attacker.sprinting() (sprintLevels = sprinting ? sprintFactor : 0, :214): if the caller's SprintVerdict/EntityState carries sprinting=false, the entire 0.5h+0.1v extra vanishes and the hit ships as a plain 0.4 knock. Therefore any REAL 'sprint hit shipped plain' incident cannot originate in this pathway's math — it must be an upstream sprint-flag/verdict capture problem (SprintWire freshness/clears, the post-hit setSprinting(false) obligation, wire-vs-view staleness).

**Trigger:** N/A within the engine — the engine faithfully ships the full extra whenever sprinting=true (matching vanilla, which read the flag inside attack()). A weak-sprint report implicates the upstream verdict, not this math.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:214-228; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java (every WtapExtra is (false, extra.h, extra.v): :36, :62, :100, :126, :148, :173, :199, :228) and KnockbackProfile.java:135; kernel/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngineTest.java:342-376.

**Maps to the report:** Load-bearing negative for the synthesis: 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback' cannot be a wtap-value or freshness-selection effect; investigate the D1 SprintWire/verdict pathway for dropped sprint flags instead.

#### `range-taper-cannot-bite-close` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** RangeReduction is DISABLED (enabled=false) on all ten presets. Even when enabled, reductionAt() returns 0.0 for 3D distance <= startDistance (default 3.0) and shaves only the horizontal BASE push (melee only, capped at maxReduction 0.12, i.e. 0.4->0.28 minimum), never the extras. It cannot reduce close-range knockback and has no interaction with the reach handicap (the handicap scales the victim's answer reach in the servo geometry and combo detection; it never enters the engine's distance()). One shape note: with default knobs the reduction is discontinuous at the start boundary (distance 3.0+eps jumps 0 -> factor*(3.0-offset) = 0.045) because offset (1.2) < startDistance (3.0) — the documented MMC-remake shape, unit-pinned.

**Trigger:** Only a custom/edited profile with rangeReduction enabled AND a small start-distance could shave close hits; no shipped configuration does. At defaults this sub-area is exonerated for the report.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/KnockbackProfile.java:113-125 (reductionAt), :146 (LEGACY_17 DISABLED); Presets.java all presets RangeReduction.DISABLED; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:200, :324, :482 (max(0, push - taper), base push only); KnockbackEngineTest.java:302-340 (pins incl. 3D distance and rod-path exemption).

**Maps to the report:** Rules out the taper as a close-range weak-hit source — it is structurally incapable of firing under 3 blocks and disabled everywhere by default.

#### `pace-and-air-multiplier-intended-shaves` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Two remaining horizontal-shaving steps, both preset-scoped and working as designed: (1) Pace scaling — signature only (PaceScaling ATTACKER, exp 0.95, clamp [0.5, 2.0]); a Slowness-affected attacker's fresh knock scales down to 0.5x; at base speed s deviates from 1.0 by ~1.5e-8 (below the wire quantum — byte-identical packets); an unavailable attribute resolves to exactly 1.0. The historical F1 stance-desync (0.769x weak knocks from a sprint-baseline divide) lives only in the deprecated 3-arg overload, which grep confirms has NO production caller — the engine uses the walk-normalized 2-arg form. (2) Air multipliers — signature trims airborne victims' WHOLE vector (residual+push+extras) x0.92 horizontal / x0.98 vertical; grounded openers untouched; all other presets 1.0. Neither can make a sprint hit ship below a plain hit at the same geometry (both scale plain and sprint fresh contributions by the same factor).

**Trigger:** signature preset: an attacker under Slowness ships up to 50% weaker fresh horizontal (intended speed-conformal design); airborne combo victims take the intended 8% horizontal trim. Neither fires on legacy presets or on plain base-speed play.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PaceScale.java:54-62 (current form), :77-86 (deprecated F1 form, no production caller — only KnockbackEngine.java:199,:282 call the 2-arg); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:518-523 (air multipliers in finish, after extras); Presets.java:229-253 (SIGNATURE air 0.92/0.98, PaceScaling(ATTACKER, 0.95, 0.5, 2.0)); KnockbackEngineTest.java:572-663 (byte-identity and 1.6x pins), :409-450 (signature airborne trim pins).

**Maps to the report:** Weak match only: pace requires Slowness (rare in the reported plain trades); the 0.92 airborne trim is small, intended, and vertical-preserving. The historical F1 bug WOULD have matched the report exactly but is fixed and dead code in production.

## Finder: `sprint-wire` — SprintWire / SprintVerdict — every writer and reader of sprint state

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

Sprint state lives in three stores. (1) The wire: per-connection SprintWire (kernel/wire/SprintWire.java), one immutable State{seen, sprinting, armed, clientSprinting, blockReset, lastWrite} swapped by CAS. Writers: netty thread — PacketTap.onEntityAction feeds START_SPRINTING→onSprintStart (sprinting=armed=clientSprinting=true, lastWrite=now) and STOP→onSprintStop (sprinting=clientSprinting=false, armed survives) in exact packet-arrival order (PacketTap.java:96-110); netty thread — reconcile(view.sprinting, now, quiet=3) runs on EVERY movement packet (PacketTap.java:85, NOT per session tick): seeds an unseen wire immediately (armed=false) or adopts the published server flag when wire!=view and now−lastWrite≥3; victim's region thread — KnockbackUnit.applyAttackerObligations→onServerClear(asOf=verdict stamp) after every accepted bonus melee (KnockbackUnit.java:432-434), dropping sprinting+armed unless lastWrite is STRICTLY newer than asOf (SprintWire.java:103); attacker's region thread — SwordBlockingUnit.resetSprintForBlock→onBlockSprintReset (all-true + sticky blockReset), gated on raw clientSprinting and on the default-OFF SWORD_BLOCKING feature. onServerClear/reconcile never touch clientSprinting. Every clear/adopt/start/stop stamps lastWrite=now. (2) The server flag: vanilla applies client STOP/START on the region thread; Mental's deferred obligation runs setSprinting(false) via runOn 1-2 ticks post-hit, skipped only if the wire re-armed by execution time (KnockbackUnit.java:435-447); SwordBlockingUnit sets it true on block re-arm. (3) The published PlayerView: sprinting = live player.isSprinting() frozen at session-tick publish (SessionService.java:535) — this stale copy is what reconcile adopts. Nothing writes the wire from Bukkit PlayerToggleSprintEvent (no listener exists — Q6 clean).

Verdict flow: on ATTACK (netty), HitRegistrationUnit.sprintVerdict peeks the wire (verdictAt, non-mutating; blockReset&&clientSprinting overrides to fresh-sprint) or falls back to view.sprinting with fresh=null for packetless attackers/feature-off (HitRegistrationUnit.java:523-535). The verdict is STAMPED into HitContext at registration (line 321-330) and used for both the pre-send vector and the region recompute; the EDBEE at MONITOR consumes the stamp for Melee sources (KnockbackUnit.java:365-371) — only Vanilla-source hits use a live isSprinting() read (safe on 1.9+: vanilla clears post-hurt). PINNED and blocked-redeliver hits carry the original stamp. Engine: verdict.sprinting selects sprintFactor levels (KnockbackEngine:214); verdict.fresh selects wtapExtra ONLY when profile.wtapExtra.enabled — which is FALSE in LEGACY_17 and all eight presets (Presets.java:36-228), so freshness is engine-inert at every shipped config; the sprint FLAG is the whole game. Freshness consumption = onServerClear, which runs for every accepted bonus hit regardless of velocity suppression (matches vanilla); registration-rejected/cancelled hits never consume.

### Findings (5)

#### `same-tick-reengage-retro-clear` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** SprintWire.onServerClear(asOf) no-ops only when lastWrite is STRICTLY newer than the hit's verdict stamp (SprintWire.java:103). The clear runs 1-2 ticks after registration (deferred EDBEE, KnockbackUnit.java:266/344 with asOf=tx.context().sprint().at()). TickStamp granularity is one server tick, so a legitimate re-engage START that arrives in the SAME server tick as the ATTACK (after it, in arrival order) has lastWrite==asOf and is retro-destroyed: wire sprinting=false, armed=false. The deferred setSprinting(false) then consults the already-retro-cleared wire (KnockbackUnit.java:442-446), sees false, and clears the vanilla-granted SERVER flag too — so the reconcile (PacketTap.java:85) can never restore it (both sides read Mental's own false). Client-side the flag is up (it re-armed), so no further START is sent; every subsequent hit ships verdict.sprinting=false = plain KB until the player's next genuine W-release/re-press.

**Trigger:** Attacker's ATTACK and re-engage START land in one server tick: (a) a fast w-tap whose re-press trails the click by <50 ms; (b) any network-jitter bunching that delivers two consecutive client-tick flushes inside one server tick — for hold-sprint-key clients ≤1.21.1 EVERY hit is followed by an auto STOP(same flush)+START(next client tick), so every hit rolls this dice; once eaten, plain hits persist for the rest of the engagement. High-CPS close trades maximize both the roll count and the visibility (see close-range amplifier finding).

**Evidence:** SprintWire.java:100-110 (strictly-greater guard; clear sets lastWrite=now), SprintWire.java:98 + docs/superpowers/plans/2026-07-04-combat-241-fix-round.md:122-123 ('Same-tick retro-clear (START after ATTACK inside one tick) is an accepted residual — physically implausible for real input') — the assumption ignores network bunching and sub-tick w-taps; KnockbackUnit.java:404-448 (deferred clear + wire-consulting skip guard that reads the poisoned wire); SprintWireTest.java:137-149 pins asOf==lastWrite ⇒ clears; compendium docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:257-263 (client sends STOP in the attack flush, re-engage is a client entity-action). Design contract violated: WtapRegistrationUnit.java:13-16 'a w-tap registers however fast the tap' and netty-fast-path skill 'the era queue applied STOP/START/ATTACK in arrival order' — vanilla's synchronous in-attack clear could never eat a later-arriving START.

**Maps to the report:** Exactly 'even if one is w-tapping ... it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback' and 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback'; intermittent (jitter-dependent), persistent once triggered, worst in close high-CPS trades — 'subtle and hard to reproduce, more like a feeling'.

#### `modern-client-no-reengage-after-clear` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** Mental's era reconstruction clears BOTH the wire and the server flag after every accepted sprint hit, and its only recovery signal is a client-sent START_SPRINTING. Era-lineage clients (≤1.21.1) run the client-side attack sprint-clear and, with the sprint key held, auto-re-arm next tick — the STOP/START pair crosses the wire and the next hit is sprint again. 1.21.2+ clients removed the attack sprint interruption, so continuous-hold sprint attacking generates NO STOP/START around hits; after Mental's clear the wire and server flag sit false while the client demonstrably sprints. Recovery then depends on the fragile self-metadata round trip (Mental's setSprinting(false) → own-entity metadata → client flag dip → resync STOP+START), which costs one RTT of plain hits at best and emits nothing if the client re-arms within the same client tick as the metadata application. The reconcile cannot rescue: it compares the wire to view.sprinting(), which is Mental's own cleared flag.

**Trigger:** Attacker on a 1.21.2+ client (owner tests with 1.21.4+) holding W+sprint continuously, landing repeated hits without w-tapping: hit 1 ships sprint KB, hits 2..n read plain — where a real 1.8.9 sprint-key-holder re-armed every hit and got full sprint KB every time. Any autosprint mod on any version behaves the same.

**Evidence:** KnockbackUnit.java:425-447 (wire clear + deferred server-flag clear — no server-side re-arm path exists for plain sprint, unlike the blockhit reconstruction); SprintWire.java:167-178 (reconcile adopts the server flag — poisoned by Mental's own clear); PacketTap.java:85 (view.sprinting is the adopted truth, SessionService.java:535 shows it is the live server flag Mental just cleared); era-accuracy skill lines 68-75 documents the identical modern-client signal-loss problem for BLOCK-hitting and reconstructs only that case (SwordBlockingUnit) — the plain held-sprint re-engage has no equivalent reconstruction. Era ground truth: compendium:257-259 (re-engage re-arms the +1 level; the re-engage is the client's entity-action).

**Maps to the report:** 'sprint hits where they sometimes have less knockback than they should' — dependent on input style (hold-to-sprint vs w-tap) and client version, hence perceived as an inconsistent feel rather than a reproducible scenario.

#### `blockhit-rearm-gated-behind-sword-blocking` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The block-hit sprint re-arm (the era technique that maintained the sprint bonus like an easy w-tap) is reconstructed ONLY by SwordBlockingUnit.resetSprintForBlock → SprintWire.onBlockSprintReset, and SwordBlockingUnit is part of the default-OFF DAMAGE family. Modern clients (1.17+) keep the sprint flag through item use, so the era's natural STOP/START pair never crosses the wire when blocking; with SWORD_BLOCKING disabled there is no re-arm signal at all — after any accepted sprint hit, a blockhitting attacker's subsequent hits ship verdict.sprinting=false (plain) permanently until a real w-tap. Additionally, even with SWORD_BLOCKING ON, the re-arm never fires for a player whose domain lacks a raised clientSprinting (e.g. the attacker was already sprinting when the domain was created and reconcile seeded sprinting=true but clientSprinting=false — seed path SprintWire.java:170 writes sprinting without clientSprinting, so verdictAt says sprinting yet resetSprintForBlock's raw-flag gate (SwordBlockingUnit.java:321-330) declines until the first genuine START packet).

**Trigger:** SWORD_BLOCKING feature off (the shipped default): any modern-client (1.17+) blockhitting attacker loses the sprint bonus on every hit after the first. With it on: an attacker whose SprintWire was seeded by reconcile (never sent a START since the domain was created — join-while-sprinting, or domain recreated after relog) blockhits and gets no re-arm despite visibly sprinting.

**Evidence:** SwordBlockingUnit.java:315-345 (feature-unit listener — only assembled when the feature is enabled; raw-clientSprinting gate; player.setSprinting(true) resync), SprintWire.java:140-159 (blockReset contract), SprintWire.java:167-171 (reconcile seed/adopt never raises clientSprinting — SprintWire.java:202-209 confirms only START packets do), era-accuracy skill lines 68-83 (the modern-client signal loss and why the reconstruction exists), CLAUDE.md (DAMAGE family 'All default OFF').

**Maps to the report:** 'even if one is ... blockhitting, it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback' — verbatim the symptom when the reconstruction is off or its raw-flag gate has never seen a START.

#### `era-clear-plus-close-range-opposition` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Two authentic era behaviors compound into 'little to no knockback' at close range. (1) The post-hit sprint clear is era truth: vanilla 1.7/1.8 cleared the attacker's sprint flag on every bonus hit, so consecutive hits without a re-engage are PLAIN — measured on real 1.8.9 (no-w-tap doubles settle 7.2 vs w-tap 11.4); Mental reproduces this deliberately (the desk obligation). (2) At face-hug range the plain hit's base 0.4 push is directed away from the ATTACKER'S POSITION — a victim at/past the attacker gets ~0.05 h, identical on actual 1.7.10; the sprint extra (0.5 along attacker YAW) is the only meaningful horizontal at that range. So whenever the sprint verdict is false — legitimately (no re-engage) or via the two defects above — a close-range hit ships nearly ZERO horizontal, while the same plain verdict at 3 blocks still ships a visible 0.4 push. This is the amplifier that turns every sprint-verdict loss into the owner's 'the victim just doesn't really move back' specifically in close trades; the close-range half is era-real and must not be 'fixed'.

**Trigger:** Mutual trade at <1 block: A's hit lands while B stands beside/past A; A's verdict is plain (post-clear, no re-engage yet — the era-legal state between w-taps). The hit deals damage but moves B almost nothing. Reproducible on real 1.7.10/1.8.9 with the same geometry.

**Evidence:** KnockbackUnit.java:425-447 + netty-fast-path skill ('without it, no-w-tap seconds keep the sprint extra forever ... real 1.8.9 separates them 7.2 vs 11.4') — the clear is contract, not defect; era-accuracy skill lines 119-122 ('The trade-opener opposition: base 0.4 pushes away from the ATTACKER'S POSITION ... a victim past the attacker (face-hug) gets ~0.05 h — era-real, identical on actual 1.7.10'); KnockbackEngine.java:214-227 (sprint extra along yaw is additive on top of the positional base — the only term that survives face-hug geometry).

**Maps to the report:** Directly explains 'especially when two players are quite close together' and why the bug reads as 'the non-sprinting knockback': the era-real geometry makes any plain verdict at close range look like NO knockback, so the owner is seeing sprint-verdict losses (the two defects above) amplified by authentic era geometry.

#### `deferred-window-double-fresh` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** Because the wire clear is deferred to the EDBEE (1-2 ticks after registration) and verdictAt is a non-mutating peek, a second ATTACK registered before the first accepted hit's onServerClear lands reads the SAME sprinting=true/armed=true state — both hits ship the sprint bonus where vanilla's synchronous in-attack clear would have made the second plain absent a re-engage. Requires two ACCEPTED hits inside the 1-2-tick window, i.e. two different victims (one victim's immunity forces a ~10-tick cadence). Direction is MORE knockback, not less — reported for completeness so the synthesizer doesn't misattribute it.

**Trigger:** Attacker sprint-hits victim V1 at tick T and victim V2 at T or T+1 (cleave through a crowd, or two adjacent opponents at high CPS) without w-tapping between: both hits ship sprint KB; era would ship the second plain.

**Evidence:** SprintWire.java:192-198 (verdictAt is a pure read), KnockbackUnit.java:266/344 (clear only at the deferred EDBEE), HitRegistrationUnit.java:523-535 (registration peeks on the netty thread at ATTACK arrival). Vanilla contract: compendium:257-263 (clear was synchronous inside attack()).

**Maps to the report:** Does not match the weak-KB report (opposite sign); included to rule it out and bound the race's other direction.

## Finder: `desk-obligations` — DeliveryDesk post-hit obligations in mutual trades

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

Post-hit flow: on an ATTACK packet the netty thread (HitRegistrationUnit.plan, core/.../delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:318) stamps a SprintVerdict from the attacker's SprintWire (arrival-order; verdictAt is NON-consuming), computes the era vector from FROZEN PlayerViews (victim residual = MotionLedger as of end of previous tick), pre-sends the burst if admitted (FeedbackGate per-victim, default auto = (maxNoDamageTicks/2−1)×50ms = 450ms; a wireless victim bypasses the gate entirely and is PINNED), marks the tx PRE_SENT/PINNED and pushes it into the victim desk's one-slot wireSlot (submitFromWire), then schedules the damage task on the victim's region thread. That task runs victim.damage() with session.activeInbound set; DamageRouter (LOWEST) establishes the tx as eventTransaction; KnockbackUnit (MONITOR) either ADOPTS the carried vector (PRE_SENT/PINNED: desk.awaitVelocityEvent only — never recomputed) or, for a REGISTERED (pace-suppressed) hit, recomputes from the ledger residual and desk.submit()+awaitVelocityEvent. It then runs the attacker obligations (KnockbackUnit.applyAttackerObligations:404, on the VICTIM's region thread): (1) attacker-session ledger.scaleHorizontal(0.6) — exactly once per accepted bonus hit, only site in the codebase, never on pre-send, never the victim's ledger; (2) SprintWire.onServerClear(asOf=registration stamp) — drops wire sprinting+armed unless lastWrite is STRICTLY newer than asOf; (3) deferred setSprinting(false) via runOn(attacker) next tick, skipped if the wire re-armed. The victim's PlayerVelocityEvent (tracker phase, end of tick) reaches DeskRouter → desk.resolve(): first drainWire() (a wireSlot tx SUPERSEDES the current armed pending and resets awaiting=false), then: unmodified PRE_SENT → SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE (ValveListener eats the one byte-identical duplicate ENTITY_VELOCITY); PINNED/REGISTERED → SHIP no valve; null vector → CANCEL (resistance roll); not awaiting → PASS_THROUGH (vanilla's damage-pass velocity stands — which is base-only 0.4 knockback with NO sprint/enchant extras, because Player.attack never ran). On SHIP, Deliveries.recordDelivered folds the shipped value into the victim's ledger (melee only when profile.combos()). Session tick order (CombatSession.tickStep:230): drain inbox → ledger.tick → publish view → desk.sweep(now, connected) — a CONNECTED victim's awaiting melee is never time-dropped (2.4.6). In a mutual trade each player has an independent desk/ledger; hits stamp verdicts at registration, so a counter-party's clear can never unsprint an already-registered hit, and the counter-attacker's own ×0.6 becomes visible to the opponent's NEXT-tick pre-send via the published view (same-tick trades read the pre-×0.6 residual — ships MORE than the era join-order mode that applied ×0.6 first, by ≈0.2×residual_h, never less).

### Findings (10)

#### `same-tick-wtap-start-destroyed` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** SprintWire.onServerClear(asOf) only survives a re-engage whose lastWrite is STRICTLY newer than the hit's registration tick (s.lastWrite().value() > asOf.value()). A genuine w-tap START that arrives on the netty thread in the SAME TickStamp tick as the ATTACK it follows gets lastWrite == asOf, so the deferred EDBEE clear (runs ~1 tick later on the victim's region thread) retroactively destroys it: wire sprinting=false, armed=false, and the deferred setSprinting(false) then also clears the server flag (its skip-guard reads the just-cleared wire). The client believes it re-engaged sprint and sends no further START, so the NEXT accepted hit's verdict is sprinting=false — the entire sprint extra (0.5 h + 0.1 v per level) is missing, not just freshness. State only recovers on the player's next full STOP/START pair. The code's own contract says 'a w-tap START in that window must survive' (F2); the javadoc waves the same-tick case away as 'physically implausible', but at 12–16 CPS a re-press 0–50ms after the click lands in the click's tick routinely — tick quantization simply cannot order within-tick events with a strict >.

**Trigger:** Attacker sprint-hits at high CPS and w-taps immediately after a click: click registers at tick T (verdict stamped asOf=T), STOP+START both arrive later within tick T (lastWrite=T), the hit's EDBEE clear runs at T+1 and wipes the re-engage; the next accepted hit (~10 ticks later) ships plain knockback. One tap per hit (the classic w-tap rhythm) maximizes exposure; continuous re-tapping masks it.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/SprintWire.java:100-110 (strict-> guard; :98 the 'accepted residual' admission; :76 onSprintStart stamps clock.current()); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:432-447 (clear at deferred EDBEE with asOf=tx.context().sprint().at(); deferred setSprinting(false) skip reads the already-cleared wire); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:523-535 (verdict stamped at registration, non-consuming).

**Maps to the report:** Directly matches 'even if one is w-tapping … it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback' and 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should': intermittent, timing-dependent (same-tick coincidence), so it reads as a subtle feeling rather than a reproducible scenario.

#### `pinned-victim-armed-pending-clobbered-to-vanilla-passthrough` — bug, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** DeliveryDesk.resolve() calls drainWire() FIRST: a transaction sitting in the netty wireSlot supersedes the currently ARMED pending (replacePending journals 'superseded' and resets awaiting=false), so the armed hit's own genuine PlayerVelocityEvent falls into the '!awaiting' branch and PASS_THROUGHs — vanilla's damage-pass velocity stands. Because Mental cancelled the ATTACK packet and re-issued victim.damage(), vanilla's velocity is knockback(0.4) BASE ONLY: no sprint extra, no enchant extra, and airborne victims keep their falling y. The accepted hit therefore ships non-sprint (or downward) knockback, is never valve-consumed, and is never folded into the victim's ledger (recordDelivered gated on directive.ship()!=null), corrupting the next hit's residual too. The window is real because a PACKETLESS victim (no PacketEvents user — in-process bots, synthetic players) bypasses the FeedbackGate entirely (admitVelocityPreSend returns true for !victimHasWire), so at spam CPS a follow-up click's PINNED submitFromWire can land between the accepted hit's EDBEE arm (task phase) and its velocity event (tracker phase) of the same tick. For WIRED victims the default 450ms gate makes the window unreachable; feedback-min-interval-ms: 0 or a small maxNoDamageTicks (auto interval → 0) reopens it.

**Trigger:** Victim without a PE user (SimpleBoxer bot, FakePlayer) being spam-clicked at 12–16 CPS: hit N accepted at tick T (adopt+arm in the damage task), hit N+1's ATTACK packet arrives on netty between that arm and tick T's tracker phase (frozen view still reads not-immune), pins into the wireSlot; hit N's velocity event supersedes-then-passes-through vanilla's base knock. Hit N+1's own damage is then invuln-rejected, so its pending is swept — net result: one accepted sprint hit delivered as vanilla base knockback.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:172-177 (resolve drains wire then early-PASS_THROUGH on !awaiting), :305-328 (drainWire/replacePending resets awaiting; last-submitter-wins is the pinned intent, DeliveryDeskTest:444-458); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:511-521 (!victimHasWire bypasses the gate), :402-433 (pinned + submitFromWire); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/DeskRouter.java:78-88 (PASS_THROUGH leaves the event; ledger fold skipped). The 2.4.6 sweep fix (DeliveryDesk.java:246-259) explicitly names late-resolve PASS_THROUGH of vanilla velocity as the infiltration failure mode — this is the same infiltration through the supersede path, which that fix did not cover.

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback (the victim just doesn't really move back) … especially when two players are quite close together and hitting each other' — close range = highest CPS on one victim = most same-tick follow-up submissions. If the owner's feel-testing is against SimpleBoxer bots (packetless), this fires at default config; against real clients it needs a shortened feedback interval or hurt window.

#### `post-hit-sprint-clear-era-economics` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The post-hit obligations correctly reconstruct vanilla's in-attack setSprinting(false): after every accepted sprint/enchant-bonus hit the wire flag and (deferred, re-arm-guarded) the server flag drop, and modern clients never re-send START unless the player genuinely w-taps/s-taps or (with SWORD_BLOCKING enabled) block-hits. Therefore only the FIRST hit of a held-W chase carries the sprint extra; follow-ups are plain until a real re-engage. Registration stamps the verdict and the authoritative pass consumes the stamp, so the clear can never unsprint an already-registered hit (the Q1 race is designed out); conversely a second click registered before the first hit's EDBEE clear reads sprint still true (era cleared synchronously), but that hit is invuln-rejected at damage, so nothing extra ships.

**Trigger:** Two players trading with W held but without crisp per-hit w-taps: every second-and-later sprint hit legitimately ships the 0.4-base plain knock — identical to real 1.7/1.8 servers (measured 7.2 vs 11.4 block separation in the repo's own no-w-tap/w-tap doubles).

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:404-449; .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md ('Sprint-flag clear' obligation, measured numbers); kernel SprintWire.reconcile only re-adopts the (already false) server flag after wire silence, so no phantom re-arm.

**Maps to the report:** Part of the owner's 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback' is authentic era behavior: the sprint extra is a per-engagement resource, not a per-hit one. Needs to be separated from finding same-tick-wtap-start-destroyed, which wrongly extends this to genuinely re-engaged sprints.

#### `face-hug-opposition-and-degenerate-direction` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The base push is directed away from the ATTACKER'S POSITION while the sprint/enchant extra is directed along the ATTACKER'S YAW (KnockbackEngine step 6). At sub-1.5-block range with strafing/circling these two directions diverge; a victim beside or slightly past the attacker has the position-push and the yaw-extra partially cancel, down to ~0.05 h net for a full face-hug pass. At truly coincident positions the direction degenerates to a tiny random jitter (vanilla-exact) so the 0.4 base goes in a random direction against the 0.5 yaw extra. Additionally, with combos:true presets the victim's ledger residual from the PREVIOUS knock keeps its old direction; after the pair swap sides in a hug, that residual now points TOWARD the new attacker position and subtracts from the fresh push (base = motion×friction − dir×push) — a visibly weak hit that is faithful 1.7 server-fields behavior.

**Trigger:** Both players inside ~1 block, hitting while strafing past each other; worst when the victim is level with or behind the attacker's position relative to its yaw, or immediately after the pair cross sides while a residual is still live.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:462-501 (position-based dir, random jitter at <1e-4 sq distance, residual×friction − dir×push), :214-228 (yaw-directed extras); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md 'The trade-opener opposition … ~0.05 h — era-real, identical on actual 1.7.10'.

**Maps to the report:** Directly matches 'this happens especially when two players are quite close together and hitting each other' — the dominant close-range weak-hit mechanism, and it is authentic; the owner should know this part is not fixable without leaving era truth.

#### `legacy-resistance-roll-zero-knock` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** ResistancePolicy.LEGACY rolls all-or-nothing per hit: random < knockbackResistance cancels the ENTIRE knock (desk CANCEL_EVENT, hurt still ships, journal 'resistance-roll'). The era item pool had zero-resistance armor so the roll never fired historically, but modern netherite armor grants 0.1 knockback-resistance per piece — full netherite = 40% of all hits ship literally no knockback, silently, with a normal hurt flinch. The pre-send is also suppressed for such victims (suppressorFor 'resistance-roll'), so nothing ever reaches the wire on cancelled hits.

**Trigger:** Profile with resistance: legacy — the bundled legacy-1.8 preset (Presets.java:46 ResistancePolicy.LEGACY) or a custom profile — plus victims wearing any knockback-resistant gear (netherite). The default legacy-1.7 (ResistancePolicy.NONE, KnockbackProfile.java:152) is NOT affected; fork presets ship resistance none.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:448-453 (resistanceCancels), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:181-186 (CANCEL_EVENT + journal); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:547-555 (pre-send suppressor); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java:28-46 (LEGACY_18 = ResistancePolicy.LEGACY); .claude/skills/knockback-profiles/SKILL.md ('legacy randomizes zero-knocks on modern gear').

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback (the victim just doesn't really move back)' exactly and randomly — but only if the server runs legacy-1.8/custom-with-legacy-resistance and players wear netherite. Verifiable in one journal read (resistance-roll entries).

#### `ledger-vy-overdecay-floored-to-zero-lift` — bug, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** MotionLedger.current() free-falls the airborne vy by pure gravity/drag per tick (Decay.decay: vy=(vy−0.08)×0.98 down to terminal), but a real juggled client hovers at −0.05..−0.34 (measured live, 914 boxer hits — 2026-07-07 research doc); the ledger runs to −1.5. The ADD-mode vertical (vy×friction.y + base.vertical, KnockbackEngine.base) then computes deeply negative, and since 2.4.8 the bundle-wide verticalMin 0.0 floor clamps it to exactly 0.0 — so an airborne/juggled victim's hit ships zero lift instead of the era's declining-but-positive combo vertical (~0.25). Horizontally the stamp is normal, so the hit reads as 'the victim doesn't really move' vertically — no pop, flat shove. The floor traded the visible DOWNWARD leak for an invisible zero-lift under-ship; the diagnosed root (ledger vy diverging from measured reality) is still open.

**Trigger:** combos:true profiles (legacy-1.7 default, kohi/minehq/badlion), victim airborne for several ticks mid-juggle (knocked, no Landing event yet), next hit lands: ledger vy has over-decayed, vertical clamps to the 0.0 floor.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:119-133 (tick/current fold), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/Decay.java:79-100 (gravity free-fall + terminal clamp), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:496-500+527-529 (vy×friction+base, verticalMin floor), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/KnockbackProfile.java:137-145 (the 2.4.8 floor rationale naming the ledger-vy divergence), core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/Deliveries.java:41-44 (only shipped knocks re-seed the ledger).

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback' for airborne/juggled victims specifically; already diagnosed live in the 2.4.8 round (memory: measured-reality clamp is the planned fix) — included because the desk's Deliveries fold and the session ledger are this pathway's files.

#### `blockhit-sprint-restore-needs-sword-blocking-on` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** The era block-hit sprint reset (block → STOP, release → START re-arms the bonus) never crosses the wire on modern clients, and Mental's reconstruction (SprintWire.onBlockSprintReset + the sticky blockReset, gated on the raw clientSprinting flag) lives exclusively in SwordBlockingUnit.resetSprintForBlock — a DAMAGE-family feature that defaults OFF. With it off, a block-hitting attacker gets no re-arm: the previous hit's onServerClear left wire+server sprint false, so every block-hit after the first ships plain knockback.

**Trigger:** SWORD_BLOCKING feature disabled (the default) while a player attempts era block-hitting; also any 'blocking' that is not the sword-block right-click (shield raise) never re-arms regardless.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/damage/SwordBlockingUnit.java:320-347 (the only onBlockSprintReset caller), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/SprintWire.java:140-159 (blockReset arm/release); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md (the one exception needing server-side reconstruction).

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'even if one is … blockhitting, it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback' whenever the deployment doesn't run the sword-blocking feature (or the block isn't Mental's sword block).

#### `wtap-registration-off-stale-view-verdict` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** With wtap-registration disabled (wtapConsultWire=false) the registration verdict falls back to the attacker's PUBLISHED view sprinting flag — up to a tick stale. A sub-tick w-tap (START then ATTACK inside one tick, the whole reason the wire view exists) reads the pre-START snapshot: sprinting=false, and the hit ships plain. Same fallback applies to any packetless attacker (fresh=null → engine never selects wtap-extra).

**Trigger:** hit-registration wtap-registration knob off, attacker re-presses W and clicks within ~50ms; every such hit loses the sprint extra.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:523-535 (peek wire only when wtapConsultWire, else view fallback with fresh=null); .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md ('the tick-frozen PlayerView is up to a tick OLDER than that contract').

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'w-tapping … non-sprinting knockback' only on deployments with the feature toggled off; default is on, so this is a config check, not the default-path cause.

#### `validation-fail-leaves-presend-orphan` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** applyPlayer's negative-validation returns (attacker null/offline/spectator, victim dead, world mismatch, out of the 7-block reach re-check) exit WITHOUT withdrawing the PRE_SENT transaction (only the cross-region branch and the scheduler-retire fallback call retract). The client already received the velocity burst, so it visibly moves without a hit (a phantom knock — MORE motion, then a rubber-band), and the orphaned pending sits on the connected victim's desk (sweep never time-drops connected) until the next hit supersedes it — the orphan is journaled only then, as 'superseded', misattributing the drop. No weak-knock effect: the desk resets awaiting on supersede and the next hit re-arms cleanly.

**Trigger:** A registered+pre-sent hit whose deferred damage task fails validation next tick — e.g. the victim dies or teleports/moves beyond ~7 blocks between netty registration and the region tick, at any CPS.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:619-649 (early returns at :627-639 without retract; retract only at :625-631 cross-region and :443 the retire fallback), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:312-328 (supersede journals the orphan later).

**Maps to the report:** Does NOT produce weak knockback (opposite direction: phantom movement then correction); reported to close the drop-vs-weak audit — the journal cannot currently distinguish this orphan from a genuine supersede (Q4 gap: silent withdraw()/retract paths journal nothing, and JournalEntry carries no sprint verdict, so a plain-shipped weak-sprint hit journals as a healthy SHIP).

#### `trade-counter-x06-one-mode-lateness` — divergence-from-era, confidence high

**Mechanism:** In a same-tick mutual trade, era 1.7.10 processed connection slots in join order: exactly one participant's received knock was computed AFTER their own counter-attack's ×0.6 self-scale bit their motion fields. Mental's pre-send always reads the FROZEN end-of-previous-tick view, and the ×0.6 lands at the deferred EDBEE mid-tick, so a same-tick counter's scale is never visible to the opponent's hit — Mental consistently ships the pre-×0.6 residual, i.e. the OTHER of era's two bimodal modes. Difference: +friction×(1−0.6)×residual ≈ +0.2×residual_h — Mental ships MORE (or equal), never less; the scale itself fires exactly once per accepted bonus hit (single call site, EDBEE-only, attacker's ledger only, cross-region-guarded so the thread is always the shared region), so no double-application or mis-attribution exists to shrink a residual.

**Trigger:** A and B land hits on each other in the same server tick (close-range trade); the participant whose era slot would have run second receives ~0.2×their-opponent's-residual more horizontal knock than the corresponding era mode.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:418-423 (sole scaleHorizontal site, bonus-gated), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:110-116; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/model/PlayerView.java:8-13 (end-of-previous-tick publish); .claude/skills/legacy-motion-physics/SKILL.md (attack() ×0.6 on the attacker's server fields; join-order bimodal wire).

**Maps to the report:** Rules OUT the ×0.6 obligation as a weak-knock source in trades: the divergence is in the MORE direction. Reported so the synthesizer does not chase it.

## Finder: `valve` — Duplicate-ENTITY_VELOCITY valve

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

The valve dedupes the one intentional double-send per pre-sent knock. Flow: (1) NETTY (attacker read thread) — HitRegistrationUnit.plan() computes the era vector from frozen views, marks the tx PRE_SENT, ships a VELOCITY+HURT burst to the victim via BurstSender (user.writePacket → full netty pipeline, so this burst itself traverses all PE send listeners, including the ValveListener), and hands the tx to the victim's desk via the atomic wireSlot (submitFromWire). (2) REGION (victim's thread, next tick) — the deferred damage runs vanilla victim.damage(); KnockbackUnit's EDBEE handler sees state==PRE_SENT and ADOPTS (desk.awaitVelocityEvent, no recompute). (3) TRACKER phase (end of tick, victim's region thread) — hurtMarked → sendChanges fires PlayerVelocityEvent; DeskRouter (priority HIGH, sole velocity writer) resolves the desk: an unmodified PRE_SENT yields SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE — event velocity set to the carried vector AND VelocityValve.arm(victimUUID, ValvePayload(entityId, 3 shorts = trunc(axis×8000), clamp ±3.9)). Vanilla then broadcasts the duplicate ENTITY_VELOCITY; the write is enqueued on the victim's event loop microseconds after the arm. (4) NETTY (victim's event loop) — ValveListener (HIGHEST) decodes every outbound ENTITY_VELOCITY whose recipient UUID has a slot, re-quantizes the decoded doubles through ValvePayload.of, and on exact integer equality of entityId+3 axes does a consume-once CAS (clears slot, cancels packet). One slot per victim (last-writer-wins overwrite, no queue, no hit id); mismatches pass through. Lifecycle: SessionService.tick calls valve.clearStale(victim) every session tick (task phase — unconditional, no age check), quit/retire calls valve.forget via forget hook. Second arm site: deliverBlockedKnock (blocked-hit redelivery, EDBEE task phase) arms BEFORE its setVelocity, whose dup only emits at that tick's tracker — a long exposure window. PINNED (no wire) never arms; resolve with a third-party-modified vector ships without arming; sweep/withdraw/journalDrop never arm. Key facts for reasoning: arm→dup are same-thread adjacent in the DeskRouter path (dup cannot miss its arm); per-channel FIFO means a later-enqueued pre-send cannot jump ahead of a pending dup; the pre-send IS valve-visible; the match key carries no hit identity, so identical quantized vectors (stationary close trades) alias across hits; PRE_SENT is stamped before the burst outcome is known; and the observed-side re-quantization does not byte-match the armed raw-double quantization on 1.21.9+ (~32% of knocks) or on ~1% of knocks below (missing PE's 1e-11 fix).

### Findings (6)

#### `presend-failure-still-marked-pre-sent-valve-eats-only-copy` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** In HitRegistrationUnit.plan() the transaction is marked PRE_SENT (tx.preSent at core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:409) BEFORE the burst is shipped (senders.ship at :427), and the BurstSender Outcome (DELIVERED vs UNSENDABLE) is DISCARDED at :427. BurstSender.ship returns UNSENDABLE when getUser() is null at the second lookup or when writePacket throws (victim mid-(re)configuration on 1.20.2+, encode failure) — core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/BurstSender.java:66-81. The tx stays PRE_SENT, submitFromWire pushes it (:431), the authoritative pass ADOPTS it (KnockbackUnit.java:256-267), and DeliveryDesk.resolve takes the PRE_SENT-unmodified branch → SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE (kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:190-194). The valve then consumes the tracker's re-emission — which was the ONLY wire copy, since the pre-send never reached the client. The victim's client receives ZERO velocity packets for the hit; player movement is client-authoritative, so the victim does not move at all. This violates the codebase's own stated contract (netty-fast-path skill: 'a pre-delivered marker for an unsendable burst would let any non-PE-level suppression mechanism silently eat the victim's knockback' — exactly what the discarded Outcome permits).

**Trigger:** Victim's PacketEvents user becomes unavailable or the write throws between the victimHasWire check (HitRegistrationUnit.java:324-325) and the ship (:427): client mid-reconfiguration (1.20.2+ resource-pack/reconfigure), transient encode throw, or user lookup gone. Rare per-hit, but every occurrence is a total silent knock loss on an otherwise healthy hit.

**Evidence:** HitRegistrationUnit.java:404-433 (state set before send, Outcome ignored); BurstSender.java:37,63-81 (UNSENDABLE exists precisely for this and is dropped); DeliveryDesk.java:186-194 (PRE_SENT resolve always arms); ValveListener.java:56-58 (matching outbound cancelled). Note ProtocolManagerAbstract.writePacket also silently releases the buffer on a CLOSED channel while ship() still returns DELIVERED — same shape, but a closed channel means the victim is quitting.

**Maps to the report:** Produces exactly 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback (the victim just doesnt really move back)' — a full, unrecoverable no-KB hit that leaves a normal journal SHIP entry (wireCarried=true), so it is invisible to the tester and unpinnable by the owner. Frequency profile matches 'very subtle and hard to reproduce'.

#### `lp-vector-1219-valve-dedup-broken-third-of-knocks` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** On servers 1.21.9+ the ENTITY_VELOCITY wire format is Mojang's low-precision LpVector3d (15 bits/axis, step = ceil(maxAxis)×2/32766 ≈ 6.1e-5), not motion×8000 shorts. The armed key is ValvePayload.of(raw vector) = trunc(raw×8000) (ValvePayload.java:17-20), but the ValveListener re-quantizes the LP-decoded double (ValveListener.java:49-56), and the LP roundtrip error (±0.244 in q-units) crosses the trunc boundary on ~12%/axis. Monte-Carlo over era knock vectors: ~32% of knocks fail the integer-equality match → the duplicate outbound ENTITY_VELOCITY is NOT cancelled and ships to the client ~1 tick after the pre-send, re-applying the identical vector after a tick of client decay (refreshes/extends the knock). The 'one wire stamp per knock, like the era' contract (knockback-profiles skill) is broken on a third of pre-sent knocks; the stale arm is swept next session tick (SessionService.java:348) and cannot mis-eat the next identical pre-send because that pre-send round-trips through the same LP encoding and mismatches identically.

**Trigger:** Any pre-sent melee knock on Paper 1.21.9+ (incl. 26.x) whose LP-quantized decode lands on the other side of a ×8000 trunc boundary on any axis — ~1 in 3 hits, value-dependent, so knockback feels version-inconsistent (some hits carry a doubled/refreshed stamp, most dedupe correctly).

**Evidence:** PE 2.12.1 WrapperPlayServerEntityVelocity.read/write (V_1_21_9 branch uses LpVector3d); LpVector3d pack/unpack (15-bit, ceil-normalized); ValvePayload.java:17-20 (short quantization only); ValveListener.java:52-56 (requantize through ValvePayload); numeric simulation: 32.1% miss over random era knocks (h∈[0.2,0.95], vy∈[0.25,0.47]). Direction is EXTRA knockback, not weak.

**Maps to the report:** Does not explain weak/no-KB directly (misses ship duplicates = slightly stronger/floatier), but explains hit-to-hit inconsistency the owner reads as 'a feeling thing', and it invalidates the valve's dedup contract on the modern half of the version range.

#### `requantize-drift-legacy-wire-valve-miss` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Below 1.21.9 the vanilla dup encodes trunc(x×8000) and PE decodes q/8000.0; ValvePayload.q re-quantizes WITHOUT PacketEvents' PRECISION_LOSS_FIX (+1e-11 before the cast, WrapperPlayServerEntityVelocity.write), so for 374 of the 62,401 legal wire shorts the roundtrip trunc((q/8000.0)×8000) yields q−1 (toward zero). ~0.61% of values in the melee horizontal band (0 in the standing-vy band ≈ [0.35,0.475]) → ~1.2% of knocks (two horizontal axes) fail to consume: the duplicate ships (client re-applies the same vector a tick later = refreshed knock) and the arm goes stale for ≤1 tick (self-neutralizing: an identical next pre-send drifts the same way and cannot match either).

**Trigger:** A knock whose horizontal component quantizes to one of the 187 positive bad shorts (e.g. odd q in 1001–2047, bands up to 16380) on any server < 1.21.9. Vector-value lottery, ~1% of hits.

**Evidence:** ValvePayload.java:17-20 vs PE WrapperPlayServerEntityVelocity.write PRECISION_LOSS_FIX comment ('vanilla just casts to an int... packetevents has to add a small number'); exhaustive numeric check: 187 positive mismatch values, 0.61% of horizontal band, 0 in vy band; VelocityValveTest.java:33-42 pins integer-equality-no-epsilon as the intended contract, which the decode side silently violates.

**Maps to the report:** Opposite direction (occasional doubled stamp = slightly stronger), so NOT the weak-hit cause; reported to prevent misattribution and because it adds hit-to-hit inconsistency.

#### `stale-arm-after-third-party-velocity-cancel-eats-next-identical-knock` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** DeskRouter resolves and arms the valve at PlayerVelocityEvent priority HIGH (DeskRouter.java:53-79); HIGHEST/MONITOR listeners run AFTER, and if one cancels the event, vanilla never sends the duplicate — the arm has no matching packet and persists until the victim's next session-tick clearStale (SessionService.java:348), a window spanning the tick boundary (up to ~50ms). Because the valve key carries NO hit identity — only (recipient UUID, entityId, 3 quantized shorts) — any later ENTITY_VELOCITY to that victim with the identical quantized triple is eaten, and stationary close-range trades produce byte-identical repeated stamps (fixed positions → same direction, constant 0.3608/0.4607 verticals, fresh-stamp profiles). The next hit's netty PRE-SEND burst (which traverses the ValveListener: BurstSender uses user.writePacket → ChannelHelper.write → full pipeline → PacketSendEvent fires) is then consumed against the dead arm; that hit still resolves PRE_SENT-unmodified, arms its own valve, and its tracker duplicate is eaten too → the second hit reaches the client with ZERO velocity copies. Unlike the healthy-flow interleave (see pathway_map) there is no surviving duplicate to mask the loss.

**Trigger:** Requires a third-party plugin cancelling or modifying PlayerVelocityEvent at HIGHEST/MONITOR after Mental resolved (anticheats, anti-KB/movement plugins) — a modify leaves the same stale arm via the resolve mismatch branch shipping the modified value (DeliveryDesk.java:196-200, no valve, but the earlier SHIP_AND_ARM path only arms on unmodified; a HIGHEST modifier AFTER resolve changes the packet so the armed value never ships). Then a quantized-identical next knock inside the ≤1-tick window. Close-range stationary trades maximize vector identity.

**Evidence:** DeskRouter.java:53 (HIGH priority); DeliveryDesk.java:190-194 (arm on resolve); VelocityValve.java:30-41 (no hit identity, exact-triple match); SessionService.java:348 (clearStale bounds the window to one session tick); ProtocolManagerAbstract.writePacket → ChannelHelper.write (full-pipeline, so pre-sends ARE visible to ValveListener); ValveListener.java:42-58 (no isCancelled or origin check).

**Maps to the report:** If the owner's servers run any velocity-event-touching plugin, this yields exactly the reported intermittent total-loss hits concentrated in close trades (identical stamps). Without such a plugin this path is dead — worth asking the owner what else is installed.

#### `blocked-path-arm-races-clearstale-and-own-burst` — bug, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** deliverBlockedKnock arms the valve on the victim's region thread during EDBEE dispatch (task phase) at KnockbackUnit.java:533, but its matching duplicate only emits at the TRACKER phase at the END of the same tick (setVelocity at :546 → hurtMarked → sendChanges). Two races: (a) the victim's own session-tick task also runs in the task phase and calls valve.clearStale (SessionService.java:348) — task ordering is unspecified, so ~half the time the arm is wiped before its duplicate exists → the duplicate ships uncancelled → the client gets the era vector TWICE (pre-send/burst + tracker re-emission), a doubled wire stamp on blocked knocks; (b) in the !wirePreSent branch the burst is flushed (:525) microseconds BEFORE the arm (:533) but is processed asynchronously on the victim's event loop — if the arm wins the race the valve eats Mental's OWN just-shipped burst velocity (identical vector, same recipient), and the knock only reaches the client at tracker time, ~a tick late (delivered but delayed; the bundled HURT ships without its velocity). Neither race loses the knock outright; both smear blocked-hit knockback timing/magnitude.

**Trigger:** (a) any partial-block redelivery (temp-shield/off-hand tier 1.9.4-1.20.6, BLOCKS_ATTACKS tier 1.21.5+) whose victim session tick is scheduled after the attacker's deferred damage task in the same tick; (b) any !wirePreSent blocked redelivery where the region thread reaches :533 before the victim's event loop encodes the burst — likely often, since only an if and a User lookup separate flush from arm.

**Evidence:** KnockbackUnit.java:515-547 (burst ship at :525, arm at :533, setVelocity at :546 — dup only at end-of-tick tracker); SessionService.java:320-348 (clearStale every session tick, task phase); VelocityValve.java:44-49 (clearStale is unconditional, no age check — it cannot distinguish a just-armed payload whose dup is still coming).

**Maps to the report:** Contributes 'some hits feel off' specifically when the victim is block-hitting — the report explicitly names blockhitting trades. Race (b) delays the knock ~1 tick (reads as mushy/weak-feeling response); race (a) doubles it. Both are inconsistent hit-to-hit.

#### `healthy-flow-interleave-self-masking-negative-result` — unknown, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The suspected healthy-flow aliasing — hit B's pre-send consumed against hit A's resolve-arm — is real but SELF-MASKING: it requires B's burst to be processed on the victim's event loop inside the sub-millisecond window between arm(A) (inside the velocity event) and the enqueue of A's duplicate (immediately after the event returns, same thread, FIFO per channel), AND requires B's vector to be quantized-identical to A's. When it fires, A's duplicate then ships (arm consumed), delivering the byte-identical value at essentially the instant B's pre-send would have applied, and B's own resolve-arm eats B's duplicate — the client still receives exactly one application per hit at approximately correct times. Likewise, arm(B) overwriting a not-yet-consumed arm(A) (VelocityValve.arm is last-writer-wins, :22-24) makes A's late duplicate SHIP as an extra packet rather than eat B. Conclusion: in pure-Mental healthy flow the valve cannot silently starve a knock; every loss path needs a stale arm whose own duplicate already died (findings 1 and 4) or a pre-send that never reached the wire (finding 1).

**Trigger:** Two knocks on the same victim with identical quantized vectors within the same tracker flush window — occurs in close stationary trades but produces no client-visible defect per the analysis above.

**Evidence:** VelocityValve.java:22-41 (single slot, last-writer-wins, consume-once); DeliveryDesk.java:186-229 (arm only inside resolve, dup enqueued synchronously after on the same thread); netty per-channel FIFO ordering; ValveListener.java:56 (consume clears the slot, so the surviving duplicate passes).

**Maps to the report:** Negative result: rules the healthy-flow valve interleave OUT as the close-range no-KB mechanism, narrowing the synthesizer's search to findings 1/4 within this pathway or to other pathways (registration/engine/ledger).

## Finder: `transactions` — HitTransaction lifecycle — paths where an admitted hit fails to ship

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

A hit's lifecycle: on the attacker's netty thread HitRegistrationUnit.register cancels the ATTACK packet, mints a HitTransaction (REGISTERED; SprintVerdict frozen at packet arrival), and — if the victim's frozen view is not damage-immune AND no suppressor (anticheat/resistance-roll) AND the per-victim FeedbackGate window (auto = (maxNoDamageTicks/2−1)×50ms ≈ 450ms) admits — computes the era vector, ships a VELOCITY+HURT burst, transitions to PRE_SENT (wire user) or PINNED (no user), and drops the tx into the victim desk's atomic wireSlot (submitFromWire). It then schedules the damage task on the victim's region thread (runOn, executes next tick).

The desk (one per victim, single-owner) holds AT MOST ONE pending decision. Every desk call first drains wireSlot via replacePending: any LIVE prior pending is suppressed("superseded")+RECORDED and `awaiting` is reset to false. The damage task brackets victim.damage() with session.activeInbound; DamageRouter (LOWEST) establishes it as eventTransaction (or mints Vanilla); KnockbackUnit (MONITOR, ENTITY_ATTACK) then either ADOPTS a PRE_SENT/PINNED tx (awaitVelocityEvent only) or recomputes and desk.submit(tx,vector)+awaitVelocityEvent — arming EVERY non-blocked hit, even ones whose frozen view reads mid-invuln; only the era-silent BLOCKED difference hit (block-shape AND immune) is submitted UNARMED. Partial-block fresh hits bypass the event entirely (deliverBlockedKnock: withdrawSuperseded original, mint fresh, inline burst+valve+setVelocity). applyAttackerObligations then clears attacker sprint (wire+deferred setSprinting(false)) and ×0.6s their ledger.

Delivery resolves at the victim's PlayerVelocityEvent (entity-tracker phase, END of the same tick — after ALL of that tick's damage tasks): DeskRouter (HIGH, sole writer) fires KnockbackApplyEvent then desk.resolve(api velocity): no-awaiting/no-pending → PASS_THROUGH (vanilla's own velocity — plain 0.4, never sprint, airborne keeps falling-y — ships to the client); null vector → CANCEL_EVENT (resistance roll); PRE_SENT unmodified → SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE (ValveListener cancels the byte-identical tracker duplicate); PINNED/REGISTERED-LIVE → SHIP the submitted FORMULA (api modifications ignored); terminal → PASS_THROUGH ("late-resolve-recorded", F6). Shipped melee feeds the MotionLedger only via DeskRouter's recordDelivered (combos-on profiles).

Per session tick (region thread, runs BEFORE that tick's damage tasks): drain the LedgerEvent inbox (≤1 tick latency, FIFO), tick the ledger, publish the frozen PlayerView (end-of-previous-tick state), then desk.sweep(now, domains.has(victim)) — a CONNECTED victim's LIVE pending is NEVER time-dropped (2.4.6); packetless ones drop at age ≥2, with ensureStrandedPacketlessMelee shipping armed strandings via desk.ensure+setVelocity just before.

The critical structural fact: the desk assumes one hit per victim per tick; two same-tick EDBEEs on one victim collide on the single pending slot, and the shared end-of-tick velocity event resolves whatever (and however armed) the LAST submitter left.

### Findings (11)

#### `same-tick-supersede-disarms-delivery-vanilla-leak` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The desk holds ONE pending per victim; replacePending (DeliveryDesk.java:312-328) suppresses any LIVE prior pending and resets `awaiting=false`. KnockbackUnit submits mid-invulnerability difference hits to the desk: a blocked-shape one UNARMED (KnockbackUnit.java:327-343 via 232-253), a non-blocked one armed. Vanilla's true difference branch applies NO knockback and fires NO velocity event for that hit — so when its submit lands in the window between an earlier same-tick hit's arm (adopt at KnockbackUnit.java:256-267 or submit+arm at :327-342) and that hit's PlayerVelocityEvent (tracker phase, end of tick, after ALL damage tasks), the earlier hit's event resolves with awaiting=false → PASS_THROUGH (DeliveryDesk.java:174-177) → vanilla's OWN velocity ships to the client as the LAST wire word. Vanilla's velocity for the fast path's victim.damage() is the plain 0.4 knock (the sprint bonus lives only in the cancelled Player.attack), with kept falling-y when airborne — so the client's pre-sent era sprint stamp (0.9, 0.46) is overwritten by a plain (~0.4) or downward vector. Additionally the superseded hit never reaches DeskRouter's recordDelivered (DeskRouter.java:80-88), so combos-on profiles lose that link in the MotionLedger and the NEXT hit's residual-based compute under-reads.

**Trigger:** Two ATTACK-caused EDBEEs on the same victim inside one region tick (clicks bunched by network jitter at 12-16 CPS, or two attackers), where hit1 is a fresh accepted hit (pre-sent+adopted, or region-computed+armed) and hit2 lands mid-invuln in a BLOCKED shape (victim blockhitting with sword-blocking on, or holding a shield partially) — hit2's era-silent unarmed submit clobbers hit1's armed pending before hit1's end-of-tick velocity event.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:312-328 (supersede resets awaiting), :174-177 (PASS_THROUGH when !awaiting), :260-283 (connected pendings never time-dropped, so nothing else catches it); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:232-253+327-343 (era-silent blocked diff submitted unarmed; every other frozen-immune hit armed); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/DeskRouter.java:77-88 (PASS_THROUGH ships nothing, no ledger record). kernel/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDeskTest.java:444-457 pins supersede-resets-arm as intended and :461+ pins unarmed-pending PASS_THROUGH — but only for a FOREIGN event; no test covers the passed-through event being the SUPERSEDED hit's own. Precedent: the 2.4.6 fix (commit 545f1dc) closed the identical vanilla-velocity-leak symptom for the sweep path only.

**Maps to the report:** Directly produces 'the victim just doesn't really move back / seems like non-sprinting knockback' during close-range trades, and names blockhitting — the exact modifiers the owner listed. Intermittent (needs same-tick packet bunching), hence 'subtle, more a feeling'.

#### `difference-hit-armed-pending-dangles-and-clobbers` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** A NON-blocked stronger-mid-invuln hit (e.g. a crit landing during the hurt window — CraftBukkit fires EDBEE with the difference) is deliberately submitted AND ARMED (KnockbackUnit.java:327-343: the comment justifies arming frozen-immune reads because 'vanilla knocks this hit and fires it' — true for boundary hits, FALSE for genuine difference hits, where vanilla skips knockback and markHurt).
