Consequences: (a) same-tick clobber — it supersedes an earlier armed pending and the shared end-of-tick velocity event then resolves the LIVE-REGISTERED branch (DeliveryDesk.java:208-213), shipping the DIFFERENCE hit's recomputed formula instead of the accepted hit's carried vector; that formula uses the difference hit's OWN SprintVerdict, frozen at ITS packet arrival (HitRegistrationUnit.java:321,523-535) — mid-w-tap that verdict reads sprint=false, so a sprint hit's delivery is replaced with a plain (~0.4 vs 0.9) knock; (b) with no earlier pending it DANGLES armed on a connected victim indefinitely (sweep never time-drops connected, DeliveryDesk.java:269-277), and because the LIVE-REGISTERED resolve branch ships the stored FORMULA while ignoring the api velocity, the NEXT foreign velocity event (rod, explosion, another plugin's setVelocity) is hijacked into shipping the stale melee knock. Era contract: a stronger mid-invuln hit deals difference damage with NO knock and no flinch — this transaction should never participate in delivery at all.

**Trigger:** (a) hit1 accepted+armed and hit2 = crit (jump-crit spam at close range) landing mid-invuln, both damage tasks in one region tick (bunched clicks / two attackers); worst when the attacker is mid-w-tap at hit2's click so its verdict is non-sprint. (b) any crit-difference hit with nothing else pending, followed by a rod/explosion/plugin velocity within the next few ticks.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:327-343 (submit+arm for every non-blocked hit incl. frozen-immune; its own comment at :246-252 concedes the frozen read cannot discriminate the genuine difference branch); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:208-213 (LIVE-REGISTERED resolve ships formula, ignores apiX/Y/Z), :269-277 (connected pending held forever); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:321 (verdict frozen at registration); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md per era-accuracy skill: 'a stronger hit mid-invuln deals difference damage with NO knock and no flinch'.

**Maps to the report:** 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' and 'even if one is w-tapping ... seems like the non-sprinting knockback' — the clobber substitutes a non-sprint-verdict recompute for the sprint hit's stamp; close-range mutual trades maximize crit-difference EDBEEs.

#### `presend-outcome-ignored-valve-eats-only-send` — bug, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** plan() transitions the tx to PRE_SENT (HitRegistrationUnit.java:404-412) BEFORE shipping the burst, and the BurstSender.ship return value at :426-429 is IGNORED. BurstSender returns UNSENDABLE and sends NOTHING on any throw (target mid-reconfiguration, PE user race — BurstSender.java:69-81). The phantom-PRE_SENT tx is still submitFromWire'd; the authoritative pass ADOPTS it; resolve returns SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE (DeliveryDesk.java:186-194); the tracker's ENTITY_VELOCITY — the ONLY copy that would ever reach the client — is then consumed by the ValveListener's exact-match cancel (ValveListener.java:56-58). The victim's client receives damage/hurt via the authoritative vanilla re-send but ZERO velocity: a hit with truly no knockback. The PINNED/PRE_SENT type-level guarantee (HitTransaction.java:22-24) guards the null-user case but not the send-failure case.

**Trigger:** Any pre-send burst whose PacketEvents write throws — victim mid-(re)configuration (1.20.2+ dimension change/resource-pack reconfigure during combat), or the PE user disappearing between the line-325 check and the line-427 ship.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:408-412 (preSent before ship), :426-429 (Outcome discarded); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/BurstSender.java:69-81 (catch-all → UNSENDABLE, nothing sent); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:186-194 (adopt → valve armed); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/ValveListener.java:49-58 (exact-quantization consume cancels the packet).

**Maps to the report:** Literal 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback (the victim just doesnt really move back)' — the hit registers (damage, flinch) but no velocity ever reaches the client. Low frequency, which fits 'very subtle and hard to reproduce'.

#### `legacy-resistance-roll-zero-knock` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** With a profile whose resistance policy is LEGACY (the default legacy-1.7 preset) and a victim wearing ANY knockback-resistance gear (netherite pieces, 0.1 each), the engine's all-or-nothing roll cancels the ENTIRE knock on a per-hit probability: the pre-send suppresses velocity ('resistance-roll', HitRegistrationUnit.java:547-555 — hurt-only burst still ships, so the victim flinches), and the authoritative resolve returns CANCEL_EVENT (DeliveryDesk.java:182-186) so no velocity packet ships at all. Era-authentic (pre-1.9 probabilistic armor resistance; era item pools could never trigger it, modern gear can), documented in the knockback-profiles skill ('legacy randomizes zero-knocks on modern gear').

**Trigger:** Default legacy-1.7 (or legacy-1.8) profile + victim in netherite or any kb-resistance gear: a full netherite set = 0.4 total → a large fraction of hits ship damage+flinch with ZERO knockback, deterministically random per hit.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:547-555 (suppressorFor 'resistance-roll' when ResistancePolicy.LEGACY && knockbackResistance > 0); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:182-186 (null formula → suppressed + CANCEL_EVENT); .claude/skills/knockback-profiles/SKILL.md ('Fork presets ship armor-resistance: none ... legacy randomizes zero-knocks on modern gear').

**Maps to the report:** If any testing happened in netherite-era loadouts on the legacy presets, this alone produces 'some hits truly just have no knockback' with the hit visibly registering. Owner should check the deployed profile's resistance policy and the test loadout before chasing the races.

#### `close-range-trade-feel-era-authentic` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Three authentic era behaviors compound at <1.5-block mutual trades: (1) face-hug opposition — base 0.4 pushes from the ATTACKER'S POSITION while the sprint extra rides the attacker's YAW, so a victim at/past the attacker nets ~0.05 horizontal (measured identical on real 1.7.10); (2) the client-side 0.6 self-velocity multiplier per sprint attack — a victim who is ALSO attacking (a trade, by definition) multiplies their own received velocity by 0.6 per click, 0.6^n at high CPS; (3) the server-side attacker ×0.6 (Mental: applyAttackerObligations' ledger scaleHorizontal(0.6), KnockbackUnit.java:418-424) shrinks the counter-hitter's residual, so with combos-on profiles their next received knock computes off a smaller base. All three are decompile-cited/wire-measured era ground truth Mental preserves by construction; none is a defect.

**Trigger:** Any close-range mutual trade with both players clicking — the higher the victim's own CPS and the tighter the hug, the weaker their received knockback reads.

**Evidence:** .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:60-63 (0.6^clicks client contract, untouchable), :119-122 (trade-opener opposition, ~0.05 h face-hug, 'era-real, identical on actual 1.7.10'); .claude/skills/legacy-motion-physics/SKILL.md:99-102 (attack() ×0.6 attacker fields, both eras); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:418-424 (ledger ×0.6 on accepted bonus hits).

**Maps to the report:** This is the authentic fraction of 'when two players are quite close together hitting each other ... the victim just doesnt really move back'. The owner needs this separated from the bugs: even a fully-fixed pipeline will feel like this at face-hug range because 1.7.10 did.

#### `stale-view-vanilla-fallthrough` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** Registration declines (returns WITHOUT cancelling the packet) when the victim's published view is missing or older than 4 ticks (HitRegistrationUnit.java:269-273; PlayerView.fresh, PlayerView.java:142-144). The whole hit is then handled by vanilla Player.attack: vanilla's MODERN sprint knock (0.7, 0.4) instead of the era stamp (0.9, 0.4607), no era ledger/combo model, no pre-send. Views go stale across respawn windows (SessionService.retire re-arms through transient invalidity — several ticks with no publish, SessionService.java:253-296), join, and region-thread lag. Working as designed (fail-safe), but the hits it passes are era-divergent and weaker-than-era sprint knocks.

**Trigger:** First hits on a freshly-respawned or just-joined victim, or any hit while the victim's region thread lags >4 ticks — those specific hits carry vanilla's weaker sprint knockback.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:269-273 (no cancel on null/stale/creative/no-pvp view); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/model/PlayerView.java:142-144; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:253-296 (respawn/invalidity window with no view publish); era reference: modern vanilla sprint (0.7, 0.4) vs era (0.9, 0.4607) per era-accuracy skill :125-127.

**Maps to the report:** Occasional 'sprint hits have less knockback than they should' clustered right after respawns/lag spikes; contributes to the diffuse, unpindownable feel.

#### `cancel-then-throw-eats-hit` — bug, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** register() cancels the ATTACK packet (HitRegistrationUnit.java:306) BEFORE plan()/dispatch() run; the listener's catch-all (:233-236) swallows any Throwable from them. A throw after the cancel (e.g. plan() line 431: sessions.sessionFor(victimId) returning null → NPE if the victim's session is forgotten between the netty-side view check and the desk submit — a quit/forget race, SessionService.forget runs on the main thread concurrently) leaves the packet cancelled with NO damage scheduled and NO feedback sent: the hit vanishes entirely — no damage, no flinch, no knockback.

**Trigger:** Victim (or any state plan() touches) torn down between the registration checks and the desk submit on the same netty invocation; any latent exception in the servo/predictor build path would have the same total-hit-loss effect.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:226-237 (catch-all after the cancel), :306 (setCancelled before plan), :431 (unguarded sessionFor(victimId).desk() — every other victim access in plan() is null-guarded); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:298-317 (concurrent forget).

**Maps to the report:** A fully-eaten hit reads as 'no knockback' to the attacker, though unlike the report's phrasing the victim also takes no damage; likely a minor contributor at most.

#### `presend-never-revoked-on-cancel` — divergence-from-era, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The pre-send is optimistic and there is NO revocation: when the authoritative damage is cancelled by another plugin (onMeleeCancelled withdraws by id, KnockbackUnit.java:348-363), when a full shield block cancels (KnockbackUnit.java:209-213), when the run-on task retires or the attacker is cross-region (retract → withdraw, HitRegistrationUnit.java:441-443,625-631,701-706), or when applyPlayer's re-validation fails (attacker offline/victim dead/out of reach, :633-640 — which doesn't even withdraw, leaving a dangling never-armed pending), the victim's client KEEPS the already-delivered knockback with no correcting packet and no damage. This is the contract's answer to Q4: victims can move on cancelled hits (opposite polarity of the report); withdraw() is silent (DeliveryDesk.java:62-67) so such transactions also never reach RECORDED, violating the class's own 'every transaction reaches terminal RECORDED' doc (HitTransaction.java:9-12). Conversely the suppressed-pre-send + successful-damage direction is sound: the REGISTERED tx is recomputed on the region thread, submitted+armed, and resolve's LIVE branch ships the formula via event.setVelocity → tracker packet (verified chain).

**Trigger:** Any protection-plugin cancel, full shield block, cross-region attacker, or damage-time re-validation failure AFTER an eligible pre-send shipped.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:348-363, :209-213; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:633-640 (early returns without retract), :701-706; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:62-67 (silent withdraw, no journal, tx never terminal); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/HitTransaction.java:9-12 (contradicted contract).

**Maps to the report:** Opposite polarity (phantom knockback, not missing) — reported because it defines the pre-send contract the synthesizer needs; the un-withdrawn dangling pending from :633-640 also feeds the stale-pending hazards in the difference-hit finding.

#### `sweep-timedrop-guard-verified-plus-wire-gate-defusal` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Q3 verification: the 2.4.6 guard is solid — sweep(now, victimConnected) never time-drops a LIVE pending when the victim has a connection domain (DeliveryDesk.java:260-283; CombatSession.tickStep passes domains.has(victim), CombatSession.java:230-239; pinned by DeliveryDeskTest 'sweepNeverTimeDropsAConnectedVictimsMelee'). No residual time-based drop exists for connected victims under any lag; packetless victims drop at age ≥2 with the F1 net (SessionService.java:389-418) shipping armed strandings first. The residual costs of holding forever are the dangling-pending hazards in the other findings. Separately: the per-victim FeedbackGate (auto ≈450ms, HitRegistrationUnit.java:398-402, FeedbackGate.java:24-35, defaults HitRegSettings.java:36-37) is what prevents two WIRE submissions being in flight for one victim simultaneously — at default it structurally defuses the wireSlot-vs-adopt races (a second submitFromWire superseding an unresolved adopt, and awaitVelocityEvent's unchecked assumption that pending==tx, DeliveryDesk.java:105-108). Setting feedback-min-interval-ms to 0 (or tiny) removes that defusal: bunched/second-attacker pre-sends then supersede unresolved adopts mid-tick, and the mis-arm can ship the wrong hit's vector then PASS_THROUGH vanilla for the next.

**Trigger:** hit-registration feedback-min-interval-ms: 0 (or a value below ~2 ticks) + close-range multi-hit pressure on one victim; at the shipped 'auto' default this family cannot fire.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:260-283 (connected hold), :105-108 (awaitVelocityEvent sets awaiting without checking pending==tx); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/CombatSession.java:230-239; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:341,389-418; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:398-402,511-521; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/HitRegSettings.java:36-37; kernel/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDeskTest.java:330-344.

**Maps to the report:** Rules OUT the pre-2.4.6 sweep leak as the current cause on connected victims; identifies the one config knob that would make the report dramatically worse and should be checked on the owner's deployed config.

#### `cps-cap-eats-clicks` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** The CpsLimiter cancels the ATTACK packet outright above maxCps (default 20) over a trailing 1s window (HitRegistrationUnit.java:250-254; CpsLimiter.java:43-62; HitRegSettings.java:36-37). An eaten click produces nothing — no damage, no flinch, no knockback. Since the window counts ALL clicks (including the mid-invuln ones that would have done nothing anyway), a 20+ CPS butterfly/drag clicker can have the boundary-LEGAL click of a combo be the one rejected, silently losing an entire hit.

**Trigger:** Attacker sustaining >20 CPS (drag/butterfly clicking) with max-cps at the default 20 — a fraction of their clicks, occasionally the legal-cadence one, are swallowed.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:250-254; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/CpsLimiter.java:43-62; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/HitRegSettings.java:36-37 (maxCps 20).

**Maps to the report:** Weak match — the report describes hits that land without moving the victim, whereas an eaten click lands nothing; include only because high-CPS close trades are the named scenario and the loss is silent.

#### `mutual-trade-keying-clean` — unknown, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Q2 negative result: A→B and B→A cannot collide structurally — desks are strictly per-victim (one DeliveryDesk per CombatSession, DeliveryDesk.java:25-48), HitIds are a single global AtomicLong (HitIds.java:12-19), activeInbound/eventTransaction are per-victim-session fields bracketed around each damage() call (CombatSession.java:31-50, HitRegistrationUnit.java:687-699), and nested events (thorns-back) are cause-gated out of the melee consumers. In a mutual trade the two directions resolve on independent desks; the only same-desk collision is two hits on the SAME victim (the supersede findings above). No finding in this sub-area beyond those.

**Trigger:** N/A — verification result, not a defect.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:25-48; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/HitIds.java:12-19; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/CombatSession.java:31-50,110-133; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:664-699 (nested-event note and slot bracketing).

**Maps to the report:** Eliminates the intuitive 'A→B and B→A collide' hypothesis; the mutual-trade symptom must come from the same-victim same-tick collisions and the era-real close-range physics instead.

## Finder: `gates` — Admission and suppression gates — flinch-without-knock

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

ATTACK packets hit HitRegistrationUnit.Listener on the attacker's netty thread. Gate order: (1) CpsLimiter.tryAcquire per-attacker (sliding 1s window, default max-cps 20) — over-limit clicks are CANCELLED outright (never vanilla, never journaled); (2) victim resolve via frozen entityId->UUID; a null/stale (>4 ticks, PlayerView.fresh) view, creative, or pvp-off RETURNS WITHOUT CANCELLING — the hit falls through to modern vanilla (0.7h sprint KB), silently; (3) reach validation (default OFF, defers to anticheat); (4) AsyncHitRegisterEvent; then the packet is cancelled and plan() runs. plan(): if the victim's frozen view reads damageImmune (noDamageTicks > max/2+1, the +1 staleness allowance for boundary hits) NOTHING ships (no velocity, no hurt) but the tx (REGISTERED) still dispatches to damage. Otherwise suppressorFor checks AnticheatPolicy.allowVelocityPreSend (false whenever GrimAC/Vulcan is installed, mode AUTO default) and the LEGACY resistance roll (default legacy-1.7 profile + victim KB-resistance>0): either suppressor -> vector=null -> HURT-ONLY burst, tx REGISTERED. Eligible vectors are computed from FROZEN state (view motion = ledger residual as of END of previous tick, frozen grounded, ring positions) — the era boundary read. admitVelocityPreSend then consults FeedbackGate ONLY for eligible velocities with a wire (auto window = (max/2-1)*50ms = 450ms per victim, registration wall-clock): paced-out -> NOTHING ships (hurt skipped too), tx stays REGISTERED; passed -> velocity+hurt burst (bundled 1.19.4+), tx PRE_SENT (wire) or PINNED (no PE user), submitFromWire into the victim desk's single wireSlot (last-write-wins). dispatch() schedules victim.damage() on the victim's region thread (~1 tick later); cross-region/failed scheduling retracts. Authoritative: DamageRouter (LOWEST) binds the tx; KnockbackUnit (MONITOR) — PRE_SENT/PINNED are ADOPTED (desk.awaitVelocityEvent; no recompute); REGISTERED is RECOMPUTED from EntityStates.captureVictim = ledger.current() (1-2 MORE decay ticks than the frozen view) + LIVE isOnGround + LIVE positions, then desk.submit + arm. There is NO feedback window on the authoritative side — vanilla's live noDamageTicks is the sole authoritative pacing, so window/anticheat/immune suppression never blocks the authoritative knock: DeskRouter (PlayerVelocityEvent) resolves the pending and SHIPS the full formula (REGISTERED) or the carried vector (PRE_SENT, arming the ValveListener to eat vanilla's one duplicate). Mid-invuln stronger (difference) hits: vanilla fires EDBEE but no velocity event; the armed pending is later journaled 'superseded' — no knock, no flinch (era-correct), except stale armed pendings can hijack a foreign velocity event. Session tick per victim: drain inbox -> ledger.tick -> publish view -> desk.sweep (connected victims' LIVE pendings are never time-dropped).

### Findings (11)

#### `legacy-resistance-roll-zero-knock` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The default profile legacy-1.7 (and legacy-1.8) ships ResistancePolicy.LEGACY. For any victim with knockbackResistance > 0 (netherite armor: +0.1/piece), registration suppresses the velocity pre-send on EVERY hit ('resistance-roll') and ships a HURT-only burst; the region compute then rolls all-or-nothing: random.nextDouble() < resistance cancels the ENTIRE knock (Paced(null) -> desk.submit(tx, null) -> resolve branch 2 CANCEL_EVENT). The victim takes full damage and flinches but does not move at all — e.g. full netherite = 40% of all hits ship zero knockback, at any range, sprinting or not.

**Trigger:** Any hit on a victim wearing netherite (or any KB-resistance gear/effect) while a LEGACY-resistance profile is selected — legacy-1.7 is the shipped DEFAULT profile. Deterministically absent on all fork presets (ResistancePolicy.NONE).

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:547-555 (suppressorFor 'resistance-roll'), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:448-453 (resistanceCancels all-or-nothing), KnockbackEngine.java:192-194 (Paced(null)), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:181-185 (formula==null -> CANCEL_EVENT, journaled 'resistance-roll'), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java:46 (LEGACY on legacy-1.8; LEGACY_17 same per knockback-profiles skill 'legacy randomizes zero-knocks on modern gear').

**Maps to the report:** Verbatim match for 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback (the victim just doesnt really move back)' — hurt-flinch + damage + zero movement, randomly, on the default preset — IF victims wear KB-resistant gear. The all-or-nothing roll is itself the authentic era mechanic (era item pools just never triggered it), so this is era-real math with a modern-gear trigger.

#### `mid-invuln-difference-hit-era-silent` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Era rule (compendium): a STRONGER hit landing mid-invulnerability deals only the damage difference with NO knockback and no flinch. Mental reproduces it: registration's frozen damageImmune() (noDamageTicks > max/2+1) returns before any burst (no velocity, no hurt); the hit still dispatches; vanilla's difference branch fires EDBEE, the KnockbackUnit computes+submits+ARMS the desk, but vanilla applies no knockback and fires no PlayerVelocityEvent, so the armed pending is never resolved and is journaled 'superseded' by the next hit — no knock ever ships. With simulate-crits + Sharpness variance at close-range spam (jump-crit clicks), difference hits are frequent: damage lands, victim does not move.

**Trigger:** Any crit/higher-damage click landing while noDamageTicks > max/2 — the norm at 12-16 CPS close trades where most clicks fall inside the 10-tick window.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:334-336 (frozen-immune skips the whole burst), core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:227-253 and 328-343 (the era-silent difference contract; only the blocked shape is left UNARMED, non-blocked difference hits arm but vanilla never fires their velocity event), kernel/.../DeliveryDesk.java:312-317 (superseded journal). docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md (difference-damage rule).

**Maps to the report:** A legitimate, authentic chunk of 'some hits have no knockback' in close-range spam: those hits deal damage but the era itself shipped no knock. The owner should know this part of the feel is correct and must not be 'fixed'.

#### `suppressed-presend-recompute-reads-late-state` — divergence-from-era, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Only the netty pre-send honors the era boundary read: preVictimState uses the frozen PlayerView (motion = ledger residual as of END of previous tick, frozen grounded) and ring positions at arrival. Whenever the pre-send is suppressed (anticheat detected, LEGACY resistance profile, feedback-gate pace-out, frozen-immune-but-vanilla-accepted boundary hits, missing view fields, vanilla-path hits), the authoritative EDBEE recompute uses EntityStates.captureVictim: ledger.current() — which has taken 1-2 MORE decay ticks (session tickStep increments before the deferred damage runs) — plus LIVE isOnGround() and LIVE attacker/victim positions. Consequences at combo cadence: the residual x friction compounding term is smaller (x0.91 or x0.546 per extra tick); a same-tick landing becomes visible, flipping friction from air 0.91 to ground 0.546 and re-stamping the grounded vertical (the exact 'grounded 0.3608 re-stamp' the era ordering contract forbids); and at face-hug range the base-push direction is computed from positions 1-2 ticks after the era moment. Net: suppressed-path combo/sprint hits ship measurably weaker horizontal (and floatier vertical) than the same hit pre-sent, and arrive one tick later on the wire.

**Trigger:** Any melee hit whose velocity pre-send was suppressed, delivered while the victim carries a live ledger residual (combo follow-ups) — systematic when GrimAC/Vulcan is installed (all hits), per-hit under gate pace-outs/tick skew, and always for server-side (Vanilla-source) melee.

**Evidence:** Pre-send era read: core/.../HitRegistrationUnit.java:466-474 (view.motion(), view.grounded()); recompute late read: core/.../feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:270-272 (EntityStates.captureVictim), core/.../EntityStates.java:73-85 (ledger.current() + live isOnGround()), kernel/.../ledger/MotionLedger.java:118-133 (current() = base decayed ticksSinceRecord times), core/.../CombatSession.java:230-239 (ledger.tick then publish then sweep, once per tick). Boundary contract: .claude/skills/era-accuracy (the three boundary contracts) and legacy-motion-physics (within-tick ordering trap).

**Maps to the report:** The 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' component: the same swing ships two different vectors depending on which path delivered it, and the suppressed path is systematically the weaker/later one — subtle, non-reproducible, feel-level.

#### `anticheat-auto-suppresses-presend-globally` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** AnticheatMode.AUTO (default) with GrimAC or Vulcan present (default known-plugins list) sets allowVelocityPreSend=false permanently. Every hit then ships hurt-only at registration and takes the authoritative recompute path (finding suppressed-presend-recompute-reads-late-state): knock arrives at vanilla cadence (one RTT-leg + up to a tick later) computed from damage-time state. Magnitude is mostly compensated but combo residual/grounded divergence and delivery latency apply to 100% of hits.

**Trigger:** GrimAC or Vulcan installed on the server (anticheat.mode: auto, the default). Silent except one boot/enable log line.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/AnticheatSettings.java:13-14 (DEFAULTS = AUTO, [GrimAC, Vulcan]), core/.../feature/delivery/AnticheatCompatUnit.java:75-95 (evaluate/permissive), core/.../coexist/AnticheatPolicy.java:20-40, HitRegistrationUnit.java:548-550 (suppressorFor 'anticheat').

**Maps to the report:** If the owner's servers have historically run Grim/Vulcan, ALL knockback has always been the recompute-path variant — a plausible root of 'as far back as I can remember' persistent subtle weakness; if no anticheat is installed this finding is inert.

#### `stale-view-silent-vanilla-fallthrough` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** At registration, a player victim with a null published view, a view older than 4 ticks (PlayerView.fresh), creative flag, or pvp-off returns WITHOUT cancelling the ATTACK packet — the hit flows through to vanilla's full pipeline: modern vanilla knockback (sprint 0.7h/0.4v vs era 0.9h/0.4607v), no ledger combos, no w-tap extra, no sprint-verdict stamp. Nothing is journaled and no debug line fires, so these hits are invisible to Mental's own accounting. Views go stale when the victim's session tick lags 4+ ticks behind the TickClock — main-thread lag spikes on Paper, region-vs-global counter skew on Folia.

**Trigger:** Any melee hit landing during a tick-lag window or Folia region skew >= 4 ticks on the victim's session; also momentarily for just-joined victims before their first session tick.

**Evidence:** core/.../HitRegistrationUnit.java:269-273 (return without setCancelled -> vanilla), kernel/.../model/PlayerView.java:139-144 (fresh = recentAt(now, 4)), plus the catch-all at HitRegistrationUnit.java:233-236 (any Throwable -> packet flows to vanilla). Contrast: era sprint 0.9 vs modern 0.7 per era-accuracy skill ('Modern vanilla reference').

**Maps to the report:** 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' and 'seems like the non-sprinting knockback' — a vanilla-fallthrough sprint hit ships 0.7h, visibly below the era 0.9h, intermittently and untraceably. The decline-to-vanilla is designed, but its silence (no journal/debug entry) makes the symptom undiagnosable.

#### `cps-limiter-hard-drops-clicks` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** CpsLimiter (sliding 1s window, default max-cps: 20, per-ATTACKER) runs before everything else on the ATTACK packet; an over-limit click is event.setCancelled(true) + return — the attack is annihilated (no damage, no knock, no flinch, NOT passed to vanilla, nothing journaled). Answer to Q4: over-limit attacks are cancelled, never handed to vanilla, so there is no modern-vanilla-KB leak here — the failure mode is a wholly eaten hit. The window counts arrivals, so network burst-delivery (a 300-500ms stall flushing queued clicks) can push a 15-16 CPS clicker over 20-in-1s and eat the one click that mattered (the boundary-legal hit); butterfly clickers at ~20 CPS trip it routinely.

**Trigger:** Trailing-1s arrival count > max-cps (20 default): sustained 20+ CPS clicking, or 14-18 CPS plus a network stall/burst — i.e. exactly the frantic close-range trade.

**Evidence:** core/.../HitRegistrationUnit.java:250-254 (tryAcquire fail -> setCancelled + return, before target resolution), kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/CpsLimiter.java:17-62 (sliding window over arrival times), core/src/main/resources/hit-registration.yml:10-12 ('before clicks are dropped at the packet layer' — documented intent), core/.../config/settings/HitRegSettings.java:36-37 (DEFAULTS maxCps=20).

**Maps to the report:** An eaten boundary click reads as 'that hit did nothing' in a close trade; because invuln masks most spam clicks anyway, only the legal-cadence click being eaten is perceptible — rare, feel-level, unpinnable, like the report.

#### `feedback-gate-paces-out-legal-hits-under-skew` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** The per-victim FeedbackGate window (auto = max(0, maxNoDamageTicks/2 - 1) * 50ms = 450ms for max 20) is enforced at PRE-SEND ONLY (Q1: the authoritative path has no window; vanilla noDamageTicks is its pacing). A paced-out ELIGIBLE velocity ships NOTHING on the wire — the hurt is deliberately skipped too (shipBurst = vector==null || velocityShips) — and the tx stays REGISTERED; the authoritative EDBEE then computes and ships the full knock through the PlayerVelocityEvent (confirmed: no window-suppression leak into the authoritative apply; DeliveryDesk.resolve REGISTERED-LIVE branch SHIPS the formula). The knock is therefore full-magnitude-by-design but late (next tick + tracker flush) and computed from damage-time state (see suppressed-presend-recompute finding). In the clean model consecutive accepted hits' registrations are >= 450ms apart (gap = 500ms + intra-tick phase in (450,550)), so healthy-Paper pace-outs are rare; Folia's acknowledged +-1 counter/region skew or a 2-tick damage deferral compresses the gap into (400,550) and a real fraction of legal combo hits lose their pre-send. The gate is also the structural guard that prevents pre-sent-velocity-then-damage-rejected phantoms (Q2 'does the victim still fly': the one-tick view blindness after an interleaved accepted hit always falls inside the 450ms window, so the phantom pre-send is paced out; it becomes reachable only if feedback-min-interval-ms is configured to 0/small).

**Trigger:** Legal-cadence combo hits whose registrations land < 450ms apart in wall clock: Folia counter/region skew, lagging ticks, or damage-deferral asymmetry; never at exact healthy-Paper cadence. Setting feedback-min-interval-ms: 0 removes the phantom guard instead.

**Evidence:** core/.../feature/delivery/FeedbackGate.java:24-35, HitRegistrationUnit.java:392-434 (B4 pacing, minInterval math line 398-400, shipBurst line 425), HitRegistrationUnit.java:511-521 (admitVelocityPreSend), core/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationPacingTest.java (pins hurt-only-never-debits + pacing), kernel/.../DeliveryDesk.java:208-213 (REGISTERED resolve SHIPS full formula), kernel/.../wire/FeedbackPlan.java:44-53 (hurt-only plan).

**Maps to the report:** Maps to 'weak sprint hits sometimes': a paced-out hit's knock is late + recompute-flavored, not absent. Also answers Q2: registration never REJECTS a hit for immunity — the immune/window gates only suppress the burst; the hit always dispatches and vanilla's live counter is the authority.

#### `frozen-immune-band-fate-unresolved` — unknown, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** The +1 staleness allowance admits frozen noDamageTicks <= max/2+1 (11) for pre-send. A click arriving one tick earlier (frozen exactly 12) is denied the pre-send but still dispatched; whether vanilla accepts it at the deferred damage depends on the intra-tick order of the damage task vs the victim's noDamageTicks decrement. If the task runs BEFORE the decrement (Paper scheduler tasks at tick start — the order the 'gap-9 spam: velocities == damage events' pin implies), live reads 11 and vanilla rejects it era-consistently (the click is simply early). If it runs AFTER, live reads 10 and the hit is ACCEPTED — and because at 12-16 CPS the first legal click lands in the frozen-12 tick roughly as often as the frozen-11 tick, up to ~half of all spam-cadence combo hits would silently take the never-pre-sent recompute path (weaker/later knock). The repo pins admitted=>accepted but nothing pins the frozen-12 band's fate; it is the single highest-leverage unknown in this pathway.

**Trigger:** Spam-cadence (12-16+ CPS) combo hits whose first post-window click lands in the tick where the frozen view still reads max/2+2 — a roughly coin-flip phase event per combo hit.

**Evidence:** kernel/.../model/PlayerView.java:129-136 (damageImmune = noDamageTicks > max/2 + 1), core/.../HitRegistrationUnit.java:334-336 (immune skips pre-send only) and 436-449 (dispatch always schedules damage via scheduling.runOn), era-accuracy skill boundary-contracts section (gap-9 spam pin covers only admitted hits).

**Maps to the report:** If the accept-after-decrement ordering holds anywhere in the support range (Paper vs Folia scheduler differences), a large share of close-range combo hits ship the recompute-path knock — the strongest candidate for a persistent, subtle 'combo hits weaker than they should be' across versions. Needs a live probe (journal paceFactor/source vs pre-send counts at pinned cadence) to resolve.

#### `trade-opener-opposition-era-real` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The base 0.4 push points away from the ATTACKER'S POSITION while the sprint extra 0.5 points along the ATTACKER'S YAW. In a face-hug trade (victim at/past the attacker), the two terms oppose and the net horizontal collapses to ~0.05 — measured identical on real 1.7.10. Mental implements exactly this (base from source position, extras along yaw). Additionally era-real in mutual trades: every bonus-KB hit a player LANDS scales their own ledger residual x0.6 (applyAttackerObligations), so a victim who counter-hits mid-knock receives the next knock compounded off the smaller residual — trades genuinely knock less than clean chases did in the era.

**Trigger:** Both players inside ~1 block of each other trading (the report's exact scenario); the x0.6 compounding on every landed bonus hit in a mutual trade.

**Evidence:** kernel/.../math/KnockbackEngine.java:212-227 (base(victim, attacker.x, attacker.z, ...) + extras along yawRadians), core/.../feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:418-424 (ledger.scaleHorizontal(0.6) on accepted bonus hits), era-accuracy skill 'The trade-opener opposition ... ~0.05 h — era-real, identical on actual 1.7.10'.

**Maps to the report:** The dominant AUTHENTIC explanation of 'especially when two players are quite close together ... it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback': at face-hug geometry even a fresh sprint hit ships almost no horizontal, on real era servers too. The owner must not tune this away without knowing it is era truth.

#### `stale-armed-pending-hijacks-foreign-velocity` — bug, confidence low

**Mechanism:** For a NON-blocked hit whose frozen read says mid-invuln, the KnockbackUnit deliberately submits AND arms the desk (to protect legal boundary hits). For a genuine mid-invuln STRONGER difference hit, vanilla fires no velocity event, and because a CONNECTED victim's LIVE pending is never time-swept (the 2.4.6 fix), the armed melee vector lies in wait indefinitely. The next PlayerVelocityEvent from ANY foreign source (explosion, another plugin's setVelocity, vanilla-path projectile) resolves it: DeliveryDesk.resolve's REGISTERED-LIVE branch SHIPS the stale withheld melee knock in place of the foreign velocity. Normally the next melee hit's EDBEE supersedes it first, so pure-melee 1v1 never sees this; it needs a foreign velocity to land between a crit-difference hit and the next melee.

**Trigger:** Crit/sharpness difference hit mid-invuln (armed, no vanilla velocity event) followed by any non-Mental velocity event on the victim before the next melee EDBEE.

**Evidence:** core/.../feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:327-343 (submit + arm deliberately includes frozen-immune non-blocked hits), kernel/.../DeliveryDesk.java:260-277 (connected LIVE pending never dropped by sweep), DeliveryDesk.java:172-213 (resolve with awaiting + REGISTERED-LIVE ships the formula over whatever the event carried).

**Maps to the report:** Weak/indirect: it ships a WRONG vector (usually extra or misdirected knock replacing a foreign one) rather than a missing knock; included because it is a real leak of the era-silent suppression class into a later apply, and misattributed knocks feed 'inconsistent knockback' perception. Low frequency in melee-only play.

#### `wire-slot-clobber-under-tick-starvation` — bug, confidence low

**Mechanism:** DeliveryDesk.submitFromWire is a single last-write-wins AtomicReference drained only by owning-thread desk operations (sweep runs once per session tick). Two PRE_SENT submissions for one victim between drains silently overwrite the first transaction with no 'superseded' journal entry — the first hit's velocity already reached the client's wire, but the desk loses all accounting of it and its valve is never armed, so vanilla's duplicate ENTITY_VELOCITY for that hit is not consumed. Requires two pre-sends >= 450ms apart (the gate) landing within one un-ticked session window — i.e. the victim's session task starved for 10+ ticks (severe lag/region stall).

**Trigger:** Victim session task stalled >= ~10 ticks while two different pre-send-eligible hits register (two attackers, or one at legal cadence), e.g. a Folia region freeze or main-thread lag spike.

**Evidence:** kernel/.../DeliveryDesk.java:36-37 and 50-53 (wireSlot.set last-write-wins), DeliveryDesk.java:305-310 (drainWire only on owning-thread ops), DeliveryDesk.java:312-317 (the superseded journal only happens for DRAINED transactions), core/.../CombatSession.java:230-238 (drain cadence = session tick).

**Maps to the report:** Marginal: manifests as doubled/uncorrected client knock and a missing journal entry during lag, not weak knockback; reported for completeness because it is unjournaled state loss on the assigned seam.

## Finder: `ledger` — MotionLedger residual

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

The MotionLedger is a per-victim D2 (region-thread) fold of the era server-motion fields. State = one base sample (vx,vy,vz, grounded, slip) + ticksSinceRecord; current() = base decayed that many ticks (Decay: air 0.91/tick, ground slip×0.91=0.546; grounded reads ALWAYS return vy=−0.0784 equilibrium, discarding any recorded vy). Writers (complete inventory): (1) Deliveries.recordDelivered (called ONLY from DeskRouter.onPlayerVelocity after a SHIP) records the final shipped knock — melee only when profile.combos=true (legacy-1.7/kohi/minehq/badlion lineage); rod/arrow/thrown/bobber always — with grounded/slip taken from the CURRENTLY published view. (2) CombatSession.apply drains D1 LedgerEvents: Liftoff (GroundFsm: grounded→airborne rising ⇒ vy overwritten to 0.42+JumpBoost, +0.2 sprint facing push from last packet yaw, carried horizontals take one extra launch ground-drag; NON-rising ⇒ vy stamped to −0.0784 equilibrium), Landing (vy→equilibrium, horizontals preserved, slip reset to stone), Reset→Landing. (3) KnockbackUnit.applyAttackerObligations: scaleHorizontal(0.6) on the ATTACKER's ledger per accepted bonus hit, executed at EDBEE time (1–2 ticks after the attack packet). No walk/strafe/ring/packet velocity ever enters — the only "input-shaped" writes are the era-authentic jump stamp + sprint-jump push.

Readers: the netty pre-send (HitRegistrationUnit.preVictimState) reads view.motion()/view.grounded() from the published PlayerView; the region recompute (KnockbackUnit → EntityStates.captureVictim) reads ledger.current() LIVE plus live isOnGround — bypassing the publication boundary. The engine seeds base = motion×friction(0.5) − dir×push, y = vy×0.5 + 0.4 (ADD), so the residual feeds every knock and the ledger vy feeds every vertical (and the latency-compensation hint).

Critical sequencing: SessionService.tick runs sampleGround → buildView (reads ledger.current() PRE-drain) → tickStep (drain inbox → ledger.tick → publish that pre-built view → desk.sweep). So a ground event arriving after tick P's session task is applied at P+1 but first VISIBLE in the view published at P+2 — the published "end-of-previous-tick" boundary actually lags inbox-fed liftoffs/landings by up to one extra tick. Direct writes (recordDelivered, ×0.6) are visible at the next view build. Grounded-decay count between record and liftoff (the era 0.4×slip² pin, MotionLedgerTest) therefore floats ±1 with velocity-event-vs-session-task intra-tick order and packet phase. Kernel math itself reproduces the era chain pins exactly (0.9×0.546², ice 0.4821).

### Findings (9)

#### `no-client-input-in-ledger` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Q1 smoking-gun check: NEGATIVE. The complete ledger write set is recordDelivered (shipped knocks only), Liftoff/Landing/Reset events, and scaleHorizontal(0.6). A victim strafing into their attacker contributes NOTHING to the residual — no PositionRing, packet-delta, or walk-accel value is ever folded in. The only input-shaped writes are the era jump stamp (0.42+boost) and the 0.2 sprint facing push at a rising liftoff, both of which the era server's own movement-handler bookkeeping also wrote into its fields. Toward-attacker residual sources that DO weaken a knock all have era precedents: rod-pull records (always, even combos=false), third-party knocks, post-crossing residuals, and the victim's own sprint-jump-into-attacker push (~0.2×0.5=0.1 h reduction, decaying).

**Trigger:** Any close-range trade; e.g. victim sprint-jumps back into the attacker → ledger holds ~0.2 toward-attacker, next knock base loses up to ~0.1 h — authentic 1.7/1.8 server-field behavior.

**Evidence:** Writers: core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/Deliveries.java:25-45; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/CombatSession.java:241-250; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:423. Liftoff push: kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/GroundFsm.java:91-100; fed only from packets: core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/PacketTap.java:89-93. Era ground truth: .claude/skills/legacy-motion-physics/SKILL.md:58-67 and era-accuracy SKILL.md:59-66.

**Maps to the report:** Rules out the hypothesized 'victim walking into attacker opposes the knock' bug; the residual-opposition that exists is authentic era behavior.

#### `ledger-vy-overdecay-and-nonrising-liftoff-misstamp` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Known, live-diagnosed (research doc): a victim who stays airborne between hits has its ledger vy free-fall toward −3.92 while the real client hovers at −0.05..−0.34 (each knock re-lifts the client; combos=false never re-records melee so nothing resets the decay clock; combos=true resets it but a >~16-tick airborne gap still crosses −0.8). Shipped y = vy×friction.y + 0.4 goes to ~0 (floored at verticalMin 0.0 since 2.4.7/2.4.8 across the whole bundle) — a no-pop hit whose horizontal then dies at the client's ground drag. Confirmed accelerant in the same doc: GroundFsm.onMovement judges rising by knownY>lastY, so a knock-induced liftoff sampled non-rising (victim knocked into a wall — or into the ATTACKER'S BODY at <1.5 blocks, exactly the report's geometry) stamps vy at −0.0784 instead of the era 0.42/knock-vy chain, starting the free-fall a full jump-impulse deep.

**Trigger:** Close-range spam where the victim never cleanly lands between hits (juggle/wall/body-block): mid-combo hits read vy −0.5..−1.5 and ship y≈0 (floored) instead of the era ~0.25 declining vertical; worst on combos=false presets (legacy-1.8, mmc, lunar: 5 downward + 12 divergent of 608 hits measured) but reachable on legacy-1.7 with combo gaps.

**Evidence:** docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-ledger-vy-divergence.md:17-45,53-61,99-103 (measured: ledgerVy −1.504 vs ring −0.341; APPLY LIFTOFF stampVy=-0.0784). Non-rising branch: kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/GroundFsm.java:85,101-104. Vertical seam: kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:496-500. Floor masking: kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/KnockbackProfile.java:137-144.

**Maps to the report:** Strongest ledger-pathway match for 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback... especially when two players are quite close together': a zero-vertical hit on a grounded-feeling client reads as the victim 'not really moving back', is intermittent (depends on airborne-gap length and sampling phase), and the 2.4.8 floor hides the downward symptom while leaving the dead-hit feel.

#### `ground-event-view-staleness-one-extra-tick` — bug, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** SessionService.tick builds the view (reading ledger.current()) BEFORE tickStep drains the inbox, and tickStep then publishes that pre-built view. So a Liftoff/Landing that arrived after tick P's session task is folded into the ledger at P+1 but first appears in the view published at P+2. The stated contract is 'view = state as of the END of the previous tick' — a P-tick landing should be visible to a P+1 hit (era servers only excluded SAME-tick movement). Consequence for a hit thrown one tick after touchdown (a common spam rhythm): the pre-send reads a still-airborne view with the pre-landing free-falling vy → ships y = vy×0.5+0.4 with vy −0.3..−0.5 → y ≈ 0.15..0.25 (or floored) instead of the era grounded re-stamp 0.3608, plus air multipliers apply (identity on legacy presets, real on signature). Nondeterministic: depends on where the movement packet lands relative to the session task's phase within the tick (~half of transitions get the extra tick).

**Trigger:** Victim touches down at tick P (packet arrives after P's session task); attacker hits at P+1: view still says airborne with deep vy; the PRE_SENT vector is adopted unchanged by the authoritative pass, so the weak vertical ships.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:325-347 (buildView at 335 precedes tickStep at 347; ledger.current() read at 533); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/CombatSession.java:230-239 (drain happens inside tickStep, after the view was built); research doc exemplar 'landing fires the NEXT tick' at docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-ledger-vy-divergence.md:55-56. Era contract: .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:29-39 (same-tick exclusion only).

**Maps to the report:** Adds a random per-hit weak-vertical mode at exactly spam cadence — 'very subtle and hard to reproduce, more like a feeling thing'; compounds with the vy over-decay (the deeper the stale vy, the deadER the hit).

#### `region-recompute-bypasses-boundary-read` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** Non-pre-sent melee (tx REGISTERED) is computed at EDBEE via EntityStates.captureVictim, which reads ledger.current() LIVE and player.isOnGround() LIVE — not the published view. The deferred damage task runs 1–2 ticks after registration, and by then the session task has usually decayed the ledger 1–2 more ticks and drained same-tick ground events. Effects vs the era end-of-previous-tick read the pre-send honors: (a) grounded residual under-read by ×0.546..×0.298 (−45..−70%) → visibly weaker combo compounding on these hits; (b) a same-tick landing becomes visible → grounded 0.3608 re-stamp where the era ships the pre-landing declining vertical. Hits that take this path: fast-path/pre-send disabled, anticheat suppressor active, LEGACY-resistance profiles with resistant victims, a paced-out velocity (feedback gate under tick-time jitter), a frozen-immune-flagged registration, and ALL vanilla ENTITY_ATTACK melee.

**Trigger:** legacy-1.7 (combos=true) with hit-registration fast-path or pre-send-feedback off (or an anticheat detected): hit 2 of a grounded trade computes base from a residual read 2 ticks late — 0.49×0.5 vs 0.27×0.5 ≈ 0.11 h missing — and boundary hits re-stamp grounded verticals.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:271 (captureVictim with live ledger); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/EntityStates.java:73-85 (live isOnGround at 77, ledger.current() at 78); contrast the pre-send boundary read at core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:466-474; exclusion-by-publication contract: kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:18-19; suppression/pacing gates: HitRegistrationUnit.java:334-336,398-413.

**Maps to the report:** On default config (pre-send on) most hits adopt the pre-sent vector and avoid this; it becomes a weak-trade contributor exactly when a suppressor is in play — a plausible reason the owner sees it 'as far back as I can remember' across setups but can never pin it.

#### `attacker-self-slow-applied-late` — divergence-from-era, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Q5: vanilla applied the ×0.6 attacker self-multiply synchronously inside attack(), in arrival order within the tick; Mental applies scaleHorizontal(0.6) at the deferred EDBEE (1–2 ticks after the counter-attack packet), and the pre-send only sees it one view-publication later. For a same-tick counter-hit trade on legacy-1.7 there is a ~2–3 tick window where the next knock's base reads the UN-scaled residual: shipped h differs by (1−0.6)×R×0.5 = 0.2R. With R ≈ 0.49 (one grounded decay of a 0.9 sprint stamp) that is ≈ +0.10 h (≈+0.3–0.4 blocks settle) STRONGER than era when the residual points away from the attacker (the common combo geometry), and the same amount WEAKER when the residual points toward the attacker (post-crossing / rod-pull residual). Note the shipped stamp itself is never ×0.6-scaled in either system (era full-stamp tracker sent before the victim's connection slot; Mental ships at registration) — the divergence is residual-only. Separately: the ×0.6 family (server residual scale + the untouchable CLIENT-side 0.6^clicks self-multiply) is the authentic reason mutual high-CPS trades feel like reduced knockback.

**Trigger:** A and B trading in the same/adjacent ticks at close range, combos=true presets: B counter-hits at tick T; A's hits at T..T+2 read B's residual pre-×0.6.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:404-424 (obligations at EDBEE, scaleHorizontal at 423); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:104-116; engine residual seam: kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:497-501; era timing: .claude/skills/legacy-motion-physics/SKILL.md:99-102, era-accuracy SKILL.md:60-63 (client 0.6^clicks is era-real and untouchable).

**Maps to the report:** The timing divergence mostly ships STRONGER (anti-report); the report-matching part — trades feeling like non-sprint knockback — is dominated by the era-real client-side 0.6^clicks plus the era-real face-hug opener opposition (~0.05 h when past the attacker, era-accuracy SKILL.md:119-122), not by a ledger defect.

#### `grounded-decay-count-jitter` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** The number of grounded decays a combo residual takes before its air segment (the era 0.4×slip² two-decay pin) floats between 1 and 3 in live operation: recordDelivered lands at PlayerVelocityEvent time whose order against the session task's ledger.tick within the same server tick is scheduler-dependent, and the Liftoff's drain tick depends on the client packet's arrival phase (plus the one-extra-tick inbox staleness). Each ± tick is ×0.546 on the residual (grounded stone), i.e. hit-2's compounding term varies ~±45% hit-to-hit (≈0.06–0.13 of the 0.4-0.9 h). The era had its own variance (join-order bimodal) but it was FIXED per player pair; Mental's is per-hit noise.

**Trigger:** Any combos=true chain; two identical-looking boundary hits ship residual terms of 0.9×0.546 vs 0.9×0.546² depending on intra-tick ordering and ping phase.

**Evidence:** Pin assumes exactly one tick between record and liftoff: kernel/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedgerTest.java:94-108,173-188; live sequencing: core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/DeskRouter.java:78-88 (record at velocity event) vs core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/CombatSession.java:230-239 (tick in session task); launch drag: kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:76-85.

**Maps to the report:** Hit-to-hit combo-strength variance with no reproducible trigger — feeds the 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' texture, though bounded (~0.2–0.4 blocks of settle).

#### `combos-false-flat-wire-confirmed` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Q3: for mmc/lunar/legacy-1.8 (combos=false), Deliveries.recordDelivered skips melee entirely, so trades never build a melee residual — base's motion term is only the jump-bookkeeping feed (0.42 stamp free-falling + 0.2 sprint push) and rod/projectile records. That reproduces 1.8.9's send-then-restore fields exactly (era 1.8 fields also kept the jump stamp — it is what produces the authentic declining combo verticals, hit-2 vy ≈0.25–0.35). For combos=true the kernel chain reproduces the era pins bit-for-bit: hit-1 (0.9, 0.4607); residual at a 10-tick hit-2 = 0.9×0.546²×0.91⁸ ≈ 0.126 → hit-2 h ≈ 0.963; ice chain 0.4×0.8918²×0.91⁷×0.5+0.4 = 0.4821 = the compendium figure. No drift found in the pure math.

**Trigger:** N/A — confirmation of intended behavior; the melee-record gate and the decay pins are unit-pinned.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/Deliveries.java:33-44; kernel/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedgerTest.java:110-125,173-188; presets: kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/KnockbackProfile.java:128-153, kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java:28-38.

**Maps to the report:** On combos=false presets, weak-feeling trades cannot come from residual math (there is none for melee) — pointing the diagnosis at the vertical family (vy over-decay/mis-stamp) and at non-ledger pathways for those presets.

#### `packetless-ensure-skips-ledger-record` — bug, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** The stranded-packetless-melee net ships via desk.ensure() which records the journal and CLEARS the decision before setVelocity; the velocity event that setVelocity later fires finds no pending and PASS_THROUGHs, so Deliveries.recordDelivered never runs — a combos=true packetless victim's ensured melee knock never enters its ledger, and its subsequent combo hits miss the residual (weaker than a real client's). Deliveries' own javadoc claims the ensure path also folds the ledger, but grep shows recordDelivered has exactly one caller (DeskRouter). Real clients are unaffected (domains.has gate skips them).

**Trigger:** SimpleBoxer/FakePlayer victims under combos=true whose velocity event lands after the 2-tick window: hit ships via the net, ledger stays empty, hit-2 loses the ~0.06–0.13 h compounding term — a lab-measurement skew, not a player-facing issue.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:389-418 (ensure → setVelocity, no record); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:286-297 (ensure clears the decision); sole recordDelivered caller: core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/DeskRouter.java:81 vs the two-caller claim in core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/Deliveries.java:9-14.

**Maps to the report:** Does not explain the owner's real-client report, but will make bot-based reproduction attempts of the weak-combo feel read WEAKER than real play — a trap for the verification round.

#### `landing-resets-slip-to-stone` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** recordLanding resets slip to DEFAULT_SLIPPERINESS (0.6) by design ('the landed block's slip arrives with the next knock'); on ice/slime arenas a mid-combo landing decays the horizontal residual at 0.546 instead of 0.8918 until the next record — up to ~1.6×/tick faster residual death than the era per-tick block read, shrinking ice-combo compounding between hits.

**Trigger:** Ice-floor combos (legacy-1.7/kohi): victim lands between hits; residual between landing and the next hit under-persists vs real 1.7.10 ice measurements.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:94-102 (slip = DEFAULT on landing); era per-segment block read: .claude/skills/legacy-motion-physics/SKILL.md:83-89; recordDelivered does refresh slip from the view at each knock: core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/Deliveries.java:42-43.

**Maps to the report:** Only on non-stone floors; irrelevant to the flat-ground report unless the owner's arena is ice — worth naming since ice arenas are common in practice servers.

## Finder: `era-truth` — Era ground truth for close-range trades (docs-only reference)

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

ERA GROUND TRUTH for close-range trades (docs-only reference; no Mental code read). Era knock = two independent terms: (1) base knockBack — strength param IGNORED, always 0.4: motion/2 per axis, then −dir·0.4 horizontal where dir = normalized (attacker.pos − victim.pos); vy = min(0.4, vy/2+0.4), standing baseline −0.0784 so vy ships 0.3608. Degenerate geometry is guarded in attackEntityFrom, not knockBack: while dx²+dz² < 1e-4 (i.e. <~0.01 blocks horizontal separation) each axis is re-rolled random ±0.01 — full 0.4 magnitude in a RANDOM direction, no NaN. (2) Extras: addVelocity(±sin/cos yaw · levels·0.5, +0.1) along ATTACKER YAW, additive past the cap; sprint = +1 level. At face-hug the two terms can OPPOSE (base positional backward vs sprint yaw forward): measured on real 1.7.10, 0.0546 h at 0.14-block separation; vertical unaffected (victim pops up in place). Gating: fresh hit arms a 20-tick window; while hurtResistantTime>10 an equal/weaker hit does NOTHING and a stronger hit deals difference damage with ZERO knock/flinch/sound — at 10 CPS same-weapon, ~80% of landed clicks move the victim zero. Delivery: 1.8.9 sends the packet INSIDE attack() then restores server fields (both trade partners receive the full stamp, symmetric, flat); 1.7.10 ships via next tick's tracker, which runs BEFORE the join-ordered connection slots — so the later-joined victim's own slot (counter-attack ×0.6 on their just-stamped fields if bonus-KB, then one physics decay ×0.546 grounded) bites BEFORE the wire ships: later-joiner sprint wire ≈ 0.9→0.4914, or ≈0.295 if they counter-sprint-hit same tick; earlier-joiner receives the full 0.9. Era 1.7 mutual trades were structurally asymmetric and WEAK for one side (measured: charge-combo victim pinned at 0.07–0.27 blocks). Client contract (untouchable, fires regardless of Mental's server-side packet cancel — prediction runs before the server sees anything): every bonus-KB click whose raycast hits a player (client attackEntityFrom for remote players returns true unconditionally — no damage/invuln requirement) multiplies the clicker's OWN motion ×0.6 and un-sprints locally; a knocked victim who counter-clicks erases their own received KB 0.6^clicks. Era clients re-sent START_SPRINTING one tick after every attack's sprint clear (with W held), so accepted-cadence hits were nearly all sprint hits; MODERN clients mirror the un-sprint/×0.6 only at ≥90% attack charge, so at 10+ CPS they neither self-slow nor re-send START. Era block-hitting dropped sprint (STOP sent) — clicks while blocking shipped PLAIN authentically; modern clients keep sprint through item use.

### Findings (10)

#### `mid-invuln-zero-knock` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Era hurt-window rule (both eras, unchanged in Mental by construction): fresh hit sets hurtResistantTime=20/lastDamage; while >10, an equal-or-weaker hit is fully ignored (no damage, no knock, no flinch) and a STRONGER hit deals only difference damage with ZERO knockback, no flinch, no sound. At click interval d ticks only ~d/10 of landed clicks knock: 10 CPS => ~80% of visually-landing hits move the victim zero; 16 CPS => ~87%. A rod/0-damage hit arms the full window at lastDamage=0, so a sword hit within 10 ticks deals damage but never knocks.

**Trigger:** Any spam trade at <=10-tick click spacing with same-damage weapons; or rod-then-sword inside 10 ticks; or a crit thrown mid-window (damage lands, still no knock — the most convincing 'hit clearly registered but no KB' case).

**Evidence:** docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:51-54 (mid-invuln branch: weaker->false, stronger->difference, fullHit=false => no knockback/animation/sound), :240-241 (maxHurtResistantTime 20, full-hit cadence 10t); SYNOPSIS.md:70-71, :442 (identical all three versions); docs/legacy-combat.md:74 (Mental damages through vanilla's own window by construction).

**Maps to the report:** The single largest authentic contributor to 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback' at high CPS — the majority of thrown hits in a spam trade produced zero motion on real 1.7.10/1.8.9 too.

#### `victim-counter-click-0.6-self-slow` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Client prediction (untouchable contract): PlayerControllerMP.attackEntity sends the ATTACK packet then runs the attack locally; EntityOtherPlayerMP.attackEntityFrom returns true UNCONDITIONALLY for player targets, so every bonus-KB click (client sprint flag true, or KB enchant) whose raycast hits a player within client reach multiplies the clicker's OWN client motion x0.6 and un-sprints locally — it does NOT require the hit to deal damage, to be outside the invuln window, or to be accepted by the server, and Mental's server-side packet cancel cannot change it (prediction already ran). A knocked victim who counter-clicks during flight cuts remaining horizontal to 0.6 (1 click), 0.36 (2), 0.216 (3); felt settle distance roughly 60-75% / 45-65% / 40-55% of full depending on click timing (earlier bites harder). In a mutual face-hug both players do this to each other continuously — both knocks get largely erased client-side. Caveat: MODERN clients gate the local x0.6 (and un-sprint) on attack charge >0.9, so at 10+ CPS on a modern client most clicks do NOT self-slow — the era 0.6^clicks reduction is weaker on modern clients unless attack-speed is spoofed to keep charge full (Mental's CADENCE cooldown removal would restore era-frequency x0.6). The related MYTH: victim sprint-KEY spamming (without clicks landing a raycast target) changes nothing — placebo, pinned live.

**Trigger:** Both players sprint-clicking each other at <1.5 blocks, 8+ CPS: each received knock is multiplied 0.6 per counter-click that raycasts onto the opponent.

**Evidence:** SYNOPSIS.md:138 (client applies bonus-KB prediction, slows itself x0.6, un-sprints — EntityOtherPlayerMP.attackEntityFrom returns true), :382 (modern RemotePlayer.hurtClient->true reproduces it); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:253-256 (0.6^clicks, the CPS-reduces-received-KB mechanic); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:62-64 (client contract, never touch), :85-88 (sprint-key-spam myth); SYNOPSIS.md:308-311+330-343 (modern x0.6 inside causeExtraKnockback, only when amount>0 = sprint AND charge>0.9).

**Maps to the report:** Directly predicts 'close trades feel like non-sprint knockback' as authentic: the wire ships the full sprint stamp but the victim's own counter-clicks delete it client-side. Also predicts the feel differs by client version (weaker reduction on modern clients).

#### `face-hug-opposed-terms` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The base 0.4 pushes away from the ATTACKER'S POSITION; the sprint/enchant extra 0.5/level pushes along the ATTACKER'S YAW. When the victim has charged past/through the attacker the two terms OPPOSE: measured on real vanilla 1.7.10, hit at 0.14-block separation shipped 0.0546 horizontal (vs 0.4914/0.9 at normal range). The vertical is untouched by the cancellation (sprint vy 0.4607 still ships) — the victim pops straight up without moving back, which reads as 'no knockback'. At realistic first-hit range (2.4-2.8 blocks) the terms agree and the full value ships. A PLAIN (non-sprint) face-hug hit has no opposing term and ships the full 0.4 — so paradoxically the sprint hit can move the victim LESS than a plain hit at face-hug, matching 'even sprinting, it seems like non-sprint knockback'.

**Trigger:** Attacker sprint-hits a victim who is beside/behind the attacker's position relative to the attacker's facing (typical after both players charge through each other in a trade), separation under ~1 block.

**Evidence:** docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md:120-129 ('The trade-opener geometry — why no knockback is sometimes era-correct'; measured 0.0546 h at 0.14 blocks on real 1.7.10 semantics; 'Face-hug trades producing near-zero openers is authentic 1.7.10 behavior, not a delivery bug'); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:118-121 (same verdict).

**Maps to the report:** Exactly the reported scenario: 'especially when two players are quite close together' + 'seems like non-sprinting knockback' — the sprint extra is what gets geometrically cancelled.

#### `coincident-position-random-direction` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The era degenerate-geometry guard lives in attackEntityFrom, NOT knockBack: while dx^2+dz^2 < 1.0e-4 (horizontal separation under ~0.01 blocks), each axis is re-rolled to random +-0.01 in a while loop — the base knock keeps full 0.4 magnitude but in a RANDOM horizontal direction; no NaN, no zero (knockBack then normalizes safely). Combined with the yaw-directed sprint extra 0.5, a truly-coincident sprint hit ships anywhere from ~0.1 (random direction opposing yaw) to ~0.9 (aligned) — unpredictable per hit. This threshold is tiny: between 0.01 and ~0.5 blocks separation the direction is well-defined and finding face-hug-opposed-terms governs instead.

**Trigger:** Both players' positions horizontally coincident within 0.01 blocks (players standing inside each other, common at 0-range wall trades).

**Evidence:** docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:60-62 (coincident-position re-roll: while < 1.0e-4 -> random +-0.01 each axis); SYNOPSIS.md:64 (degeneracy fallback (random-random)*0.01 while d^2+d2^2 < 1e-4), :262 (modern moved it inside knockback, <1e-5). Not a doc gap — the compendium cites the decompile explicitly.

**Maps to the report:** Adds an authentic randomness component at extreme close range — some hits push sideways/into the attacker rather than back, read as 'no knockback'.

#### `era-17-trade-asymmetry-decayed-counter-wire` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** SAME-TICK MUTUAL TRADE reconstruction. 1.7.10: the tracker (which ships pending velocity) runs BEFORE the per-connection phase, whose slots run in JOIN ORDER with each player's physics fused to their slot. Later-joined victim B (A joined first): tick T — A's slot stamps B; B's slot then processes B's counter-ATTACK (an accepted bonus-KB counter multiplies B's OWN just-stamped server fields x0.6, compendium 1.5), then B's physics decays once (x0.546 grounded h, one gravity step v); tick T+1 tracker ships the survivor: sprint stamp 0.9 -> 0.4914 decayed, or ~0.295 h if B counter-sprint-hit in the same tick (0.9*0.6*0.546; component facts decompile-cited, the combined number is an ordering derivation, not separately wire-measured). Earlier-joiner A is stamped in B's slot AFTER A's physics already ran — tracker ships A the FULL 0.9/0.4607. So vanilla 1.7.10 mutual trades were structurally one-sided: the later joiner takes half-or-less knockback every trade ('relog for less KB' folklore). Wire-measured: standing 0.2184/0.2751 vs 0.4/0.3608, sprint 0.4914/0.3731 vs 0.9/0.4607 by join order (3/3 deterministic); charge-combo (both sprint, w-tap, attacker-first staging) pinned the victim at 0.07-0.27 blocks per hit. 1.8.9: the packet leaves INSIDE attack() and fields are restored before the victim's own slot runs — both partners receive the full stamp, symmetric; the counter x0.6 can only act client-side after arrival. MENTAL deliberately does NOT replicate the coin flip: tracker and immediate both ship the FULL stamp; tracker-decayed is opt-in; the pre-send fixes the wire at registration so a counter-attack's ledger x0.6 only shapes the NEXT knock. Mental's close trades are therefore era-1.8.9-shaped and STRONGER than vanilla-1.7.10 for the later joiner.

**Trigger:** Any mutual same/adjacent-tick trade on real vanilla 1.7.10; the weak side is always the later-joined player, weaker still when they counter-sprint-hit.

**Evidence:** docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md:161-222 (addendum 2: tracker-before-connection phases, join-order slots, measured both orders), :18 (charge-combo victim pinned 0.07-0.27), :44-46 (one stamp per knock, never re-sent); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:129-143 (1.5: attacker-side x0.6 is a SERVER-field write, shapes 1.7 trade exchanges), :287-299 (1.7.10 decayed-wire table); .claude/skills/knockback-profiles/SKILL.md:90-108 (both deliveries ship the full stamp; never ship decayed by default).

**Maps to the report:** The owner's memory of close trades having weak/no KB is authentic vanilla-1.7.10 for one side of every pairing — but Mental deliberately ships the full stamp both ways, so THIS mechanism cannot be the cause in Mental unless a profile opts into tracker-decayed (config-dependent: delivery.melee tracker-decayed). If the owner's baseline feel expectation is era-1.7 trades, Mental is actually stronger, not weaker.

#### `blockhit-clicks-are-plain-in-era` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** On 1.7/1.8 clients, using an item multiplies moveForward x0.2, dropping it below the 0.8 sprint threshold — starting a block STOPS sprint the same tick and the client sends STOP_SPRINTING. Every click thrown WHILE blocking is therefore authentically a PLAIN (non-sprint) hit; the sprint bonus only returns on release + re-engage (which is why block-hitting worked as an easy w-tap: the reset re-armed the bonus for the NEXT hit). Modern 1.17+ clients keep the sprint flag through item use ('using an item no longer stops an ongoing sprint'), so that STOP never crosses the wire; Mental reconstructs only the FUNCTIONAL w-tap re-arm (SwordBlockingUnit re-arms the SprintWire on the block right-click, gated on the raw client sprint flag) — the docs do not state that Mental makes during-block clicks plain, so on modern clients Mental plausibly ships SPRINT knockback for during-block hits where era shipped plain (a divergence toward MORE KB, for the code readers to verify).

**Trigger:** Attacker block-hitting: any click thrown while the block is held (before release/re-engage) on an era client.

**Evidence:** SYNOPSIS.md:145 (item use multiplies moveForward x0.2 -> kills sprint same tick), :387 (modern: item use no longer stops ongoing sprint); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:69-83 (block-hitting's sprint reset, modern-client divergence, SwordBlockingUnit reconstruction gated on raw client sprint).

**Maps to the report:** Directly addresses 'even if one is blockhitting, it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback' — on era clients that was literally true for clicks during the block; the perception may be authentic era feel rather than a bug.

#### `sprint-rearm-cadence-fraction` — era-real, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** Era servers cleared the attacker's sprint flag inside every accepted bonus-KB attack; the client (key held) re-sprints the very next tick and sends START_SPRINTING. Because KNOCKING hits are gated to >=10-tick spacing by the hurt window, the flag is re-armed long before the next accepted hit — for a W-holding spammer, essentially ALL era accepted hits were sprint-bonus hits. The authentically-PLAIN accepted hits came from: (a) clicks landing during a w-tap's released phase (a tap cycle is ~4-6 ticks; a hit timed into the 2-3 released ticks ships plain — 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback' is real for aggressive tappers whose hit lands mid-tap), (b) clicks while block-hitting (separate finding), (c) sub-tick arrival races: the era queue applied STOP/START/ATTACK in ARRIVAL order — an ATTACK flushed together with its own post-hit STOP was still a sprint hit (flag read inside attack, ahead of the packet), but an ATTACK arriving ahead of its re-arm START shipped plain. GAP: the docs contain NO measurement of the sprint-bonus duty cycle at CPS (no wire count of sprint vs plain hits in a spam run) — the fraction is inferred from the documented state machine, not measured. Mental's own historical failure modes here (registration reading the flag after the client's same-flush STOP; the desk never clearing the flag) are both documented as found-and-fixed (1.5.0), with the SprintVerdict stamp and SprintWire arrival-order view as the current contracts.

**Trigger:** Attacker w-tapping with hits landing during the released phase, or an ATTACK racing its own re-arm START in the same flush.

**Evidence:** SYNOPSIS.md:146 (client re-sprints the very next tick after the attack's sprint-reset); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:257-264 (w-tap re-arm; 1.8.9 attack-time flag read ahead of same-flush STOP); docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md:250-260 (addendum 3 items 1-2: the two Mental sprint bugs and fixes); .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md:229-257 (sprint-clear obligation, SprintVerdict stamp, SprintWire arrival-order contract). Gap: no measured sprint-hit fraction anywhere in the docs.

**Maps to the report:** Part of 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' is authentic: mid-tap and mid-block clicks were plain in era; but the docs cannot bound how much — a Mental-side sprint-state regression would present identically and must be excluded by the code investigators.

#### `modern-client-no-rearm-below-90pct-charge` — unknown, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** The era re-arm contract ('client re-sends START next tick') silently does NOT hold on modern clients below full charge: modern client prediction runs the un-sprint/x0.6 only when kbAttack = sprinting AND charge>0.9 (causeExtraKnockback amount>0), and the docs state explicitly 'modern clients only do the client-side part of this at >=90% charge'. At 10+ CPS with a sword (12.5-tick full charge) virtually no click is >90%, so the modern client's local sprint flag NEVER flips on attack — and a client whose state never changed sends no STOP/START pair. Meanwhile Mental's desk (era rule, charge-blind) clears the SERVER sprint flag after every accepted sprint-bonus hit. On an era client the next-tick START restored it; on a modern client no START ever comes, so whatever mechanism restores the server-side/wire sprint view (the raw clientSprinting read that 'survives Mental's own post-hit setSprinting(false)', the >=3-tick wire-silence reconcile) is load-bearing for EVERY subsequent hit's sprint bonus. The docs establish the contract break; whether Mental's bridge (raw clientSprinting / SprintWire freshness / reconcile) fully covers a no-w-tap W-holder at high CPS is NOT verifiable from the docs and must be checked in code. If any path consumes the cleared flag instead of the raw client flag, subsequent hits ship plain until a real STOP/START (w-tap) arrives — intermittent, feel-level, worst for non-tappers, exactly shaped like the report.

**Trigger:** Modern-client attacker holding W (no w-tap), spam-clicking at high CPS: server flag cleared by Mental after hit N, no client START before hit N+1.

**Evidence:** docs/legacy-combat.md:96-100 ('All eras un-sprint the attacker... modern clients only do the client-side part of this at >=90% charge. Mental keeps the server's sprint flag client-authoritative'); SYNOPSIS.md:330-343 (x0.6/setSprinting(false) prediction inside amount>0 branch), :384-387 (modern sprint state machine); .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md:229-257 (desk's post-hit clear, wire clear mirror, >=3-tick reconcile re-adopting server-granted setSprinting); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:76-80 (raw client sprint flag is 'the only signal that survives Mental's own post-hit setSprinting(false)').
