**Maps to the report:** Prime doc-derivable candidate for the non-era component of 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback': the era assumption behind the post-hit sprint clear is false on modern clients, so a gap in the raw-flag bridge would ship plain hits intermittently. Needs code verification — do not treat as confirmed.

#### `blocked-knock-cancel-config` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** Era truth: sword blocking halves DAMAGE only, applied AFTER knockBack — a blocking victim takes FULL knockback (wire-verified: blocking victim shipped (0.3608, 0.4) at 4.5 dmg). The compendium flags that Mental's era presets ship shield-blocking-cancels: true, 'which deviates whenever a BLOCKING damage modifier appears (OCM sword-block) — validation item, likely preset default change'. The era-accuracy skill states the current rule as 'era blocking knocks FULL (cancel only full blocks) — Mental cancels only FULL blocks', and the 2.4.0 round record describes the full-block delivery fix — suggesting partial blocks now knock full. If any configuration still routes a sword-block/partial-block damage modifier into the cancel (era preset knob true + a sword-blocking rule feature enabled, Mental's own DAMAGE family or another plugin's), a block-hitting VICTIM receives ZERO knockback where era shipped full.

**Trigger:** Victim block-hitting while a BLOCKING damage modifier source is active (Mental DAMAGE sword-blocking feature or third-party) and the selected profile has shield-blocking-cancels: true (the era presets' shipped value per the compendium note) treating the partial block as a cancel.

**Evidence:** docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:232-236 (blocking halves damage AFTER knockBack ran; 'Mental's era presets ship shield-blocking-cancels: true, which deviates whenever a BLOCKING damage modifier appears... validation item'); :329 (scoreboard: partial block knocks FULL, full block cancels — era-identical when validated); SYNOPSIS.md:169 (blocking never reduces KB in 1.7/1.8); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:47-49 (cancel only FULL blocks).

**Maps to the report:** Would produce literal zero knockback on hits against a block-hitting opponent — one of the two named report scenarios. The docs internally disagree on whether this is resolved (compendium open item vs skill's stated rule); code readers must determine the current cancel predicate and preset values.

#### `mental-full-stamp-divergence-context` — divergence-from-era, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Deliberate, documented divergences of Mental from vanilla-1.7.10 trade delivery, ALL in the direction of MORE knockback: (1) both tracker and immediate deliveries ship the FULL undecayed stamp (the join-order coin flip is not replicated; tracker-decayed is opt-in and must never ship by default — the decayed wire shipping universally is the known '~1 block standing / players barely move' misconfiguration signature); (2) the pre-send fixes the wire at registration, so the victim's same-tick counter-attack x0.6 (which on era 1.7.10 physically reduced the later-joiner's pending tracker wire) only shapes the NEXT knock via the ledger's scaleHorizontal; (3) one stamp per knock is preserved (era never re-sent; Mental's valve consumes the duplicate). Consequence for triage: if the owner is on a default/era preset, none of the era 1.7 weak-wire modes can be shipping; a genuine ~1-block standing flight means the decayed wire (or another regression) is live, NOT era truth — that verdict was reversed once already and is a named trap.

**Trigger:** Context for all trade scenarios; the config-dependent arm triggers only with delivery.melee: tracker-decayed set on the active profile (no shipped preset defaults to it).

**Evidence:** .claude/skills/knockback-profiles/SKILL.md:90-103 (tracker/immediate both full stamp; 'Never ship the decayed wire by default — that artifact survived a release as era truth and read as broken knockback (~1-block standing flights)'); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:20-24 ('A players only move ~1 block report means the decayed wire is shipping — that is a misconfiguration or a bug, NOT era truth'); docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md:203-215 (addendum 2: determinism is the product, no coin-flip replication); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:333 (attacker-side x0.6 -> ledger.scaleHorizontal, next-knock effect).

**Maps to the report:** Frames the whole investigation: relative to real 1.7.10 close trades Mental should feel STRONGER, so any genuinely-weak wire values (as opposed to the client-side/geometry/invuln era-real effects above) point at a Mental-side bug or a tracker-decayed/preset misconfiguration, not at era authenticity.

## Finder: `registration-fallthrough` — Routes where an ATTACK is not handled end-to-end by the fast path

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

Inbound ATTACK (netty thread, HitRegistrationUnit.Listener, core/.../feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java): non-INTERACT_ENTITY/non-ATTACK/null-user/targetId<0 → pass to vanilla. CPS limiter over cap (default 20/s sliding window) → packet CANCELLED, nothing else happens. Victim resolved via frozen entityId→UUID index (SessionService.playerIdByEntityId, written only at join; entity ids are stable across respawn/dimension on CraftBukkit lineage). For player victims: Bukkit.getPlayer==null, view==null, view stale (>4 ticks, PlayerView.fresh), creative, or !pvp → packet PASSES TO VANILLA. Non-player/unindexed: Folia → vanilla; Paper → live scan, damage applied via applyNonPlayer. Then optional reach gate (default OFF) → cancel; AsyncHitRegisterEvent cancel → cancel; fastPath=false → vanilla. Otherwise packet CANCELLED, plan() runs: pre-send only if both views exist, preSendFeedback on, and frozen view not damageImmune (immune ⇒ bare REGISTERED tx, NO burst at all). Velocity suppressed (anticheat gate, LEGACY resistance roll) ⇒ hurt-only burst. Eligible velocity consults FeedbackGate (per-VICTIM wall-clock min interval, auto=(max/2−1)×50=450ms); paced-out ⇒ NO burst at all, tx REGISTERED. Admitted ⇒ tx.planned()+preSent(vector) (PINNED if no PE user), burst shipped via BurstSender (ship Outcome IGNORED), tx handed to victim desk via single-slot submitFromWire. Damage deferred to victim's region thread (applyPlayer): attacker offline/spectator, victim dead/world/gamemode/pvp/>7-block re-check → silent return, NO retract, NO vanilla fallback (only the Folia cross-region branch retracts). Accepted ⇒ victim.damage() with activeInbound slot set.

Region thread: DamageRouter (LOWEST) establishes the tx (or mints Vanilla(ENTITY_ATTACK) with a live-read path for any melee that bypassed the fast path — vanilla fallthroughs are therefore STILL knocked by Mental). KnockbackUnit (MONITOR): PRE_SENT/PINNED ⇒ ADOPT carried vector, arm desk await; REGISTERED/Vanilla ⇒ RECOMPUTE from live ledger (EntityStates.captureVictim: ledger.current(), live positions, live/verdict sprint) and submit+await. DeskRouter is the sole PlayerVelocityEvent writer: resolve ships Mental's vector; PRE_SENT unmodified additionally arms the VelocityValve, whose ValveListener cancels the ONE byte-identical outbound ENTITY_VELOCITY (the tracker duplicate). Sweep never time-drops a connected victim's pending; packetless victims get the ensure net. MirrorListener only rewrites EntityKnockbackEvent for observers. Pure-vanilla KB reaches a player victim only when the session is null or KNOCKBACK is off.

### Findings (10)

#### `presend-accounted-before-ship-valve-eats-knock` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** plan() commits tx.preSent(shipped) BEFORE the burst is shipped and ignores BurstSender.ship()'s Outcome. ship() catches ALL Throwables and returns UNSENDABLE (its javadoc says the caller must then pin, not account wire-delivered) — but the caller only pre-checks the null-user case (victimHasWire), never the runtime failure. On a ship failure the tx stays PRE_SENT: the region pass ADOPTS the carried vector, resolve() returns SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE, and ValveListener then CANCELS the authoritative tracker ENTITY_VELOCITY (exact quantized match). The victim's client receives NEITHER the pre-send NOR the re-emission: damage lands, victim does not move at all — total zero knockback.

**Trigger:** Any PE write failure with a live user: victim mid-(re)configuration (1.20.2+ resource-pack/reconfig window), PE encode exception for a pre-1.19.4 CLIENT behind ViaVersion if PE does not hand the HURT_ANIMATION/BUNDLE wrappers to Via (BurstSender.modernProtocol is keyed to the SERVER version, not the client's), or a disconnect race between the two getUser calls. Intermittent, unpinnable — the exact 'some hits truly just have no knockback' shape.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:404-413 (preSent before ship), 425-429 (senders.ship result discarded; grep shows zero Outcome references in the unit); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/BurstSender.java:63-82 (catch(Throwable)→UNSENDABLE) and 22-23 (contract: 'caller pins the value instead of accounting it wire-delivered'), 42-44+90-92 (modernProtocol = server version); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:186-201 (PRE_SENT adopt → SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/ValveListener.java:40-58 (cancels the matching outbound velocity)

**Maps to the report:** Directly produces 'victim just doesn't really move back' with the hit visibly landing (damage applies). Frequency depends on how often PE writes fail on the owner's stack; the mechanism is unconditional once a write fails.

#### `paced-out-presend-recomputes-off-live-ledger` — divergence-from-era, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The FeedbackGate paces velocity pre-sends per VICTIM on WALL CLOCK (auto = (maxNoDamageTicks/2−1)×50 = 450ms) while the legal hit cadence is 10 server ticks (500ms). When a hit is paced out, plan() ships NO burst at all (shipBurst=false when vector!=null && !velocityShips) and leaves the tx REGISTERED; the KnockbackUnit then RECOMPUTES at EDBEE one-two ticks later from EntityStates.captureVictim(ledger.current()) — the LIVE ledger, which by then has taken 1-2 extra decay steps (×0.546/step grounded) and has same-tick landings applied (grounded re-stamp instead of the declining era vertical), plus live positions instead of the frozen boundary read. The era contract ('pre-send victim state is the published PlayerView, end-of-previous-tick') is broken on exactly this path, so the paced-out hit ships a measurably weaker/flatter stamp than its neighbours.

**Trigger:** Network jitter compressing ATTACK-packet arrival gaps below 450ms at a legal 500ms tick cadence (routine at high CPS / any latency); 2v1 (gate is per-victim, all attackers share the budget); every hit when an anticheat is detected (AnticheatPolicy suppresses all velocity pre-sends → all knocks recompute); frozen-immune-view hits that vanilla's live counter accepts. Intermittent by construction — a 'feeling' level inconsistency.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:398-402 (450ms auto window), 425-429 (paced-out ⇒ no burst), 334-336 (immune view ⇒ bare REGISTERED tx); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/FeedbackGate.java:24-35 (wall-clock per-victim); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:255-271 (REGISTERED ⇒ recompute), core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/EntityStates.java:73-85 (ledger.current() + live location); .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md:272-284 (the boundary contract this path skips); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/coexist/AnticheatPolicy.java:20-27

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' — a jitter-selected subset of otherwise-identical hits ships with extra residual decay and grounded re-stamps, subtly weaker, impossible to pin to a scenario.

#### `stale-position-ring-direction-at-close-range` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** The pre-send computes the knock DIRECTION from PositionRing.latest() for BOTH parties, and the ring is written exactly once per owning-thread tick (end of the session tick), so at registration time both positions are up to one full tick (plus phase) stale. In a face-hug mutual trade both players close at up to ~0.57 blocks/tick combined, so at <1.5-block separation the stale relative offset is a large fraction of — and can invert past — the true separation. The base 0.4 push (away from attacker POSITION) then computes near-zero or oblique, and the authoritative pass ADOPTS the pre-sent vector unchanged (era stamped once, but era read LIVE positions at packet processing). Recomputed (non-pre-sent) hits use live locations instead, adding hit-to-hit variance between the two paths.

**Trigger:** Two players at <1.5 blocks closing on each other (mutual trade), attacker or victim moved meaningfully since the last session tick; every pre-sent hit reads the stale pair. Era-real face-hug weakness (~0.05h when the victim is past the attacker) becomes MORE frequent than on a real era server because the geometry is judged a tick behind.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:451-484 (preAttackerState/preVictimState/positionX/Z from sessions.positions().latest()); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:349-355 ('One owning-thread position sample per tick'); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:119-122 (the era-real trade-opener opposition this amplifies); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:256-267 (adopt — no direction re-check with live positions)

**Maps to the report:** Directly matches 'especially when two players are quite close together and hitting each other' — the base component collapses more often than era truth, reading as non-sprint/no knockback even on sprint hits (the 0.5 yaw extra survives but the 0.4 base cancels or misaligns).

#### `cps-limiter-silently-eats-hits` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** cps.tryAcquire failure CANCELS the ATTACK packet outright: no Mental registration, no vanilla fallthrough, no damage, no knockback — the click simply vanishes (the swing animation is client-side, so the attacker sees a normal swing). The limiter counts every ATTACK packet in a trailing 1s window (default cap 20); which packets are eaten is arrival-order arbitrary relative to the 10-tick legal damage cadence, so at >20 CPS a fraction of the LEGAL boundary hits get eaten pseudo-randomly.

**Trigger:** Butterfly/drag clicking above 20 CPS with the crosshair on the target (routine in close-range 1.8-style trades — every click emits ATTACK at melee range). hit-registration max-cps: 20 default; 0 disables.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:250-254 (cancel+return, nothing scheduled); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/CpsLimiter.java:43-62 (sliding 1s window); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/HitRegSettings.java:36-37 (DEFAULTS maxCps=20)

**Maps to the report:** 'Some hits truly just have no knockback' for high-CPS players — though these hits also deal no damage, which the owner may read as ordinary immunity misses.

#### `legacy18-resistance-roll-zero-knocks` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** KnockbackEngine step 1 under ResistancePolicy.LEGACY is an all-or-nothing roll against the victim's knockback-resistance attribute: a losing roll suppresses the ENTIRE knock (desk resolve → CANCEL_EVENT, the velocity event itself is cancelled, client gets nothing). Netherite armor grants 0.1 knockback resistance per piece on modern servers, so a full-netherite victim silently loses ~40% of ALL knocks. Additionally, any resistance>0 victim has the velocity PRE-SEND suppressed on every hit ('resistance-roll' suppressor — the roll must run once, authoritatively), pushing all their knocks onto the live-ledger recompute path (finding paced-out family).

**Trigger:** knockback profile legacy-1.8 selected (ships armor-resistance: legacy — the ONLY bundled preset that does) + victims wearing any knockback-resistance gear (netherite, relevant armor trims/plugins). Era-authentic mechanic (1.8.9 rolled probabilistically) but NO era item could trigger it — on modern gear it manifests as random total zero-knocks.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/resources/profiles/legacy-1.8.yml:65 (armor-resistance: legacy); core/src/main/resources/profiles/custom.yml:122-125 (comment: 'the 1.7.10 item pool couldn't trigger it'); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:547-555 (suppressorFor 'resistance-roll' whenever resistance>0); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:181-186 (formula null → CANCEL_EVENT 'resistance-roll'); .claude/skills/knockback-profiles/SKILL.md:82-84

**Maps to the report:** If the owner runs legacy-1.8 (or a custom profile with legacy resistance) with netherite kits, this alone reproduces the exact report: random hits with literally no knockback, 'as far back as I can remember', unpinnable.

#### `cancelled-hit-eaten-when-authoritative-declines` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Once register() calls event.setCancelled(true) (line 306), there is NO vanilla fallback. If the pre-send was suppressed (immune view / anticheat / paced-out / resistance) AND applyPlayer then declines, the attack produces nothing at all: (a) attacker null/offline/spectator at the region tick; (b) victim null/dead/cross-world/gamemode/pvp-off/>7.0-block live re-check; (c) any Throwable inside plan()/dispatch() after the cancel (e.g. sessions.sessionFor(victimId) NPE at line 431 on a quit race) is swallowed by the listener catch-all. None of branches (a)/(b) retract the desk pending (only the Folia cross-region branch does), so a PRE_SENT orphan also lingers on the desk — never time-dropped for connected victims (2.4.7 sweep rule) — until superseded, and meanwhile DeskRouter fires a spurious KnockbackApplyEvent on any foreign velocity (pendingFormula() is non-null even unarmed) that then resolves PASS_THROUGH.

**Trigger:** Same-tick victim death mid-trade (era-ish), attacker logout/spectator switch in the 1-tick netty→region gap, plugin-teleport across worlds in that gap, or the quit-race NPE. All rare individually but a close-range trade maximizes same-tick death/interruption coincidences.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:303-309 (cancel before plan/dispatch), 619-649 (applyPlayer silent returns; retract only at 625-632 cross-region), 231-237 (catch-all after cancel), 429-432 (sessionFor(victimId).desk() NPE surface), 758-763 (7.0-block live re-check); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:260-283 (connected pendings never time-dropped), 111-118+172-176 (pendingFormula non-null while unarmed → spurious API event, PASS_THROUGH without clear)

**Maps to the report:** A legal-looking swing that produces neither damage nor movement — contributes rare 'hit did nothing' moments; the orphan-pending side is contract noise rather than felt KB loss.

#### `vanilla-fallthrough-still-mental-knocked-but-degraded` — divergence-from-era, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Every pass-to-vanilla branch for a PLAYER victim with a live session (getPlayer null race, view null, view stale >4 ticks, creative, pvp-off, fastPath=false) does NOT ship vanilla (0.7,0.4) knockback to real clients: vanilla's attack fires EDBEE, DamageRouter mints Vanilla(ENTITY_ATTACK), KnockbackUnit recomputes the era vector and DeskRouter overwrites the PlayerVelocityEvent. What IS lost on these hits: the arrival-order SprintWire verdict (live attacker.isSprinting() is read instead — fine for flag truth, but freshSprint is hardcoded false for Vanilla sources, so wtap-extra pricing never applies: a no-op on all bundled presets where wtap-extra is disabled/equal, config-dependent otherwise), the boundary-frozen ledger read (live-ledger recompute — the paced-out finding's divergence), the pre-send, AND vanilla's own 1.9+ cooldown-scaled damage/sweep semantics apply instead of the fast path's era DamageShaper. The one branch that yields PURE vanilla knockback is session==null (KnockbackUnit returns at line 163-165) — rare post-2.4.4. The realistic intermittent trigger for stale views is the documented respawn/chunk-reload transient-invalidity window where the session tick retires and re-arms for several ticks without publishing (arena PvP re-engage).

**Trigger:** Hits landed on a player within the several-tick respawn/chunk-reload window (view older than 4 ticks → fresh() false → fallthrough), or on Folia under region lag/counter skew; plus any server with hit-registration fast-path: false (all melee takes this route permanently).

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:260-286 (fallthrough branches), 303-305 (fastPath=false); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/model/PlayerView.java:142-144 (4-tick freshness); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:253-296 (retire/re-arm across respawn, 'several ticks'); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/DamageRouter.java:53-68 (mint Vanilla); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:163-165 (session null → pure vanilla), 273-274 (freshSprint false for Vanilla source), 365-371 (live sprint read); core/src/main/resources/profiles/legacy-1.7.yml:23-26 (wtap-extra disabled by default)

**Maps to the report:** Weak-FEELING hits right after respawns and under lag: damage is cooldown-scaled by vanilla (tiny on spam) even though KB magnitude stays Mental's — reads as 'that hit did nothing'. Important negative result: the classic 'fallthrough = vanilla 0.7 sprint KB' leak does NOT exist for sessioned player victims.

#### `wire-slot-overwrite-and-arm-steal-races` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** DeliveryDesk.submitFromWire is a single AtomicReference slot with silent overwrite. (a) Two pre-sent hits on one victim before an owning-thread drain (two attackers in one tick): the first tx vanishes unjournaled; the first hit's EDBEE-adopt then calls awaitVelocityEvent, whose drainWire installs the SECOND tx as pending and arms IT — the tick's single velocity event ships the second attacker's vector even if the second's damage was immunity-rejected (its pre-send already moved the client anyway). (b) A wire submission draining inside DeskRouter's resolve path between an armed pending and its velocity event supersedes the armed decision (replacePending clears `awaiting`), so the in-flight resolve returns PASS_THROUGH and VANILLA's velocity (airborne = kept falling-y, i.e. downward/weak) ships for that hit. Both require a second pre-send inside a ~one-tick window, which the default 450ms FeedbackGate normally forbids — reachable with feedback-min-interval-ms lowered/0, with multi-attacker timing under lag, or when the server stalls ≥ the gate window.

**Trigger:** 2v1 same-tick pre-sends on one victim; or 1v1 with feedback-min-interval-ms: 0/small (or severe tick lag) letting consecutive pre-sends land within one tick.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:37+51-53 (single slot, set() overwrite), 305-328 (drainWire/replacePending; awaiting=false on replace), 172-176 (!awaiting → PASS_THROUGH); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:264-266 (adopt arms whatever drainWire installed); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:398-402 (the default gate that normally masks it)

**Maps to the report:** Under multi-attacker close-range scraps (arena cleanups) an occasional hit resolves to vanilla's weak/downward vector or ships the wrong attacker's stamp — sporadic weak knocks that never reproduce in 1v1 testing.

#### `face-hug-base-opposition` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The era base 0.4 pushes away from the ATTACKER'S POSITION while the sprint extra 0.5 rides the attacker's YAW; a victim at/past the attacker's position receives a near-cancelled horizontal (~0.05h measured on real 1.7.10). Mental reproduces this faithfully; in sustained face-hug trades a meaningful fraction of hits legitimately barely move the victim, and the received-KB reduction from the attacker-side ×0.6 self-multiplier at high CPS (0.6^clicks, client-side contract) stacks on top.

**Trigger:** Both players inside ~0.5-1.0 blocks, victim overlapping or past the attacker — precisely the reported 'quite close together and hitting each other' scenario. Authentic on real era servers; the stale-ring finding makes Mental hit this regime somewhat MORE often than era, but the core weakness is genuine.

**Evidence:** .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:119-122 ('trade-opener opposition... ~0.05 h — era-real, identical on actual 1.7.10') and 60-63 (0.6^clicks self-multiplier); docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md (wire-measured basis per the skill); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:161-227 (base −direction×push vs yaw-aligned extras)

**Maps to the report:** The owner needs to know a large slice of 'close-range hits feel like no knockback' is authentic 1.7/1.8 behavior — misreading it as a bug would push toward the anti-feature fixes the community history rejects.

#### `legacy-tier-registration-clean` — unknown, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** No registration-side degradation specific to legacy SERVERS (<1.17) or legacy CLIENTS was found in the assigned pathway: PacketTap compares Play.Client constants by reference (pre-Play traffic safe), ENTITY_ACTION START/STOP and INTERACT_ENTITY ATTACK exist across the whole client range, the latency probe rides window-confirmation transactions below 1.17 feeding the same compensationY, and BurstSender degrades to bare velocity + entity-status-2 below 1.19.4 (both universally supported). The one legacy-shaped risk is OUTBOUND: BurstSender selects HURT_ANIMATION/BUNDLE wrappers by SERVER version, so a pre-1.19.4 client behind ViaVersion on a modern server depends entirely on the PE↔Via hand-off translating/dropping those packets; if PE encodes at the client version instead, the write throws and feeds the presend-accounted-before-ship bug for EVERY hit on that client.

**Trigger:** Old-version clients (1.8.x-1.19.3) via ViaVersion on a 1.19.4+ server, bundle-feedback: true (default). Modern-client-only servers and pre-1.19.4 servers are unaffected.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/PacketTap.java:52-68 (reference compares, catch-all observe-only); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/BurstSender.java:39-49 (server-version flag), 84-94 (wrapper selection); .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md:202-222 (legacy transport: 'the rest of the fast path is version-graceful')

**Maps to the report:** If any regulars play on old client versions via Via, their received knockback could be systematically eaten (see the valve finding); otherwise no legacy-specific contribution.

## Finder: `servo-modifiers` — Post-engine modifiers — pocket servo / dynamic chase / pace scaling

### Pathway map (how it actually works, as read)

The post-engine modifiers are all folded INSIDE KnockbackEngine.computePaced — nothing scales the vector after the engine returns. Order: (1) PaceScale factor s from the attacker's walk-normalized MOVEMENT_SPEED attribute (sprint x1.3 divided back out at capture; attribute only, never measured velocity; clamp [0.5,2.0]; active only on the signature preset, exponent 0.95). (2) Pocket-servo factor sigma, active only when the COMBO_HOLD module (default OFF) is enabled AND the frozen victim PlayerView's comboAttackerId equals this hit's attacker (a ComboTracker chain of >=2 hits, gap<=20t, victim not retaliated/grounded-run/blown-out). sigma = clamp(0.93, 1.35, 1 + gain*(sigma*-1)) where sigma* is an exact inverse solve landing the victim at the answer-denial boundary target (~2.7-3.15; static 2.85; targetFloor 2.5, folded lower by the reach handicap when that module is also on). Both s and sigma multiply ONLY the fresh horizontal (base push + sprint/wtap/enchant extras); the ledger residual and the vertical are never scaled. At 1.0 the multiplies are skipped (byte-identity). The solve prices: a drag schedule over the measured cadence window (per-combo EMA, config 10t fallback), victim drift (ring-estimated), ping horizons, and a chase = dynamic ramp (attacker ResetModel sprinting+not-blocking) OR measured post-hit window EMA OR 0.2806*attr model, with a floor of alignment*0.70*sprint. Alignment = the attacker's 5-sample (4-tick) ring-heading dot with the knock axis, clamped [cos45,1]; net movement <0.05 blocks reads NaN -> 1.0 (fully aligned), so a stationary attacker biases sigma UP; a just-counter-knocked trade attacker reads misaligned -> cos45 floor -> sigma pins the 0.93 min more often. Compute sites: D1 netty pre-send (HitRegistrationUnit.plan; frozen views + PositionRing latest + LatencyModel; skipped when victimView.damageImmune) and D2 region EDBEE (KnockbackUnit; live captures for positions/sprint, same frozen combo gate). A PRE_SENT/PINNED hit is adopted at D2 without recompute, so exactly one seam solves each hit; ComboPredictor.MEMORY (per-victim chase/cadence EMA + attacker anchor, ConcurrentHashMap) is committed by whichever seam solved, double-commits filtered by a 5-tick minimum window gap, and cleared on every combo END. Sanity: parse(empty)==LEGACY_17 carries PaceScaling.OFF; RangeReduction (the only distance-keyed knob) is DISABLED in all ten presets and shaves only BEYOND 3.0 blocks anyway. At shipped defaults this entire pathway is a byte-identical no-op; enabled, its worst-case shave is 1-minFactor = 7% of the fresh component (was 20% and effectively always-on in 2.4.2-2.4.5 — the fixed undershoot bug).

### Findings (7)

#### `servo-by-design-fresh-shave` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** When the COMBO_HOLD module is on and the frozen victim view says THIS attacker holds the victim's active combo (comboServoFor, KnockbackUnit.java:620-630 / HitRegistrationUnit.java:182-192), KnockbackEngine.computePaced multiplies the FRESH horizontal (base push + sprint/wtap/enchant extras; never the residual, never the vertical) by sigma = clamp(minFactor, maxFactor, PocketServo.solve) — defaults [0.93, 1.35] (ComboSettings.DEFAULTS, ComboSettings.java:59-64). The solve inverts the era flight equations to land the victim at the answer-denial boundary target (~2.7-3.15, static fallback 2.85); sigma* drops ~0.11 per 0.1 of axis residual at sprint fresh 0.9 (2026-07-07 doc: 'residual carry has enormous leverage'), so residual-carrying mid-combo hits (hit 3+ of a chain; the tracker needs minHits=2 before the view publishes an attacker) routinely pin the 0.93 min clamp. Max shave at defaults = 7% of the fresh component; an operator-lowered min-factor deepens it arbitrarily. Note the geometry sign: a CLOSER victim (small d0) solves a HIGHER sigma (they must travel further to the target), so close-range servo hits bias toward the 1.35 max, not the min — the shave concentrates on hits whose natural carry overshoots the pocket, i.e. exactly full sprint stamps mid-combo.

**Trigger:** COMBO_HOLD enabled (default OFF, Feature.java:282-290 carries defaultEnabled=false); attacker lands hits 3+ of a <=20-tick-gap chain on a non-retaliating victim; the victim carries ledger residual (combos:true presets like legacy-1.7 make this common; velt/signature friction 0.1 wipes residual so sigma stays nearer 1.0). Any preset — the servo is a module, not a profile knob.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:206-230 (combo factor folded into freshFactor, extras scaled at :221-222); kernel/.../math/PocketServo.java:339-342 (sigma* inversion + clamp); core/.../config/settings/ComboSettings.java:59-64 (min 0.93 / max 1.35 / staticTarget 2.85 / windowTicks 10); core/.../feature/Feature.java:282-290 (default off); docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md (post-fix sigma* band 0.85-1.35, centre ~1.1).

**Maps to the report:** Directly matches 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' — but ONLY on servers with combo-hold enabled, only on hit 3+ of a held combo, and bounded to a 7% fresh-component shave at shipped defaults, which cannot reduce a sprint stamp (0.9) to non-sprint scale (0.4). It is the servo's stated purpose (hold the ~2.85 pocket), deliberately clamped so era physics wins past the honesty band. With defaults (module off) this pathway is a byte-identical no-op and cannot explain the report.

#### `servo-historical-undershoot-2.4.2-2.4.5` — bug, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Before the 2.4.6 chase-alignment floor, the servo's measured chase channel under-priced the attacker's close: the pre-2.4.5 pre-hit ring-velocity trend read the attacker's at-ring idle/w-tap phase ('~0 to negative in every lab cell'), and the 2.4.5 post-hit window averaged net displacement over the whole inter-hit gap (~0.11 b/t, 41% of sprint). Under-priced chase inflates the predicted settle, so sigma* solved 0.36-0.86 and pinned the then-min clamp 0.8 on essentially every landed mid-combo hit — 'shipping every landed hit below era' (ComboPredictor javadoc). Fixed in the current tree by CHASE_ALIGNMENT=0.70 floor + [0.93,1.35] recalibration (PocketServo.java:519-541); the bug no longer exists as written, but any 2.4.2-2.4.5 playtest with combo-hold on systematically shipped ~20%-weak fresh sprint knocks during combos.

**Trigger:** Historical: versions 2.4.2-beta through 2.4.5-beta with COMBO_HOLD enabled, any sustained combo (the measured chase channel activates from the combo's second window). Not reproducible on the current tree.

**Evidence:** docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md:26-42 (root cause: measured window under-reads, sigma* 0.36-0.86 false-low min-clamp mode); core/.../feature/combo/ComboPredictor.java:134-142 (javadoc: 'driving sigma* into the false-low min-clamp mode and shipping every landed hit below era'); kernel/.../math/PocketServo.java:81-93 + :519-541 (the 2.4.6 floor that fixed it).

**Maps to the report:** The owner says the weakness goes back 'as far back as I can remember'; if their memory includes 2.4.2-2.4.5 sessions with combo-hold on, this acknowledged-and-fixed defect is a genuine past source of 'sprint hits with less knockback than they should' during combos. It cannot explain weakness observed on the current build or on servo-off configs, and combo-hold shipped only in 2.4.2 — reports older than that need a different pathway.

#### `stationary-nan-alignment-refuted-trade-clamp-real` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** Two-part answer to the alignment question. (a) STATIONARY attacker: ComboPredictor.attackerHeadingAlignment reads the attacker's net displacement over 5 per-tick ring samples (4 tick deltas, one sample/tick guaranteed by SessionService:349-354 recording every tick regardless of movement); net < MIN_HEADING_BLOCKS=0.05 returns NaN (PocketServo.headingAlignment:736-742), and chaseAlignmentFactor(NaN)=1.0 (PocketServo.java:755-760) — the FULLY-ALIGNED model. A stationary face-hug attacker therefore has their chase OVER-priced (full 0.70x sprint floor), which biases sigma* UP toward the 1.35 max — stronger, not weaker, knock. The hypothesized ~30% stationary shave does not exist. (b) MUTUAL TRADE: an attacker who was just counter-knocked has a ring heading dominated by their own received knock (0.4-0.9 b/t easily clears the 0.05 gate) pointing off-axis or backward; headingAlignment reads <=0 and clamps to cos45=0.7071 (deliberately floored there — the comment names 'the attacker's own received knock' as the case the clamp bounds), scaling the model chase channels and the chase floor by 0.7071. Under-priced chase lowers sigma*, so trade hits pin the 0.93 min clamp more often — still bounded to the 7% fresh shave.

**Trigger:** COMBO_HOLD on; mutual close-range trade where the servo-holding attacker was knocked within the last ~4 ticks (their heading reads misaligned). The pure-stationary case triggers nothing weak.

**Evidence:** kernel/.../math/PocketServo.java:107-115 (MIN_CHASE_ALIGNMENT=cos45, MIN_HEADING_BLOCKS=0.05), :491 + :535-541 (alignment scales model channels and the floor), :736-760 (NaN->1.0; measured dot clamps [cos45,1]); core/.../feature/combo/ComboPredictor.java:59-66 + :311-321 (5-sample heading read); core/.../session/SessionService.java:349-354 (one ring sample per tick, always).

**Maps to the report:** Partially maps onto 'close-range trades feel weak' on servo-enabled configs: trade hits are the hits most likely to ride the 0.93 min clamp. But the effect is capped at 7% at defaults and requires an active held combo — which a mutual trade keeps ending (every hit the victim lands fires onOwnHitLanded -> RETALIATION end, ComboTracker.java:162-167, via KnockbackUnit.applyAttackerObligations:415-417), so the servo is mostly INACTIVE during genuine trades. The stationary-NaN weak-hit hypothesis is refuted.

#### `pace-scaling-attribute-only-signature-only` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** PaceScale reads ONLY the attacker's walk-stance-normalized MOVEMENT_SPEED attribute — KnockbackEngine.java:199 passes attacker.moveSpeedAttr(); capture is Attributes.movementSpeedWalkNormalized (Attributes.java:103-110), a same-thread pair-read of isSprinting()+effective attribute that divides the 1.3 sprint modifier back out. No measured velocity feeds it anywhere (verified all callers: engine lines 199/282; pre-send uses the view's attr, HitRegistrationUnit.java:459-463). Blockhitting, sneaking, and soul sand are input/block-side slowdowns that never touch the attribute, so none of them can shave the knock. Slowness DOES (attribute modifier): Slowness II -> 0.07/0.10 -> 0.7^0.95 ~ 0.71x fresh on signature — the intended speed-conformal behavior, clamped [0.5, 2.0]. Only the signature preset opts in (Presets.java:240-253, PaceScaling(ATTACKER, 0.95, 0.5, 2.0)); every other preset and parse(empty) carries PaceScaling.OFF (KnockbackProfile 17-arg ctor default, KnockbackProfile.java:42-69), and at factor exactly 1.0 the engine skips the multiply (byte-identity, KnockbackEngine.java:221, :489). The deprecated stance-baseline 3-arg factor (the old F1 ~23% weak-knock desync) has NO production caller — grep shows only the 2-arg form at both engine sites.

**Trigger:** signature preset selected AND the attacker under a genuine speed-attribute debuff (Slowness potion, attribute-modifying gear). Base-speed play, blockhitting, sneaking, soul sand: factor stays ~1.0 (ratio float slack ~1.5e-8, below the 1.25e-4 wire quantum — packets byte-identical).

**Evidence:** kernel/.../math/KnockbackEngine.java:199, :221-222, :282, :489-492; kernel/.../math/PaceScale.java:54-62 (2-arg attr-only form; sentinel -> exactly 1.0), :77-86 (deprecated stance form, pins only); platform/.../Attributes.java:81-110 (walk normalization, coherent pair-read); core/.../EntityStates.java:62-64; kernel/.../profile/Presets.java:240-253 (signature-only opt-in); kernel/.../profile/PaceScaling.java:38 (OFF = parse-empty default).

**Maps to the report:** Does NOT explain the report: a blockhitting or w-tapping attacker's pace factor is unaffected (blocking is not an attribute change, and walk-normalization makes the factor stance-agnostic). Only a Slowness-debuffed attacker on signature ships proportionally weaker knocks — intended and clearly bounded. No close-range or trade-specific pace path exists.

#### `no-close-range-distance-reducer` — config-dependent, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The only distance-keyed knock modifier in the engine is the RangeReduction taper (KnockbackProfile.java:107-125): it returns 0.0 for distance <= startDistance (3.0) and only shaves hits BEYOND it — point-blank hits are structurally untouched — and it is RangeReduction.DISABLED in every bundled preset including mmc (Presets.java, all constructors). The servo is distance-aware but, per its inversion sign, a SMALLER d0 solves a LARGER sigma (the victim needs more travel to reach the ~2.85 target), so close range biases the servo toward its 1.35 max, not the min. ComboReachHandicap never touches knockback vectors — it modifies the juggled VICTIM's entity-interaction-range attribute (their answer reach, 1.20.5+ only); its one knock-relevant interplay is the servo fold: victimReach x scale (0.87 -> 2.61) lowers sepDeny, lowering the boundary target toward targetFloor 2.5 (PocketServo.boundaryTarget:637-646), which lowers sigma* slightly for hits that would overshoot — bounded by the same 0.93 clamp (KnockbackUnit.effectiveVictimReach:643-651; HitRegistrationUnit:204-212).

**Trigger:** The handicap-target fold needs COMBO_HOLD + COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP both enabled on 1.20.5+; the taper needs an operator hand-editing range-reduction.enabled into a profile (no bundled preset ships it).

**Evidence:** kernel/.../profile/KnockbackProfile.java:113-125 (reductionAt returns 0 at close range), :116 (DISABLED); kernel/.../profile/Presets.java (RangeReduction.DISABLED in all ten presets); kernel/.../math/PocketServo.java:582-646 (sepDeny/boundaryTarget geometry, targetFloor 2.5); core/.../feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:643-651.

**Maps to the report:** Refutes the 'distance-keyed reducer at close range' hypothesis for this pathway: nothing here reduces knock BECAUSE the players are close. The face-hug ~0.05h weak trade-opener the owner may be feeling is the era-real position-vs-yaw opposition (base 0.4 away from attacker POSITION vs sprint 0.5 along attacker YAW, era-accuracy skill) — outside this pathway but the closest era-real match to 'close-together hits barely move the victim'.

#### `combo-gate-frozen-view-staleness` — config-dependent, confidence medium

**Mechanism:** Both seams gate the servo on the FROZEN view's comboAttackerId (published at session-tick start, after driveCombo — SessionService.java:332-335). The tracker mutates mid-tick: a retaliation (victim lands their own melee) resets the chain at EDBEE time (KnockbackUnit.applyAttackerObligations:415-417 -> ComboTracker.onOwnHitLanded), but the view still carries the old combo until the next publish. A netty pre-send in that <=1-tick window still solves and applies sigma for a combo the design contract says has ended (and symmetrically, a freshly-started combo is un-shaved for its first post-activation tick). The staleness is documented as intentional ('one frozen truth' so pre-send and recompute agree), and the effect is bounded by the [0.93, 1.35] clamps for at most one tick per transition. ComboPredictor.MEMORY hygiene is correct: forget() fires on every combo END via ComboEvents.fire (ComboEvents.java:62-70), and attacker switches produce a balanced END-then-START (ComboTracker.onKnockShipped:110-153), so no cross-attacker chase/cadence leakage.

**Trigger:** COMBO_HOLD on; high-CPS mutual trade where combo transitions (retaliation ends, restarts) happen every few ticks — each transition gives up to one tick of mis-gated sigma application in either direction.

**Evidence:** core/.../feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:620-630 + core/.../feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:182-192 (frozen-view gate, both seams); core/.../session/SessionService.java:332-335 (view publishes combo state once per tick); kernel/.../combo/ComboTracker.java:162-167 (mid-tick retaliation reset); core/.../feature/combo/ComboEvents.java:62-70 (memory forget on END).

**Maps to the report:** A weak (0.93x fresh) hit can land one tick AFTER the victim retaliated — subtly wrong per the design's own gate contract, and it lands precisely in mutual trades, matching the report's texture ('hard to pin, a feeling thing'). But magnitude is capped at 7% of the fresh component and requires combo-hold on; not the primary cause.

#### `pathway-noop-at-defaults` — era-real, confidence high

**Mechanism:** The entire assigned pathway is verified byte-identical no-op at shipped defaults: COMBO_HOLD and COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP Features default false (Feature.java:282-304, 'every ported rule defaults OFF'); with the module off comboServoFor returns PocketServoConfig.INACTIVE and computePaced's servo branch short-circuits to combo=1.0 before any predictor work (KnockbackEngine.java:206-210); PaceScaling.OFF is the parse-empty default and every preset except signature carries it, with the engine skipping the multiply entirely at factor 1.0 (freshFactor != 1.0 guards, KnockbackEngine.java:221, :489); RangeReduction.DISABLED in all presets returns 0.0 always. parse(empty)==LEGACY_17 holds through this pathway (17-arg constructor defaults paceScaling to OFF, KnockbackProfile.java:42-69). Threads: the servo/pace compute runs on the netty thread at pre-send (HitRegistrationUnit.plan, frozen views + ring + latency only) and on the victim's region thread at the EDBEE recompute (KnockbackUnit, live captures for positions/sprint); a PRE_SENT/PINNED hit is ADOPTED at the region seam without recompute (KnockbackUnit.java:256-267), so exactly one seam solves each hit and ComboPredictor.rememberWindow's dual-commit is serialized by the MIN_WINDOW_GAP_TICKS=5 artifact guard.

**Trigger:** Default configuration / era presets (legacy-1.7, legacy-1.8, kohi, etc.) with the COMBO family off — the owner's baseline unless they enabled the Combo Solver in the GUI.

**Evidence:** core/.../feature/Feature.java:282-304; kernel/.../math/KnockbackEngine.java:121-130, :206-230, :489-492; kernel/.../profile/KnockbackProfile.java:42-69, :116, :128-153; kernel/.../profile/PaceScaling.java:38; core/.../feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:256-267; core/.../feature/combo/ComboPredictor.java:69-83 (MIN/MAX window gap guards).

**Maps to the report:** Load-bearing negative result for the synthesizer: if the owner's report reproduces with COMBO_HOLD off and a non-signature preset, the weak/no-KB close-range hits CANNOT originate in the post-engine modifier pathway — the cause must sit in registration/sprint-verdict, delivery/valve, ledger residual, or the era-real face-hug opposition (base pushes from attacker POSITION; a victim past/inside the attacker gets ~0.05 horizontal — identical on real 1.7.10).

---

# Round-1 verification verdicts (Opus adversarial lenses)

Each merged finding was attacked by two independent Opus verifiers: a CODE lens
(default stance: the finding is wrong — hunt for missed guards/threads/tests) and a
SYMPTOM lens (assume the mechanism; hand-compute whether it produces the reported feel).
Four lens runs died on a structured-output retry cap (marked MISSING — re-verification
dispatched); seven low-relevance merged findings were capped out of verification (listed at the end).

## `same-tick-wtap-start-retro-clear` — merged as bug, sources: sprint-wire, desk-obligations

**Mechanism:** SprintWire.onServerClear(asOf) survives a re-engage only when lastWrite is STRICTLY newer than the hit's verdict stamp (SprintWire.java:100-110). TickStamp granularity is one server tick, so a genuine w-tap/re-engage START arriving in the SAME tick as the ATTACK (after it in arrival order) has lastWrite==asOf and is retroactively destroyed by the deferred EDBEE clear 1-2 ticks later: wire sprinting=false, armed=false; the deferred setSprinting(false) then consults the already-poisoned wire (KnockbackUnit.java:432-447) and clears the vanilla server flag too, so the reconcile (PacketTap.java:85) can never restore it — both sides read Mental's own false. The client believes it re-engaged and sends no further START; every subsequent hit ships verdict.sprinting=false = plain 0.4 knockback until the next genuine full STOP/START pair. The javadoc waves the same-tick case away as 'physically implausible', but at 12-16 CPS a re-press 0-50ms after the click routinely lands in the click's tick, and for hold-sprint clients <=1.21.1 EVERY hit is followed by an auto STOP+START that rolls this dice; network jitter bunching two client flushes into one server tick triggers it too. Violates the code's own contracts (WtapRegistrationUnit.java:13-16 'a w-tap registers however fast the tap'; netty-fast-path arrival-order rule — vanilla's synchronous in-attack clear could never eat a later-arriving START). Companion opposite-direction race from the same deferred clear: verdictAt is a pure peek, so two ACCEPTED hits (necessarily on two different victims) inside the 1-2-tick pre-clear window BOTH read sprint=true and both ship the bonus where era would ship the second plain (SprintWire.java:192-198, HitRegistrationUnit.java:523-535) — extra KB, not weak; reported so it is not misattributed.

**Trigger:** Attacker's ATTACK and re-engage START land in one server tick: fast w-tap with re-press trailing the click by <50ms, hold-sprint clients <=1.21.1 whose auto STOP+START bunches into the attack's tick, or any jitter delivering two client-tick flushes in one server tick. Once eaten, all hits ship plain for the rest of the engagement. High-CPS close trades maximize both roll count and visibility.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/SprintWire.java:100-110 (strict-> guard; :98 'accepted residual' admission; :76 onSprintStart stamps clock.current()); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:266/344 (deferred EDBEE clear with asOf=tx.context().sprint().at()), :404-448 (deferred setSprinting(false) skip-guard reads the poisoned wire); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:523-535 (verdict stamped at registration, non-consuming); SprintWireTest.java:137-149 pins asOf==lastWrite => clears; docs/superpowers/plans/2026-07-04-combat-241-fix-round.md:122-123 (the implausibility assumption); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:257-263 (client sends STOP in the attack flush, re-engage is a client entity-action; vanilla clear was synchronous inside attack()); WtapRegistrationUnit.java:13-16 (violated contract).

**Maps to the report:** Exactly 'even if one is w-tapping ... it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback' and 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should': intermittent (jitter/timing dependent), persistent once triggered, worst in close high-CPS trades — 'subtle and hard to reproduce, more like a feeling'.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Cannot refute. Every load-bearing claim checks out against the code and tests. (1) The strict `>` guard at SprintWire.java:103 leaves the equal case (lastWrite==asOf) unprotected — pinned explicitly by SprintWireTest.guardedServerClearAtOrBeforeTheStampClears (:138-149). (2) asOf is the ATTACK's registration tick: HitRegistrationUnit.sprintVerdict calls verdictAt(clock.current()), which stamps at=now; a same-tick re-engage START stamps lastWrite=clock.current()=T, so lastWrite==asOf and is cleared. (3) The poison chain is real: onServerClear sets sprinting/armed=false; the deferred setSprinting(false) (KnockbackUnit.java:442-446) reads the now-false wire, so its skip-guard does not fire and it clears the server flag too; reconcile then sees server==wire==false and cannot restore; clientSprinting survives but is inert in verdictAt for a non-block w-tap (line 194 gates it behind blockReset). (4) Genuine divergence from era: compendium §5 (:257-264) establishes the STOP is same-flush/same-tick with the ATTACK and the re-engage is a later client action; vanilla cleared sprint synchronously inside attack() and could never eat a later-arriving START, whereas Mental's clear runs 1-2 ticks late at the deferred EDBEE and does. The javadoc and plan doc both concede the same-tick case and defend it only as 'physically implausible input' — which is exactly the disputed assumption. (5) Not disabled: wtapConsultWire defaults true and WTAP_REGISTRATION is default-on, so the wire path is live in real PvP. Both the PRE_SENT/PINNED fast path (KnockbackUnit:266) and the region path (:344) reach applyAttackerObligations with asOf=verdict.at, so both paths are exposed. Refinements: the finding's 'persistent for the rest of the engagement' is overstated — a real w-tapper emits a fresh STOP+START per hit, so the defect re-rolls per hit and any clean (non-same-tick) re-engage restores the bonus; it is intermittent, not latched. The 'especially close together' emphasis is not a direct trigger of THIS mechanism (trigger is packet timing/jitter, distance-independent); the link is indirect (close range -> higher CPS -> more packets bunched per server tick -> higher same-tick collision probability, and the lost separation is more visible up close). The companion two-victim peek race is real but secondary (extra-KB, needs two targets within 1-2 ticks; rare in 1v1).
- Corrections: Mechanism, guard, poison chain, and era-divergence all confirmed. Two overstatements to correct: (a) 'persistent once triggered / until the next genuine full STOP/START pair' — for an actual w-tapper each hit already generates its own STOP+START, so the defect re-rolls per hit and self-heals whenever a re-engage START lands in a tick other than the ATTACK's; it is per-hit intermittent, not a latched stuck state (the hold-sprint-client case merely re-rolls the same dice every attack). (b) The 'especially when close together' correlation is not a direct causal trigger of this specific mechanism — the trigger is purely whether the re-engage START flushes into the ATTACK's own server tick (jitter/phase/bunching dependent, distance-independent). Proximity correlates only via higher CPS packing more packets into each server tick and via close-range making the missing knockback push more visible. The vulnerable window is exactly the single server tick T of the ATTACK (a START at T+1 is protected by lastWrite>asOf), so the trigger requires the re-engage START to bunch into tick T, which normally needs jitter/favorable phase alignment given client sprint packets are ~50ms (one tick) apart.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss when triggered: full sprint bonus dropped — the accepted hit ships plain 0.4-style knockback instead of sprint knockback (the extra ~0.4 horizontal push is lost), i.e. the victim visibly barely steps back exactly as the report describes ('non-sprinting knockback' on a w-tap/sprint hit). Frequency: a minority of close high-CPS sprint/w-tap hits — the re-engage START must land in the ATTACK's own server tick, which typically needs network jitter or favorable client/server tick phase alignment (client sprint packets are ~one tick apart, so the START usually falls in T+1 and is protected). On smooth connections rare; on jittery/high-ping connections and in dense high-CPS close trades non-trivially frequent, per hit re-rolled. Matches the owner's 'subtle, hard to reproduce, more like a feeling' precisely. Companion extra-KB two-victim race: real but rare (needs two accepted hits on two victims within the 1-2-tick pre-clear window), negligible in 1v1.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: The finding's code claims all check out against the main tree. TickStamp is a single int server-tick index (kernel/model/TickStamp.java:10), so 50ms granularity — any two events read in one server tick collide at equal .value(). onServerClear's guard (SprintWire.java:103) is a strict `>`; the attack's verdict stamp asOf (= tx.context().sprint().at(), stamped clock.current() at registration, HitRegistrationUnit.java:530-534) and a re-engage START stamped in the SAME tick (onSprintStart → clock.current(), SprintWire.java:75) satisfy lastWrite == asOf, so the strict-> guard does NOT no-op and the deferred EDBEE clear (1-2 ticks later) retro-destroys the re-engage: sprinting=false, armed=false. The deferred setSprinting(false) then reads the poisoned wire (KnockbackUnit.java:442-447), fails its skip-guard, and clears the vanilla server flag too; reconcile reads view.sprinting() (PacketTap.java:85) = that same false flag, so there is no true signal left to restore from. The guard's own javadoc dismisses the same-tick case as "physically implausible input" — the finding correctly contests exactly this: at 12-16 CPS against a 50ms tick, a re-engage landing in the click's tick is routine, not implausible.

This IS a divergence from era: the era server cleared sprint synchronously INSIDE attack(), so it could never eat a re-engage that arrived afterwards; Mental's clear runs deferred and, on tick-granular stamps, eats a same-tick-later START. So it's a genuine implementation defect that produces non-era (weak) knockback.

Magnitude: on SIGNATURE (default, Presets.java:225-234) the sprint bonus is 0.5 horizontal (sprintFactor 1.0 x extra.horizontal 0.5), vertical 0.0. Head-on, sprint ships ~0.825 horizontal, plain ships ~0.325 — losing the bonus is a ~60% horizontal cut. The wire-measured compendium table puts plain settle at 1.994 blocks and a sprint hit at ~4.948 blocks, so the victim travels ~2 blocks instead of ~5. This is exactly the reported "the victim just doesn't really move back" / "it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback" — the report's own words name the non-sprint outcome, and losing the sprint bonus produces precisely that shipped velocity.

Frequency: fires whenever a re-engage START bunches into the attack's server tick — either a manual w-tap re-press <50ms after the click (common at 12-16 CPS, click interval 62-83ms) or jitter bunching two consecutive client flushes (the attack+STOP flush and the very next re-engage flush — the pair most likely to bunch) into one server-tick read (endemic on any residential connection). With per-hit re-engage STARTs (which vanilla hold-sprint and w-tap both generate — vanilla needs them or hold-sprint combos would only sprint-KB on the first hit), the effect is a self-correcting SINGLE plain hit per bunching event: the next non-bunched hit re-arms and restores the bonus. That transient form — sporadic weak hits sprinkled through fast combos — matches "subtle and hard to reproduce, more like a feeling thing" better than a hard lock would. The finding's stronger permanence claim (all subsequent hits plain until a genuine STOP/START) additionally holds for any client that re-engages sprint only ONCE per session and never re-sends START — because the poisoned server flag defeats reconcile there is then no path back to true; how often that applies is version/technique-dependent and is the finding's weakest link, but even without it the transient form reproduces the symptom. Close-range emphasis is well-explained indirectly: closer trades run higher effective CPS and heavier STOP/START churn (more dice rolls per second) and a failed knock at point-blank fails to create space and is far more salient than at range. The w-tap half of "even if one is w-tapping or blockhitting" is the finding's exact trigger; the blockhit half is partly protected by the sticky blockReset (survives onServerClear) so is only weakly explained by this finding.
- Corrections: The finding is sound; two refinements. (1) Its permanence claim ("every subsequent hit ships false until the next genuine STOP/START") is only guaranteed when the client re-engages sprint just once per session; with the per-hit re-engage STARTs that vanilla w-tap and hold-sprint both actually generate, the dominant real-world form is a self-correcting SINGLE plain hit per bunching event (the next non-bunched hit re-arms), which still fully reproduces the reported symptom and arguably matches "subtle/feeling" even better. (2) The "even if one is w-tapping or blockhitting" report line: this finding is the exact w-tap mechanism, but the blockhit half is largely covered by the sticky blockReset contract (blockReset survives onServerClear, SprintWire.java:194) — so blockhit weak-KB is only weakly attributable here and may point at a separate path. Magnitude and the strict-> / tick-granular root cause are confirmed exactly as stated.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss per fired hit: the entire sprint bonus — shipped horizontal drops ~0.825 to ~0.325 on the default SIGNATURE preset (~60% cut; 0.5 velocity units), settle distance ~4.95 blocks to ~1.99 blocks (compendium wire table). This is the maximum KB loss short of a whole miss and is literally the "non-sprinting knockback" the user names. Frequency: fires on any sprint hit whose re-engage START lands in the attack's 50ms server tick — a <50ms w-tap re-press or jitter bunching the attack-flush and the next re-engage-flush into one tick read; a routine minority of hits in fast close-range trades (order-of-magnitude ~5-30% of sprint hits depending on jitter and technique), producing sporadic single weak hits (self-correcting transient form) or, for clients that re-engage only once per sprint session, a persistent weak streak until the next genuine stop/start. Sporadic + timing-dependent + worst at close-range high-CPS = a precise match to "subtle, hard to reproduce, feeling thing."

## `face-hug-opposition-and-degenerate-direction-era-real` — merged as era-real, sources: engine-math, era-truth, desk-obligations, gates, registration-fallthrough, sprint-wire, transactions

**Mechanism:** The base push (0.4 on legacy-1.7) is directed away from the ATTACKER'S POSITION (normalized, magnitude preserved, no distance taper) while the sprint/enchant extras (0.5h) ride the ATTACKER'S YAW. Net sprint horizontal = sqrt(push^2+extra^2+2*push*extra*cos(theta)); with 0.6-wide hitboxes the victim's center drifts beside/past the attacker constantly in face-hug trades, and at theta>~129deg a SPRINT hit ships WEAKER than a plain hit — victim slightly past the attacker nets ~0.05-0.10h (measured 0.0546h at 0.14-block separation on real vanilla 1.7.10). At truly coincident positions (dx^2+dz^2<1e-4) the direction degenerates to the era's random re-roll ((rand-rand)*0.01/axis, vanilla-equivalent to the while-loop, then normalized to FULL 0.4 magnitude in a RANDOM direction) — a coincident sprint hit's net is uniformly random in [0.1, 0.9]h. Byte-identical to vanilla 1.7.10/1.8.9 (knockBack positional dir, attack() yaw-directed addVelocity extras). This geometry is the AMPLIFIER that turns every sprint-verdict loss (the wire bugs above) into 'the victim just doesn't move': a plain-verdict hit at face-hug ships near-ZERO horizontal while the same plain verdict at 3 blocks still visibly pushes 0.4.

**Trigger:** Two players inside ~1 block trading; victim beside/past/coincident with the attacker's center while the crosshair still lands the hit. The closer and more head-on the charge, the nearer the opener horizontal is to zero; direction is RNG at true coincidence. Reproducible on real 1.7.10/1.8.9 with the same geometry — must NOT be 'fixed'.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:212 (base away from position), :224-227 (extras -sin/+cos along yaw), :474-481 (degenerate re-roll), :487-501 (normalize, magnitude preserved); KnockbackEngineTest.java:184-195, :240-257 (zero-distance full-magnitude pins); docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md:118-129 (measured 0.0546h, 'authentic 1.7.10 behavior, not a delivery bug'); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:56-64, :90-100 (decompile: positional dir, yaw extras, while-loop re-roll); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:119-122 ('~0.05h — era-real, identical on actual 1.7.10'); SYNOPSIS.md:48-64, :93-96 (EntityLivingBase.java:586-594 degeneracy fallback).

**Maps to the report:** Strongest era-real match for 'especially when two players are quite close together... even if one is w-tapping... seems like the non-sprinting knockback' plus the random 'feeling thing' character. If it feels MORE frequent than era, the cause is upstream position/verdict capture (stale ring, wire bugs), not this math.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The finding accurately describes the engine and correctly classifies it. Verified against the code:

1. Base push away from ATTACKER POSITION: base() (KnockbackEngine.java:472-488) computes deltaX/deltaZ = source − victim, normalizes by magnitude, and subtracts direction×push (0.4 default). Directed away from the attacker's position, no default distance taper (rangeReduction is an era-exact no-op at defaults, taper=0). Confirmed.

2. Sprint/enchant extras along ATTACKER YAW: lines 214-227 add −sin(yaw)·bonus to x and +cos(yaw)·bonus to z, with the flat +0.1 vertical added once regardless of level. This is byte-faithful to vanilla EntityPlayer.attackTargetEntityWithCurrentItem's addVelocity(−sin·i·0.5, 0.1, cos·i·0.5) guarded by i>0 — I confirmed the vanilla shape matches (i = (sprint?1:0)+enchant, factor 0.5/level, flat 0.1 vertical).

3. Two-opposed-terms math: net = sqrt(push²+extra²+2·push·extra·cosθ). For a sprint hit (push 0.4, extra 0.5) to ship weaker than a plain 0.4 hit, cosθ < −0.625 → θ > 128.7°. The finding's "~129deg" is exactly right.

4. Degenerate coincident re-roll: base() lines 474-480 enters the tiny-random-direction branch at dx²+dz² < 1e-4 (matches vanilla's 1.0E-4 threshold), then normalizes to FULL 0.4 magnitude in a random direction. The single-if-with-1e-8-fallback differs distributionally from vanilla's re-rolling while-loop, but because the output is normalized to a unit direction, only direction matters — full-magnitude holds, which test zeroDistanceHitStaysFiniteWithBaseMagnitude (:193) pins at hypot=0.4. Negligible divergence; the finding fairly calls it "vanilla-equivalent."

5. Coincident sprint net ∈ [0.1, 0.9]h: 0.4 (random dir) + 0.5 (yaw) resultant ranges |0.5−0.4|=0.1 to 0.5+0.4=0.9. The RANGE is correct; "uniformly random" is slightly imprecise (the resultant magnitude of a fixed vector plus a uniform-random-direction vector is not uniformly distributed), a minor overstatement that does not affect the conclusion.

era_call = era-real is correct and doubly corroborated by the cited docs, which I read directly:
- era-wire-measurements.md:120-129 states verbatim the trade-opener opposition, the measured 0.0546 horizontal at 0.14-block separation, and "Face-hug trades producing near-zero openers is authentic 1.7.10 behavior, not a delivery bug."
- era-accuracy SKILL.md:119-122: "A victim past the attacker (face-hug) gets ~0.05 h — era-real, identical on actual 1.7.10."

No guard refutes it on the default legacy-1.7 profile: there is no horizontal floor (only a vertical-min floor exists), no yaw-alignment of the base push, no theta clamp. The pocket-servo chase-alignment path only scales magnitude and is off/servo-only by default, so the default engine path is pure vanilla geometry.

Crucially, the finding does NOT claim this math is the bug to fix — it explicitly frames it as the era-real AMPLIFIER and hedges that any felt-MORE-than-era frequency traces to upstream position/verdict capture (stale ring, wire bugs). That framing is the honest one: the engine math is authentic and must not be "fixed" (doing so would break era accuracy); the actionable defect, if any, lives upstream in what position/verdict is captured at hit time.

I could not refute the finding. It is confirmed as stated, with only a trivial imprecision in the "uniformly random" wording.
- Corrections: Two minor imprecisions, neither affecting the conclusion: (1) "coincident sprint hit's net is uniformly random in [0.1, 0.9]h" — the RANGE [0.1, 0.9] is correct (|0.5−0.4| to 0.5+0.4), but the resultant magnitude of the 0.4 random-direction base plus the 0.5 fixed-yaw extra is NOT uniformly distributed over that range; it clusters toward the higher end. (2) The degenerate branch (KnockbackEngine.java:474-480) is a single-roll if-with-1e-8-fallback, not vanilla's re-rolling while-loop, so the direction DISTRIBUTION differs slightly from vanilla; this is immaterial because the direction is normalized (only its angle matters) and full 0.4 magnitude always ships — the finding's "vanilla-equivalent to the while-loop" is a fair characterization. Everything else in the finding — the positional-base/yaw-extra opposition, the ~129° weaker-than-plain threshold, the 0.0546h @ 0.14-block measurement, the full-magnitude-random-direction degeneracy, and the era-real classification with its upstream-capture hedge — is confirmed against both the code and the two cited research docs.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss: up to ~0.44h in moderate face-hug (θ≈150°, sprint extra contributes almost nothing forward so net ≈ the bare 0.4 base — this is the "seems like the non-sprinting knockback" the user reports) and up to ~0.85h in the extreme charged-past case (measured 0.0546h vs a normal ~0.9h full-stamp sprint wire). At true coincidence, net is random in [0.1, 0.9]h — the "feeling thing / sometimes less than it should be" character. Frequency in real close-range PvP: intermittent, tightly correlated with tight face-hug trades where the victim's center drifts beside/past the attacker while the crosshair still lands — plausibly a meaningful fraction of sub-1-block exchanges, near-zero at normal 2.4-2.8-block range. Actionable severity as a Mental defect: essentially nil — this is era-authentic and changing it would break 1.7.10 parity; the real severity lives in whether upstream position/verdict capture inflates the frequency above era.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: Mechanism verified against code and constants. LEGACY_17 base.horizontal=0.4 is normalized away from the attacker's POSITION (KnockbackEngine.base(), lines 472-488), while the sprint extra 0.5 rides the attacker's YAW (lines 224-227) — two vectors that agree only when the victim's center is dead ahead of both the crosshair and the attacker's position. Net sprint horizontal = sqrt(0.41 + 0.4·cosθ): 0.9 at θ=0, 0.64 at 90°, exactly 0.4 (a plain-strength hit) at θ≈129°, and 0.1 at θ=180°. The crossover math in the finding is exactly right, and the degenerate re-roll (lines 474-480) restores full 0.4 magnitude in a RANDOM direction at coincidence, making a coincident SPRINT hit's net uniformly random in [0.1,0.9]. In a real charge the victim's own inbound momentum (×0.5 friction, pointing back toward the attacker) opposes the base push, so genuine face-hugs cross below plain strength even earlier than 129°.

Does it PRODUCE the report? Yes, cleanly, for the core of it: (1) "especially when two players are quite close together" is precisely the trigger — the closer and more head-on the charge, the larger θ and the deeper the cancellation; (2) "seems like the non-sprinting knockback... even if w-tapping/blockhitting" maps directly to the sprint bonus (the 0.5 yaw term, which w-tap/blockhit re-arm) being geometrically cancelled to leave ~0.4 or less — it literally ships the plain value or below; (3) "sprint hits sometimes less than they should" is the whole partial-opposition band (θ=60–120° → net 0.75 down to 0.44, i.e. losing 0.15–0.46 b/t of the 0.9 expected); (4) "very subtle, hard to reproduce, a feeling thing" matches because the loss is a continuous function of sub-tick relative position at the hit tick — it never repeats identically, and the coincident-RNG edge adds genuine randomness. It being present "as far back as I can remember" fits an era-real geometry that has always been in the formula.

Caveat carried from the finding (correct): this geometry is era-real and NOT itself a Mental bug — it is byte-identical to vanilla 1.7.10/1.8.9. If it fires MORE often or harder than a real 1.7/1.8 server, the actual defect is upstream (a stale position-ring feeding a wrong attacker.x/z into base(), or a sprint-verdict wire loss), which this geometry then AMPLIFIES into "the victim just doesn't move." So the mechanism plausibly produces the reported experience, but confirming it as the WHOLE story (vs an amplifier of an upstream capture bug) requires checking the position source feeding base() — which is outside this reproduction's scope.
- Corrections: Two refinements, neither weakening the finding: (1) The 129° crossover assumes a fresh standing victim; in an actual charge the victim's own velocity toward the attacker is carried at ×0.5 and opposes the base push, so real face-hug trades cross into below-plain territory at angles shallower than 129° — the effect is somewhat MORE reachable than the fresh-victim calc implies. (2) The severe "victim doesn't move at all" cases require the victim substantially beside/past the attacker's position; the common case is the partial band (net 0.44–0.75), which reads as "weaker than a sprint should be" rather than literally zero — still fully consistent with the report's "little to no" wording spanning both. The era-real classification is correct: base-away-from-position + yaw-directed-extra + degenerate re-roll are all byte-identical to vanilla; this is authentic 1.7/1.8, so any FIX would be an intentional divergence, and the productive next step is auditing whether the attacker position fed into base() (the ring/PlayerView capture) is stale, which would make it fire harder than era.
- Severity: Per-hit horizontal loss is large when it fires: partial opposition (θ 60–120°, common in face-hugs) costs 0.15–0.46 b/t off the 0.9 sprint value (17–51%); θ≈129° drops a sprint hit to the 0.4 plain value (full 0.5 bonus gone, ~55% loss); θ→180° (victim charged fully past) or worst-case measured ships 0.05–0.10 b/t (~89–94% loss). Frequency: SOME reduction is near-ubiquitous in true close-range (<~1 block) sprint/w-tap trades because the crosshair-to-center offset is nonzero whenever hitboxes overlap; SEVERE below-plain cases (θ>129°, victim beside/past the attacker) are a modest minority — order ~10–25% of face-hug openers, and the coincident-RNG edge (dx²+dz²<1e-4, ~within 0.01 block) is rare. That profile — frequent mild + occasional dramatic + position-dependent + never-repeating — is a strong match for "subtle, hard to reproduce, more a feeling than a scenario."

## `client-side-felt-kb-reduction-era-real` — merged as era-real, sources: era-truth, transactions

**Mechanism:** Two client-side era contracts make received knockback FEEL weak in mutual trades while the wire ships the correct full stamp. (1) Counter-click x0.6: every on-target bonus-KB attack (client-sprinting or KB-enchant) makes the clicking player's OWN client multiply its motion x0.6 and un-sprint via local prediction — unconditional against player targets regardless of server accept/reject/cancel; counter-clicks landing AFTER the knock packet cut remaining flight to 0.6^n (1 click=60%, 3=21.6%). In a close trade BOTH players counter-click at high CPS during each other's flights. (2) Held input: the velocity packet replaces client motion, then held-W air accel (0.02-0.026/tick, sprint terminal ~0.286 b/t) reclaims displacement — strongest on short face-hug flights. Modern nuance: on UNSPOOFED modern clients the self-x0.6 requires attack charge >0.9, so spam counter-clicks rarely fire it — but if Mental's CADENCE cooldown-removal spoofs attack_speed to keep the meter full, the era 0.6^clicks mechanic returns at full strength on every sprint counter-click (config-coupled, easy to misread as an engine regression). Myth guard: victim sprint-KEY spamming is a documented placebo — the reducer is the attack CLICK and held movement, never the sprint flag.

**Trigger:** Mutual close trade with both players clicking and holding W toward each other — the report's exact scenario; the higher the victim's CPS the weaker their received knock reads. The charge-gate branch depends on whether the CADENCE attack-speed spoof is enabled.

**Evidence:** docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:249-256 (0.6^clicks, client contracts); SYNOPSIS.md:131-138, :304-343 (kbAttack = isSprinting() && charge>0.9; causeExtraKnockback x0.6 + setSprinting(false)), :352-356 (attackStrengthTicker), :382; docs/legacy-combat.md:43-45; .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:57-66 (untouchable client contract), :85-90 (sprint-key spam placebo, pinned live); .claude/skills/legacy-motion-physics/SKILL.md:17-20 (air accel constants).

**Maps to the report:** The single biggest authentic explanation for 'when two players are hitting each other the knockback seems like non-sprinting': both players' received flights are cut to 0.6^n and eaten by held input; the server and Mental's journal shipped the correct full stamp. Constrains interpretation: the victim's sprint STATE is irrelevant, only their clicks and movement.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The finding's two mechanisms are genuine era truths, correctly cited and verifiable in-repo. (1) Attacker self-×0.6 + un-sprint on player targets is confirmed in SYNOPSIS.md:322 (legacy client prediction) and :335-341 (26.x causeExtraKnockback: multiply(0.6,1,0.6)+setSprinting(false), inside if(amount>0), i.e. only on bonus-KB attacks). The 0.6^clicks reduction of the victim's OWN received horizontal flight when they counter-click at high CPS is documented (compendium §5 :250-256; era-accuracy skill :62). (2) Held-input reclaim is confirmed (legacy-combat.md:43-45; air accel 0.02/0.026, sprint terminal 0.286 b/t in the motion skill). The modern charge-gate nuance is correct: SYNOPSIS.md:317 kbAttack=isSprinting()&&full with full=scale>0.9, and :352 the ticker resets on every attack, so spam-clicking an unspoofed modern client keeps charge low and the ×0.6 rarely fires — restored only if a CADENCE attack_speed spoof holds the meter full (config-coupled, correctly reasoned). The ×0.6 is horizontal-only (matches the report's 'moving back'). The sprint-KEY-spam placebo guard is accurate (era-accuracy skill :87). I cannot refute any of these mechanisms.

However, the finding OVER-REACHES in claiming it is 'the single biggest authentic explanation' and it rests on an unverified assumption. Two problems: (a) It omits the most direct close-range era-real cause that the era-accuracy skill itself documents — face-hug positional/yaw geometry gives ~0.05 h (skill :119-121), which matches 'little to no knockback especially when two players are quite close' far more literally than counter-click ×0.6. (b) It ASSUMES 'the wire ships the correct full stamp' with no code evidence. The report's phrase 'seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback' literally describes an attacker sprint-stamp that failed to reach the server fresh — and Mental has dedicated arrival-order/freshness machinery for exactly that (kernel/.../wire/SprintWire.java:10,20,196) with a documented history of sprint-family parity bugs (1.5.0/1.7.0/2.4.1 per memory). A SprintWire freshness race in close w-tap/blockhit trades is a live BUG candidate the finding does not exclude. So the mechanisms are era-real, but the finding does not establish that the REPORT is fully era-real.
- Corrections: Mechanisms are era-real and correctly cited; keep them. But downgrade the confidence/framing: (1) Drop 'the single biggest authentic explanation' — the most direct close-range 'no knockback' era-real cause is the face-hug positional/yaw geometry (~0.05 h, era-accuracy skill :119-121), which the finding omits and which matches the report's 'two players quite close' better than counter-click ×0.6.
