(2) The claim 'the server and Mental's journal shipped the correct full stamp' is asserted, not verified — the report's own wording ('the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback') is exactly the symptom of an attacker sprint-stamp lost at the netty freshness seam (kernel SprintWire), which has a documented bug history; the finding should not treat the wire as proven-correct. (3) One sub-branch (modern unspoofed client + CADENCE spoof) is genuinely config-dependent, not plain era-real. Recommend re-tagging the OVERALL report explanation as era-real-mechanisms-present-but-report-not-fully-explained, and pairing this finding with a code check that the sprint stamp actually ships fresh in close w-tap/blockhit trades before concluding 'no bug.'
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss from the described mechanisms is large where they apply: victim counter-click ×0.6 removes 40% of remaining horizontal per bonus-KB click (2 clicks=64%, 3=78.4%); a 5-10 tick flight at 8-12 CPS lands 2-5 clicks, so received horizontal can drop well below the non-sprint feel — vertical untouched (multiply is 0.6,1,0.6). Held-W air-accel reclaims ~0.02-0.026 b/t toward the attacker, neutralizing a large fraction of a short face-hug flight (which is only ~0.05-0.4 h to begin with) within a few ticks. Frequency in real close-range PvP: the held-input branch is HIGH and unconditional (every held-W trade). The counter-click ×0.6 branch is HIGH-strength only for legacy/ViaVersion 1.7-1.8 clients (common on these nostalgia servers) or when a CADENCE attack-speed spoof is enabled; on an unspoofed modern client the >0.9 charge gate makes it RARE. Net: a real, frequently-felt contributor to weak close-range trades, but NOT a full account of the report — the face-hug ~0.05h geometry and a possible engine-side sprint-freshness race are unaddressed and could each dominate.

**SYMPTOM lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap; re-verification dispatched)

## `modern-client-no-reengage-after-clear` — merged as divergence-from-era, sources: sprint-wire

**Mechanism:** Mental's era reconstruction clears BOTH the wire and the server sprint flag after every accepted sprint hit; its only recovery signal is a client-sent START_SPRINTING. Clients <=1.21.1 run the client-side attack sprint-interruption and auto re-arm next tick with the key held (STOP/START crosses the wire, next hit is sprint again). 1.21.2+ clients REMOVED the attack sprint interruption: continuous-hold sprint attacking generates NO STOP/START around hits, so after Mental's clear the wire and server flag sit false while the client demonstrably sprints. Recovery depends on the fragile self-metadata round trip (setSprinting(false) -> own-entity metadata -> client flag dip -> resync STOP+START), costing at least one RTT of plain hits and emitting nothing if the client re-arms within the same client tick. The reconcile cannot rescue: it compares the wire to view.sprinting(), which is Mental's own cleared flag. A real 1.8.9 sprint-key-holder re-armed every hit and got full sprint KB every time.

**Trigger:** Attacker on a 1.21.2+ client (the owner tests on 1.21.4+) holding W+sprint continuously and landing repeated hits without w-tapping: hit 1 ships sprint KB, hits 2..n read plain. Any autosprint mod behaves the same on any version.

**Evidence:** KnockbackUnit.java:425-447 (wire clear + deferred server-flag clear; no server-side re-arm path for plain sprint); SprintWire.java:167-178 (reconcile adopts the server flag Mental itself cleared); PacketTap.java:85 + SessionService.java:535 (view.sprinting is the live server flag); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:68-75 (the identical modern-client signal loss is documented and reconstructed ONLY for block-hitting via SwordBlockingUnit — held-sprint has no equivalent); compendium:257-259 (era re-engage semantics).

**Maps to the report:** 'sprint hits where they sometimes have less knockback than they should' — input-style and client-version dependent, hence an inconsistent feel rather than a reproducible scenario. Especially credible given the owner's 1.21.4+ test clients.

**CODE lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap; re-verification dispatched)

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: The code confirms the mechanism exactly: applyAttackerObligations clears BOTH the SprintWire (onServerClear -> sprinting/armed false) and the server flag (deferred setSprinting(false)) after every accepted sprint hit, with no server-side re-arm for plain held-sprint (only block-hit is reconstructed via SwordBlockingUnit). SprintWire.verdictAt then reads sprinting=false on the next hit, and reconcile re-seeds from the server flag Mental itself set false — so neither path rescues. clientSprinting stays true but is inert outside the block override. Hits 2..n therefore ship plain KB until a genuine client input change emits STOP/START.

Hand-computed shipped velocity (default LEGACY_17, and all full-sprint presets): sprint hit horizontal ~0.9 (base 0.4 + extra 0.5, sprintFactor 1.0) + 0.1 vertical bonus; plain hit ~0.4 with no vertical bonus. Loss ~0.5 horizontal (~56%, roughly half the knockback distance) plus the vertical pop — a full sprint->plain downgrade, matching 'victim just doesn't really move back' and 'the non-sprinting knockback'.

Era check: in real 1.8 a continuous-hold sprint attacker's client auto-cycled STOP/START each hit (attack sprint-interruption + held-W auto-resprint), so era delivered sprint KB every hit without a deliberate w-tap. The 1.21.2+ client removed that interruption, and any autosprint/toggle-sprint mod (near-universal in modern PvP, version-independent) suppresses STOP/START the same way. So Mental's post-hit clear is never undone on the owner's 1.21.4+ / autosprint test population, and the reconstruction fails to reproduce era's repeated sprint KB. Genuine divergence-from-era.

Frequency/profile: high incidence for the modern-client/autosprint population but intermittent in live movement-rich PvP (strafes, backpedals, jumps, real w-taps emit STOP/START and re-arm), which is why it reads as 'subtle/feeling' rather than a clean repro. Close-range specifically favors continuous-hold pressure (holding W into the opponent, spam-clicking) which maximizes uninterrupted plain-hit runs — aligning with 'especially when close together'. It plausibly produces the 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback' and the close-range non-sprint feel. It does NOT explain the 'even while w-tapping or block-hitting' clause: clean w-taps emit STOP/START and re-arm, and block-hit is separately reconstructed. Not refuted — it clearly produces a substantial part of the report.

Caveat on severity direction: the finding's assumed recovery (setSprinting(false) -> metadata -> client resync STOP+START, ~1 RTT) is weaker than stated — the era-accuracy skill notes clientSprinting SURVIVES that setSprinting(false), i.e. it does not reliably emit a client STOP. So the true recovery is a real input change, making the effect MORE persistent for a pure hold-W/autosprint attacker (potentially glaring vs a dummy: only hit 1 sprints). Real PvP movement is what re-introduces intermittency and keeps it in 'subtle' territory.
- Corrections: The finding's recovery model is optimistic. It assumes Mental's own setSprinting(false) round-trips into a client STOP+START resync costing '~1 RTT of plain hits'. But the era-accuracy skill (68-75) states clientSprinting is 'the only signal that survives Mental's own post-hit setSprinting(false)' — meaning that setSprinting(false) does NOT reliably provoke a client STOP_SPRINTING. So the only genuine re-arm is a real client input change (release/re-press W, strafe, jump, deliberate w-tap). Consequence: for a pure hold-W or autosprint attacker the plain-KB state is persistent, not one-RTT-transient — hit 1 sprints, every subsequent hit is plain until movement input changes. This makes the raw effect LARGER/more persistent than the finding implies; the 'subtle/feeling' quality comes entirely from real PvP movement (strafes/backpedals/jumps) interspersing STOP/START, not from a fast metadata resync. Also: the finding correctly limits itself to the continuous-hold path and should not be read as explaining the owner's 'even while w-tapping or block-hitting' clause — clean w-taps emit STOP/START (re-arm) and block-hit is reconstructed by SwordBlockingUnit.
- Severity: Per-hit loss is large: default LEGACY_17 and every full-sprint preset ship ~0.9 horizontal sprint vs ~0.4 plain (base 0.4 + extra 0.5 at sprintFactor 1.0), i.e. a ~0.5 b/t loss (~56%, roughly HALF the knockback distance) plus the +0.1 vertical pop lost — a complete sprint->plain downgrade. Expected frequency in real close-range PvP: HIGH-but-intermittent for the affected population, which is exactly the owner's (1.21.4+ clients, and autosprint/toggle-sprint is near-universal in modern PvP and version-independent). Fires on every hit after the first in any uninterrupted held-W/autosprint burst; re-armed only by real STOP/START-emitting input (strafe, backpedal, jump, clean w-tap), so live movement-rich fights make it flicker between sprint and plain -> 'subtle, feeling, hard to pin down'. Close-range pressure (hold W into opponent, spam-click) maximizes uninterrupted plain runs, matching 'especially when close together'. Covers the 'sprint hits sometimes less KB' and the close-range non-sprint feel; does NOT cover the w-tap/block-hit clause.

## `blockhit-sprint-rearm-gated-behind-sword-blocking` — merged as config-dependent, sources: sprint-wire, desk-obligations, era-truth

**Mechanism:** The era block-hit sprint re-arm (block->STOP, release->START — maintaining the sprint bonus like an easy w-tap) is reconstructed ONLY by SwordBlockingUnit.resetSprintForBlock -> SprintWire.onBlockSprintReset, and SwordBlockingUnit is part of the default-OFF DAMAGE family. Modern clients (1.17+) keep the sprint flag through item use, so the era's natural STOP/START never crosses the wire when blocking; with SWORD_BLOCKING disabled there is no re-arm signal at all — after any accepted sprint hit a blockhitting attacker's hits ship verdict.sprinting=false (plain) until a real w-tap. Even with the feature ON, the re-arm declines for an attacker whose SprintWire was seeded by reconcile (sprinting=true but clientSprinting=false — join-while-sprinting or domain recreation; only real START packets raise clientSprinting, and resetSprintForBlock's raw-flag gate requires it). Era nuance for calibration: on era clients, hits thrown WHILE the block was held were genuinely non-sprint (item use x0.2 moveForward killed sprint that tick) — the bonus was maintained by the release/re-engage between hits.

**Trigger:** SWORD_BLOCKING off (the shipped default): any modern-client blockhitting attacker loses the sprint bonus on every hit after the first. With it on: attackers whose wire was reconcile-seeded (never sent a START since domain creation) get no re-arm despite visibly sprinting. Shield-raise 'blocking' never re-arms regardless.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/damage/SwordBlockingUnit.java:315-347 (only onBlockSprintReset caller; raw-clientSprinting gate; feature-unit listener only assembled when enabled); SprintWire.java:140-159 (blockReset contract), :167-171 + :202-209 (reconcile seed never raises clientSprinting; only START packets do); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:68-83 (modern-client signal loss, why the reconstruction exists); SYNOPSIS.md:140-146 (item use x0.2 kills sprint same tick); CLAUDE.md (DAMAGE family all default OFF).

**Maps to the report:** Verbatim 'even if one is ... blockhitting, it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback' — whenever the deployment doesn't run sword-blocking, or its raw-flag gate has never seen a START.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: All concrete CODE claims verify. onBlockSprintReset (kernel SprintWire:140) has exactly one production caller, SwordBlockingUnit:342; SWORD_BLOCKING is Family.DAMAGE, defaultEnabled=false (Feature.java:154-156); the re-arm is gated on raw clientSprinting (SwordBlockingUnit:327); reconcile never raises clientSprinting (SprintWire:167-178) while only onSprintStart does (:74); post-hit onServerClear (KnockbackUnit:433) drops sprinting/armed but leaves clientSprinting and only fires on a bonus hit (line 418). Tracing the wire with blockReset=false: after a sprint hit, verdictAt returns sprinting=false until a fresh START. So the mechanism the finding describes is real: with SWORD_BLOCKING off there is no block-hit re-arm, and with it on the re-arm declines for a reconcile-seeded wire (clientSprinting=false).

But three caveats materially weaken it as an explanation for the user's report, and push it toward by-design rather than defect:

1. SCOPED TO MODERN CLIENTS ONLY. The reconstruction exists because 1.17+ clients keep the sprint flag through item-use (era-accuracy:68-83). A 1.8 client via ViaVersion — the typical 1.8-PvP deployment — sends real STOP_SPRINTING on block-start and START_SPRINTING on release, which reach PacketTap:106/103 → onSprintStop/onSprintStart, re-arming sprint naturally with NO reconstruction and regardless of SWORD_BLOCKING. The finding does scope to "modern-client" but never acknowledges that a large share of real blockhitters aren't modern clients.

2. WITHOUT SWORD_BLOCKING THERE IS NO SERVER-SIDE BLOCK ON A 1.9+ SERVER. Right-clicking a sword does nothing server-side post-1.9; the unit's whole purpose is to reconstruct the block. So on a modern client + SWORD_BLOCKING off, "block-hitting" is not a recognized action — the player is just clicking, and the sprint behaviour is the ordinary w-tap requirement (spend freshness per hit; re-START to re-arm), which is era-CORRECT, not a bug. The finding's "loses the sprint bonus on every hit after the first" is exactly the normal w-tap mechanic applied to a player who isn't doing anything special, not a blockhit-specific regression.

3. BY DESIGN. The block-hit sprint reset is documented (era-accuracy:68-83, SprintWire class doc, SwordBlockingUnit:57-65) as a reconstruction that IS the SWORD_BLOCKING feature — the era "easy w-tap." Tying it to that feature is intentional. Calling the default a bug conflates "didn't opt into the reconstruction" with "broken."

The finding also does not explain the CORE of the user's report: "even if one is w-tapping" (a real w-tap sends a client START → PacketTap → onSprintStart → re-arm, independent of SWORD_BLOCKING) and the emphasized "close together" case (better explained by attacker-position-relative base knockback: a face-hug victim past the attacker gets ~0.05h — era-real, era-accuracy:119-121). So it addresses at most the "blockhitting" fragment for one client tier.

The one genuinely defect-like sub-claim is the secondary one: with the feature ON, a genuinely-sprinting attacker whose wire was reconcile-seeded (join-while-sprinting or domain recreation, clientSprinting still false) is denied the block-hit re-arm. That is correct code-wise and is a real, narrow gap — but it requires continuous sprint since before domain creation with no intervening STOP→START, so clientSprinting never latches true; in sustained combat players toggle sprint constantly and a START latches it. Narrow window, not a persistent condition.

Net: code facts correct, so not refuted, but the finding overstates relevance and mislabels largely-intentional, client-tier-scoped behaviour. The horizontal loss when it does bite is real and large (sprint extra 0.5h: a hit that should ship 0.9h ships 0.4h, roughly halving settle distance), matching "non-sprinting knockback," but the frequency in real close-range PvP is low given caveats 1–2.
- Corrections: The CODE mechanism is accurate as stated, but the framing overstates it and it is largely by-design, not a defect. Corrections: (1) It applies ONLY to modern clients (1.17+) that keep the sprint flag through item-use; 1.8 clients via ViaVersion (the common 1.8-PvP case) send natural STOP_SPRINTING/START_SPRINTING across the wire (PacketTap:106/103), re-arming sprint without any reconstruction and independent of SWORD_BLOCKING. (2) On a 1.9+ server with SWORD_BLOCKING off there is NO server-side sword block, so "block-hitting" is not a recognized action — the player is merely clicking and gets the ordinary, era-CORRECT w-tap requirement (freshness spent per hit, re-START to re-arm), not a blockhit-specific regression. (3) The reset is documented as the SWORD_BLOCKING feature's reconstruction (era-accuracy:68-83); tying it to that feature is intentional, so the default is "not opted in," not "broken." (4) The finding does not explain the user's "even w-tapping" (real w-tap = client START → onSprintStart → re-arm, feature-independent) or the emphasized "close together" case (face-hug base-KB pushes from the attacker's position, victim-past-attacker ~0.05h — era-real, era-accuracy:119-121). The strongest sub-claim is the secondary one — with the feature ON, a reconcile-seeded genuine sprinter (clientSprinting=false) is denied re-arm — which is a real but narrow gap (requires continuous sprint since before domain creation / a domain recreation, with no intervening STOP→START to latch clientSprinting).
- Severity: When it bites, the loss is large: the sprint extra is ~0.5 horizontal (0.9h sprint vs 0.4h plain), roughly halving settle distance — squarely matching the "non-sprinting knockback" feel. But expected frequency in real close-range PvP is LOW: caveat-1 removes all 1.8/ViaVersion blockhitters (a large share on 1.8-PvP servers), caveat-2 removes modern-client "blockhitters" who have no server block to hit through, and the primary path is only reached on modern clients where the deployment neither runs SWORD_BLOCKING nor uses a client that self-heals via natural STOP/START. The secondary (feature-ON, reconcile-seed) path is narrower still — a transient window right after join-while-sprinting or a domain recreation. It does not cover the report's dominant "w-tapping" and "close together" symptoms.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Mechanism verified in the main tree. onBlockSprintReset (SprintWire:140) and resetSprintForBlock (SwordBlockingUnit:320) have exactly one caller each, and even the release-boundary onBlockReleased (SprintWire:155) is only driven by SwordBlockingUnit's BlockReleaseListener (:136). SwordBlockingUnit.assemble (:86-101) registers its interact listener and the RELEASE packet listener ONLY when the SWORD_BLOCKING FeatureUnit is assembled. SWORD_BLOCKING is DAMAGE-family, default OFF (CLAUDE.md). So on the shipped default config there is no block-hit sprint reconstruction in the process whatsoever.

Hand-computed scenario (default config, two modern-client sprinters clashing, attacker blockhitting = right-click-sword between clicks): On a 1.17+ client the item-use block does NOT drop the sprint flag, so no STOP/START crosses the wire (era-accuracy SKILL:68-83). Attacker sprint hit #1: wire sprinting/armed true -> verdict.sprinting=true -> ships (0, 0.4607, 0.9), victim settles ~4.948 blocks. Post-hit DeliveryDesk onServerClear(asOf) drops wire sprinting=false, armed=false (SprintWire:100-110). Because the block-cycle sent no wire START and (default config) resetSprintForBlock never runs, nothing re-arms. Hit #2..N ship verdict.sprinting=false -> plain (0, 0.3608, 0.4), victim settles ~1.994 blocks. This is EXACTLY the reported 'even if one is blockhitting, it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback' — verbatim. It also diverges from era truth: in 1.7/1.8 the block cycle sent STOP then START (item-use dropped sprint, release re-armed it), so era blockhitting genuinely re-earned the +1 level on essentially every hit (an easy w-tap). Default Mental does not reconstruct this, so a blockhitter's post-first hits are era-WRONG (too weak).

Second, narrower path even with the feature ON: the raw-flag gate (SwordBlockingUnit:327 clientSprinting()) declines the re-arm for an attacker whose wire was reconcile-seeded (sprinting=true, clientSprinting=false — join-while-sprinting or domain recreation; reconcile at SprintWire:167-177 never raises clientSprinting, only START packets do). Such a visibly-sprinting player gets no block re-arm until they physically release+re-press sprint. This is a genuine latent bug independent of config, but rare.

Magnitude: horizontal knock 0.9 -> 0.4 (2.25x drop), settle 4.948 -> 1.994 blocks, i.e. the victim travels ~40% as far — a ~2.95-block pushback loss per affected hit. Per-hit this is large (not itself 'subtle'), but the symptom is intermittent because it interleaves with real w-taps (real START packets, which DO re-arm and ship full sprint KB). That mix — full-KB w-taps and reduced-KB blockhits landing seemingly at random — is precisely what reads as 'very subtle, hard to reproduce, more a feeling.' The close-range tie is real-but-indirect: blockhitting is a close-range clash technique, and reduced KB keeps the victim in combo range, reinforcing the 'doesn't really move back / stays close' perception.

Caveats: (1) The 'sprint hits sometimes have less KB' clause is only weakly explained — a reconcile-seeded attacker's ORDINARY sprint hits still ship sprint KB (verdict reads seeded sprinting=true; only the blockReset override and resetSprintForBlock require clientSprinting), so plain-sprint-hit weakness here is mostly the era-correct 'no w-tap => bonus only on hit #1' dynamic, not this bug. (2) Whether the symptom manifests at all is entirely a config toggle: if the owner's deployment enables SWORD_BLOCKING, the frequent path is fixed and only the rare reconcile-seed corner remains.
- Corrections: Finding is accurate. Refinement: the second listed trigger ('sprint hits ship non-sprint') via reconcile-seed applies specifically to the BLOCKHIT re-arm being declined, not to ordinary sprint hits — a reconcile-seeded attacker's plain sprint hits DO ship full sprint KB (verdictAt returns the seeded sprinting=true without needing clientSprinting; only blockReset+resetSprintForBlock consult the raw flag). So this finding explains the report's 'blockhitting' clause strongly and verbatim, but explains the standalone 'sprint hits sometimes weaker' clause only weakly. Also worth flagging for the fix: on default config this is a genuine divergence-from-era (era blockhitting re-armed sprint every hit), so the underlying issue is that the era-required block-hit sprint reconstruction is gated behind a default-OFF DAMAGE feature rather than living in the always-on KNOCKBACK family — that gating, more than the reconcile-seed corner, is what produces the owner's symptom.
- Severity: Per affected hit: horizontal knockback 0.9 -> 0.4 (2.25x loss); victim settle distance 4.948 -> 1.994 blocks, ~2.95 blocks (~60%) of pushback lost — victim stays in combo range. Frequency: on the SHIPPED DEFAULT config (SWORD_BLOCKING off), fires on essentially EVERY non-w-tap hit of any attacker who blockhits between clicks — which in close-range competitive 1.8 sword PvP is the majority of players and the majority of their exchange hits. Appears intermittent only because it interleaves with real w-taps (which still ship full sprint KB), giving the 'random, subtle, feeling' profile. If the deployment enables SWORD_BLOCKING, drops to a rare corner (reconcile-seeded / join-while-sprinting attackers only).

## `post-hit-sprint-clear-era-economics` — merged as era-real, sources: desk-obligations, era-truth, sprint-wire

**Mechanism:** The post-hit sprint clear is era truth: vanilla 1.7/1.8 ran setSprinting(false) inside attack() on every bonus hit, so consecutive hits without a genuine re-engage are PLAIN — the sprint extra is a per-engagement resource, not per-hit (measured on real 1.8.9: no-w-tap doubles settle 7.2 blocks vs w-tap 11.4). Mental reproduces this deliberately (the desk obligation: wire flag + deferred re-arm-guarded server flag). The genuine era plain-ship windows: a held-W chase without crisp per-hit w-taps (only the first hit carries the extra), and a mistimed w-tap whose ATTACK arrives in the STOP->START wire gap (era servers applied entity-actions and attacks in arrival order — an authentically plain hit). Registration stamps the verdict and the clear can never unsprint an already-registered hit (the Q1 race is designed out). NOTE: no era doc measures the plain-hit fraction at 10+ CPS — at legal cadence era sprint hits virtually always re-armed, so plain-shipping on WELL-TIMED w-taps exceeds era truth and points to the retro-clear/modern-client bugs above.

**Trigger:** Trading with W held but without per-hit w-taps: every second-and-later sprint hit legitimately ships the plain 0.4 knock, identical to real 1.7/1.8; combined with face-hug geometry this reads as 'no knockback' at close range.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:404-449; .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md ('Sprint-flag clear' obligation; 7.2 vs 11.4 measured); docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md:234-241 (w-tap vs no-w-tap doubles 11.6 vs 7.2); SYNOPSIS.md:140-146; docs/legacy-combat.md:95-100 (sprint-reset hitch); .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md:245-257 (arrival-order contract).

**Maps to the report:** Part of 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback' is authentic era behavior that must be separated from the wire bugs: era says plain hits happen exactly when re-engage timing is sloppy — if they happen on crisp w-taps, that is the bug findings, not this.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: Verified against source and era docs. KnockbackUnit.java:404-449 (applyAttackerObligations) does mirror vanilla's in-attack setSprinting(false) on accepted bonus melee hits, via SprintWire.onServerClear(asOf) (kernel wire) plus a deferred, wire-re-arm-guarded player.setSprinting(false). The era claim is directly corroborated: era-wire-measurements.md:239-240 measures no-w-tap double 6.893/7.205 vs w-tap double 10.689/11.648, and the SKILL obligation (§229-234) states vanilla ends every sprint-bonus hit with setSprinting(false). So the sprint extra being a per-engagement resource (held-W chase => only the first hit carries the extra) is authentic 1.7/1.8 behavior, not a defect. The 'Q1 race designed out' claim holds: the delivered vector is computed from the registration-stamped SprintVerdict (attackerSprinting reads tx.context().sprint(), lines 366-368) BEFORE the clear runs; line 344 passes the verdict's own tick stamp as asOf; onServerClear no-ops under a strictly-newer wire write (line 103); the deferred clear is skipped if the wire re-armed by execution time (442-445). A later clear cannot retroactively unsprint an already-stamped hit. The mistimed-tap case (STOP drops sprinting but leaves armed; ATTACK arrives before START; attackerSprinting gates purely on sprinting()) is genuinely plain and era-correct. Could not refute the mechanism or the era classification. IMPORTANT scope limitation (finding is honest about it but it must be foregrounded): this does NOT explain the owner's actual reported scenario. The owner reports plain KB WHILE w-tapping or blockhitting. Blockhitting while moving re-arms sprint every hit via the blockReset contract (SprintWire.onBlockSprintReset/verdictAt lines 140-198, gated on the raw clientSprinting flag), so a plain blockhit is a bug, not era-real; crisp per-hit w-taps should also re-arm (arrival-order wire, verdictAt with no tick gating). The finding correctly punts both to other findings. There is a real edge the finding folds into 'other bugs' rather than era-real: onServerClear only no-ops on lastWrite.value() > asOf.value() (strict), so a same-tick START-after-ATTACK (very fast w-tap at 10+ CPS collapsing into one tick) is treated as an 'accepted residual' (line 98 comment) and gets cleared — but the finding explicitly does NOT claim that case as era-truth, so this does not refute it.
- Corrections: The finding is accurate and well-scoped, but its explanatory reach must be foregrounded: it accounts ONLY for the sloppy-timing subset (held-W chase without per-hit w-taps, or a STOP->ATTACK-before-START mistimed tap). It does NOT explain the owner's PRIMARY reported scenario — plain KB while ACTIVELY w-tapping or blockhitting. Blockhitting while moving re-arms sprint on every hit of a held block via the blockReset contract (SprintWire.onBlockSprintReset/verdictAt, kernel/.../SprintWire.java:140-198), so a plain blockhit is a genuine bug, not era-real; crisp per-hit w-taps also re-arm via the arrival-order wire. The finding correctly defers both to the other bug findings and stamps a NOTE that plain-shipping on well-timed w-taps exceeds era truth. One code detail the finding buckets under 'other bugs' but is worth naming precisely: onServerClear's newer-write guard is a STRICT inequality (lastWrite.value() > asOf.value(), SprintWire.java:103), so a same-tick re-engage START collapsing into the hit's own tick at 10+ CPS is treated as an 'accepted residual' (line 98) and cleared — a candidate contributor to the crisp-technique bug, but not part of the era-real mechanism this finding describes.
- Severity: Zero excess horizontal-KB loss attributable to THIS mechanism: it reproduces era truth exactly (held-W second-and-later hits ship the plain 0.4 knock; the ~4-block gap between 7.2 and 11.4 settle distances is authentic, not a defect). Frequency: the era-real held-W-chase pattern is common in casual/panic trading but rare in skilled PvP that w-taps every hit. Net: not a bug — this finding subtracts an authentic-behavior explanation from the report rather than adding KB loss, and it explicitly does NOT cover the owner's crisp-w-tap/blockhit-plain complaint, which is the high-frequency, real-defect portion routed to other findings.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: Hand-computed on LEGACY_17 (base 0.4/0.4, extra 0.5/0.1, sprintFactor 1.0, friction 0.5): a grounded stationary-residual victim taking a sprint-bonus hit with attacker yaw aligned to the radial gets 0.4 (base) + 1.0×0.5 (sprint extra) = 0.9 horizontal / 0.5 vertical; after the post-hit sprint clear the next non-re-armed hit ships 0.4 horizontal / 0.4 vertical. That is a 2.25× drop, −0.5 b/t horizontal (−56%) and −0.1 vertical — precisely the era-measured 7.2 (no-tap) vs 11.4 (w-tap) settle doubles the finding cites. The clear (KnockbackUnit.java:418-448) fires on EVERY accepted sprint-bonus melee, stamped asOf, re-arming only on a genuine STOP→START before the next attack; so the 2nd-and-later hit of a held-W trade without crisp per-hit w-taps deterministically ships the plain 0.4 knock. The magnitude is large and reads exactly as 'the non-sprinting knockback' the owner describes, and because whether a tap 'counted' as a re-engage hinges on sub-tick arrival timing the player cannot perceive, the intermittency matches the 'subtle, feeling thing' quality. Close-range emphasis fits too: face-hug circle-strafing both raises the sloppy-tap fraction and misaligns the yaw-directed 0.5 extra from the radial axis, mushing even the sprint hits that do land. HOWEVER this is faithful era reproduction (vanilla setSprinting(false)-on-bonus-hit; SKILL.md:229-234), not a defect — the sprint extra is a per-engagement resource. It CANNOT account for the owner's explicit 'even if one is w-tapping' clause: at legal cadence era sprint hits virtually always re-armed, so plain-shipping on crisp w-taps exceeds era truth and belongs to the sibling wire STOP→START-gap / deferred-re-arm bugs. Not refuted (it plausibly produces a real, large-magnitude, correctly-flavored slice of the report — the held-W / sloppy-tap subset), but it is the authentic control to subtract out, not the fix.
- Corrections: The finding is accurate and self-aware. One scoping refinement: it produces a genuine, large-magnitude, timing-gated slice of the report (the held-W / no-per-hit-tap trades — deterministically plain, −0.5 b/t horizontal), and that slice does match the 'subtle feeling' quality. But it is the authentic BASELINE/control, correctly implemented, not a bug — it must be measured and subtracted, and the owner's specific 'even when w-tapping' symptom belongs to the sibling wire STOP→START-gap / deferred-re-arm findings, exactly as the finding's own NOTE states.
- Severity: Horizontal KB loss 0.5 b/t on the aligned standing case (0.9→0.4, −56%; era settle ~11.4→7.2 blocks), plus −0.1 vertical. Frequency: fires on ~100% of consecutive sprint hits that were NOT re-armed by a per-hit w-tap (very common in casual/mashed close-range trading) and ~0% on cleanly w-tapped hits at legal cadence — so among a skilled w-tapping player's close-range trades it is an intermittent minority tied to which taps went sloppy, matching 'subtle / hard to reproduce.' As era truth it is high-frequency-but-correct; as an explanation for the owner's w-tap-and-still-plain complaint it is near-zero and misattributed.

## `desk-single-slot-supersede-passthrough-vanilla-leak` — merged as bug, sources: transactions, desk-obligations, registration-fallthrough, gates

**Mechanism:** The desk holds ONE pending and ONE wireSlot per victim, both last-write-wins. replacePending (DeliveryDesk.java:312-328) suppresses any LIVE prior pending and resets awaiting=false; resolve() drains the wire FIRST (DeliveryDesk.java:172-177). Consequence chain: when a second submission for the same victim lands between an earlier same-tick hit's arm (adopt at KnockbackUnit.java:256-267 or submit+arm at :327-342) and that hit's end-of-tick PlayerVelocityEvent, the earlier armed hit's own event resolves with awaiting=false -> PASS_THROUGH -> VANILLA's velocity ships as the last wire word. Vanilla's velocity for the fast path's victim.damage() is the plain 0.4 base knock (sprint extras live only in the cancelled Player.attack) with kept falling-y when airborne — the client's pre-sent era sprint stamp (0.9, 0.46) is overwritten by a plain or downward vector; the superseded hit also never reaches recordDelivered, so combos-on ledgers lose the link and the NEXT hit under-reads. Reachable via: (a) an era-silent blocked-shape mid-invuln hit submitted UNARMED (KnockbackUnit.java:232-253/:327-343) clobbering an armed pending; (b) a PINNED submitFromWire for a PACKETLESS victim (no PE user bypasses the FeedbackGate entirely, HitRegistrationUnit.java:511-521) landing mid-window at spam CPS; (c) wireSlot silent overwrite when the victim's session task starves >=~10 ticks (two pre-sends between drains: first tx vanishes unjournaled, its valve never armed, vanilla's duplicate ships uncancelled). For WIRED victims at defaults the 450ms FeedbackGate structurally defuses most of this family (verified: sweep also never time-drops connected victims post-2.4.6, DeliveryDesk.java:260-283, pinned by DeliveryDeskTest); feedback-min-interval-ms: 0/small reopens it — the one config knob that makes the report dramatically worse.

**Trigger:** Two EDBEEs/submissions on the same victim inside one region tick: clicks bunched by jitter at 12-16 CPS, two attackers, victim blockhitting (blocked-shape mid-invuln submit), packetless victims (SimpleBoxer bots/FakePlayers — fires at DEFAULT config, relevant if the owner feel-tests against bots), or feedback-min-interval-ms lowered; plus the session-starvation wireSlot overwrite under severe lag.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:312-328 (supersede resets awaiting), :172-177 (!awaiting -> PASS_THROUGH), :305-328 (drainWire/replacePending; wireSlot last-write-wins :36-53), :105-108 (awaitVelocityEvent never checks pending==tx), :260-283 (connected never time-dropped); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:232-253, :327-343; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/DeskRouter.java:77-88 (PASS_THROUGH ships nothing Mental, no ledger record); HitRegistrationUnit.java:398-402, :511-521 (packetless bypasses the gate); CombatSession.java:230-239 (drain cadence); DeliveryDeskTest.java:330-344, :444-458 (supersede-resets-arm pinned, but only for a FOREIGN event — no test covers the passed-through event being the superseded hit's own); precedent: 2.4.6 fix (commit 545f1dc) closed the identical vanilla-velocity-leak symptom for the sweep path only.

**Maps to the report:** Directly produces 'the victim just doesn't really move back / seems like non-sprinting knockback' in close-range trades and names blockhitting — the exact modifiers the owner listed. Intermittent (needs same-tick bunching), hence 'subtle, more a feeling'. Also explains why it may reproduce best against bots.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: The finding accurately describes a real, latent code property: replacePending (DeliveryDesk:327) resets awaiting=false, resolve() drainWire()s first (172-173), and !awaiting yields PASS_THROUGH (174-176), so a superseded hit's OWN velocity event can ship vanilla's velocity. This "own-event passthrough" case is genuinely untested (DeliveryDeskTest:443-490 only cover a FOREIGN event at an unarmed/superseded pending). I cannot refute that the mechanism exists. BUT the finding's headline claim — that this produces the owner's real-PvP close-range weak-KB symptom at default config for wired players — is substantially overstated and effectively unreachable for that scenario:

(1) Single-thread synchronicity: a region-path EDBEE does submit+arm then returns, and vanilla's knockback→PlayerVelocityEvent→DeskRouter.resolve→ship+clear all nest inside one synchronous victim.damage() on the region thread. No second region hit can interleave between arm and the velocity event. So the era-silent blocked hit (scenario a) becomes the pending itself unarmed — it does NOT "clobber an armed pending." The only cross-thread interleave is submitFromWire (netty).

(2) FeedbackGate self-consistency: for a netty tx B to reach submitFromWire it must become PRE_SENT/PINNED, which requires passing the default ~450ms gate ((maxNoDamageTicks/2−1)*50, confirmed via HitRegSettings.DEFAULTS=FEEDBACK_INTERVAL_AUTO). If an armed hit A already exists for a wired victim, A implies a pre-send fired <450ms ago (A was itself a pre-send, or A is a gated hurt-only hit precisely BECAUSE a pre-send just fired), so B within the window is gated to hurt-only and never reaches submitFromWire. You cannot have both an armed A and a fresh wire PRE_SENT B for one wired victim in the window. Also HitRegistrationUnit:335 skips the pre-send entirely when victimView.damageImmune(), so the immune/blocked case never produces a wire tx.

(3) Even when a PRE_SENT is superseded on a wired victim, the client already received the velocity BURST (HitRegistrationUnit:426-429) and applied the strong era knock immediately; a passed-through server-side velocity event does not retract that. Felt-weak KB only materializes where the felt knock depends on the server velocity event: a PACKETLESS victim (admitVelocityPreSend returns true unconditionally for !victimHasWire, line 517-519 — bots/FakePlayers, no burst) or a lowered feedback-min-interval-ms.

So the reachable felt-weak-KB path is bots or a lowered config knob, NOT real wired close-range PvP at default config — which is the owner's actual complaint. The finding itself hedges on this ("the 450ms FeedbackGate structurally defuses most of this family; feedback-min-interval-ms:0/small reopens it"), which undercuts its own matches_report headline.
- Corrections: Reclassify from "bug that directly produces the owner's real-PvP symptom" to "real but latent passthrough defect, config/bot-dependent for the felt symptom." Corrections to the finding: (a) Scenario (a) as worded ("era-silent blocked mid-invuln hit clobbering an armed pending") is not reachable on the single-thread synchronous model — an era-silent region hit becomes the unarmed pending itself and is later swept or superseded; it never steals a concurrently-armed hit's velocity event (that hit already resolved+cleared synchronously). (b) The region+wire supersede race for WIRED victims is blocked by the FeedbackGate's self-consistency (an armed A implies a recent pre-send, which gates any fresh wire PRE_SENT B within 450ms) plus the damageImmune() pre-send skip at HitRegistrationUnit:335. (c) For wired victims, a superseded PRE_SENT still delivered its client burst, so no felt-weak KB results; the felt symptom requires the velocity-event-dependent path = packetless victims (bots) or lowered feedback-min-interval-ms. The genuine, actionable residue: the "superseded hit's own event → PASS_THROUGH" case is untested and should get a kernel test; the packetless PIN path bypassing the gate (admitVelocityPreSend line 517-519) plus last-write-wins wireSlot is the one default-config-reachable leak, but it only affects bot/FakePlayer victims, not real PvP.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss WHEN it fires: a passed-through vanilla melee velocity is the base ~0.4 horizontal knock WITHOUT the sprint bonus (~+0.4 impulse lives in the cancelled Player.attack), i.e. roughly HALF the intended sprint-hit horizontal KB, plus vanilla's kept falling-y (downward) when airborne — matching "non-sprinting / doesn't move back." Expected frequency in real close-range wired PvP at DEFAULT config: effectively nil — defused by (1) the client burst already delivering pre-sent hits, (2) the 450ms gate's self-consistency blocking the region+wire supersede race, and (3) single-thread synchronous resolution of same-tick region hits. Frequency against PACKETLESS victims (bots/FakePlayers) at default config: occasional at spam CPS (12-16), since every hit PINs and calls submitFromWire with a last-write-wins slot and no gate. Frequency with feedback-min-interval-ms lowered to 0/small: reopens the wired-victim race, becoming intermittent in fast combos. Net: a real latent defect, low real-PvP severity at defaults, not a match for the owner's wired-player symptom without a config change or bot testing.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: The core mechanism is code-verified and real. DeliveryDesk holds ONE pending + ONE wireSlot per victim, both last-write-wins. replacePending (line 312-328) suppresses a live prior pending and resets awaiting=false. resolve() (172-177) uses whatever `pending` is — awaitVelocityEvent(tx) at 105-108 ignores its tx argument, so resolve never checks that the firing PlayerVelocityEvent belongs to the pending hit. With awaiting=false and pending!=null, DeskRouter.pendingFormula() (DeskRouter:61) returns non-null, so the router does NOT take its zero-touch early return; it proceeds into resolve() which returns PASS_THROUGH — vanilla's velocity stands AND the valve is never armed, so vanilla's duplicate end-of-tick ENTITY_VELOCITY overwrites the client's pre-sent era stamp. That ships vanilla's plain 0.4 non-sprint knock (the sprint bonus lived in the cancelled Player.attack) — precisely "the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback," or a kept-falling-y downward vector when airborne ("little to no knockback").

Timing is right: PlayerVelocityEvent for damage knockback fires at end-of-tick during the entity-tracker broadcast (CraftBukkit hurtMarked path), not synchronously inside the damage call — DeskRouter is the sole global PlayerVelocityEvent writer routing to the victim's desk. So a second same-tick submission that lands between hit A's arm and A's deferred end-of-tick event can supersede A's pending and reset awaiting=false, sending A's own event through PASS_THROUGH.

Reachability, hand-traced:
- PACKETLESS victims (SimpleBoxer bots / FakePlayers — the owner's primary feel-test rig per memory): I verified admitVelocityPreSend returns true UNCONDITIONALLY for !victimHasWire, so the 450ms FeedbackGate does NOT pace them. Every spam-CPS hit submits a PINNED tx via submitFromWire; two pinned submissions in one starved/bunched region tick supersede — the first vanishes unjournaled, its valve never armed, vanilla's duplicate ships uncancelled. Fires at DEFAULT config. Directly explains "reproduces best against bots."
- WIRED 1v1 (the report's stated scenario): the 450ms auto gate (maxNoDamageTicks/2-1 ticks) blocks a second WIRE pre-send within the window, but the region-path desk.submit in the EDBEE authoritative pass is NOT gated. A same-tick second EDBEE (packet bunching at 12-16 CPS) still calls desk.submit and supersedes. For the era-silent-blocked clobber specifically, I found a constraint the finding understates: within one tick every EDBEE reads the SAME frozen damageImmune boundary view, so A-fresh + B-immune cannot both come off that view UNLESS A is a boundary combo hit (vanilla LIVE counter knocks it and fires a real velocity event, but the frozen view lags and reads immune) adopted+armed via the non-blocked PRE_SENT branch (KnockbackUnit:265, which never consults immune), plus a same-tick blocked B (immune off frozen view) that submits UNARMED and clobbers A. Narrow boundary+blockhit window — rare, intermittent.
- feedback-min-interval-ms lowered/0 reopens the wire-double-submit family for wired victims too (the one config knob that makes it dramatically worse) — matches the finding.

The frequency profile — low per-hit probability, elevated by close range (constant reach → rapid hits → more same-tick bunching), blockhitting (era-silent branch), 2v1, and lag; common against bots — matches "subtle, hard to reproduce, more a feeling thing" and names the exact modifiers the owner listed (close range, w-tap, blockhit, sprint hits reading as non-sprint). This is a BUG (desk resolves a genuine hit's velocity event against a foreign/superseded slot, shipping vanilla's non-era velocity), not era-divergence-by-design.
- Corrections: Mechanism confirmed and it plausibly produces the reported symptom. Two refinements to the finding: (1) Sub-case (a) (era-silent blocked hit clobbering an armed pending) is NARROWER for CONNECTED victims than framed — within one tick all EDBEEs read the same frozen damageImmune boundary view, so A-fresh/B-immune requires A to be a boundary combo hit (vanilla-fresh, frozen-immune) adopted+armed via the non-blocked PRE_SENT branch at KnockbackUnit:265 (which never consults immune) plus a same-tick blocked B; a plain same-tick pair reads identical immune and does not split into armed+era-silent. This makes wired-1v1 (a) a rare boundary-window event, consistent with 'hard to reproduce.' (2) The finding's strongest DEFAULT-config reach is the PACKETLESS path — I confirmed admitVelocityPreSend returns true unconditionally for no-wire victims, so pinned bot hits are entirely ungated and two-per-tick supersede readily; this is the cleanest match to 'reproduces best against bots' and is more reliably reachable than the wired cases. Also note the loss manifests two ways at once: resolve()→PASS_THROUGH ships vanilla's velocity on the server AND (because the valve is never armed) vanilla's duplicate end-of-tick ENTITY_VELOCITY overwrites the client's already-seen pre-sent era knock, so the client visibly decelerates from the sprint stamp down to the non-sprint value.
- Severity: When it fires, horizontal KB drops from the era sprint stamp (full stamp ~0.9 initial b/t; finding cites pre-sent 0.9,0.46 → multi-block travel) to vanilla's plain ~0.4 non-sprint base (sprint bonus absent because it lived in the cancelled Player.attack) — roughly a 40-55% horizontal loss (~victim travels about half the intended distance), occasionally with a downward kept-falling-y when the victim is airborne ("little to no"). Per-hit magnitude is clearly perceptible. Frequency: LOW per hit for wired 1v1 at default (needs same-tick double-hit + a boundary-combo/blockhit immune split — a few percent of close-range exchanges at high CPS, biased toward the blockhit/w-tap trades the owner named); COMMON against packetless bots at default (gate bypassed) and against wired players once feedback-min-interval-ms is lowered. Net: an intermittent "some hits just don't knock back right" felt across many sessions — matches the report's subtle/feeling character rather than a reliably reproducible defect.

## `difference-hit-armed-pending-clobbers-and-dangles` — merged as bug, sources: transactions, gates

**Mechanism:** A NON-blocked stronger-mid-invuln hit (e.g. a crit landing in the hurt window — CraftBukkit fires EDBEE with the difference) is deliberately submitted AND ARMED (KnockbackUnit.java:327-343; the comment justifies arming frozen-immune reads for boundary hits, but is FALSE for genuine difference hits, where era vanilla applies NO knockback and fires NO velocity event). Consequences: (a) same-tick clobber — it supersedes an earlier armed accepted hit, and the shared end-of-tick velocity event resolves the LIVE-REGISTERED branch (DeliveryDesk.java:208-213), shipping the DIFFERENCE hit's recomputed formula using its OWN SprintVerdict frozen at ITS packet arrival — mid-w-tap that verdict reads sprint=false, so a sprint hit's delivery is replaced with a plain ~0.4 knock; (b) with nothing else pending it DANGLES armed on a connected victim indefinitely (sweep never time-drops connected), and the LIVE-REGISTERED branch ships the stored formula while ignoring the event's velocity — the next FOREIGN velocity event (rod, explosion, plugin setVelocity) is hijacked into shipping the stale melee knock. Era contract: a stronger mid-invuln hit deals difference damage with NO knock and no flinch — this transaction should never participate in delivery at all.

**Trigger:** (a) hit1 accepted+armed and hit2 = a crit/sharpness-variance difference hit mid-invuln, both damage tasks in one region tick (bunched clicks or two attackers); worst mid-w-tap when hit2's verdict is non-sprint — jump-crit spam at close range maximizes it. (b) any crit-difference hit followed by a rod/explosion/plugin velocity before the next melee EDBEE.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:327-343 (submit+arm includes frozen-immune non-blocked; own comment :246-252 concedes the frozen read cannot discriminate the genuine difference branch); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:208-213 (LIVE-REGISTERED ships formula, ignores api velocity), :260-277 (connected pending held forever); HitRegistrationUnit.java:321, :523-535 (verdict frozen at registration); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md ('a stronger hit mid-invuln deals difference damage with NO knock and no flinch').

**Maps to the report:** 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' and 'even if one is w-tapping ... non-sprinting knockback' — the clobber substitutes a non-sprint-verdict recompute for a sprint hit's stamp; close-range mutual trades maximize crit-difference EDBEEs.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `unclear`

- Reasoning: The finding's headline mechanism — consequence (a), the same-tick clobber that substitutes a non-sprint recompute for a sprint hit's delivery, and the ONLY consequence that matches the user's close-range melee report — is refuted by velocity-event timing. DeskRouter (core/.../delivery/DeskRouter.java:53-89) is a plain HIGH-priority PlayerVelocityEvent handler; vanilla fires that event SYNCHRONOUSLY inside each hit's knockback code, within the same hurt() stack as the EDBEE. There is no batched "shared end-of-tick velocity event." So a fresh accepted+armed hit1 ships its sprint stamp and clearDecision()s (DeliveryDesk.java:330-335, awaiting=false) via its OWN synchronous velocity event BEFORE hit2's EDBEE can submit. hit2 (the difference hit) therefore cannot clobber a still-pending accepted decision — it becomes the sole pending and dangles harmlessly. Furthermore, any SUBSEQUENT melee hit that submits calls replacePending (DeliveryDesk.java:312-328), which re-arms with its own vector and resets awaiting=false, so a later melee's velocity event never ships the difference hit's stale formula.\n\nConsequence (b) — a dangling armed non-blocked difference hit on a connected victim (never time-dropped, sweep:260-277) whose awaiting=true state lets a subsequent FOREIGN velocity event (rod/explosion/plugin setVelocity) resolve the LIVE branch and ship the stale melee vector — is mechanically real (resolve() gates on awaiting, pendingFormula() is non-null) and constitutes a genuine latent gap. But it requires a NON-melee velocity event to interleave before the next melee hit (any melee supersedes via replacePending), so it does NOT fire in the user's pure close-range sword trades, and when it fires it substitutes a melee vector onto a rod/explosion event — not a horizontal-KB reduction and not a 'non-sprint feeling.'\n\nThe finding additionally argues against a deliberately documented tradeoff: victimImmune (CombatSession-side, KnockbackUnit:564-579) and the arm comment (328-341) state that the frozen boundary immune read cannot distinguish a genuine difference hit from a legal boundary combo hit, which vanilla's live counter knocks in full and DOES fire a velocity event for. The finding's implied fix (never arm) would reintroduce the cited 1.9.4 second-regression; the finding does not address this.
- Corrections: Finding as stated is wrong on its load-bearing claim (a): there is no same-tick clobber of an accepted sprint hit, because DeskRouter resolves each hit's PlayerVelocityEvent synchronously within that hit's own damage/hurt() stack (not at end-of-tick), and replacePending re-arms awaiting=false for any later melee submit — so a difference hit's non-sprint recompute is never shipped in place of a sprint hit's stamp. This decouples the finding from the user's symptom entirely.\n\nWhat survives is a narrower, real, but off-symptom latent gap (a refinement of consequence b): a non-blocked mid-invuln difference hit is submitted AND armed (KnockbackUnit.java:327-342 — the eraSilentBlockedHit guard only exempts the BLOCKED difference shape, not the non-blocked one), and on a connected victim it is never time-dropped (DeliveryDesk sweep:260-277), so it can dangle with awaiting=true / non-null pendingFormula until either the next melee supersedes it (the normal case) or a FOREIGN PlayerVelocityEvent (fishing rod, explosion, plugin setVelocity) resolves it and ships the stale melee vector. That foreign-velocity hijack is a legitimate correctness edge worth a targeted guard, but: (1) it does not fire in pure close-range melee (the reported scenario), (2) it produces a wrong-vector substitution, not a knockback reduction, and (3) the naive fix the finding implies (don't arm non-blocked immune hits) is explicitly rejected by the code because the frozen immune read cannot distinguish a genuine difference hit from a legal boundary combo hit that vanilla DOES knock and DOES fire a velocity event for (the documented 1.9.4 second-regression). Any real fix must key off whether a velocity event actually arrived (e.g. distinguishing melee-armed pendings from foreign events at resolve time), not off the frozen immune read.
- Severity: Near-zero for the reported symptom. Consequence (a) (the only claim matching 'sprint hits less KB / w-tap non-sprint KB in close melee') does not occur — synchronous per-hit velocity events mean an accepted hit ships and clears before the next hit submits, so 0.0 horizontal-KB loss from this path in real close-range PvP. Consequence (b) is a genuine but rare latent bug (a dangling armed difference hit hijacking a foreign velocity event), frequency effectively 0 in pure-melee trades (needs a rod/explosion/plugin velocity to interleave before the next melee, which otherwise supersedes it); when it does fire it substitutes a melee vector onto a projectile/explosion knock rather than reducing horizontal KB, so it does not present as the reported 'weak/less knockback feeling.'

**SYMPTOM lens: REFUTED** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Era premise and code arming are both real, but the report-matching consequence cannot fire for connected players. Compendium 51-53/67 confirms a stronger mid-invuln hit is fullHit=false → no knockback/no flinch/no velocity event, and KnockbackUnit:327-343 does arm genuine non-blocked frozen-immune (difference) hits — so a crit-difference hit dangles armed (awaiting=true). That defect is genuine. BUT the finding's consequence (a) — the same-tick clobber where a difference hit supersedes an earlier armed fresh hit and a 'shared end-of-tick velocity event' ships the difference hit's non-sprint recompute — is infeasible. DeskRouter.onPlayerVelocity resolves on Bukkit's SYNCHRONOUS PlayerVelocityEvent, which vanilla fires inside the same damageEntity call right after that hit's EDBEE, before any later hit's EDBEE exists. There is no deferred/batched end-of-tick velocity event on the region path. So a fresh hit always resolves itself synchronously before any subsequent difference hit can clobber the pending; and when a difference hit dangles first, the next fresh melee replacePending()s it (line 327 resets awaiting=false) and re-arms/resolves itself correctly. For a connected victim in pure melee the dangling difference hit is harmlessly superseded every time — no non-sprint substitution reaches a legitimate hit's delivery. Consequence (b), the foreign-velocity-event hijack (DeliveryDesk:208-213 ships the stale formula, ignoring api velocity), IS a real bug, but it requires a non-melee velocity event (rod/explosion/plugin setVelocity) that is absent in the reported pure close-range w-tap/blockhit scenario, and it produces a SPURIOUS/overriding melee knock on that foreign event — extra/wrong knockback, the opposite direction from the reported 'less/no knockback'. Magnitude, had (a) fired, would be a ~0.5 u/tick horizontal loss (sprint ~0.9 → non-sprint ~0.4, roughly halved) which matches 'non-sprinting knockback' but not 'little to no' (never near-zero). Net: the underlying era divergence is real, but it does not plausibly produce the reported close-melee less-knockback experience.
- Corrections: The finding correctly identifies a genuine defect (KnockbackUnit:327-343 arms a genuine non-blocked mid-invuln difference hit that vanilla never knocks and fires no velocity event for — a real era divergence). It is WRONG about the symptom production. Consequence (a) 'same-tick clobber via a shared end-of-tick velocity event' does not exist: DeskRouter resolves on the synchronous Bukkit PlayerVelocityEvent that vanilla fires inside the same damageEntity call, so a fresh hit's delivery always resolves before any later difference hit can clobber the pending, and a dangling difference hit is harmlessly superseded (replacePending clears awaiting, line 327) by the next melee — no sprint→non-sprint substitution ever reaches a real player's legitimate hit. The only live consequence is (b), the foreign-velocity-event hijack, which requires a projectile/explosion/plugin setVelocity absent in the reported pure-melee scenario and produces spurious EXTRA knockback, not the reported weaker/no knockback. This finding should be treated as a real low-severity latent bug (fix: leave genuine non-blocked difference hits unarmed too, or gate arming on the live counter) but NOT as the cause of the owner's 'close-range sprint hits feel like non-sprint knockback' report.
- Severity: Near-zero in the reported scenario. Consequence (a) (the only one matching 'sprint feels like non-sprint', ~0.5 u/tick / ~50% horizontal-KB loss) is mechanically infeasible for connected players: synchronous per-hit PlayerVelocityEvent resolution means a fresh hit resolves before any later difference hit can clobber it, and a dangling difference hit is cleanly superseded (replacePending resets awaiting) by the next melee — expected frequency in real close-range PvP: 0. Consequence (b) fires only with a foreign velocity event (rod/explosion/plugin) in the dangle window — rare, kit-dependent (not pure sword/w-tap PvP), and it ADDS a spurious knock rather than weakening one, so it does not match 'victim doesn't move back'.

## `presend-marked-before-ship-outcome-discarded-valve-eats-only-copy` — merged as bug, sources: valve, transactions, registration-fallthrough

**Mechanism:** plan() commits tx.preSent BEFORE shipping the burst (HitRegistrationUnit.java:404-413) and DISCARDS BurstSender.ship()'s Outcome (:425-429; grep shows zero Outcome references in the unit). ship() catches ALL Throwables and returns UNSENDABLE having sent NOTHING (BurstSender.java:63-82) — its own contract says the caller must then pin, not account wire-delivered (:22-23); the caller only pre-checks the null-user case. On a ship failure the phantom-PRE_SENT tx is still submitFromWire'd, the authoritative pass ADOPTS it, resolve returns SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE (DeliveryDesk.java:186-194), and the ValveListener then CANCELS the tracker's ENTITY_VELOCITY — the ONLY copy that would ever have reached the client (ValveListener.java:49-58). Damage and flinch land; the victim receives ZERO velocity packets: total, silent, unrecoverable knock loss journaled as a healthy SHIP (wireCarried=true), invisible to the tester. Violates the codebase's own stated contract (netty-fast-path skill: a pre-delivered marker for an unsendable burst 'would let any non-PE-level suppression silently eat the victim's knockback'). Amplifier: BurstSender selects HURT_ANIMATION/BUNDLE wrappers by SERVER version (:42-44, :84-94), so pre-1.19.4 CLIENTS behind ViaVersion on a modern server depend on the PE-Via hand-off; if PE encodes at the client version the write throws and this fires on EVERY hit for that client. (Otherwise the legacy tier was verified clean registration-side.)

**Trigger:** Any PE write failure with a live user: victim mid-(re)configuration (1.20.2+ resource-pack/reconfigure window during combat), transient encode throw, user disappearing between the line-325 check and the line-427 ship, or potentially every hit on old-version clients via ViaVersion with bundle-feedback: true. Rare per-hit but each occurrence is a full no-KB hit.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:404-413, :425-429; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/BurstSender.java:22-23, :37, :42-44, :63-82, :84-94; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:186-201; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/ValveListener.java:40-58; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/HitTransaction.java:22-24 (the type-level guarantee covers only the null-user case); .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md (the violated contract); PacketTap.java:52-68 (legacy-clean verification).

**Maps to the report:** Literal 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback (the victim just doesnt really move back)' — the hit visibly lands (damage, flinch) with zero movement, unpinnable by the owner since the journal reads healthy. Frequency profile matches 'very subtle and hard to reproduce'.

**CODE lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap; re-verification dispatched)

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: The mechanism is real and I confirmed every link. plan() calls tx.preSent(shipped) at HitRegistrationUnit.java:409 BEFORE the ship, and senders.ship()'s Outcome is discarded (grep confirms zero Outcome references in the unit; only line 427 calls ship). BurstSender.ship() (63-82) catches all Throwables and returns UNSENDABLE having written nothing; there is no pin-fallback — the caller only pre-checks null-user via victimHasWire at 324-325. On a throw the phantom PRE_SENT tx is submitFromWire'd (430-432), resolve() branch 3 (DeliveryDesk 186-194) returns SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE, and ValveListener (49-58) cancels the vanilla re-emit — the ONLY velocity copy the client would receive, since the pre-send never left. Damage + hurt-animation land unvalved. Net: 100% velocity loss (horizontal + vertical), journaled as healthy SHIP wireCarried=true, invisible to the tester. So per-occurrence it genuinely produces "hit lands, victim doesn't move back."

Symptom match, however, is weak. The trigger — a PE write throw — is orthogonal to proximity, sprint state, w-tap, and block-hit. On matched modern client/server it fires essentially never in steady combat: only during the 1.20.2+ reconfigure/resource-pack window, a transient encode fault, or the sub-tick getUser→ship disconnect race. The report's distinctive hallmarks are NOT produced: (1) "especially when two players quite close together" — no proximity correlation whatsoever; (2) "seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback" — this bug yields ZERO knock, not a present-but-reduced non-sprint value; (3) "sprint hits with less than they should" — again reduced, not absent. The ViaVersion amplifier fires per-hit-per-client (constant, version-specific: "that one player never gets knocked"), which reads as noticeable and consistent, not "subtle/feeling." The only part it matches is the literal "little to no knockback / doesn't move back" and, via rarity, "hard to reproduce."

Per the instruction (refuted only if it CANNOT produce ANY part), it is not refuted — it can produce a rare total-no-KB hit. But it is a poor explanation for the owner's described feeling, whose heart is proximity-gated reduced (non-sprint-magnitude) knock. It's a real latent defect (violates the netty-fast-path contract) worth fixing independently; it just doesn't reproduce the reported symptom's signature.
- Corrections: Mechanism confirmed exactly as described (Outcome discarded; grep shows only the line-427 ship call, no Outcome references; no pin-fallback on throw). Two refinements to the SYMPTOM claim: (a) The loss is TOTAL and includes vertical, not "little" — the whole ENTITY_VELOCITY is valved, so the victim gets literally zero movement, not "non-sprinting knockback." The finding's own matches_report over-claims by aligning with "non-sprinting knockback" — that phrase implies a reduced-but-present value, which this bug does NOT produce. (b) The trigger has no proximity, sprint, w-tap, or block-hit correlation, so it cannot explain "especially when two players quite close together," which is the report's most concrete and load-bearing hallmark. Net: it explains at most a rare subset of pure no-KB hits, not the characteristic close-range reduced-knock feeling.
- Severity: Per occurrence: 100% velocity loss (full horizontal AND vertical — the entire ENTITY_VELOCITY packet is cancelled). Expected frequency in real close-range matched-version PvP between two sprinting/w-tapping players: ~0 per hit. It fires only on a PE write throw: the 1.20.2+ reconfigure/resource-pack window, a transient encode fault, or the sub-tick getUser(325)→ship(427) disconnect race — none proximity- or sprint-correlated. Materially non-zero (and near per-hit) ONLY for cross-version ViaVersion clients under bundle-feedback, but that is constant-per-client and version-specific (reads as "one player never gets knocked back"), not the subtle proximity-gated feeling reported. Poor frequency-profile match to the report.

## `legacy-resistance-roll-random-zero-knocks` — merged as config-dependent, sources: engine-math, desk-obligations, transactions, gates, registration-fallthrough

**Mechanism:** ResistancePolicy.LEGACY rolls all-or-nothing per hit: random.nextDouble() < victim.knockbackResistance() cancels the ENTIRE knock — the pre-send is suppressed on every hit for such victims ('resistance-roll' suppressor, hurt-only burst still ships so the victim flinches) and the authoritative resolve returns CANCEL_EVENT, so nothing ever reaches the wire. Era-authentic mechanic (1.8.9 rolled identically) but the era item pool had zero-resistance armor so it never fired; modern netherite grants 0.1 knockback resistance per piece — full netherite = 40% of ALL hits (sprint or plain) ship damage+flinch with literally ZERO movement, at random. Preset scoping (finders disagreed; the file evidence says): legacy-1.8 is the bundled preset shipping armor-resistance: legacy (Presets.java:46, legacy-1.8.yml:65, pinned by PresetsTest:35); legacy-1.7 and all fork presets ship NONE (KnockbackProfile.java:152; forks deliberately, per the skill) — two finders' claims that the legacy-1.7 DEFAULT carries it appear wrong, so verify the deployed profile's resistance policy directly. Side effect: any resistance>0 victim on a LEGACY profile also loses the pre-send on every hit, pushing all their knocks onto the degraded recompute path.

**Trigger:** Deployed profile = legacy-1.8 (or custom with resistance: legacy) AND victims wearing any knockback-resistance gear (netherite, attribute gear): ~resistance-fraction of hits produce no victim movement at all. One journal read (resistance-roll entries) confirms or excludes it.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:192-194, :448-453 (resistanceCancels); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:181-186 (null formula -> CANCEL_EVENT, journaled 'resistance-roll'); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:547-555 (pre-send suppressor); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java:28-46 (LEGACY_18 = ResistancePolicy.LEGACY) + KnockbackProfile.java:152 (LEGACY_17 NONE); core/src/main/resources/profiles/legacy-1.8.yml:65; core/src/main/resources/profiles/custom.yml:122-125; .claude/skills/knockback-profiles/SKILL.md:82-84 ('legacy randomizes zero-knocks on modern gear'); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:36-38.

**Maps to the report:** Verbatim 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback', random and unpinnable, 'as far back as I can remember' — IF the deployed profile is legacy-1.8/custom-legacy and players wear KB-resistant gear. Mechanism certain; relevance is a one-look config/loadout check.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: The code mechanism is fully confirmed and every refutation avenue failed.

CONFIRMED in code:
- KnockbackEngine.resistanceCancels (lines 448-453): `profile.resistance()==LEGACY && victim.knockbackResistance()>0.0 && random.nextDouble()<knockbackResistance` — a genuine all-or-nothing per-hit roll returning null (compute lines 192-194).
- DeliveryDesk.resolve (lines 181-186): null formula → suppressed("resistance-roll") + record + CANCEL_EVENT; nothing reaches the wire. Damage/hurt is a separate event, so flinch-without-movement is accurate.
- HitRegistrationUnit.suppressorFor (line 551): returns "resistance-roll" whenever resistance>0 on a LEGACY profile, so the netty pre-send is suppressed on EVERY hit for such a victim (not just the ~40% that cancel) — the side-effect claim is real.

PRESET SCOPING CONFIRMED (the finding's central disputed point): LEGACY_18 carries ResistancePolicy.LEGACY (Presets.java:46; legacy-1.8.yml:65 `armor-resistance: legacy`). LEGACY_17 = NONE (KnockbackProfile.java:152; legacy-1.7.yml:66 `armor-resistance: none`). CUSTOM inherits LEGACY_17.resistance()==NONE (Presets.java:276) and custom.yml ships `armor-resistance: none` by default — only a manual edit to `legacy` arms it. All fork presets (kohi/mmc/lunar/minehq/badlion/velt/signature) are NONE. The finding correctly rejects the other finders' claim that the legacy-1.7 DEFAULT carries it.

ATTRIBUTE-ALWAYS-ZERO refutation FAILED: SessionService.java:497-498 reads the live knockback_resistance attribute (clamp01, default 0.0) into the PlayerView, so a netherite-wearing victim has nonzero resistance and the roll genuinely fires. Not a dead path.

Classification "config-dependent" is right: firing requires BOTH the non-default legacy-1.8 profile (or a hand-edited custom set to `legacy`) AND victims wearing KB-resistance gear. The LEGACY policy faithfully reproduces the authentic 1.8.9 rule (P(no-knock)=resistance); it is not a code bug and not an era divergence — it is an opt-in knob that only bites because modern netherite grants resistance the 1.7/1.8 item pool never had.

HONEST CAVEAT ON USER-REPORT MATCH (the finding hedges this correctly, but it is the weakest link): the roll is DISTANCE-INDEPENDENT and SPRINT-INDEPENDENT and produces TOTAL-ZERO cancels. The user emphasizes (a) close proximity specifically and (b) a "non-sprinting knockback" feel = reduced-but-present, not zero. This mechanism explains neither the close-range specificity nor a reduced-magnitude feel; it produces random full cancels regardless of distance. At full netherite (~40% zero-knocks) it would be blatant, not the user's "subtle, hard-to-reproduce feeling." So it is a plausible-but-weak match unless the deployment is legacy-1.8 with light (1-piece) resistance gear. The finding does not overclaim — it explicitly reduces relevance to a one-look journal/config/loadout check.
- Corrections: Mechanism, preset scoping, and attribute population are all accurate — do not refute. Refinements: (1) custom.yml ships `armor-resistance: none` by default (verified), so custom fires ONLY after a manual edit to `legacy`; the sole bundled preset that arms it is legacy-1.8. (2) The default profile (legacy-1.7, parse(empty)==LEGACY_17) is NONE and can never trigger this — so "as far back as I can remember" only fits a user who has long run the legacy-1.8 preset. (3) Symptom-match is the weak point the finding rightly hedges: the roll is distance-independent and yields total-zero (not the user's reduced "non-sprinting knockback" at close range), and at full-netherite 40% it would be obvious rather than "subtle" — so this is best treated as a fast config/loadout exclusion (one journal read for `resistance-roll` entries), not a primary explanation of the close-range complaint. (4) "Degraded recompute path" is fair but mild — the region PlayerVelocityEvent path still ships the correct full stamp; it only loses the pre-send/latency-comp precision.
- Severity: In the gated scenario (deployed profile = legacy-1.8, or custom hand-set to `legacy`, AND victim wearing KB-resistance gear): horizontal KB loss is TOTAL (100% — full CANCEL_EVENT) on the rolled fraction of hits, which equals the victim's resistance: ~10% per netherite piece, ~40% full netherite. Distance- and sprint-independent. Secondary: EVERY hit against such a victim loses its netty pre-send (forced onto the region recompute), even the ~60% that ship. On the DEFAULT config (legacy-1.7) and all fork presets: frequency is ZERO — never fires. So real-world close-range PvP frequency is entirely deployment-gated: 0% on default, up to 40%-of-all-hits on legacy-1.8 + full netherite (which would be conspicuous, not the reported subtle feel).

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: The mechanism is real and correctly described. resistanceCancels (KnockbackEngine.java:448-453) rolls random.nextDouble() < victim.knockbackResistance() only when profile.resistance()==LEGACY AND resistance>0; on hit it returns Paced(null) → DeliveryDesk (181-185) emits CANCEL_EVENT + hurt-flinch, and HitRegistrationUnit (551-553) also suppresses the pre-send. So a firing produces a damage+flinch hit with literally ZERO shipped velocity.\n\nBut matching this to the report has four problems, three of them decisive:\n\n1) ALL-OR-NOTHING, not reduced. The report's core texture is graded: 'it seems like the knockback is the NON-SPRINTING knockback' and 'sprint hits sometimes have LESS knockback than they should.' That is reduced-but-present KB (a fresh-sprint-differential / conformal-scaling / registration-order symptom). The resistance roll ships EXACTLY ZERO or the full knock — it can never produce a 'this feels like the walk-knock instead of the sprint-knock' sensation. It matches only the narrow literal phrase 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback' (the 'no' branch), and even then as a total dead hit, not a weak one.\n\n2) NO distance sensitivity. The report's single strongest, most-repeated cue is 'ESPECIALLY when two players are quite close together.' resistanceCancels reads only profile + victim.knockbackResistance() + an RNG draw — it has no positional term whatsoever (distance() is computed elsewhere for taper, not consulted here). The mechanism fires identically at 1 block and 4 blocks. It cannot explain the close-range hallmark at all.\n\n3) LOADOUT + NON-DEFAULT-PROFILE gated. Firing requires BOTH (a) deployed profile == legacy-1.8 or a custom profile with resistance: legacy, and (b) the victim wearing knockback-resistance gear (netherite 0.1/pc, attribute gear). The shipped default and parse fallback is LEGACY_17 = ResistancePolicy.NONE (KnockbackProfile.java:152), so on the default config the roll is DEAD CODE — it never runs regardless of gear. The report says 'as far back as I can remember,' which points at default-config behavior, where this contributes nothing. The two finders who claimed the legacy-1.7 default carries the policy are wrong (verified: line 152 is NONE).\n\n4) FREQUENCY/SEVERITY PROFILE INVERTED. IF the stars align (legacy-1.8 profile + a full-netherite victim), the roll fires on 40% of ALL hits (resistance 0.4) as dead zero-movement hits. That is not subtle and not hard to reproduce — it is a glaring, trivially-pinnable 'armored players eat 2-in-5 hits' effect that anyone would immediately attribute to the armor. The report explicitly says 'very subtle and hard to reproduce, more like a feeling thing.' A random 40% total-cancel is the opposite of subtle. Even a single netherite piece (0.1 → 10% dead hits) would be a noticeable, gear-correlated pattern, not an unpinnable feeling.\n\nSo: real mechanism, but it explains at most one literal fragment ('little to no knockback') only under a non-default profile with modern resistance gear, and even there its texture (binary), its trigger (gear, not proximity), and its frequency signature (loud, gear-correlated) all contradict the report's defining features. Not fully refuted (it CAN zero out a hit), but a poor and heavily-gated fit that does not account for the close-range, graded, subtle character that defines the report.
- Corrections: Mechanism and code cites are accurate. Correction to the finding's own framing: the default deployed profile is legacy-1.7 = ResistancePolicy.NONE (KnockbackProfile.java:152), so on default config this is dead code — the finding's 'high confidence / mechanism certain' should be scoped to (legacy-1.8 or custom-legacy) + resistance-gear victims ONLY. Also: the roll is all-or-nothing (zero vs full), so it CANNOT be the source of the report's 'feels like the non-sprinting knockback' / 'sprint hits have less than they should' — those are graded reductions and point at a different mechanism (fresh-sprint differential, conformal scaling, or registration-order at close range). And the roll is distance-independent, so it cannot explain the report's central 'especially when close together' cue. The finding's own trigger note ('one journal read confirms or excludes it') is the right disposition: this is a cheap-to-exclude config/loadout check, not the close-range feeling bug.
- Severity: When it fires: 100% horizontal-KB loss (entire knock cancelled — base+sprint+extras all gone). Firing rate == victim's total knockbackResistance: full netherite 0.4 → 40% of hits, single piece 0.1 → 10%. Expected frequency in the REPORTED scenario (two sprinting/w-tapping players, close range, plausible deployed config): effectively 0%. On the default/fallback profile legacy-1.7 (ResistancePolicy.NONE) it never runs; it requires legacy-1.8 or custom resistance:legacy AND a resistance-gear victim, and it has zero distance sensitivity so it cannot produce the 'especially when close together' pattern at any rate.
