Where it CAN fire (legacy-1.8 + netherite victim), it is high-magnitude but loud and gear-pinnable — inconsistent with 'subtle, hard to reproduce, feeling thing.'

## `mid-invuln-difference-and-ignored-hits-era-real` — merged as era-real, sources: gates, era-truth

**Mechanism:** Era hurt-window rule (20 ticks): while hurtResistantTime > 10, a weaker-or-equal hit is FULLY ignored (no damage/knock/flinch/sound) and a STRONGER hit deals only the damage difference with ZERO knockback and no flinch. At 10+ CPS with equal weapons only every ~10th-tick click is a full hit (~80% of clicks produce no motion at all); damage-visible-but-no-knock needs an escalation inside the window — crit after normal (1.5x), rod-then-sword (rod arms the window at lastDamage=0 so the sword deals near-full damage with zero knock), weapon swap up. Mental reproduces it by construction: registration's frozen damageImmune skips the whole burst, the hit dispatches through vanilla's own difference branch, and the era-silent (blocked-shape) submit stays unarmed / vanilla fires no velocity event, so no knock ships (see the separate armed-pending bug for the non-blocked leak).

**Trigger:** Spam-cadence close trading on any version — most visible when a crit or rod precedes a sword hit inside 10 ticks: health drops, victim does not move. Frequent at 12-16 CPS where most clicks fall inside the window.

**Evidence:** docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:50-54 (branch 4), :64-67 ('A stronger hit mid-invuln deals difference damage with ZERO knockback'), :189-199 (rod arms the full window at 0 damage); SYNOPSIS.md:70-71, :442; docs/legacy-combat.md:74; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:334-336; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:227-253, :328-343; DeliveryDesk.java:312-317 (superseded journal).

**Maps to the report:** A legitimate, authentic slice of 'some hits have no knockback' in close-range spam: those hits deal damage but the era itself shipped no knock — must not be 'fixed'.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The era mechanism is accurately described and confirmed by ground truth. compendium §1.2 branch 4 (lines 51-53) and §3.1 (lines 194-200) confirm: mid-invuln (hurtResistantTime > 10) a weaker-or-equal hit is fully ignored; a stronger hit deals difference damage with fullHit=false → NO knockback, no flinch, no sound; a rod (0.0 damage) arms the full 20-tick window at lastDamage=0 so a following sword deals near-full difference damage with zero knock. All era-real. The vanilla 20-tick maximumNoDamageTicks window is present by default on every modern host, so Mental inherits it.\n\nCode faithfulness: Mental reproduces the difference-branch silence, but the finding slightly mischaracterizes HOW. It says the frozen damageImmune read "skips the whole burst" and the era-silent submit "stays unarmed." That is only true for the BLOCKED shape. The code (HitRegistrationUnit.java:238-253, 328-343) is explicit that the bare frozen immune read is NOT a discriminator on its own — it is a boundary snapshot that also flags legal boundary combo hits, so Mental deliberately ARMS the velocity event for every non-blocked hit including frozen-immune ones. Only eraSilentBlockedHit (blockedKnockShape && immune) stays unarmed. For a non-blocked crit-after-normal mid-invuln hit, the zero-knock comes from VANILLA's own difference branch firing no PlayerVelocityEvent (no markHurt) and the desk sweeping the unresolved await — not from Mental unarming. Net behavior matches the era; the causal path in the finding is imprecise. victimView.damageImmune() at line 335 only suppresses the netty PRE-SEND (leaves tx REGISTERED for the region recompute), it does not by itself withhold the knock.\n\nRelevance to the report: the mechanism is authentic but explains only the "victim doesn't really move / no motion at all" slice at spam cadence — which is standard, universally-known 1.8 combo timing that an experienced PvP plugin owner would not report as a mysterious subtle bug. It does NOT explain the report's actual emphasis: "seems like the knockback is the NON-SPRINTING knockback" and "sprint hits sometimes have LESS knockback than they should." The mid-invuln rule produces ZERO knock, never reduced/non-sprinting knock — reduced-magnitude KB points to a sprint-flag/arrival-order desync at close range, a different mechanism. So the finding is correct as an era-truth guardrail ("don't try to fix these no-motion hits") but is largely orthogonal to the specific feel the owner describes.
- Corrections: Two refinements. (1) The Mental reproduction path is mis-stated: the frozen damageImmune read does NOT unarm non-blocked mid-invuln hits — the code deliberately arms them (HitRegistrationUnit.java:328-343 comment) because the boundary snapshot also flags legal combo hits; the zero-knock for a non-blocked crit-after-normal comes from vanilla's own difference branch firing no PlayerVelocityEvent, which the desk sweep then drops. Only eraSilentBlockedHit (blockedKnockShape && immune) is explicitly left unarmed. (2) Scope: the finding is a valid don't-fix guardrail for the pure no-motion / difference-damage slice, but it does not account for the report's central complaint of REDUCED (non-sprinting-feeling) knockback on sprint and w-tap hits at close range, which is a distinct sprint-arrival/desync class, not the mid-invuln rule. Treat this finding as an era-truth boundary marker, not as the explanation of the reported bug.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss on affected clicks is total (100%, the hit is ignored or knock-silent) but by design — it is era-exact behavior, not a defect. Frequency: very high at 12-16 CPS equal-weapon spam (~80% of clicks fall inside the 10-tick half-window and produce no motion), but this is the desired era-authentic combo cadence, so the bug-severity is effectively zero. The escalation sub-case (crit/rod/weapon-swap-up inside 10 ticks yielding damage-visible-but-no-knock) is much rarer and also era-real. This does not overlap the report's "reduced/non-sprinting KB on sprint and w-tap hits" symptom, which is where real horizontal-KB loss for a genuine bug would live.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The mechanism is real and faithfully reproduced. The era hurt window (maxNoDamageTicks 20, mid-invuln check at >max/2) is confirmed in kernel (PlayerView.damageImmune = noDamageTicks > 11, +1 staleness allowance) and KnockbackUnit routes the era-silent difference hit through vanilla's own no-event path rather than fabricating a knock. So it DOES produce a genuine slice of "some hits have little/no knockback in close-range spam."

But I must split the report into its three claims and judge each against the mechanism:

(1) "some hits truly have little to no knockback / victim doesn't move back, especially close spam." The mechanism produces this abundantly — but almost entirely as the WEAKER-OR-EQUAL mid-invuln branch, which deals ZERO damage AND zero knock. At 12-16 CPS on one victim only ~1 click per 10 ticks (0.5s) lands fresh; the other ~5-6 are fully ignored no-ops. Crucially these produce no health drop, so an experienced 1.8 player (the reporter says "as far back as I can remember") reads them as "clicks that didn't register" — the fundamental invuln rhythm every 1.8 PvPer knows — NOT a mysterious knockback bug. So this bulk case matches the literal words but not the reporter's framing of it as a subtle unexplained BUG.

(2) The genuinely-confusing subset — damage visible but no knock — requires an ESCALATION inside the window (crit-after-normal, rod-then-sword, weapon swap up). This is the only part that truly reads as "health dropped, victim didn't move back" and could confuse even a veteran. But in pure sword-vs-sword close trading (the report's core scenario) escalations are incidental and low-frequency; rod→sword is a deliberate technique, not spam. So this subset is real and subtle but explains only a thin slice of a fight.

(3) The report's MOST DIAGNOSTIC detail — "the knockback seems like the NON-SPRINTING knockback" and "sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should" — describes a REDUCED-but-present knock at non-sprint magnitude. The mid-invuln mechanism produces ZERO base knock (a full no-op), not a reduced/non-sprint-magnitude knock. It therefore does NOT reproduce this component at all; that symptom points to a separate sprint-registration mechanism (SprintWire arrival-order/freshness), a different finding.

Net: the mechanism plausibly produces PART of the report (claims 1 and 2) and is era-authentic, so not refuted. But the finding's self-description ("~80% of clicks produce no motion at all") conflates the loud, well-understood no-damage invuln window with the confusing damage-but-no-knock case, overstating how much of the reporter's "feeling" it explains, and it does not touch the non-sprint-magnitude symptom which is the report's sharpest clue.
- Corrections: Two refinements. (a) The "~80% of clicks produce no motion" figure conflates two distinct outcomes: the WEAKER-OR-EQUAL mid-invuln branch (the bulk) produces NO DAMAGE at all — this is the ordinary invuln window every 1.8 PvPer already understands as "the click didn't register," not a knockback anomaly. Only the ESCALATION subset (stronger hit mid-invuln: crit-after-normal, rod-then-sword, weapon-swap-up) yields the confusing "health dropped but victim didn't move," and that subset is low-frequency in pure sword-vs-sword close trading. So the finding overstates how much of the reporter's subtle "feeling" it accounts for. (b) The mechanism ships ZERO base knock, i.e. a full no-op — it does NOT reproduce the report's most specific symptom ("seems like the NON-SPRINTING knockback" / "sprint hits with less knockback than they should"), which describes a reduced-but-present knock and belongs to a separate sprint-registration mechanism. Classification era-real and "must not be fixed" is correct; Mental's reproduction is faithful (frozen immune read is only a corroborator for the blocked-shape hit; non-blocked hits ride vanilla's own missing velocity event).
- Severity: Per affected hit: total horizontal-KB loss (0 b/t vs a full era knock ~0.4 base horizontal, or ~0.5-0.6 with the sprint extra) — but this is era-CORRECT, not a loss relative to era. Frequency: at 12-16 CPS on one victim ~5 of every 6 clicks fall inside the window, but the vast majority are zero-DAMAGE no-ops (the recognized invuln rhythm, not a bug). The genuinely "subtle, feeling" subset (damage visible, no knock) fires only when an escalation lands inside the 10-tick window — a handful of times per fight in incidental sword trading, more with deliberate rod/crit play. Matches the "subtle, hard to reproduce" texture for that thin escalation slice only; does not explain the non-sprint-magnitude component of the report.

## `ledger-vy-over-decay-zero-lift` — merged as bug, sources: ledger, desk-obligations

**Mechanism:** MotionLedger.current() free-falls the airborne vy by pure gravity/drag per tick (Decay.decay: vy=(vy-0.08)*0.98 toward the -3.92 terminal) while a real juggled client, re-lifted by each knock, hovers at -0.05..-0.34 (owner-measured live, 914 boxer hits). On combos=false presets nothing resets the decay clock (Deliveries.recordDelivered skips melee), so ticksSinceRecord grows 15-28 and ledgerVy reaches -0.96..-1.50; on combos=true divergence is bounded (~12 ticks) but a >~16-tick airborne gap still crosses -0.8. The ADD-mode vertical y = vy*friction.y + base.vertical then computes deeply negative, and the 2.4.8 bundle-wide verticalMin 0.0 floor clamps it to exactly 0.0 — the hit ships zero lift instead of the era's declining-but-positive combo vertical (~0.25): flight time collapses, flat shove, no pop. The floor traded the visible DOWNWARD leak for an invisible zero-lift under-ship; the diagnosed root (ledger vy diverging from measured reality) is still open (planned fix: measured-reality clamp max(ledgerVy, ringVy-0.15)).

**Trigger:** Victim airborne for several ticks mid-juggle (knocked, no Landing yet) when the next hit lands — juggle/wall pressure in close-range spam; especially mmc/lunar/legacy-1.8/velt/signature (combos=false), on legacy-1.7 only past ~16 airborne ticks.

**Evidence:** docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-ledger-vy-divergence.md (whole doc: verdict + trace table; missed-landing REFUTED); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:119-133; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/Decay.java:79-101; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/Deliveries.java:33-45 (combos gate; only shipped knocks re-seed); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:496-500, :527-529 (vy*friction+base, verticalMin floor); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/KnockbackProfile.java:137-145 (the 2.4.8 floor rationale naming this divergence).

**Maps to the report:** Directly explains 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback' for airborne/juggled victims at close range; already diagnosed live in the 2.4.8 round with a planned fix.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: The core mechanism is real and independently confirmed by both the code and the live-capture research doc (2026-07-07-ledger-vy-divergence.md). Trace verified end-to-end: captureVictim (EntityStates.java:78) reads ledger.current().vy() — the pure-gravity decayed estimate that free-falls toward -3.92 while a juggled client hovers at -0.05..-0.34; base() (KnockbackEngine.java:498-500) computes ADD-mode y = victimVy·friction.y + base.vertical; finish() (:527-529) floors at verticalMin; the floored presets carry verticalMin 0.0 (Presets.java 38/75/102/128/149/175 + LEGACY_17); Deliveries.recordDelivered (:33-45) skips melee when combos=false so nothing resets ticksSinceRecord. I tried to refute via the compensation path — CompensationQuery.verticalFor does NOT clamp to reality; it simulates the already-divergent baseVy forward and only escapes on clientOnGround / noDamageTicks>8 / predicted-landing, none of which save a never-landing wall-juggle victim (matching the doc's observed negative shippedVy). So the mechanism survives.

However the finding contains TWO factual errors in its affected set. (1) velt and signature are NOT floored: Presets.java:201 and :230 give them verticalMin=-3.9 (unfloored), and their friction.y=0.1 (lines 200/229) makes y=vy·0.1+~0.36 stay positive until vy<-3.6 (terminal) — they are essentially immune, a fact the 2.4.7 memory already recorded ('velt also immune, friction.y=0.1 immunity'). Listing them as zero-lift victims is wrong. (2) The default profile legacy-1.7 and the combos=true floored presets (kohi/minehq/badlion) are largely protected because combos=true resets the decay clock each melee (doc: legacy-1.7 worst ledgerVy -0.445, 0/127 downward). Hand-computing 12 airborne ticks from the +0.42 liftoff gives vy≈-0.51 — above the per-preset zero-crossing thresholds (legacy-1.8 -0.8, kohi -0.7, mmc/lunar -0.58, minehq -0.72, badlion -0.68). So the hard zero-lift bites mainly the combos=FALSE floored presets: legacy-1.8, mmc, lunar (lunar worst, base.vertical=0.44 but friction.y=0.7634 → crosses at -0.58). combos=true presets only cross via longer gaps or the secondary liftoff mis-stamp starting decay at -0.0784.

Classification: this is a genuine input-fidelity defect (ledger over-decay diverging from the real motY era servers used), already diagnosed live with a planned measured-reality-clamp fix — so 'bug', though it is fundamentally a divergence-from-era in the ledger estimate, and the zero-lift specifically is config-dependent (the 2.4.8 owner floor converting the downward leak into an under-ship). Match to the report: it explains 'little to no knockback / doesn't really move back' for juggled victims, but the direct effect is VERTICAL under-ship (~0.25 lost lift); it does NOT explain the user's 'feels like the non-sprinting knockback' horizontal-magnitude perception, which is a sprint-flag/horizontal-differential mechanism, not this one. The finding overreaches slightly in claiming it 'directly explains' the whole report.
- Corrections: Remove velt and signature from the affected/trigger list: both are UNFLOORED (verticalMin=-3.9, Presets.java:201/230) and friction.y=0.1 keeps their vertical positive until vy<-3.6 — they are immune, not victims. The hard zero-lift (y computed <0, hard-floored to exactly 0.0) reliably bites only the combos=FALSE floored presets: legacy-1.8, mmc, lunar. kohi/minehq/badlion are combos=TRUE floored presets, mostly protected by the per-hit decay-clock reset (~12-tick cap → vy≈-0.51, short of their -0.68..-0.72 crossing thresholds) except under the secondary liftoff mis-stamp. The DEFAULT profile (legacy-1.7, combos=true) showed 0/127 zero-lifts in the capture (worst -0.445), so on a stock server this bug is largely dormant; it manifests when the admin has selected a combos=false profile. Also distinguish two symptoms the finding merges: (a) the hard zero-lift (only when vy crosses the ~-0.58..-0.8 per-preset threshold), and (b) a broader unfloored under-ship (era +0.25 vs shipped e.g. +0.1) present at milder divergence regardless of the floor. The direct effect is vertical (lost lift/air-time); horizontal-push magnitude is unchanged.
- Severity: Direct effect: vertical under-ship of ~0.25 b/t of lift (era declining-but-positive combo vertical → shipped 0.0). No direct horizontal-push reduction — the horizontal knock value is untouched. Indirect horizontal-KB loss: the victim stays grounded (ground drag slip·0.91≈0.546 vs airborne 0.91) and loses ~5-6 ticks of air-carry, cutting total horizontal travel on an affected hit by roughly a few tenths of a block (~0.2-0.5 blocks), which reads as 'doesn't really move back.' Frequency: hard zero-lift ≈0.8% of hits (5/608) in a DELIBERATELY-staged wall juggle on legacy-1.8; effectively 0% in open-arena play where the victim lands between hits and the ledger resets (the doc's faithful control). Concentrated in sustained close-range corner/wall juggle spam — matching the owner's 'very subtle, hard to reproduce, more a feeling.' Only bites when a combos=false profile is configured; dormant on the stock legacy-1.7 default. Partial explanation of the report (juggle 'no pop / doesn't move back'); does NOT account for the 'feels like non-sprinting knockback' horizontal complaint.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: The mechanism is real and correctly traced, but it is a VERTICAL-only defect, and that distinction decides how much of the report it can explain.

WHAT IT ACTUALLY DOES. On ADD-mode presets y = vy·friction.y + base.vertical, floored at verticalMin. The ledger's vy free-falls during a sustained airborne stretch (toward −3.92) while the real juggled client hovers at −0.05..−0.34. For legacy-1.7/1.8 the ship goes negative only when ledger vy < −0.8; the 2.4.8 verticalMin 0.0 floor then clamps it to exactly 0.0 instead of the era-true +0.23..+0.375. The horizontal path x = vx·friction.x − pushX is completely untouched by this — the fresh directional push, INCLUDING the sprint bonus, ships at full magnitude. So a sprint hit that hits this bug still launches the victim horizontally at full sprint force; it just fails to pop them up.

CONSEQUENCE ON "MOVES BACK." Zero lift means the victim never leaves the ground, so its horizontal glide decays at ground drag (~0.546/tick on stone) instead of air drag (0.91/tick) for the ~8-10 airborne ticks a +0.3 lift would have bought. That roughly halves total displacement (~1.5-2 blocks with lift vs ~0.9 grounded) — a genuine ~0.5-1 block felt loss in a juggle. So it CAN produce part of "the victim doesn't really move back" — but as a shorter glide, not a weaker impulse.

WHAT IT DOES NOT EXPLAIN. The report's headline symptoms are HORIZONTAL: "feels like the non-sprinting knockback," "sprint hits with less knockback than they should." Non-sprint feel = missing horizontal sprint impulse. This mechanism leaves horizontal impulse fully intact, so it cannot make a sprint hit feel like a non-sprint hit. And the flat close-range trade the user describes ("two players quite close together," w-tap/blockhit) is exactly the OPEN-ARENA case the research doc found FAITHFUL — the victim lands each hit, the ledger resets, divergence stays small. The bug needs a sustained no-landing airborne stretch (wall juggle / pin), which is not the primary reported scenario.

FINDING OVERSTATES ITS TRIGGER SET. It lists mmc/lunar/legacy-1.8/velt/signature as affected. velt and signature are NOT floored to 0.0 — both carry verticalMin = −3.9, and their friction.y 0.1 puts the negative threshold at vy < −3.65 (near terminal, unreachable in a juggle). So the actual zero-lift set is only legacy-1.8, mmc, lunar (combos=false AND floored 0.0). legacy-1.7/kohi/minehq/badlion floor to 0.0 but reset every combo hit and never crossed −0.8 in the capture (0/127). The bundled default is legacy-1.7 → on a stock server this mechanism is essentially inert.

So: real bug, correctly diagnosed, but it accounts only for a narrow "combo drops / no pop / shorter glide" feel on three combos=false presets during wall/sustained-air juggles. It does not account for the flat-trade, sprint-feels-weak, close-range horizontal complaint that is the core of the report.
- Corrections: Two corrections to the finding. (1) Trigger set is wrong on velt/signature: both carry verticalMin = −3.9 (Limits(0.36, −3.9, −1.0)), so they are NOT floored to zero-lift — their friction.y 0.1 threshold (vy < −3.65) is unreachable in a juggle. The real zero-lift set is legacy-1.8, mmc, lunar (combos=false AND verticalMin 0.0); legacy-1.7/kohi/minehq/badlion floor to 0.0 but reset every combo hit and stayed positive (0 downward in the 914-hit capture). (2) Scope of match: the mechanism is vertical-only. It does NOT explain the report's horizontal core — "feels like non-sprinting knockback" and "sprint hits with less knockback" — because the horizontal impulse (including the sprint bonus) ships at full magnitude regardless. It explains only the "shorter glide / no pop / combo drops" felt-distance loss for a victim already airborne several ticks mid-juggle, on legacy-1.8/mmc/lunar, in wall/sustained-air situations — not the flat close-range trade (which the research doc found faithful) that the user emphasizes.
- Severity: Direct horizontal-velocity loss: 0 — the horizontal push (incl. sprint bonus) is untouched. Indirect displacement loss: ~0.5-1.0 block per affected hit, via collapsed air-time (victim grounds immediately, glides at ~0.546 ground drag instead of ~8-10 ticks of 0.91 air drag). Vertical loss vs era: ~0.23-0.375 (era-true +0.23..+0.375 → floored 0.0). Frequency in real close-range PvP between two sprinting/w-tapping players: effectively 0 on flat open ground (victim lands each hit → ledger resets → faithful) and 0 on the default legacy-1.7 preset; ~1-2% of hits ONLY in deliberately-sustained wall/pin juggles on combos=false floored presets (legacy-1.8/mmc/lunar — measured 5/608 downward, 12/608 >0.30 airborne divergence in a staged wall juggle); 0 on velt/signature (verticalMin −3.9, not floored). Matches "subtle/rare" but not the described flat close-range scenario or the horizontal sprint-feel symptom.

## `non-rising-liftoff-mis-stamp` — merged as bug, sources: ledger

**Mechanism:** GroundFsm.onMovement judges a grounded->airborne transition 'rising' by knownY > lastY (GroundFsm.java:87). A knock-induced liftoff whose first airborne sample reads non-rising (wall contact, small floored vertical, sampler phase) takes the ledge-step branch and stamps vy = groundedEquilibrium (-0.0784) instead of the 0.42 jump stamp (:101-104), so vy decay starts deep — the confirmed secondary accelerant of the over-decay finding. With the verticalMin 0.0 floor now shipping near-zero verticals, victims leave ground barely rising more often, feeding this branch — a self-reinforcing loop.

**Trigger:** A knocked victim whose first airborne movement packet shows no Y gain: pinned against a wall, or launched with a floored ~0 vertical — close-quarters scenarios.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/GroundFsm.java:87-104; docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-ledger-vy-divergence.md ('Non-rising liftoff mis-stamp — CONFIRMED secondary accelerant', exemplar 'APPLY LIFTOFF stampVy=-0.07840').

**Maps to the report:** Amplifies the weak-vertical hits of the over-decay finding in exactly the close-quarters scenarios the owner describes.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: CODE-CONFIRMED, real defect, but the finding overstates two specifics.

Core mechanism verified against source:
- GroundFsm.onMovement (kernel/.../wire/GroundFsm.java): rising = knownY > lastY at line 85 (finding cites :87, off by 2); the non-rising else-branch stamps jumpVy = Decay.groundedEquilibrium(gravity) = -0.0784 at lines 101-104 (matches). groundedEquilibrium = -gravity*0.98 = -0.0784 confirmed in Decay.java:64.
- MotionLedger.recordLiftoff (line 76-85) UNCONDITIONALLY sets this.vy = jumpVy and grounded=false. So a Liftoff clobbers the vy that record() (the knock) correctly wrote. No precedence/suppression.
- CombatSession.apply (line 242-243) drains every Liftoff → recordLiftoff, no guard against a knock-induced transition firing a Liftoff.
- Both feed paths share onMovement: the rim packet FSM AND SessionService.sampleGround (line 438-461) tick-sampler, which reads player.isOnGround()+location.getY() once per owning-thread tick. The reported exemplar came from the packetless sampler path (SimpleBoxer boxers are packetless per the doc).
- Empirically confirmed: research doc 2026-07-07-ledger-vy-divergence.md exemplar "APPLY LIFTOFF stampVy=-0.07840" → ledgerVy=-1.13946 vs measuredRingVy=-0.14371, and the doc's own fix list says "Also worth fixing... the non-rising liftoff mis-stamp." Marked there as a CONFIRMED secondary accelerant.

Could not refute the existence/unguarded-ness of the path. It is a genuine reconstruction defect: the jump-detector FSM cannot distinguish a knock-induced grounded->airborne transition from a player jump, and its non-rising guess (-0.0784) destroys the vertical residual, driving the ledger's free-fall deep (feeding the downward-ship / over-decay family).

Refutations of the OVERSTATED specifics:
1. The "instead of the 0.42 jump stamp" framing is imprecise. Neither branch is correct for a knock-liftoff — the correct vy is the knock's own recorded value (~+0.4, already in the ledger). Even the rising branch (0.42 + optional sprint push, recomputed horizontals) mildly corrupts a knock residual. The real defect is that a Liftoff fires AT ALL for a knock transition; the -0.0784 non-rising case is merely the severe instance.
2. The "verticalMin 0.0 floor ... shipping near-zero verticals ... self-reinforcing loop" claim is unsupported and arguably backwards. Verified in KnockbackEngine.java:381/527 and Presets.java:38: verticalMin is a FLOOR (y = max(y, 0.0)); it clamps would-be-negative verticals up to 0.0, it does NOT manufacture near-zero verticals, and it does not touch the standing-hit 0.36 vertical. A knock floored to exactly 0.0 gives zero upward velocity → the victim does NOT leave the ground → NO grounded->airborne edge → FEWER liftoffs, not more. So the floor does not "feed this branch"; the self-reinforcing-loop narrative is not supported by the code.

Relevance to the owner's report: this is a VERTICAL-residual corruption (vy set to -0.0784, grounded=false), NOT a direct horizontal-KB reduction. recordLiftoff applies the same one-tick launchDrag to the carried horizontals whether it stamps 0.42 or -0.0784, so the mis-stamp itself costs ~0 horizontal directly. Its effect on the owner's "victim doesn't move back" is INDIRECT: deep vy → downward-ship (y = vy*friction.y + base.v goes negative) → victim pinned into ground → subsequent combo hits find them grounded (ground drag 0.546 vs air 0.91) → faster horizontal decay. This matches the doc's own classification as a SECONDARY accelerant of the over-decay finding (the dominant mode), which is itself only loosely coupled to the horizontal complaint.

Classification: bug is correct — an implementation defect in Mental's own jump-detection reconstruction, not a faithful era mechanic. Era servers ticked the victim's real motY directly; there is no jump-stamp overwrite for a knocked victim.
- Corrections: Keep the core (real, unguarded, empirically confirmed) but correct two specifics: (1) Frame the defect as "a knock-induced grounded->airborne transition fires a Liftoff that clobbers the correctly-recorded knock vy (record() already holds ~+0.4); the non-rising branch's -0.0784 is the severe case" rather than "-0.0784 instead of the 0.42 jump stamp" — 0.42 is also wrong for a knock. (2) Drop/reverse the "verticalMin 0.0 floor feeds this branch, self-reinforcing loop" claim: verticalMin is a max(y,0.0) floor that only prevents downward ships; a floored-to-0.0 knock leaves the victim grounded (no liftoff edge), so the floor does not increase non-rising liftoffs. Also: line for the rising heuristic is GroundFsm.java:85, not :87. Reclassify the owner-relevance as an INDIRECT/vertical path (downward-pinning -> premature grounding -> ground-drag horizontal decay), consistent with the doc calling it a secondary accelerant of the dominant over-decay mode — not a direct horizontal-KB loss.
- Severity: Direct horizontal-KB loss from the mis-stamp itself: ~0 (recordLiftoff applies the same one-tick launchDrag to carried horizontals regardless of the vy it stamps; only the vertical residual is corrupted, by ~0.48 vy: -0.0784 stamped vs ~+0.4 true). Indirect horizontal loss via downward-pinning -> premature grounding -> ground drag (0.546) on the next combo hit vs air drag (0.91): a ~40% faster horizontal decay for the hits following a mis-stamp, but only when the cascade actually grounds the victim. Frequency: measured 5/608 downward-shipped hits on legacy-1.8 packetless boxers (~0.8%), 0/127 on legacy-1.7, concentrated in wall-juggle geometry; for REAL connected players on the packet path it is likely lower (a genuinely knocked-up client reports rising Y on its first airborne packet) except in wall-pin / floored-near-zero-vertical situations. Net: a real but SECONDARY, mostly-vertical accelerant; small and situational contribution to the owner's horizontal "little-to-no knockback" feel, dominated by the separate over-decay finding.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: MECHANISM (sanity-checked, real): GroundFsm.onMovement (kernel/.../wire/GroundFsm.java:85-104) judges a grounded->airborne transition "rising" by knownY > lastY. When a knock-induced liftoff's first airborne position sample reads non-rising, it takes the ledge-step branch and stamps jumpVy = groundedEquilibrium(gravity) = -0.08*0.98 = -0.0784 (Decay.java:64) instead of the +0.42 jump impulse, AND zeroes pushX/pushZ. The ledger then free-falls its vy from -0.0784 deep toward terminal. Live capture (docs/.../2026-07-07-ledger-vy-divergence.md:30-34, exemplar "APPLY LIFTOFF stampVy=-0.07840", ledgerVy=-1.13946) confirms this as a "CONFIRMED secondary accelerant" of the over-decay downward-knock family. This is authoritative live evidence, so the mechanism is real.

AXIS-COUPLING (the load-bearing question for THIS report): The report is about weak HORIZONTAL knockback ("victim just doesn't really move back", "non-sprinting knockback"). The mis-stamp corrupts only the VERTICAL vy input. I verified in KnockbackEngine.java that horizontal is decoupled: residualCarry (line 341-343) is built from victim.vx()/vz()*friction.x/z and is vy-INDEPENDENT; freshEra (line 340) is attacker-geometry only; victimVy enters ONLY shippedVertical (line 363-384, baseY = victimVy*friction.y + base.vertical). So the mis-stamp does NOT directly reduce the horizontal knockback impulse. Its route to a felt "doesn't move back" is INDIRECT: a deep-negative/floored-to-verticalMin shipped vy grounds the victim's client -> the victim then decays horizontal at ground drag 0.546 (Decay.java:82) instead of air drag 0.91, collapsing settle distance from ~2.99 blocks (stone airborne) to ~0.9 blocks (grounded geometric sum 0.4/(1-0.546)), a ~65-70% distance loss; and airHorizontal (line 339) drops from air().horizontal() to 1.0 on subsequent grounded hits. Direct horizontal effect (losing the victim's own 0.2 sprint-jump push from pushX/pushZ -> residualCarry) is minor and sign-ambiguous (for a victim sprinting toward the attacker, losing forward push slightly INCREASES net KB). So this is the SAME symptom pathway as the over-decay PRIMARY finding; this finding is a genuine but secondary accelerant of it.

DOES IT MATCH THE REPORT? Partially. It plausibly produces the "little to no knockback / doesn't move back, especially two players close together" facet via grounding the victim. It does NOT explain the "sprint hit reads as non-sprint" / sprint-differential facet — that is attacker-side sprint bonus (KnockbackEngine.java:330-337, driven by attacker sprintLevels/pace), entirely unrelated to victim vy. So it covers the vertical-suppression half of the report, not the sprint-attribution half.

FREQUENCY: Low and close-range-concentrated. In the 914-hit live capture, only 5/608 legacy-1.8 hits shipped downward AT ALL, and the mis-stamp is a SUBSET accelerant within that class; 0/127 on legacy-1.7 (combos=true keeps resetting the decay clock). Trigger requires a grounded->airborne transition whose FIRST airborne sample reads non-rising: wall-pin, floored ~0 vertical, or sampler-phase noise — i.e. close-quarters juggles where the victim is kept airborne against a wall or barely leaves the ground. Open-arena combos are documented FAITHFUL (victim lands between hits, ledger resets). The self-reinforcing-loop claim (verticalMin 0.0 -> barely-rising liftoffs -> more non-rising reads) is plausible but second-order. This sub-1% frequency, concentrated exactly in the "two players close together" pocket the owner names, with an intermittent "sometimes weak" character, matches the "subtle, hard to reproduce, feeling thing" description well.

NET: Not refuted. Real confirmed bug that produces PART of the reported experience (the close-range weak-knock "doesn't move back" feel) at a frequency profile that fits "subtle/hard to reproduce". But it is a secondary accelerant of the over-decay primary (they share the grounding pathway), its horizontal effect is entirely indirect, and it does not account for the sprint-attribution facet.
- Corrections: Two corrections to the finding's framing: (1) The mis-stamp has ZERO direct effect on horizontal knockback — verified in KnockbackEngine.java that residualCarry/freshEra are vy-independent and victimVy feeds only shippedVertical. Its contribution to the reported HORIZONTAL "doesn't move back" symptom is entirely indirect (a downward/floored shipped vy grounds the victim, who then bleeds horizontal at ground drag 0.546 vs air 0.91 and loses the air-horizontal multiplier on follow-ups). So it is the SAME symptom pathway as the over-decay primary, i.e. an accelerant of it, not an independent cause. (2) It does not explain the report's "sprint hit reads as non-sprint" facet, which is attacker-side sprint-bonus territory, unrelated to victim vy. The finding's own "secondary accelerant" language is correct; the matches_report line should be scoped to the vertical-suppression half of the report only.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss WHEN it fires: large but indirect — the corrupted vy carries no horizontal impulse itself, but grounding the victim collapses settle distance ~2.99 -> ~0.9 blocks (~65-70%), reading as "barely moves back". Direct horizontal loss (victim's 0.2 sprint-jump push dropped from residual) is negligible/sign-ambiguous. Frequency in real close-range PvP: sub-1% of hits (live: <=5/608 legacy-1.8 downward total, of which this is a subset; 0/127 legacy-1.7), concentrated in wall-pin / floored-vertical close-quarters juggles, near-zero in open arena. Intermittent, close-range-clustered, "sometimes weak" — a good match for "subtle, hard to reproduce, feeling thing, especially when two players close together", but only the vertical-suppression half of the report and only as a secondary accelerant of the over-decay primary.

## `suppressed-or-fallthrough-hits-take-degraded-recompute-path` — merged as divergence-from-era, sources: gates, registration-fallthrough, ledger, transactions

**Mechanism:** Only the netty pre-send honors the era boundary read (frozen PlayerView: end-of-previous-tick ledger residual + frozen grounded + ring positions). Whenever a hit misses the pre-send it is recomputed at the EDBEE 1-2 ticks later from EntityStates.captureVictim: ledger.current() LIVE (1-2 extra decay steps, x0.546/step grounded), LIVE isOnGround (a same-tick landing flips friction air 0.91 -> ground 0.546 and re-stamps the grounded 0.3608 vertical — the exact within-tick ordering the era contract forbids), and LIVE positions. The paced-out/suppressed hit therefore ships measurably weaker horizontal (or floatier vertical) than its pre-sent neighbours, one tick later on the wire. Suppression/fallthrough sources: (1) AnticheatMode.AUTO (default) with GrimAC/Vulcan present suppresses ALL velocity pre-sends permanently — every knock takes this path (silent except one boot log line); (2) FeedbackGate pace-outs: the 450ms auto window vs 500ms legal cadence means jitter-compressed gaps, 2v1 (per-victim budget), or Folia +-1 skew pace out real combo hits — the full knock still ships via the authoritative event (verified: no magnitude suppression leak), just late and recompute-flavored; (3) resistance-roll and frozen-immune-view hits vanilla accepts; (4) stale-view fallthroughs (view null or >4 ticks old — respawn/chunk-reload transient-invalidity windows, Folia region lag): the packet is NOT cancelled, but for sessioned player victims the classic 'vanilla 0.7 sprint KB leak' does NOT exist — vanilla's attack fires EDBEE, KnockbackUnit recomputes the era vector and DeskRouter overwrites the event; what IS lost: the arrival-order SprintWire verdict (live isSprinting read; freshSprint=false), the boundary read, the pre-send, and vanilla's 1.9+ cooldown-scaled damage applies (tiny on spam — reads as 'that hit did nothing'). Pure vanilla KB only when session==null (rare post-2.4.4). These hits are unjournaled/undebugged, making the symptom undiagnosable. Two finders' claims that fallthrough ships vanilla (0.7,0.4) directly were refuted by the deeper trace.

**Trigger:** Systematic if GrimAC/Vulcan is installed (anticheat.mode: auto default) — a plausible root of 'as far back as I can remember' if the owner's servers historically ran one; per-hit under jitter pace-outs, 2v1, Folia skew; clustered after respawns/lag spikes for stale-view fallthroughs; always for server-side (Vanilla-source) melee.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:260-286 (fallthrough branches, no cancel), :334-336, :392-434 (pacing; shipBurst), :398-402 (450ms auto), :466-474 (frozen boundary read); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/FeedbackGate.java:24-35; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:163-165, :255-297, :365-371; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/EntityStates.java:73-85; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:118-133; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/model/PlayerView.java:139-144; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:253-296 (respawn window); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/AnticheatSettings.java:13-14; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/coexist/AnticheatPolicy.java:20-40; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/DamageRouter.java:53-68; HitRegistrationPacingTest.java; .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md:272-284 (the boundary contract this path skips); .claude/skills/era-accuracy (era 0.9 vs modern 0.7 reference).

**Maps to the report:** 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should': the same swing ships two different vectors depending on which path delivered it, and the suppressed path is systematically the weaker/later one — subtle, non-reproducible, feel-level; anticheat presence would make it universal and historical.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Verified against KnockbackUnit.java, HitRegistrationUnit.java, EntityStates.java, MotionLedger.java, FeedbackGate.java, DeliveryDesk.java, AnticheatSettings/Policy, and the netty-fast-path boundary contract.

The finding's architectural skeleton is accurate: PRE_SENT/PINNED hits adopt the frozen pre-send vector (KnockbackUnit:256-268), while REGISTERED hits (pre-send suppressed by anticheat/resistance, or the whole hit fell through to Vanilla source) recompute at EDBEE via EntityStates.captureVictim, which reads ledger.current() decayed-to-now and player.isOnGround() LIVE (EntityStates:73-85). AnticheatMode.AUTO is the default and GrimAC/Vulcan are in the known-plugins list (AnticheatSettings:13), so with either present suppressorFor returns "anticheat" and every pre-send is suppressed. The pacing gate paces the wire burst only; the authoritative pass ships full magnitude (FeedbackGate javadoc; DeliveryDesk:209 'ship the formula, no valve'). So the finding's own concession 'no magnitude suppression leak' is correct.

But the finding's CAUSAL claim — that this path explains the user's 'non-sprinting knockback / victim doesn't move back / sprint hits sometimes weaker' — is refuted on three counts:

(1) The sprint verdict is NOT lost on the anticheat/pacing recompute path. For HitSource.Melee, attackerSprinting reads tx.context().sprint().sprinting() and freshSprint reads tx.context().sprint().fresh() (KnockbackUnit:273-274, 365-371) — the arrival-order SprintWire verdict stamped by the fast path's sprintVerdict(), NOT a live read. The live isSprinting / freshSprint=false read the finding invokes applies ONLY to the pure Vanilla-source fallthrough (session view null/stale — a rare respawn/chunk transient), which the finding acknowledges then conflates into its 'systematic if anticheat installed' headline. So scenarios (1) and (2) preserve the sprint bonus and cannot produce 'non-sprinting knockback'.

(2) Direction and magnitude don't match the symptom. The legacy horizontal knock component (dx/dist·strength) is fixed, independent of victim residual; the residual contributes only the halved carry, and for a fresh hit the residual is ~0 (grounded equilibrium), so the two paths AGREE — no horizontal weakening. The one genuine divergence is the LIVE grounded flag: for a boundary combo hit where the victim lands within the tick, captureVictim's player.isOnGround()=true selects the grounded 0.3608 vertical where the era ordering (attack processed before same-tick movement) ships the pre-landing ~0.25 (documented in netty-fast-path SKILL boundary contract). That makes the hit FLOATIER, the opposite of 'victim just doesn't really move back'.

(3) Scenario (1) is uniform, not intermittent. If anticheat suppresses ALL pre-sends, every hit consistently takes the recompute path (sprint intact, full magnitude) — not the 'some hits, subtle, feel-level' inconsistency the report describes.

(4) 'Degraded recompute' inverts authority: the region EDBEE recompute is the authoritative era computation (vanilla applies KB during attack processing); the pre-send is the latency-compensation prediction. Reading state closer to attack time is more accurate, not degraded — except for the one grounded-flag ordering concern.

So the finding AS STATED (weaker horizontal, non-sprint feel, matches the user's report) is wrong. What survives is a narrow, real, config-gated era divergence: suppressed/paced-out boundary combo hits can ship a floatier vertical via the live grounded flag. That is genuinely divergence-from-era but gated by anticheat presence (or pacing/2v1/Folia skew) AND a same-tick landing, and it is the wrong symptom direction for this report.
- Corrections: The finding's central causal claim is wrong: the recompute path does NOT strip the sprint bonus (it carries tx.context().sprint(), the arrival-order verdict, via attackerSprinting/freshSprint — KnockbackUnit:273-274,365-371), and it does NOT weaken horizontal KB (the knock component is residual-independent; a fresh hit's residual is ~0 so both paths agree; DeliveryDesk:209 ships the full formula). The 'weaker horizontal / non-sprinting knockback / doesn't move back' symptom match is unsupported.

What is actually TRUE and survives: for hits whose netty pre-send is suppressed (anticheat AUTO+Grim/Vulcan default, or resistance roll) OR paced out (2v1, jitter, Folia skew) OR that fell through to Vanilla source, the authoritative region recompute uses EntityStates.captureVictim, reading player.isOnGround() LIVE. For a boundary combo hit that lands within the EDBEE tick (which runs 1-2 ticks after the cancelled attack), that live grounded=true selects the grounded 0.3608 vertical where the era ordering ships the pre-landing ~0.25 (the exact same-tick-landing invisibility the netty-fast-path boundary contract names, honored by the frozen pre-send view but NOT re-honored on the region path's captureVictim). Net effect: a FLOATIER vertical on suppressed/paced boundary landings — a genuine but narrow divergence-from-era, opposite in direction to the user's report. The only sprint-verdict loss (live isSprinting, freshSprint=false) is confined to the true Vanilla-source fallthrough (session null/stale), a rare transient, not the anticheat-systematic case.
- Severity: Horizontal KB loss for the user's reported symptom: ~0 (knock component is residual-independent; fresh-hit residual ~0; sprint bonus carried; full formula shipped). The single genuine divergence is vertical: up to ~0.11 floatier (0.3608 grounded vs ~0.25 pre-landing) on a same-tick-landing boundary combo hit, and only when the pre-send is suppressed/paced. Frequency in real close-range PvP: requires (anticheat installed OR pacing/2v1/Folia skew) AND a boundary combo hit landing within the deferred-EDBEE tick — uncommon, and produces MORE vertical, not the 'no knockback' feel. Severity for the reported symptom: LOW/effectively nil. Severity of the surviving narrow vertical divergence: LOW, config-gated.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Traced both delivery paths and the knockback math end-to-end. The finding correctly identifies that a suppressed pre-send is recomputed at the EDBEE from EntityStates.captureVictim (ledger.current() LIVE + live isOnGround), 1-2 ticks staler than the frozen PlayerView the adopted pre-sends use — so the same swing can ship two different vectors. That divergence is real.

But the finding conflates two very different consequences:
- Residual over-decay (all Melee-source suppression cases): a small horizontal loss (0.5·Δvx), ~0.09-0.14 b/t only when the victim is moving away, zero for a standing victim, and even a GAIN when the victim moves toward the attacker. Sprint bonus fully preserved (verdict from the wire, freshSprint from tx). This is the systematic-under-anticheat case.
- Sprint-bonus loss (Vanilla-source stale-view fallthrough only): freshSprint=false + live-sprint-race can drop the sprint bonus outright → true non-sprint knockback. But this only fires when the view is null/>4 ticks stale (respawn/chunk/region-lag), which is rare and not proximity-coupled.

The report's most concrete claim ("close together → feels like non-sprinting knockback") maps to LOSING THE SPRINT BONUS, which the common/systematic path preserves. The path that loses it is rare and not close-range-specific. So the finding's matches_report justification ("anticheat presence would make it universal and historical") is wrong on the mechanism: universal anticheat suppression preserves the bonus and yields only the ~10% residual wobble, not a non-sprint feel.

I verified against source, not guesses: HitRegistrationUnit.java (:270-306 cancel/return branches, :367 verdict, :466-474 frozen victim read), KnockbackUnit.java (:271 captureVictim, :273 freshSprint gate, :370 live sprint), EntityStates.java (:73-85 live ledger read), KnockbackEngine.java (base :462-516, air-multiplier identity), Presets.java (:29-46 legacy profile constants), AnticheatCompatUnit.java (:83-91 AUTO = suppress iff detected), FeedbackGate.java (pace window). Math is hand-computed from friction 0.5 and grounded drag 0.546.

Not refuted because the mechanism does produce a genuine, if mild, part of the report (the "sprint hits sometimes weaker, feel-level, non-reproducible" strand during juggles, and a real path inconsistency). But severity is low and the headline symptom is largely unexplained here.
- Corrections: The mechanism is real but its match to the report is much narrower than stated, and the headline symptom ("close-range → non-sprinting knockback") is essentially NOT produced by this path.

(1) Sprint bonus is NOT lost on the common suppression sources. For anticheat AUTO, FeedbackGate pace-outs, and resistance-roll the packet is still cancelled (HitRegistrationUnit:306), so the transaction is Melee-source: KnockbackUnit reads the arrival-order SprintWire verdict from tx.context().sprint() (:367) and freshSprint from tx.context().sprint().fresh() (:273). The full sprint/w-tap bonus is preserved. These paths therefore CANNOT produce "feels like the non-sprinting knockback" — they only diverge in the over-decayed residual term.

(2) The only sub-case that loses the sprint bonus is the Vanilla-source stale-view fallthrough (view null/stale at :270-273, packet NOT cancelled → vanilla attack runs → source is Vanilla, freshSprint forced false at :273, sprinting read live at :370, race-losable). This genuinely can ship non-sprint knockback, but it fires only in respawn/chunk-load/region-lag transient windows — rare and clustered, NOT "especially when two players are close together." The finding's own trigger list admits this.

(3) What the recompute path actually costs for the common (Melee-source) cases is only the residual-decay divergence: engine air multipliers are identity for the default legacy profile (Presets air=Push(1.0,1.0)), so victim.grounded() has no direct engine effect and the whole divergence is 0.5·(vx_frozen − vx_live) horizontally. Magnitude: 0 when the victim stands still; ~0.09 b/t at 1 tick stale, ~0.14 b/t at 2 ticks for a victim carrying a ~0.4 away-residual (roughly 5-13% of a sprint hit's horizontal). Crucially the SIGN can flip to a GAIN when the victim's residual points toward the attacker — the exact close-range w-tap-into-each-other geometry the report describes — so "systematically weaker at close range" is not even reliably the direction.

(4) The "systematic/historical/as-far-back-as-I-remember" framing is entirely contingent on the owner running GrimAC/Vulcan (anticheat.mode AUTO). No evidence in project memory that production runs Grim/Vulcan. And even under Grim/Vulcan the effect is ONLY the subtle residual divergence, never the sprint-bonus loss — so it still would not read as "non-sprinting knockback."

Net: this is a genuine divergence-from-era (suppressed hits ship a 1-2-tick-over-decayed residual vs the frozen boundary read the adopted pre-sends use, an inconsistency between two delivery paths for the same swing), and it can plausibly contribute the mild "sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should" feel during high-CPS juggles where pace-outs interleave frozen and live vectors. It does NOT explain the report's core "close-range non-sprinting knockback" symptom, which points at the SprintWire/close-range verdict domain, not this recompute path.
- Severity: LOW. Horizontal KB loss on suppressed Melee-source hits: 0 for a standing victim; ~0.09 b/t (1 tick stale) to ~0.14 b/t (2 ticks) for a victim carrying a ~0.4 away-residual — roughly 5-13% of a sprint hit's horizontal, and the sign can flip to a small GAIN when the victim moves toward the attacker (the close-range w-tap case). Vertical divergence ~0.05-0.09 b/t. Frequency without GrimAC/Vulcan: only FeedbackGate pace-outs (a fraction of >2.2 CPS combo hits) plus rare respawn/lag stale-view hits — so intermittent, juggle-only. With anticheat AUTO + Grim/Vulcan installed: EVERY hit takes the recompute path, so the residual wobble becomes systematic, but the sprint BONUS is still preserved, so it never reads as non-sprint KB. The sprint-bonus-losing sub-case (Vanilla-source stale-view) is rare and clustered (respawn/chunk/region-lag), well under ~1% of close-range exchanges and not proximity-coupled. Expected contribution to the reported experience: a mild, occasional "that combo hit felt a touch weaker" during hard juggles — plausible but minor; it does NOT account for the primary "close-range non-sprinting knockback" complaint.

## `frozen-immune-band-fate-unresolved` — merged as unknown, sources: gates

**Mechanism:** The +1 staleness allowance admits frozen noDamageTicks <= max/2+1 (11) for pre-send; a click at frozen exactly 12 is denied the pre-send but still dispatched. Whether vanilla accepts it depends on the intra-tick order of the deferred damage task vs the victim's noDamageTicks decrement: task-before-decrement reads 11 and rejects era-consistently; task-after-decrement reads 10 and ACCEPTS — and at 12-16 CPS the first legal click lands in the frozen-12 tick roughly as often as frozen-11, so up to ~half of all spam-cadence combo hits would silently take the never-pre-sent degraded recompute path. The repo pins admitted=>accepted but nothing pins the frozen-12 band's fate; the finder flags it as the single highest-leverage unknown for persistent subtle combo weakness across versions (Paper vs Folia scheduler ordering may differ).

**Trigger:** Spam-cadence (12-16+ CPS) combo hits whose first post-window click lands in the tick where the frozen view still reads max/2+2 — roughly a coin-flip phase event per combo hit. Needs a live probe (journal paceFactor/source vs pre-send counts at pinned cadence) to resolve.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/model/PlayerView.java:129-136 (damageImmune = noDamageTicks > max/2+1); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:334-336 (immune skips pre-send only), :436-449 (dispatch always schedules damage); .claude/skills/era-accuracy boundary-contracts (gap-9 spam pin covers only admitted hits).

**Maps to the report:** If the accept-after-decrement ordering holds anywhere in the support range, a large share of close-range combo hits ship the recompute-path knock — the strongest candidate for a persistent, subtle 'combo hits weaker than they should be' across versions.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The finding's central premise — that a hit denied the pre-send takes a "degraded recompute path" shipping a weaker knock — is false. I traced the full delivery chain:

1. When `victimView.damageImmune()` is true (frozen noDamageTicks >= max/2+2, i.e. >= 12 for max=20), `plan()` returns the tx REGISTERED with no pre-send (HitRegistrationUnit.java:334-337). `dispatch()` still schedules `applyPlayer` → `damageWithSlot` → `victim.damage(composedAmount, attacker)` on the victim's region thread.

2. Before that damage call, `damageWithSlot` (line 690) sets `session.activeInbound(tx)`. The DamageRouter promotes it to `currentEventTransaction`, and KnockbackUnit's EDBEE handler (line 167) picks it up. Because `tx.state()` is REGISTERED (not PRE_SENT/PINNED), it falls through the adopt branch (lines 256-268) into the recompute branch (lines 270-345): `KnockbackEngine.computePaced(attackerState, victimState, ...)` off the LIVE MotionLedger, then `desk.submit(tx, vector)` + `desk.awaitVelocityEvent(tx)`.

This recompute path is the AUTHORITATIVE full-stamp path — the SAME engine (`KnockbackEngine.computePaced`) and the same base+sprint era vector the pre-send would have carried. It is not "degraded." The pre-send is purely a latency-compensation optimization (ships the knock early via a wire burst); skipping it shifts delivery to the normal PlayerVelocityEvent timing (~ping/2 later for a laggy attacker) but never reduces magnitude.

3. The sprint bonus is determined by the attacker's SprintVerdict (`freshSprint`/`sprinting`), computed identically in both the pre-send (line 365) and the recompute (lines 273-274). It has ZERO dependence on the immune band. So the finding cannot explain the user's "reads as non-sprinting knockback" symptom — the immune band gates pre-send eligibility, not the sprint-bonus magnitude.

4. The frozen-12 band's fate is actually well-defined and era-correct regardless of the intra-tick decrement ordering the finding frets over:
   - If vanilla's live read accepts (<= max/2): vanilla fires PlayerVelocityEvent, KnockbackUnit recomputes and ships the FULL era knock.
   - If vanilla's live read rejects (> max/2, a difference hit): no velocity event, no knock — which is era-CORRECT (compendium/era-accuracy: a stronger mid-invuln hit deals difference damage with NO knock and no flinch; KnockbackUnit.java:224-253 and 328-343 encode exactly this, deliberately arming the desk for every non-blocked hit and only leaving the era-silent BLOCKED difference hit unarmed).
   Both branches are era-faithful; neither loses a knock the era would have shipped.

5. The immune band itself is affirmatively era-real: the era-accuracy skill pins "the +1 staleness allowance in the view's immune check" as the era-faithful mechanism for boundary combo hits, and PlayerView.java:129-136's javadoc matches. KnockbackUnit.java:564-572 explicitly documents that the frozen immune read is only ever a discriminator when CORROBORATED by the blocked event shape and "never gate a non-blocked hit's delivery on it alone" — precisely to avoid dropping the very hits the finding worries about (the 1.9.4 second-regression they cite as prior art was the bug of unarming on the bare read; it was fixed exactly this way).

The user's real close-range "weak knock" report is separately and fully explained by era-real geometry (era-accuracy: base 0.4 pushes from the attacker's POSITION, sprint 0.5 along the attacker's YAW; a face-hug victim past the attacker gets ~0.05h — "era-real, identical on actual 1.7.10"), not by this immune band.
- Corrections: The frozen-12 band's fate is NOT an "unresolved highest-leverage unknown." It is resolved and era-correct by construction: (a) if vanilla accepts the hit at its live counter, KnockbackUnit's REGISTERED branch recomputes the full era vector from the live MotionLedger and ships it via desk.submit + awaitVelocityEvent (KnockbackUnit.java:270-345) — the same magnitude the pre-send would carry, not a "degraded" one; (b) if vanilla rejects it as a difference hit, withholding the knock is era-faithful (no knock, no flinch). There is no path here where a hit that vanilla knocks in full loses its knock — that specific regression existed once (unarming on the bare frozen read, the 1.9.4 second-regression) and was deliberately fixed by arming every non-blocked hit and leaving only the corroborated era-silent BLOCKED difference hit unarmed (lines 328-343). A live probe would confirm full paceFactor/full-vector ships on frozen-12 accepts, but it is not needed to resolve a correctness risk — there is none. The finding also misattributes the user's symptom: the immune band has no influence on the sprint-vs-non-sprint magnitude.
- Severity: Zero horizontal-KB loss attributable to this finding. The immune band gates only pre-send (latency-compensation) eligibility; a denied hit still ships the FULL era vector via the authoritative region recompute whenever vanilla accepts it, and withholds the knock only for era-silent difference hits (correct). The sprint bonus is decided by the SprintVerdict independently of the band, so the finding cannot produce a "non-sprinting knockback" outcome. Expected real-PvP frequency of a Mental-caused KB reduction from this path: nil.

**SYMPTOM lens: REFUTED** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The finding conflates "hit took the non-pre-sent (region recompute) path" with "hit shipped weaker knockback." Code refutes that link. On the non-pre-sent path, applyPlayer→damageWithSlot calls victim.damage(composedAmount) (HitRegistrationUnit.java:687-698), which fires vanilla knockback→PlayerVelocityEvent, which KnockbackUnit overwrites with the FULL computed era vector via victim.setVelocity (KnockbackUnit.java:543-546). The immune-read on the frozen boundary view is explicitly documented as a pre-send discriminator only, NOT a magnitude truth: "a legal boundary combo hit — accepted and knocked in full by vanilla's LIVE read — can still read immune here" (KnockbackUnit.java:564-572). So a hit that skips the pre-send because damageImmune() (PlayerView.java:134-135) reads true is knocked at full magnitude on the region path — it only arrives ~1 RTT later. The pre-send is a latency optimization, not a magnitude source; the recompute is not "degraded."\n\nThe two possible fates of the frozen-12 band are: (a) vanilla's live noDamageTicks is still >max/2 when the deferred task runs → victim.damage() rejects entirely → zero knockback, which is exactly era-correct vanilla immunity (a click inside the hurt window legitimately produces no knock, and under the 1-tick-stale model frozen-view=12 ≈ live=11, genuinely still immune); or (b) live counter has decremented ≤10 → vanilla accepts → full-magnitude knock via the velocity event. Neither branch produces a weaker-but-nonzero knockback, and neither drops sprint scaling (this mechanism never touches sprint detection, so it cannot make a sprint hit read as non-sprinting). The report's "non-sprinting knockback" and "sprint hits with less knockback than they should" are therefore unreachable by this mechanism. The only report fragment it touches — "little to no knockback, victim doesn't move back" — is reachable solely via branch (a), which is era-faithful immunity, not a divergence. The finding's own classification is 'unknown' and it asks for a live probe; as a symptom producer for the weak-knockback feeling, it is refuted.
- Corrections: The frozen-12 band governs only whether the netty pre-send fires (a latency optimization), not knockback magnitude. When such a hit lands, it lands at full magnitude via the region recompute path (KnockbackUnit velocity-event handler overwrites vanilla's blocked delta with the full era vector). When it does not land, vanilla itself rejected it as immune — era-correct, since a click inside the hurt-immunity window produces no knockback in vanilla too. There is no degraded-magnitude ('non-sprinting') path in this mechanism, and sprint scaling is never dropped by it. The finding's premise that "half of spam-cadence combo hits ship the recompute-path knock" would, even if true, be latency-only and magnitude-identical — not weaker.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss on landed hits: 0 blocks — the region recompute ships the identical full stamp (sprint bonus included) as the pre-send would have. Only difference is arrival latency (~1 RTT / ~50-150ms later), which yields tighter combos by design, not reduced magnitude. Expected frequency of actual KB weakening in real close-range PvP: nil, because no code path in this mechanism produces a reduced-magnitude knock. The frozen-12 phase band does occur (a narrow slice of spam-cadence timing) but only ever resolves to an era-correct dropped hit or a full-magnitude late hit.

## `combo-residual-opposition-and-liftoff-facing-push` — merged as era-real, sources: engine-math, ledger, desk-obligations

**Mechanism:** Step 4 base = victimMotion*friction - dir*push folds the victim's world-fixed ledger residual against the per-hit recomputed push axis. Two era-real residual sources oppose the push at close range: (1) previous-knock residual after the pair rotates/crosses — on combos:true presets (legacy-1.7 default, kohi, minehq, badlion) the ledger keeps the full shipped stamp (even when the client fully countered it — era fields did too); after a side-swap/circle/2v1 cross-fire the residual points TOWARD the new attacker and residual*friction cancels the push (a decayed 0.7 residual x0.5 friction eats 0.35 of a 0.4 push, leaving ~0.05 base). combos:false presets never record melee residual and are immune — why mmc/lunar feel more consistent in scrappy fights. (2) sprint-jump facing push: recordLiftoff adds the era 0.2 along the victim's OWN yaw on every rising liftoff; a victim sprint-jumping TOWARD their attacker carries a toward-attacker residual shaving up to ~0.1 (~25% of base) at friction 0.5 — ALL presets (liftoffs always write the ledger), negligible only at friction 0.1 (velt/signature). Both are faithful 1.7 server-field behavior; any ledger-vs-reality divergence upstream would make them fire on geometries where era would not. Sub-case leaning divergence: no ledger reset exists for same-world teleports (GroundFsm.onTeleport has no caller), so a residual survives ~2.5s past an enderpearl.

**Trigger:** combos:true preset with close-range circling/side-swap within the residual decay window, 2v1 cross-fire, or (all presets) a victim sprint-jumping toward the attacker when hit — the normal aggressive close-range approach.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:496-501 (x = vx*friction - pushX); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java (combos flags: LEGACY_17:149 true, KOHI:80, MINEHQ:154, BADLION:180 true; LEGACY_18:43, MMC:107, LUNAR:133, VELT:206, SIGNATURE:236 false); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:76-85 (facing push); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/GroundFsm.java:64-70, :91-99, :119-124 (onTeleport uncalled — grep-verified); MotionLedgerTest.java:128-136 (liftoffAddsThePreResolvedFacingPush); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:117-120 (1.7.10 fields never restored); .claude/skills/era-accuracy (era jump stamp 0.42 + 0.2 facing push).

**Maps to the report:** Directly produces 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback... when two players are quite close together and hitting each other' on the 1.7-lineage presets — era-authentic hit-to-hit inconsistency in exactly the reported geometry.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: All cited code is accurate. KnockbackEngine.base() (kernel/.../math/KnockbackEngine.java:497,501) computes x = victim.vx()*friction.x() - pushX and z = victim.vz()*friction.z() - pushZ, folding the WORLD-FIXED ledger residual against the per-hit push axis (pushX/Z point away from the attacker's current position). This is the faithful 1.7 motX/=2; motX-=dx*f server-field fold. Deliveries.java:36 records melee into the ledger only when view.profile().combos() is true; every preset combos flag matches the finding (LEGACY_17 default true / friction 0.5 / base 0.4 verified line 136,144,149; kohi/minehq/badlion true, friction 0.5; legacy-1.8/mmc/lunar/velt/signature false; velt/signature friction 0.1). So on combos:true presets a prior melee residual persists and, after a side-swap/circle/2v1 cross-fire, points toward the new attacker and its friction-halved value subtracts from the fresh push — up to ~0.35 of a 0.4 base in the worst geometry, more typically 0.1-0.24. combos:false presets never record melee residual, so they are immune (why mmc/lunar/velt/signature feel more consistent) — CONFIRMED. MotionLedger.recordLiftoff (lines 76-85) adds facingPushX/Z sourced from GroundFsm lines 96-100 (Decay.SPRINT_JUMP_PUSH = 0.2 along the victim's OWN yaw when sprinting+rising); CombatSession:242-243 applies Liftoff events un-gated by combos, so the toward-attacker facing residual folds on ALL presets, shaving up to ~0.1 at friction 0.5 and negligibly at friction 0.1 (velt/signature) — CONFIRMED. record() stores the shipped stamp regardless of what the client did, so the server fields carry the full knock even when client-countered — era-accurate.

GroundFsm.onTeleport() has no production caller (only GroundFsmTest:124) — CONFIRMED. The only Reset producers are SessionService:231 (world change) and :238 (death); a same-world enderpearl produces no reset. Crucially, even those Reset paths route through CombatSession:248 -> ledger.recordLanding(), which PRESERVES the horizontal residual (this.vx = carried.vx(); this.vz = carried.vz()) and only re-equilibrates the vertical — so there is genuinely NO horizontal-residual clear anywhere in production except natural decay. That strengthens the finding's 'no reset' observation.

Two refinements against the finding: (1) the '~2.5s past an enderpearl' window is overstated — ground drag (slip*AIR_DRAG = 0.546/tick) drives the horizontal residual to negligible within <1s; only an airborne victim (air drag 0.91/tick) keeps it meaningful, and only for ~0.5s. (2) The report's specific 'seems like the non-sprinting knockback' is NOT what this mechanism produces: residual opposition and facing-push attenuate the horizontal MAGNITUDE, they do not select the walk-KB path (that would be a sprint-flag read elsewhere). This finding is a real contributing factor to the general 'weak KB when two players are close' feel, but it does not explain the 'non-sprinting' specificity. Both attenuations are faithful 1.7 server-field behavior, so no fix to the primary mechanism is warranted; they only become a bug if an upstream ledger-vs-reality divergence (the known open ledger-vy issue) makes them fire on geometries a real era server would not.
- Corrections: Finding's code and mechanism are accurate; keep as era-real. Refine two points: (1) The enderpearl 'residual survives ~2.5s' is overstated — ground drag (0.546/tick) zeroes the horizontal residual in <1s; only an airborne victim keeps it meaningful (~0.5s via 0.91/tick air drag). Also note even the wired Reset paths (SessionService:231 world-change, :238 death) route through CombatSession:248 recordLanding, which PRESERVES the horizontal residual and only re-equilibrates the vertical — so no horizontal-residual clear exists anywhere except natural decay (this strengthens the 'no reset' point but shrinks its temporal window). (2) This mechanism attenuates horizontal MAGNITUDE; it does not reproduce the report's specific 'seems like the non-sprinting knockback' (that is a sprint-flag/path selection, a different mechanism). Treat this as a contributing era-real factor to the general 'weak KB when close together' feel, not the non-sprinting-selection symptom. The only bug angle is conditional on the separate known ledger-vy/upstream divergence making these fire on non-era geometries.
- Severity: Moderate feel-level attenuation, era-faithful (not a KB loss vs era truth, only vs naive expectation). Residual opposition: on combos:true presets (legacy-1.7 DEFAULT, kohi, minehq, badlion, friction 0.5) a toward-attacker residual shaves ~0.10-0.24 (worst-case circling ~0.35) off the ~0.4 base push, firing in close-range circling / side-swap / 2v1 cross-fire — common in real PvP, so moderate frequency. Facing-push: on all presets except friction-0.1 (velt/signature), a victim sprint-jumping toward the attacker carries a ~0.2*decay*0.5 ≈ up to ~0.1 (~25% of base) opposing residual — sprint-jump approach is the normal aggressive close-range pattern, so moderate-to-high frequency but small per-hit magnitude. Enderpearl sub-case: rare and short-lived (<1s meaningful, not the stated ~2.5s), low severity.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: I verified the engine math, ledger, and preset values and hand-computed both mechanisms.

STEP-4 CONFIRMED (KnockbackEngine.java:497,501): base x = victim.vx()*friction.x - pushX, where pushX points AWAY from the attacker on the per-hit-recomputed axis, and victim.vx() is the world-fixed ledger residual. Sprint/enchant extras (lines 214-228) are added AFTER base along the attacker's yaw and are NOT touched by the residual — load-bearing for the "feels like non-sprint" clue below.

MECHANISM 1 (combos:true residual opposition). Only LEGACY_17/KOHI/MINEHQ/BADLION record melee residual (Deliveries.java:35-36 gates on combos()). Straight 1v1 chase: residual points away from attacker and COMPOUNDS (correct). Opposition needs the attacker on the residual side (side-swap / fast circle crossing / 2v1 crossfire). Hand-computed LEGACY_17 sprint stamp vx≈0.9: ground decay 0.546/tick → after 3 ticks 0.146, ·0.5=0.073, base 0.4→0.327 (only ~18% loss, MILD — same-attacker ground circle decays before crossing). But airborne victim (air drag 0.91/tick, common in juggles): residual ~0.75-0.82 after 1-2 ticks, ·0.5≈0.38 → cancels the 0.4 base → ~0.05 (the finding's number) = "victim doesn't move back." Close-range clue explained: point-blank, small position change = large angle change, so the attacker crosses the residual axis inside its live window; long range barely rotates it so it compounds. Matches "especially when close."

"Feels like non-sprint KB": sprint hit under opposition — base 0.4 cancelled, 0.5 yaw extra survives → net ~0.5-0.55 = ordinary non-sprint magnitude (matches "seems like the non-sprinting knockback"; sprint hits drop from compounding ~1.25 to ~0.55, roughly halved). Non-sprint/block/w-tap-miss hit: no extra → base→0.05, ~85% horizontal loss = "truly little to no knockback."

MECHANISM 2 (sprint-jump facing push, all friction>=0.5 presets). recordLiftoff (MotionLedger.java:79-81) writes +0.2 (Decay.SPRINT_JUMP_PUSH) along victim's own yaw on every rising sprint-jump; CombatSession.apply:242-243 records it regardless of combos. Victim sprint-jumping TOWARD the attacker (default aggressive approach) → toward-attacker residual. Peak loss 0.2·friction: 0.1 at 0.5 (25% of 0.4 base), 0.111 at MMC 0.556 (35% of 0.32 base), 0.137 at LUNAR 0.685 (25% of 0.54). Only base shaved, extra survives. High frequency, modest magnitude = pervasive subtle weakening = the reported "feeling thing." Divergence note: ledger carries only the 0.2 jump push, not the WASD approach velocity the era field also held → Mental UNDER-produces vs era (milder, not worse).

FREQUENCY MATCH. Mechanism 2 = high-frequency/low-magnitude (subtle pervasive); Mechanism 1 = lower-frequency/high-magnitude (occasional dramatic, worst airborne/2v1). Together they cover both halves of the report and its "subtle, hard to reproduce, feeling" character, both worst at close range, both on combos:true legacy presets — consistent with "as far back as I can remember."

DIVERGENCE vs ERA. Both are faithful 1.7.10 world-fixed field folding (compendium 1.3; era knockBack does motX/=2 then subtracts push). A real 1.7 server shows the same cancellation. Candidate Mental-vs-era divergences (vertical over-decay; recording grounded=true for an airborne knock → ground over-decay of the residual; uncalled GroundFsm.onTeleport reset) mostly make the horizontal residual SMALLER than era → milder, not a "fires where era wouldn't" bug. So it is era-authentic behavior perceived as a bug; a fix trades away era fidelity.

CRITICAL CONFIG CAVEAT. On VELT/SIGNATURE (friction 0.1, combos:false — SIGNATURE is Mental's flagship and a plausible deployed default): mechanism 1 off, mechanism 2 loses 0.2·0.1=0.02 (~5% of base). Effectively immune → if the owner runs signature/velt this finding does NOT explain their bug (matches memory: mmc/lunar/velt feel more consistent). Reproduces strongly ONLY on combos:true friction-0.5 presets (legacy-1.7 default, kohi, minehq, badlion) and weakly (mechanism 2) on mmc/lunar/legacy-1.8. Check the deployed preset first.
- Corrections: Two refinements to the finding, both sharpening rather than refuting it: (1) Mechanism 1 is much MILDER than "0.05 base" for the grounded same-attacker circle case — the ledger records grounded=true at hit and decays the residual at 0.546/tick, so it is nearly gone (~0.146 after 3 ticks) by the time a circle crosses to the far side. The dramatic near-total cancellation requires the victim to be hit AIRBORNE (air drag 0.91/tick keeps the residual ~0.8), i.e. juggle/2v1-crossfire geometry, not a flat-ground 1v1 circle. (2) The finding does not surface that the sprint EXTRA (0.5 along attacker yaw) always survives the opposition — this is precisely why an opposed sprint hit "feels like non-sprint KB" (net ~0.55) rather than truly zero, which the user's own wording confirms. Also worth stating plainly: this is era-authentic, so the owner's likely-flagship signature/velt (friction 0.1, combos off) is essentially immune — verify the deployed preset before treating this as the cause.
- Severity: Mechanism 1 (combos:true only): horizontal base loss up to ~0.35 of a 0.4 base — base 0.4→~0.05 (~85% loss) on non-sprint/block/w-tap-miss hits ("no knockback"), and sprint hits drop from ~1.25 compounding to ~0.55 (base cancelled, 0.5 extra survives → reads as non-sprint KB). Fires only on the swap/fast-circle/2v1-crossfire subset, worst when the victim is airborne (residual decays at 0.91/tick not 0.546) — roughly low-single-digit to ~10-15% of close-range exchanges on legacy presets. Mechanism 2 (all friction>=0.5 presets): base loss 0.1-0.18 (25-44% of base; sprint extra unaffected) whenever the victim sprint-jumps toward the attacker — high frequency (the default aggressive approach) → pervasive subtle weakening. Combined they match both halves of the report and its close-range emphasis. NEAR-ZERO on velt/signature (friction 0.1, combos off): <5% base loss — if that is the deployed preset the finding does not reproduce the bug.

## `attacker-x06-residual-write-era-and-timing` — merged as divergence-from-era, sources: ledger, desk-obligations, era-truth, transactions

**Mechanism:** Era attack() multiplied the ATTACKER'S server motion fields x0.6 on every accepted bonus-KB hit (both eras, decompile-cited) — so in trades a counter-hitting player's own residual shrinks and the NEXT knock they receive compounds off residual/2 of a smaller number; trades legitimately compound less than one-sided combos. Mental replicates the write (ledger.scaleHorizontal(0.6) in applyAttackerObligations, unit-pinned) but at the deferred EDBEE 1-2 ticks after registration, while the pre-send reads the counter-attacker's residual from the END-OF-PREVIOUS-TICK view — a same/next-tick received knock always folds the UNSCALED residual, where era's join-order made it bimodal (one side folded the scaled fields). Direction of the divergence is sign-dependent and the finders disagreed: desk-obligations argues the unscaled (larger) residual always ships MORE-or-equal; ledger's sign analysis shows that when the residual OPPOSES the incoming push (victim sprint-jumping toward their attacker) folding the larger unscaled opposing residual ships WEAKER (~0.2r delta, ~0.2-0.3 blocks) than era's victim-slot-first mode. Either way Mental deterministically matches one of era's two bimodal modes. Completeness: the fast-path non-player branch (applyNonPlayer) never applies the x0.6 (mob hits keep an unscaled residual — slightly MORE than era, PvE-adjacent).

**Trigger:** Mutual trade on combos:true presets: victim counter-hits with a bonus hit in the same/adjacent tick as receiving one; the weak direction fires when their live residual opposes the incoming push (moving into their attacker).
