**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:157-160, :404-449 (deferred obligations, scaleHorizontal at :418-424, sole call site, bonus-gated, cross-region-guarded — no double-application exists); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:466-474 (view-frozen residual read), :651-685 (non-player path skips obligations); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:110-116; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/model/PlayerView.java:8-13; docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:129-143 (x0.6 both eras, 'shapes trade exchanges'), :333 (unit-pin scoreboard); .claude/skills/legacy-motion-physics/SKILL.md:99-102 (join-order bimodal wire).

**Maps to the report:** Second-order contributor to 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback' in active trades: era-correct compounding reduction plus a timing divergence whose weak branch fires precisely in mutual close trades with an opposing residual — subtle by construction.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The finding replicates era truth accurately in code but frames a faithful era replication as a knockback-reducing divergence. Era's x0.6 attacker self-multiply was join-order sensitive (two attacks in one tick — whichever attack() runs first decides whether the scaled or unscaled residual compounds into the counter-knock). Mental's pre-send folds the frozen end-of-previous-tick residual = era's 'A-processed-first' mode, a legitimate era ordering; the authoritative region path folds the live (possibly already-scaled) ledger. Deterministically realizing one of two era-valid orderings is era-real, not a divergence — the finding's own 'matches one of era's two bimodal modes' admits this. The 'always unscaled' claim is contradicted by captureVictim's live-ledger read at KnockbackUnit:271. The finders disagreed on even the sign, and the magnitude is ~0.2-0.3 blocks confined to a razor-thin same-tick opposing-residual counter-hit window on combos:true presets only (combos:false never records melee residual, so the path is inert there). The one genuine gap — player-hits-mob not scaling the attacker — is PvE, irrelevant to the PvP report, and mis-cited to the delivery path rather than the obligation gate. As stated (a divergence-from-era contributing to 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback'), the finding does not hold.
- Corrections: The code facts are mostly accurate (scaleHorizontal(0.6) on attacker ledger, bonus-gated, cross-region-guarded, unit-pinned; player-attacks-mob does not scale the attacker via the Player-victim gate at KnockbackUnit:160). But the finding's THESIS is wrong in three concrete ways: (a) 'a same/next-tick received knock always folds the UNSCALED residual' is false — the authoritative region path (KnockbackUnit:271) reads the LIVE ledger via captureVictim, which reflects same-tick scaling; only the netty pre-send reads the frozen view. (b) The finding's own conclusion ('Mental deterministically matches one of era's two bimodal modes') means Mental realizes a LEGITIMATE era join-order ordering — that is era-real, not a divergence. (c) The PvE sub-claim is cited to applyNonPlayer (a delivery path, HitRegistrationUnit:651) when the actual gate is the Player-victim check in KnockbackUnit.onEntityDamageByEntity:160. The 'bimodal' era premise is the finder's inference, not supported by the cited compendium/skill lines (which call the effect era-faithful and 'mostly invisible' on 1.8.9). Finders explicitly disagreed on the sign of the effect.
- Severity: Negligible and sign-contested. Claimed horizontal-KB loss is at most ~0.2r (~0.2-0.3 blocks) and ONLY in the finding's weak sub-case (victim sprint-jumping INTO their attacker while counter-hitting with a bonus hit inside the same/adjacent tick, on a combos:true preset, via the pre-send path). The competing analysis in the same finding argues the opposite sign (more-or-equal KB). Required simultaneity (mutual bonus hits within one tick + opposing residual) is rare in real close-range PvP, and even when it fires Mental matches a legitimate era join-order mode, so there is no systematic under-shoot. Effectively no measurable contribution to the reported 'weak close-range knockback' feel.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: MECHANISM SANITY: Confirmed real. `KnockbackUnit.applyAttackerObligations` (:418-424) calls `attackerSession.ledger().scaleHorizontal(0.6)` at the deferred EDBEE, bonus-gated, sole call site. `MotionLedger.scaleHorizontal` (:110-116) multiplies vx/vz by 0.6, leaves vy. The pre-send reads the frozen END-OF-PREVIOUS-TICK residual: `HitRegistrationUnit.preVictimState` (:466-474) pulls `view.motion()` which SessionService:533 sets to `session.ledger().current()`. So a counter-hitter who lands a bonus hit at tick T has their x0.6 scheduled for T+1/T+2; a knock they RECEIVE within that window folds their still-unscaled residual. Era wrote motX/motZ *= 0.6 synchronously inside attack(), so its join-order made this bimodal (compendium :128-142). Mental is deterministically the "unscaled" mode. Real divergence.

TICK-BY-TICK, default preset legacy-1.7 (combos:true, base.h 0.4, sprint extra 0.5, friction.x/z 0.5, air.h 1.0):
The residual folded is `residualCarry = victim.vx*friction.x*ux + victim.vz*friction.z*uz`. Delta from the missing x0.6 = (1 - 0.6) * friction.x * |r_proj| = 0.4 * 0.5 * |r_proj| = 0.2*|r_proj|. A fresh sprint knock horizontal freshEra ≈ base+bonus ≈ 0.55-0.7 b/t. So the fold delta is ~0.04-0.08 b/t on a live residual of |r_proj|≈0.2-0.4. Sign: when the residual OPPOSES the incoming push (residualCarry negative), unscaled = more-negative = shipped WEAKER by ~0.06 b/t; integrated over a ~8-12 tick flight at friction 0.91 that is ~0.2-0.4 blocks of landing displacement. When the residual is ALIGNED (with the push, the common combo case where A comboed B so B's residual points away from A) the unscaled residual ships STRONGER — the desk-obligations "more-or-equal" branch, which INCREASES knockback and contradicts the report.

CRITICAL CORRECTION to the trigger: `PlayerView.motion()` is the LEDGER knockback residual (MotionLedger records the FINAL delivered knock value and decays it; grounded horizontals decay toward zero equilibrium), NOT the raw sprint-jump movement velocity — measuredVx/Vz is a separate servo-only signal that never enters the fold. So the finding's "victim sprint-jumping toward their attacker" cannot itself produce an opposing residual: a sprint-jump's walking velocity is invisible to the fold. The weak branch requires B to carry a LIVE airborne KNOCKBACK residual that projects TOWARD A — i.e. the players crossed over / circle-strafed so a prior push now points back at the current attacker. That is a genuine but minority sub-case of close swirling combat, and a grounded fighter's horizontal residual has already decayed toward zero, shrinking |r_proj| and the delta further.

MATCH TO REPORT: Headline symptom ("little to no knockback, feels like the NON-SPRINTING knockback at close range") is a LARGE effect — the sprint bonus adds ~0.5 b/t (roughly doubles the knock). This mechanism shaves at most ~0.06-0.08 b/t (~10%). It CANNOT produce a "feels like non-sprinting" gap and does not explain the primary symptom. Secondary clause ("sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should... very subtle, feeling thing") is plausibly touched: the effect is genuinely subtle, fires specifically in close mutual bonus-trades, and is inherently probabilistic-feeling. But it is a weak, second-order contributor, and it only diverges from era's STRONG mode (~half of real 1.7 servers hit exactly Mental's outcome), so it is "worse than a real server would have felt" only a small fraction of the time. Not refuted: it can produce a real subtle sliver of the secondary clause.
- Corrections: Trigger mischaracterization: the folded residual is the ledger KNOCKBACK residual (SessionService:533 → ledger().current()), NOT the counter-hitter's raw sprint-jump movement velocity (that is measuredVx/Vz, servo-only, never folded). A player "sprint-jumping toward their attacker" therefore does NOT create an opposing residual by itself; the weak branch needs a prior airborne knock pointing back toward the current attacker (crossed/strafed geometry), and grounded horizontals decay toward zero — so the opposing sub-case is rarer and smaller than the finding implies. The finding correctly self-flags the direction dispute: the aligned-residual case (the common combo geometry, B's residual pointing away from A) ships STRONGER unscaled, which raises KB and cannot match the report; only the opposing sub-case weakens. Classification divergence-from-era is right (era was join-order bimodal; Mental deterministically folds unscaled — weaker when opposing, stronger when aligned). This is a legitimate second-order contributor to the "sprint hits sometimes slightly weak" clause but is magnitude-incapable of the headline "non-sprinting knockback" symptom.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss in the weak branch: ~0.04-0.08 b/t off the fold term (delta = 0.2*|r_proj|, friction.x 0.5), i.e. ~0.2-0.4 blocks of landing displacement, ~10% of a ~0.6 b/t sprint knock — never the ~0.5 b/t sprint-vs-nonsprint gap the headline describes. Frequency in real close PvP: combos:true only (default legacy-1.7 qualifies; legacy-1.8/mmc/lunar combos:false are EXEMPT — no persisted melee residual to mis-fold); requires a bonus counter-hit within 1-2 ticks AND the counter-hitter carrying a live airborne knockback residual projecting toward the attacker (crossed-over geometry) — a minority (~10-25%) of close mutual bonus-trades, and vs era's strong mode only ~half of those. Net: a barely-perceptible weakening in a low-single-digit % of close trades; matches the "subtle feeling" texture but far too small in magnitude and too narrow to be the reported primary symptom. Non-player path (applyNonPlayer skips obligations) is PvE-only, irrelevant to the PvP report.

## `stale-position-ring-direction-at-close-range` — merged as divergence-from-era, sources: registration-fallthrough

**Mechanism:** The pre-send computes the knock DIRECTION from PositionRing.latest() for BOTH parties, and the ring is written exactly once per owning-thread tick, so at registration both positions are up to one full tick (plus phase) stale. In a face-hug mutual trade the pair closes at up to ~0.57 blocks/tick combined, so at <1.5-block separation the stale relative offset is a large fraction of — and can invert past — the true separation: the base 0.4 push computes near-zero or oblique, and the authoritative pass ADOPTS the pre-sent vector unchanged (era read LIVE positions at packet processing). The era-real face-hug weakness therefore fires MORE OFTEN through Mental than on a real era server; recomputed hits use live locations, adding path-dependent hit-to-hit variance.

**Trigger:** Two players at <1.5 blocks closing on each other, either having moved meaningfully since the last session tick — every pre-sent hit reads the stale pair.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:451-484 (pre states from sessions.positions().latest()); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:349-355 ('One owning-thread position sample per tick'); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:256-267 (adopt, no live-direction re-check); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:119-122 (the era-real opposition this amplifies).

**Maps to the report:** Directly matches 'especially when two players are quite close together and hitting each other' — the base component collapses more often than era truth, reading as non-sprint/no knockback even on sprint hits (the yaw extra survives, the positional base cancels or misaligns).

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: The finding's architectural facts are correct: the pre-send reads knock direction (and hurtYaw) from sessions.positions().latest(), the D2 PositionRing written exactly once per owning-thread tick (SessionService.tick:353, the sole writer), for both parties; PacketTap.onMovement feeds only y/onGround/lastYaw into the netty domain, so no fresher x/z source exists; and KnockbackUnit:264-266 adopts the pre-sent vector with no live-direction recheck. So there IS a once-per-tick stale-position feed vs. vanilla's per-movement-packet freshness.

But the finding's causal mechanism and severity are wrong:
(1) KnockbackEngine.base (462-516) normalizes: pushX = (deltaX/magnitude)*push, so |horizontal push| is ALWAYS profile.base().horizontal() (0.4) regardless of separation. It never "computes near-zero." Coincident (<1e-4) still yields a full-magnitude push in a random direction (vanilla-exact). Magnitude collapse is impossible.
(2) The finding derives its error budget from combined closing speed (~0.57 b/t). Closing is along the attacker↔victim axis — precisely the component normalization discards. Only LATERAL (strafe) relative displacement rotates the unit direction, bounded to ~0.28 b/t per player over a sub-tick fraction, i.e. a small angular error (~10-15°, cos≈0.9) at 0.6-1.5 block separations. Direction inversion needs lateral displacement > separation within one tick — impossible at contact distances.
(3) The sprint/wtap bonus (KnockbackEngine:224-226, 335-337) is attacker.yaw()-directed, independent of position, and fully survives the stale read — the finding concedes "the yaw extra survives." So a sprint hit cannot read as non-sprint via this path.

Therefore the described amplification of the face-hug weakness ("base component collapses/cancels more often," "reads as non-sprint knockback") does not occur; the real effect is a small direction obliquity in fast lateral-strafe exchanges only. It does not explain the reported "little to no knockback / non-sprinting knockback." Refuted as an explanation for the bug; the bare divergence fact is real but negligible.
- Corrections: Keep only the raw architectural observation: the netty pre-send computes the base knock DIRECTION from a once-per-tick PositionRing snapshot (both parties), and the authoritative pass adopts it unchanged — a real but negligible divergence from vanilla's per-movement-packet position freshness. Drop all three severity claims: (a) the base push magnitude cannot go near-zero (it is normalized to a constant 0.4); (b) the cited ~0.57 b/t closing speed is along-axis and normalization-invariant, so it produces zero direction error — only lateral strafe motion errors the direction, and only by a small angle at contact, never an inversion; (c) the sprint bonus is yaw-directed and fully survives, so this cannot turn a sprint hit into a non-sprint-feeling hit. The finding does not match the reported "little to no knockback / non-sprinting knockback" symptom.
- Severity: Negligible horizontal-KB loss. The stale-position error affects only the DIRECTION of the fixed-magnitude (0.4) base push, and only via lateral/strafe relative displacement — worst-case ~0.28 b/t over a sub-tick at ~0.6-1.5 block separation = ~10-15 degrees obliquity, i.e. ~5-10% loss of the along-axis component, no magnitude loss, no inversion. The yaw-directed sprint bonus is unaffected. Expected frequency in close PvP: the geometric condition (significant perpendicular relative motion sampled at an unlucky tick phase) is common, but the resulting KB delta is below perceptual threshold and cannot present as "non-sprint" or "no" knockback. Not a plausible source of the owner's symptom.

**SYMPTOM lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap; re-verification dispatched)

## `era-1710-join-order-trade-asymmetry-baseline` — merged as era-real, sources: era-truth

**Mechanism:** Reconstructed era ground truth for calibration: on real 1.7.10, same-tick mutual sprint trades were massively asymmetric by join order — the later-joined trader's received knock passed through their own counter-attack's x0.6 on server fields plus one extra physics decay, shipping ~0.9*0.6*0.546 ≈ 0.29h (below the 0.4 plain base; measured era charge-trades pinned the victim at 0.07-0.27 blocks/hit), while the other side received the full 0.9. On 1.8.9 the in-attack send + restore made both sides symmetric full-stamp. Mental deliberately ships the full stamp to both (determinism is the product; the 1.5.0 bimodality reversal).

**Trigger:** Both players attack in the same server tick at close range, both sprinting — the mutual-trade norm; on era 1.7.10 one side's knock was cut to roughly a third, coin-flipped by join order.

**Evidence:** docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md:161-222 (addendum 2: tracker-before-connection, join-order slots, measured bimodal wires), :12-18 (charge-combo row); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:88-104, :129-143; SYNOPSIS.md:100-113, :183-204.

**Maps to the report:** Calibrates the report: 'close trades feel like non-sprint knockback' was LITERALLY true on real 1.7.10 for the later-joined trader. Mental's trades ship equal-or-MORE than era wire-side — so genuine weakness through Mental must come from the client-side mechanisms, geometry, or the actual bugs, not this mode.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: This is an era-truth calibration finding, not a Mental-code bug claim, and it holds up against the cited sources. The two documented era mechanics it composes are both real in this codebase's ground truth: (1) join-order tracker bimodality (era-wire-measurements addendum 2, :161-222) — the later-joined victim's physics slot decays the stamp once (sprint 0.9→0.4914h via ×0.546 ground slip) while the earlier-joiner ships the undecayed full 0.9 stamp; and (2) the attacker-side ×0.6 self-multiply (compendium §1.5, :128-142), which fires only when kbLevels>0 (sprint or KB-enchant) on the counter-attacker's own server fields. Composing them for a same-tick mutual sprint trade is ordering-coherent: within the later-joiner V's connection slot, V's counter-attack runs AFTER A's knock was already written into V.motX (A's slot ran first), so V's own ×0.6 scales the received knock, then V's physics decays it: 0.9 × 0.6 × 0.546 ≈ 0.295h. Symmetrically, the earlier-joiner A's own ×0.6 fired before it received V's knock, so A retains the full stamp — that is exactly the join-order coin-flip asymmetry the finding describes. I could not refute the mechanism.

Mental-side claims verified in code: default delivery is KnockbackDelivery.TRACKER = full stamp (HitRegistrationUnit.java:406 'TRACKER (full stamp)'); TRACKER_DECAYED is opt-in, handled specially by the desk (SuiteDelivery.java:11-35); and the attacker-side ×0.6 is an explicit Mental GAP (compendium §1.5 marks it MENTAL ✗ — the ledger never applies it). Therefore Mental deterministically ships full stamp to BOTH traders and does NOT reproduce the counter-×0.6 cut. The finding's exculpatory conclusion — 'genuine weakness through Mental must come from client-side mechanisms, geometry, or the actual bugs, not this mode' — is correct for THIS mechanism.

era_call = era-real: the phenomenon (close mutual sprint trades feeling like non-sprint KB for one side) was genuinely real on vanilla 1.7.10, and Mental's divergence from it (full stamp both sides) is intentional and documented (1.5.0 bimodality reversal, determinism = product), not a defect. It is not a Mental bug and not an unintended divergence.

Minor corrections (see corrected field) do not change the verdict.
- Corrections: Two imprecisions, neither fatal: (1) The doc's charge-combo '0.07–0.27' is victim FLIGHT DISTANCE in blocks (net travel), not a per-hit horizontal-knock magnitude — the finding labels it 'blocks/hit', conflating it with its computed 0.29h velocity. Those are different quantities; the measured pinning is actually more severe than a single ×0.6 explains, because repeated w-tap/compounding further suppresses net travel. So the clean single-factor 0.29h decomposition UNDERSTATES the measured pinning rather than matching it. (2) 'plus one extra physics decay' is loose: the ×0.546 is the SAME single decay the plain later-joiner ('tracker-decayed') wire already carries; the only factor ADDED over that wire is the counter-attacker's ×0.6. Otherwise the reconstruction and the Mental-side exculpatory conclusion are correct.
- Severity: In the 1.7.10 ERA (reconstruction target): later-joined trader loses ~67% horizontal on a same-tick mutual sprint trade (0.9→~0.29h; net travel measured at 0.07–0.27 blocks with w-tap compounding). Frequency: ~50% of mutual-sprint pairings (join-order coin flip), and mutual same-tick sprint trades are the close-range PvP norm — so era-frequently for one of the two players. IN MENTAL: effectively ZERO horizontal-KB loss from this mechanism — default TRACKER ships full 0.9 stamp to both sides and the counter-×0.6 is never applied (documented Mental gap). This finding therefore contributes nothing to the user's Mental 'weak close trades' report; it is baseline/exculpatory only, ruling this era mode OUT as the cause and redirecting to client-side geometry or the actual Mental bugs.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: This finding is not a Mental-side defect claim — it is explicitly reconstructed era ground truth ("classification: era-real") whose stated purpose is to CALIBRATE the report, and it self-disclaims being the current cause ("Mental's trades ship equal-or-MORE than era wire-side — so genuine weakness through Mental must come from... not this mode"). My job is to check whether it plausibly produces the reported experience, and whether it correctly locates that production in era history vs current Mental.

FACT CHECK — all claims land:
1. Join-order bimodal mechanism is real, decompile-cited (docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md:161-222, MinecraftServer.v()/nc.c()/nh.a(jd)/mw.i()): later-joined victim's physics runs in the same connection phase after the attacker's, decaying the stamp once; earlier-joined victim ships undecayed (byte-identical to 1.8.9).
2. Measured sprint wire: victim-after (0.4914h, 0.3731v)→2.54 blocks vs victim-before (0.9h, 0.4607v)→~4.9 blocks (:190-193). The full 1.8.9 wire is symmetric in both orders via the in-attack send+restore.
3. Charge-combo (both sprint, w-tap) row (:18): "victim pinned at 0.07-0.27 blocks, v 0.21-0.37" vs 1.8.9 "flat h 0.78-0.87" — exactly the finding's cited 0.07-0.27/hit. The finding's arithmetic 0.9*0.6*0.546 ≈ 0.29 sits just above the measured band, consistent order of magnitude (roughly a third of full, below the 0.4 plain base).
4. "Mental ships full stamp to both, deterministically" is CONFIRMED: :208-211 "KnockbackDelivery.TRACKER therefore ships the full stamp as of 1.5.0... Determinism is the product — Mental does not replicate the coin flip." Every bundled preset in kernel Presets.java uses KnockbackDelivery.TRACKER for melee/projectile; the tracker-decayed later-joiner mode is opt-in only.

REPRODUCTION JUDGMENT: On real 1.7.10 this mechanism LITERALLY was the reported feeling — the later-joined trader in a close mutual sprint/w-tap trade received ~0.29h (or lower, per the 0.07-0.27 measured band) versus a full 0.9h, i.e. worse than the 0.4 non-sprint base, coin-flipped per pairing. That is precisely "close trades feel like non-sprinting knockback, subtle, hard to reproduce." So the mechanism DOES produce the report — but in ERA, not in current Mental. Current Mental (2.4.8-beta) ships the full stamp to BOTH traders via TRACKER, so this mode fires at zero frequency through the plugin. The finding correctly says so and correctly points the live investigation elsewhere (client-side geometry, ledger-vy divergence, the actual close-range bugs). One caveat: if the owner ran Mental pre-1.5.0 (when the decayed/asymmetric wire could be the default), "as far back as I can remember" would have included genuine instances of this — but that is historical, not the current jar.

VERDICT: The finding as stated is accurate and self-consistent; not refuted. It is era-real calibration, not a current Mental cause.
- Corrections: The finding is a correctly-labeled era-real calibration note, not a Mental bug, and it is accurate: mechanism, decompile citations, and the measured 0.07-0.27 blocks/hit charge-trade band all check out, as does "Mental ships full stamp to both deterministically" (Presets.java: all presets TRACKER; era-wire doc :208-211). It reproduces the reported FEELING only in the era, not through current Mental. One refinement for the investigation: this mode IS a plausible source of the report's "as far back as I can remember" clause IF the owner ran Mental before 1.5.0 (when the decayed/asymmetric tracker wire could be the delivered default) — worth confirming the earliest-deployed jar version, since that would make the phenomenon partly real-in-Mental historically even though the 2.4.8-beta jar does not reproduce it.
- Severity: In CURRENT Mental: ~0 horizontal-KB loss, ~0% frequency — every bundled preset ships KnockbackDelivery.TRACKER = full stamp to BOTH traders since the 1.5.0 bimodality reversal; the join-order coin flip is not replicated, so this mode does not reproduce the symptom through the plugin. On real 1.7.10 (where the finding lives): ~0.6 block/hit loss — the later-joined trader in a same-tick close mutual sprint/w-tap trade shipped ~0.29h (measured band 0.07-0.27h, below the 0.4 non-sprint base) vs the full 0.9h the other side got, a per-pairing coin flip. Frequency there was high (the mutual-trade norm) and the feel exactly matched "close trades feel like non-sprint KB, subtle, hard to pin" — but that is era history Mental deliberately fixed, not a live cause. Relevant only as pre-1.5.0 provenance for "as far back as I can remember."

## `cancel-then-decline-eats-hit-entirely` — merged as bug, sources: transactions, registration-fallthrough

**Mechanism:** register() cancels the ATTACK packet (HitRegistrationUnit.java:306) BEFORE plan()/dispatch() run, and there is NO vanilla fallback afterward. If the pre-send was suppressed AND the deferred authoritative apply then declines, the attack produces nothing at all — no damage, no flinch, no knock (the swing animation is client-side so the attacker sees a normal swing): (a) applyPlayer's silent negative-validation returns (attacker null/offline/spectator, victim dead/cross-world/gamemode/pvp-off, >7.0-block live re-check) at :619-649; (b) any Throwable after the cancel is swallowed by the listener catch-all (:233-236) — e.g. the unguarded sessions.sessionFor(victimId).desk() NPE at :431 on a concurrent quit/forget race (every other victim access in plan() is null-guarded). Branches (a) also fail to retract the desk pending (only the cross-region branch and retire fallback retract), leaving danglers that feed the stale-pending hazards.

**Trigger:** Same-tick victim death mid-trade, attacker logout/spectator switch in the netty->region gap, plugin cross-world teleport in that gap, or the quit-race NPE — rare individually, but close-range trades maximize same-tick death/interruption coincidences.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:226-237 (catch-all after the cancel), :303-309 (setCancelled before plan/dispatch), :429-432 (unguarded sessionFor NPE surface), :619-649 (silent returns; retract only at :625-632), :758-763 (7.0-block re-check); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:298-317 (concurrent forget).

**Maps to the report:** A legal-looking swing that produces neither damage nor movement — contributes rare 'hit did nothing' moments; unlike the report's phrasing the victim also takes no damage, so likely a minor contributor.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The finding's raw code observations are partly accurate but its conclusion (a knockback-loss bug contributing to the report) is wrong.

WHAT IS TRUE: (1) the ATTACK packet is cancelled at HitRegistrationUnit:306 before plan()/dispatch(), with no vanilla fallback afterward — confirmed; (2) applyPlayer (:619-649) returns without damage on invalid state; (3) the sessions.sessionFor(victimId).desk() call at :431 is genuinely unguarded against a null session, unlike the null-guarded victim reads earlier in plan().

WHY IT IS REFUTED AS A BUG / AS A MATCH:

a) The "produces nothing at all" path requires BOTH pre-send suppressed AND applyPlayer declining. applyPlayer declines only for legitimately-invalid state: attacker null/offline/spectator (:622,:633), victim null/dead (:637), cross-world/pvp-off via isStillAttackable (:638,:746-755), or beyond 7.0 blocks via isInReach (:758-763). In every one of these cases VANILLA would also reject the hit — the interact packet is processed on the main thread with the same netty→main latency, so cancelling+re-validating on the region thread is timing-equivalent and era-faithful. This is era-real behavior, not a divergence. A normally-landing suppressed hit still schedules applyPlayer, which fires victim.damage() → the region-path PlayerVelocityEvent → the desk ships the era vector; suppressed pre-send does NOT mean lost knockback.

b) The mechanism is internally contradictory. The desk pending at :431 is submitted ONLY when tx.state()==PRE_SENT/PINNED, i.e. the pre-send actually SHIPPED. In the "pre-send suppressed" scenario tx stays REGISTERED and nothing is ever submitted to the desk, so there is no dangling pending. The "leaving danglers" claim therefore applies only when the pre-send shipped — in which case the victim already received knockback+hurt from the burst at :426-429, so it is NOT "nothing at all." The two halves of the finding cannot both apply to the same hit.

c) The :431 NPE is benign. sessionFor returns null only after forget(), which runs on quit / shutdown / retire-when-offline. retire (:287-296) re-arms the session while the player is still online and forgets only a genuinely-departed player. So the NPE can fire only for a victim who is quitting the server — where dropping the hit is irrelevant. For a wired (real) victim the burst already shipped before :431 anyway, so even then it is not "nothing." The catch-all at :233-236 swallows it; its "flows through to vanilla" comment is stale (packet already cancelled) but inconsequential here.

d) It does not match the report. The user reports REDUCED knockback with damage still landing ("victim just doesn't really move back", "non-sprinting knockback", subtle feel). This finding produces NO DAMAGE AND NO KNOCK — a glaring "my hit whiffed / health didn't drop" event, not a subtle KB-strength feeling. Its triggers (same-tick death, logout/spectator/teleport in the sub-tick gap, quit-race) are state-change coincidences, not a function of close-range trading; the finding's "close range maximizes same-tick death coincidences" is a hand-wave (same-tick death is about low-HP endgame, unrelated to proximity). It contributes exactly 0 horizontal-KB reduction.

The finding's own matches_report field already concedes it is a poor match ("victim also takes no damage... likely a minor contributor"), which is the honest read: at most a rare, benign robustness nit, not the reported bug.
- Corrections: Accurate code facts: the packet is cancelled at :306 before the authoritative pass, and the sessions.sessionFor(victimId).desk() call at :431 is genuinely unguarded (a latent NPE, unlike the null-guarded victim reads earlier in plan()). But the finding's conclusion is wrong on three counts: (1) every applyPlayer decline branch drops a hit only on legitimately-invalid state that vanilla would also reject, so it is era-faithful, not a divergence; (2) the "produces nothing" case and the "dangling desk pending" case are mutually exclusive — a suppressed pre-send submits nothing to the desk (no dangler), and a shipped pre-send already delivered knockback via the burst (not nothing); (3) the :431 NPE can only fire for a victim who is quitting (sessionFor returns null only post-forget, and retire re-arms while online), making it benign. The manifestation (no damage at all) is the opposite of the report's symptom (damage lands, knockback is weak). If anything, the :431 unguarded deref is worth a defensive null-check as a code-hygiene nit, but it does not affect close-range knockback strength.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss attributable to this finding: 0 (the paths are all-or-nothing hit drops in invalid-state edge cases, never a reduction of an otherwise-landed hit's knockback). Expected frequency in real close-range PvP: negligible — requires victim same-tick death, attacker logout/spectator-switch, or cross-world teleport inside the ~1-tick netty→region gap, or a victim mid-quit for the :431 NPE. None are amplified by proximity. When it does fire the victim takes no damage (visibly a whiffed hit), which does not match the reported subtle weak-knockback feel.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: The finding's code claims check out (setCancelled at :306 before plan/dispatch with no vanilla fallback; silent non-retracting returns at :633/:637; unguarded sessionFor().desk() at :431 vs the null-guarded sibling at :688; catch-all swallow at :233-236). It is a real bug. But as an explanation of THIS report it is a near-total symptom mismatch, for two independent reasons.

WRONG SYMPTOM. The report describes hits that clearly CONNECT — the victim is being damaged, the trade proceeds — but move back too little, "like the non-sprinting knockback," i.e. a present-but-reduced-magnitude knock. This mechanism can never produce a present-but-reduced knock. Its two branches produce the opposite of a connecting-hit-with-weak-KB:
 (a) pre-send suppressed AND deferred apply declines ⇒ the ENTIRE hit is eaten: no damage, no flinch, no knock — a ghost hit. A player perceives that as "my hit didn't register," a loud, noticeable event, not "knockback felt weak." The report's victim keeps taking damage; the ghost-hit victim does not.
 (b) the NPE at :431 fires only when tx.state() is PRE_SENT/PINNED, which is AFTER senders.ship() already put the burst on the wire at :426-429. So the victim got the full pre-sent knock; only the desk submit (damage reconciliation) is lost. That yields a full knock with missing/duplicated damage — again not "reduced knockback."
So neither branch produces "non-sprint-feeling knockback on a connecting hit," which is the literal core of the report.

WRONG FREQUENCY / not close-range-correlated. The joint condition for the ghost hit is (pre-send suppressed) AND (region apply declines). Pre-send suppression is indeed common at high CPS (the pacing gate paces roughly alternate hits), but the authoritative region pass is then the reliable deliverer. It only DECLINES on: victim.isDead() (only the exact kill tick), isInReach() failing (>7.0 blocks live) — which is ANTI-correlated with "quite close together": at 2-3 blocks the live re-check passes trivially — isStillAttackable failing (world/gamemode/pvp toggling mid-trade, essentially never), or attacker offline/spectator in the netty→region gap (rare). None of these are position-correlated toward closeness; the >7 gate points the other way. So the ghost hit is confined to rare edge ticks (kill moment, teleport/logout races), not a recurring close-range texture. The report's defining qualifier — "especially when two players are quite close together" — has no mechanism here to make it fire MORE at close range.

I do not mark refuted=true only because the ghost-hit case technically yields "the victim doesn't move back," a sliver of literal overlap with "little to no knockback." But that overlap comes bundled with no-damage (which the report doesn't describe) and rare, non-close-correlated triggers, so it cannot be the source of the reported feeling. The finding author's own matches_report concedes this ("the victim also takes no damage… likely a minor contributor"). Verified: minor-to-negligible, and specifically NOT the "non-sprint knockback at close range" the owner is reporting.
- Corrections: Real bug (ghost hits, dangling non-retracted pendings, and an unguarded NPE at :431 that should be null-guarded like :688), worth fixing on its own merits — but it is a wrong-symptom, wrong-frequency explanation for THIS report. Its firing case removes damage AND knock together (a ghost hit the player notices as 'didn't register'), or, on the NPE path, ships the full knock and only loses damage bookkeeping; neither produces the report's signature 'connecting hit that knocks like a non-sprint hit at close range.' The one gate that could decline an otherwise-good hit mid-trade (isInReach >7.0) fires when players are FAR apart, the opposite of the report's 'quite close together.' Fix it as a robustness/correctness issue, not as the cause of the weak-knockback feeling.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss in the firing case: total (0 knock) — but jointly with total damage loss, so it reads as a ghost hit, not weak KB. In the NPE case: 0 horizontal-KB loss (full pre-sent burst already shipped). Expected frequency in real close-range sprinting/w-tap PvP: very low and NOT elevated by closeness — the only realistic close-range trigger is the exact same-tick kill, since the >7-block live re-check (the one gate that could decline mid-trade) is anti-correlated with players being close. Contribution to the reported 'subtle weak-knockback feeling': negligible; the symptom it actually produces (no-damage ghost hit) is absent from the report.

## `cps-limiter-silently-eats-clicks` — merged as config-dependent, sources: transactions, gates, registration-fallthrough

**Mechanism:** CpsLimiter (trailing 1s sliding window over ATTACK arrivals, default max-cps 20, per-attacker) runs before everything else; an over-limit click is setCancelled+return — annihilated (no damage, no knock, no flinch, NOT passed to vanilla, nothing journaled). The window counts ALL clicks including mid-invuln ones that would have done nothing, and network burst-delivery (a 300-500ms stall flushing queued clicks) can push a 15-16 CPS clicker over 20-in-1s — so the boundary-LEGAL click of a combo can be the one eaten, pseudo-randomly relative to the 10-tick damage cadence. Verified: over-limit attacks are never handed to vanilla, so there is no modern-vanilla-KB leak here — the failure mode is a wholly eaten hit.

**Trigger:** Sustained >20 CPS butterfly/drag clicking, or 14-18 CPS plus a network stall/burst — exactly the frantic close-range trade. hit-registration max-cps: 20 default; 0 disables.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:250-254 (cancel+return before target resolution); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/CpsLimiter.java:17-62; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/HitRegSettings.java:36-37; core/src/main/resources/hit-registration.yml:10-12 (documented intent).

**Maps to the report:** An eaten boundary click reads as 'that hit did nothing' in a close trade — rare, feel-level, unpinnable; note these hits also deal no damage, which the owner may read as ordinary immunity misses.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Every code claim in the finding is accurate. CpsLimiter.tryAcquire (HitRegistrationUnit.java:251) runs before target resolution (line 255) and before all freshness/immune/cadence gates, so it counts every INTERACT_ENTITY ATTACK packet — including mid-invuln clicks that would do nothing. Over-limit → event.setCancelled(true)+return (252-254): the vanilla packet is dropped, no damage/knock/flinch/journal, and correctly NOT a modern-vanilla-KB leak (it's a total drop). HitRegSettings.DEFAULTS max-cps=20 (line 37) and Feature.HIT_REGISTRATION.defaultEnabled=true (Feature.java:37) confirm the path is live by default. `now` is netty-receive wall-clock (line 250), so a burst flush assigns near-identical timestamps and can trip the 20-in-1000ms count. The finding actually UNDERSTATES robustness: the CPS cancel sits before the fastPath fork (line 303), so an over-limit click is eaten regardless of fast-path.enabled — the finding tied the eating to fast-path being on. I could not find any guard, test, or default that prevents this. What I CANNOT confirm is that it explains the owner's report: an eaten click produces NO hit at all (no damage, no hurt animation, no knockback), whereas the owner describes hits that LAND but with reduced/non-sprint knockback ('the victim just doesn't really move back', 'seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback'). Those are categorically different symptoms — a dropped packet shows no hurt flash. The finding itself hedges (medium confidence, 'may read as ordinary immunity misses'), so it does not over-claim, but as a match to THIS bug it is weak.
- Corrections: The mechanism is real and default-on, but it does not produce the reported symptom. An over-limit click is wholly eaten — zero damage, zero hurt animation, zero knockback — so it cannot manifest as 'a hit that landed with weak/non-sprint knockback', which is the owner's actual description. It would present as a click that visibly did nothing (no flash), which the owner more likely already dismisses as an immunity miss. Two refinements to the finding's own text: (a) the eating is unconditional w.r.t. fast-path — the CPS cancel at 251-254 precedes the `if (!settings.fastPath())` fork at line 303, so it drops the packet even with fast-path disabled; (b) INTERACT_ENTITY only fires on entity-targeted clicks, so air swings don't debit the window — reaching 20-in-1s requires 20+ actual on-target clicks in the trailing second, which is above typical sustained human rates (butterfly ~12-16 CPS) and only realistic for drag-clicking or a genuine network burst.
- Severity: When it triggers, horizontal-KB loss is 100% (the entire hit vanishes), not a partial reduction. But expected frequency in real close-range PvP is LOW: default threshold 20 CPS exceeds normal sustained clicking, so it fires only for >20 CPS drag/butterfly clickers or a 14-18 CPS clicker hit by a 300-500ms stall/burst. Combined with the symptom mismatch (eaten hit vs. weak-KB hit), this is an unlikely explanation for the owner's 'subtle, feel-level, reduced-knockback' report. Real but low-severity and low-relevance to this specific bug.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: CpsLimiter is real and default-on (config.yml:25 hit-registration: true; HitRegSettings.DEFAULTS max-cps 20). It is a strict 20-click/rolling-1000ms binary gate (CpsLimiter.java:43-62): even-spaced 20 CPS passes; only a >20-in-1s burst trims excess. A rejected click is setCancelled+return at HitRegistrationUnit.java:251-254 BEFORE target/damage/knock/immunity — a wholly eaten hit with no vanilla leak. Two facts break the symptom match: (1) The gate has zero effect on knockback MAGNITUDE when it passes — it cannot produce 'non-sprinting knockback' on a landed hit, which is the user's actual descriptor (that requires a non-sprint value in the KB calc, a different SprintWire path). (2) An eaten click does not consume the victim's noDamageTicks (cancel happens before dispatch), so the next passing click ~50ms later lands with FULL damage and FULL sprint knockback — the net observable is a ~50ms-delayed/skipped click, not a weak hit. There is also no close-range correlation: proximity does not raise click rate, so the 'especially when close together' pattern has no mechanism here. Frequency: only >20 CPS clickers or network-burst flushes trip it, and even then the trimmed clicks are overwhelmingly the ~18/20 mid-invuln no-ops rather than the ~2/20 damaging boundary clicks, so an eaten damaging hit is rare; sub-20-CPS players (a large share) never trip it yet still report the symptom. The only surface overlap is that a wholly-eaten click does make the victim 'not move back' for that one click — so the mechanism cannot be said to produce nothing, but it is the wrong symptom class for the core report (landed hits with reduced sprint knockback, close-range-correlated). The finding itself concedes eaten hits read as ordinary immunity misses.
- Corrections: The finding overstates the match. Two corrections: (1) An eaten click does NOT consume the victim's immunity, so it does not steal a hit outright — the next passing click ~50ms later lands full damage + full SPRINT knockback. The net effect is a micro-stutter/skipped click, not a hit with reduced knockback. (2) The gate is binary pass/eat and has no influence on knockback magnitude on passing clicks, so it structurally cannot produce the user's 'non-sprinting knockback' descriptor, which requires a landed hit carrying a non-sprint value (a SprintWire-path phenomenon, not this one). The '15-16 CPS clicker pushed over 20 by a 300-500ms stall' scenario is plausible for producing a dropped click, but a burst-flush drops the queued no-op clicks, and the invuln window is untouched, so a damaging hit is rarely the one lost.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss on a genuinely eaten damaging click: transiently 100% for ~50ms until the next click re-lands full KB — i.e. effectively a one-click, ~50ms delay, NOT a reduced-magnitude hit. Expected frequency in real close-range PvP: near-zero for the majority of players (competitive click rates 8-14 CPS never reach the 20 cap); non-zero only for sustained >20 CPS butterfly/drag clickers or a network-burst flush, and even then the eaten click is almost always a mid-invuln no-op (~18 of ~20 clicks are no-ops), so an eaten DAMAGING boundary hit is rare. Net contribution to the reported 'weak/non-sprint knockback on landed hits' symptom: essentially nil; contribution to a generic 'that click didn't register' feel: small and config/CPS-gated.

## `pocket-servo-min-clamp-fresh-shave` — merged as config-dependent, sources: engine-math, servo-modifiers

**Mechanism:** With modules.combo-hold ON (default OFF — a byte-identical no-op at defaults) and the frozen view saying this attacker holds the victim's active combo, sigma = clamp(0.93, 1.35, PocketServo solve) multiplies the FRESH horizontal (base push + sprint/wtap/enchant extras; never residual, never vertical). A full sprint hit mid-combo naturally overshoots the ~2.85 answer-denial pocket, so sigma* routinely solves below the min and the hit rides the 0.93 floor — a systematic ~7% shave on mid-combo sprint hits (deeper only if an operator lowers min-factor); residual carry has enormous leverage on the solve (~0.11 sigma per 0.1 axis residual), so combos:true presets pin the floor most. Alignment sub-analysis: the hypothesized stationary-attacker ~30% shave is REFUTED (net displacement <0.05 -> NaN heading -> chaseAlignmentFactor 1.0 -> biases sigma UP); but a just-counter-knocked attacker's ring heading reads misaligned and clamps to cos45, under-pricing chase and pinning the 0.93 min more often in trades — still bounded to 7%. Gate staleness: the frozen-view combo gate lags mid-tick retaliation resets by up to one tick, so a 0.93x hit can land one tick after the victim retaliated (bounded, one tick per transition). Mostly INACTIVE in genuine mutual trades since every victim retaliation ends the combo. Degenerate paths decline safely to sigma=1. CLOSE range biases sigma toward the 1.35 MAX (smaller d0 needs more travel), so the servo cannot be the close-range weak-hit source.

**Trigger:** COMBO_HOLD enabled (the owner's 'Combo Solver') + attacker holding >=2 unanswered hits; follow-up sprint knocks ship 0.93x fresh whenever the solve predicts pocket overshoot — the common case for full sprint stamps mid-combo; worst just after the attacker was counter-knocked.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:206-231, :489-492; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:107-115, :331-342, :450-456, :491, :519-541, :535-541, :637-646, :736-760; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/ComboSettings.java:59-64; core/src/main/resources/config.yml:273 (combo-hold: false default); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/Feature.java:282-290; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/combo/ComboPredictor.java:59-66, :311-321; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/combo/ComboTracker.java:110-167; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:332-335, :349-354; KnockbackEngineServoTest.java:60-113; docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md.

**Maps to the report:** A plausible contributor to 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' IF combo-hold is enabled on the owner's server — bounded at ~7%, mid-combo only, and cannot reduce a sprint stamp (0.9) to non-sprint scale (0.4) or explain close-range no-KB (close range biases the servo STRONGER).

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: The core mechanism is real and I could not refute it. Verified in code: (1) the servo sigma is clamped to [config.min(), config.max()] with defaults minFactor=0.93/maxFactor=1.35 (ComboSettings.DEFAULTS:60-61, PocketServo.solve:342); (2) sigma multiplies ONLY the fresh horizontal — KnockbackEngine:210 freshFactor=pace*combo, :212 applied to base push, :221-223 to the sprint/wtap/enchant fresh extras, while :227 leaves the vertical bonus unscaled and the ledger residual is never touched (the A3 law, documented at PocketServo:29-30); (3) sigmaStar=(target−constant−slope·residual)/(freshEra·slope), so a fresh knock that would overshoot the ~2.85 target solves σ*<1 and can pin the 0.93 floor, giving up to a 7% shave on the fresh horizontal. The residual-leverage figure (~0.11 σ per 0.1 axis residual) is correct: dσ*/dresidual=−1/freshEra≈−0.11 at freshEra≈0.9. The finding's own self-limitations are also verified: close range biases σ toward MAX (smaller d0 → smaller constant → larger σ*), so the servo cannot be the close-range weak-hit source; and since residual/vertical/non-sprint scale are untouched it cannot demote a sprint stamp (0.9) to non-sprint scale (0.4). Config gating is confirmed: combo-hold defaults false (config.yml:273) with no bundled preset enabling it, so config-dependent is the correct classification and at defaults this path is a byte-identical no-op.

Where the finding overstates: it calls the 0.93-floor case "systematic/routine" for mid-combo sprint hits, but CHASE_ALIGNMENT=0.70 (PocketServo:80-93) was explicitly calibrated so σ* "centres near 1.0–1.1 at a typical mid-combo residual, landing inside the [0.93,1.35] band." So floor-riding is the worst-case (strongest fresh sprint + large positive residual, or a just-counter-knocked misaligned attacker clamping chase to cos45), not the average mid-combo hit — the 7% is a per-hit worst-case bound, not a mean shave, and it is 7% of the FRESH horizontal only, not of total shipped displacement (residual carry dilutes it further). Also, riding the min clamp is the feature working as designed (the servo's job is to shrink an overshoot into the pocket), not a defect. Most decisively for matches_report: combo-hold is a recent Mental-novel feature (2.4.x/2.5.0 combo era), whereas the owner reports the weak-KB feeling "as far back as I can remember / every version" — a symptom predating combo-hold entirely, so this path cannot be the long-standing bug the owner describes even on an opted-in server.
- Corrections: Mechanism, math, and config gating all verified — not refuted. Refinements: (1) Reframe "systematic/routine ~7% shave on mid-combo sprint hits" to "worst-case per-hit bound of ~7% on the fresh horizontal"; the CHASE_ALIGNMENT=0.70 calibration deliberately centres σ near 1.0–1.1 to keep typical mid-combo hits OFF the floor, so floor-riding is the tail case (strongest fresh sprint + large positive residual, or the just-counter-knocked misaligned attacker), not the norm. (2) The 7% is of the fresh horizontal only; total displacement loss is smaller because the residual carry ships unscaled. (3) Riding the 0.93 clamp is the servo functioning as designed (shrinking an overshoot into the answer-denial pocket), gated entirely behind an opt-in module — not a defect. (4) matches_report should be downgraded: combo-hold is a recent Mental-novel feature, but the owner reports the weak-KB feeling as present "as far back as I can remember / every version," so this path cannot be the long-standing bug even on servers that enabled it. The finding's own conclusions — cannot explain close-range no-KB (servo biases STRONGER at close range) and cannot demote a sprint stamp to non-sprint scale — are correct and load-bearing.
- Severity: Max horizontal-KB loss ≈ 7% of the FRESH horizontal component (base push + sprint/wtap/enchant extras) on a mid-combo hit that rides the 0.93 floor; less than 7% of total shipped displacement once the unscaled residual carry is included; vertical and residual are never reduced. Frequency in real close-range PvP: effectively ZERO — (a) combo-hold defaults OFF and no bundled config enables it, so unaffected unless an operator opted into the "Combo Solver"; (b) even when enabled, genuine close range biases σ toward the 1.35 MAX (boosts, not shaves); the floor is hit only at pocket-or-greater separation with a strong fresh sprint stamp / positive residual, or transiently after the attacker was counter-knocked. Net contribution to the owner's "close-range weak/no-KB feeling": negligible, and temporally inconsistent (predates the feature).

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Mechanism verified against source. combo-hold defaults FALSE (config.yml:273); ComboSettings.DEFAULTS min=0.93/max=1.35 (line 61). The servo scales only fresh horizontal via freshFactor=pace*combo (KnockbackEngine:210, 221-223), never residual, never vertical (shippedVertical is σ-invariant, :346). Solve: sigmaStar=(target-constant-slope*residual)/(freshEra*slope), constant=d0-chaseTravel+drift+tail (PocketServo:340,565). I hand-ran the two report scenarios.

CLOSE-RANGE (the owner's primary scenario): d0 small → constant small → (target-constant) large → sigmaStar LARGE → rides the 1.35 MAX clamp. The servo, when active, INCREASES knockback at close range (it pushes the too-close victim OUT to the ~2.85 pocket). This is the exact OPPOSITE of the reported close-range weak hits. The finding's own "close range biases sigma STRONGER, cannot be the close-range source" is correct. So the mechanism cannot produce the headline "two players close together, little to no knockback" symptom — at close range it would if anything add KB.

MAGNITUDE of the min-clamp shave (the only symptom-relevant path): LEGACY_17 fresh sprint horizontal ≈ base 0.4 + sprint extra (sprintFactor 1.0 × 0.5) = ~0.9 b/t aligned. 0.93× floor → 0.837, loss ≈ 0.063 b/t. Over the flight window (0.4 vertical launch ~8 airborne ticks, dragSum(8)≈5.87) the displacement shortfall is ≈0.063×5.87 ≈ 0.37 block. That is a subtle "slightly less than it should" — but the report's "non-sprinting knockback" feel requires dropping fresh 0.9→0.4 (σ≈0.44), and the clamp floor is 0.93. The servo cannot turn a sprint stamp into a non-sprint stamp. It is bounded at ~7% (deeper only if an operator lowers min-factor).

FREQUENCY in the reported scenario: the servo needs a DETECTED one-sided combo (minHits 2, second hit fires start). In genuine mutual close-range trades — precisely the owner's scenario — every victim retaliation ends the combo (ComboTracker resets on the victim answering), so the servo is mostly INACTIVE there. Combined with default-OFF, the expected frequency in the owner's described mutual-trade close range is essentially nil.

TEMPORAL mismatch: the owner reports the bug "as far back as I can remember." combo-hold is a recent novel Mental feature (2.4.x, 2026-07) with no community precedent, default OFF, never pre-enabled by any bundled config. It did not exist in the early versions the owner references, so it cannot explain the historical breadth.

NOT REFUTED strictly: IF the owner has enabled the Combo Solver AND a one-sided combo is sustaining (attacker landing 2+ unanswered hits), a full sprint stamp that overshoots the pocket does ship at 0.93× — a real, subtle ~7% shave on that sprint hit, matching the narrow clause "sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should, subtle feeling thing." That is a genuine slice of one clause. But it matches NONE of the load-bearing qualifiers: not close-range (biases stronger), not non-sprint magnitude (bounded 7%), not longstanding, not mutual trades. The finding's self-assessment (config-dependent, ~7%, mid-combo only, not the close-range source) is accurate and honest; I confirm it rather than re-litigate.
- Corrections: The finding is accurate as written; no numeric corrections. Two refinements: (1) The servo engages from the SECOND hit (minHits=2, "second hit fires COMBO START"), slightly earlier than the config comment's "3+ hits" prose — does not change the verdict. (2) Note the stale doc: ComboSettings.java:17 still says clamps "[0.8, 1.2]" while DEFAULTS (line 61) are [0.93, 1.35]; the finding correctly used the live 0.93/1.35. Emphasis correction on framing: this is a config-gated contributor to at most the narrowest clause of the report ("sprint hits sometimes slightly weak"), and demonstrably NOT the source of the two headline symptoms (close-range no-KB — servo biases UP there; and non-sprint-feel — bounded at 7%, cannot reach σ≈0.44). It also postdates the "as far back as I can remember" window, so it cannot be the longstanding cause the owner describes.
- Severity: With combo-hold OFF (the default, and no bundled config pre-enables it): ZERO — byte-identical no-op. With combo-hold ON and a sustained one-sided combo: horizontal-KB loss ≈ 0.063 b/t on a mid-combo full-sprint stamp (fresh ~0.9 → 0.837 at the 0.93 floor), ≈ 0.37 block less displacement over the flight; bounded at ~7% (deeper only if an operator lowers min-factor). Expected frequency in real close-range mutual PvP: very low — the module is default-off, and even enabled the servo is mostly inactive in mutual trades because each victim retaliation ends the combo; it fires only during a one-sided beatdown, where it also biases toward the 1.35 MAX at close range rather than the min. Cannot produce close-range no-KB or a sprint→non-sprint magnitude drop.

## `servo-historical-undershoot-242-245` — merged as bug, sources: servo-modifiers

**Mechanism:** In versions 2.4.2-beta through 2.4.5-beta the servo's measured chase channel was systematically under-priced (pre-2.4.5: at-ring idle/w-tap phase read ~0-negative; 2.4.5: post-hit window averaged ~0.11 b/t, 41% of sprint), inflating predicted settle so sigma* solved 0.36-0.86 and pinned the then-min clamp 0.8 on essentially every landed mid-combo hit — 'shipping every landed hit below era' (~20% weak fresh sprint knocks during combos). Fixed in the current tree by the CHASE_ALIGNMENT=0.70 floor + [0.93,1.35] recalibration; not reproducible on current builds.

**Trigger:** Historical only: 2.4.2-2.4.5 with COMBO_HOLD enabled, any sustained combo. Combo-hold shipped in 2.4.2, so reports older than that need a different pathway.

**Evidence:** docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md:26-42; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/combo/ComboPredictor.java:134-142 (javadoc naming the false-low min-clamp mode); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:81-93, :519-541 (the fix).

**Maps to the report:** If the owner's 'as far back as I can remember' includes 2.4.2-2.4.5 sessions with combo-hold on, this acknowledged-and-fixed defect genuinely produced weak mid-combo sprint hits; cannot explain the current build or servo-off configs.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: The finding's code claims are all corroborated. git show v2.4.2-beta:PocketServoConfig.java confirms the min/max clamp was [0.8,1.2] (now [0.93,1.35]); the research doc (2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md:26-42) documents sigma* 0.36-0.86 from the measured post-hit window reading ~0.11 b/t (41% of sprint); the current ComboPredictor javadoc (lines 138-142) itself states the old pre-hit trend read the attacker's "at-ring idle/w-tap phase (approx 0 to negative)" and was "under-pricing the chase, driving sigma* into the false-low min-clamp mode and shipping every landed hit below era"; and the fix (CHASE_ALIGNMENT floor at PocketServo.java:519-541) is present. As a historical code fact it is not wrong — I could not refute it.

Timeline also holds: the pre-hit velocity-trend chase existed pre-2.4.5 and was replaced by the measured post-hit window in commit 7a068dd (2.4.5), then floored in 9af1a2e (2.4.6). Both the pre-2.4.5 trend and the 2.4.5 window under-priced, by the two distinct mechanisms the finding names.

What the finding cannot do — and honestly admits it cannot — is explain the LIVE report. It is a fixed defect gated behind a default-OFF opt-in module (ComboSettings javadoc: no-op "only because the MODULE defaults OFF"). The owner describes an ONGOING "feeling" going back further than 2.4.2 (combo-hold's ship date), with no indication the Combo Solver was ever enabled. So this is at best a partial, historical, conditional contributor for the narrow slice of the owner's memory that overlaps 2.4.2-2.4.5 sessions WITH combo-hold on. On default configs and on the current build it contributes nothing.
- Corrections: Facts verified and accurate, but four qualifications materially shrink relevance to the live report:

(1) DEFAULT-OFF / opt-in. The combo-hold/pocket-servo module is strictly server-opt-in — ComboSettings javadoc: the record is a no-op "only because the MODULE defaults OFF." On any default install this path is dead (zero-touch), so it can only ever have touched servers that explicitly enabled Combo Solver in 2.4.2-2.4.5. The owner's report gives no sign the servo was ever enabled.

(2) Already fixed. Confirmed in current tree: CHASE_ALIGNMENT=0.70 floor (PocketServo.java:93, :535-541) + clamp recalibration to [0.93,1.35] (ComboSettings.DEFAULTS). git show v2.4.2-beta confirms the historical clamp was [0.8,1.2]. Not reproducible on current builds — which contradicts the owner describing the issue as ONGOING ("there is this issue").

(3) "~20% weak" overstates total-KB loss. sigma scales ONLY the fresh era horizontal; the residual carry is never scaled (A3 law, PocketServo javadoc). So a mid-combo hit with real residual carry loses less than 20% of TOTAL horizontal KB even at the 0.8 clamp floor. 20% is the worst case on the fresh component alone.

(4) Phenomenology mismatch. The servo pulls the victim to a controlled ~2.85-3.15 block target SEPARATION — reduced but clearly-visible knockback, not the owner's "victim just doesn't really move back" / "feels like non-sprinting knockback." sigma=0.8 fresh scale is 80% sprint KB, not non-sprint-level.
- Severity: Historical + conditional. Worst case: fresh-horizontal knock scaled to the 0.8 clamp floor = up to 20% loss of the FRESH era horizontal component (less of TOTAL horizontal KB, since residual carry is unscaled). Unclamped sigma* reached as low as 0.36, but the 0.8 floor capped realized loss at ~20%. Frequency in real close-range PvP: ZERO on default installs (module default-OFF), ZERO on current builds (2.4.6+ fix), confined to mid-combo sustained hits on 2.4.2-2.4.5 servers that opted into Combo Solver. Not a match for the owner's generic, still-present, non-sprint-feel complaint.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Verified the mechanism as coded. σ (comboFactor) scales only the FRESH horizontal knock — KnockbackEngine.java:158-226 (fresh = (base−taper)×pace×σ; extras ×σ; residual and vertical never scaled). In 2.4.2–2.4.5 the active clamp band was [0.8,1.2] (the value still living in PocketServoConfig.INACTIVE:58); ComboSettings.java:61 shows the current fixed band [0.93,1.35]. The research doc (2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md) is literally the owner's own playtest report that the servo "frequently undershoots," with σ* solving 0.36–0.86 and pinning the 0.8 min clamp on mid-combo hits — so the mechanism is real and owner-observed.

Hand-computed on the signature/LEGACY_18 preset (base Push(0.4,0.4), sprint extra Push(0.5,0.1)): a fresh sprint hit along the axis is ~0.90 b/t horizontal; σ=0.8 ships 0.72 b/t. Absolute loss 0.18 b/t, ~20% of the fresh horizontal — translating to roughly 0.3–0.6 block shorter settle. Because mid-combo the shipped total also carries the UNscaled residual-half, the felt fraction is even smaller than 20%. Crucially the σ floor is 0.8, so the fresh sprint knock (0.72) never drops to or below the non-sprint value (0.40) — the mechanism CANNOT produce literal "little to no knockback," only a subtle "sprint hit weaker than it should be."

Match against the report:
- STRONG match: "sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should," "very subtle, feeling thing" — a ~20% fresh-horizontal shave is exactly this register.
- STRONG spatial match: "especially when two players are quite close together." The servo engages during sustained close combos and, at close range with accumulated residual, σ* sinks to the min clamp — so close range is precisely where the undershoot pins hardest. w-tap and blockhit both get the same σ scale (wtapExtra 0.5 == extra 0.5), consistent with "even if w-tapping or blockhitting."
- OVERSTATED: "little to no knockback / non-sprinting knockback" — the 0.8 floor caps loss at ~20%, well above the non-sprint floor. The owner's "non-sprinting" is subjective exaggeration; the true effect is "weaker sprint," not "sprint downgraded to walk."

Two hard limiters against it being THE cause of the ongoing report:
1. Config gate: COMBO_HOLD defaults OFF (ComboSettings.java:14, "strictly server-opt-in"). In default config this mechanism produces NOTHING. The owner-as-developer plausibly had it enabled during 2.4.2–2.4.5 playtests (the research doc proves he did), but a stock server never sees it.
2. Temporal gate: combo-hold shipped 2.4.2 (2026-07-04) and the undershoot was fixed 2.4.6+; today is 2026-07-09 on 2.4.8-beta. So this covers a ~5-day historical window only and is NOT reproducible on the current build. It cannot explain "ever since versions as far back as I can remember" (StrikeSync predates combo-hold by the entire 1.1.0→2.4.1 history) nor the present-tense ongoing nature of the report.

So the mechanism plausibly produced a genuine, matching slice of the experience (subtle weak mid-combo sprint hits, close-range-weighted) during a narrow opt-in historical window — but it is an already-acknowledged, already-fixed defect that cannot be the persistent, servo-off, pre-2.4.2 phenomenon the owner is describing. Not refuted (it produces part of the report), but strictly bounded.

One nuance on the "hard to reproduce" claim: the finding says σ pinned on "essentially every landed mid-combo hit," which is actually fairly SYSTEMATIC — more consistent than the owner's "hard to reproduce." A 20% shave on every combo hit would show up reliably whenever combo-hold was on. The small magnitude keeps it in "feeling" territory, but the frequency profile is more deterministic than the report's phrasing, a mild mismatch.
- Corrections: The finding is accurate but must be read with two bounds it slightly understates. (1) Magnitude ceiling: σ floors at 0.8, so the mechanism produces a ~20% fresh-horizontal shave at most — it CANNOT produce the report's literal "little to no knockback" nor genuine "non-sprinting knockback" (0.72 b/t stays well above the 0.40 non-sprint value). It matches "sprint hit weaker than it should be," not "sprint hit downgraded to walk." (2) It is doubly gated: not just historical (2.4.2–2.4.5, fixed in current tree) but also config-dependent — COMBO_HOLD defaults OFF (server-opt-in), so a stock/default deployment never experiences it at all. Also, "essentially every mid-combo hit" is more systematic than the owner's "hard to reproduce"; the small magnitude is what keeps it feeling like a vague "feeling" rather than a consistent nerf. Confidence "high" is fair for the mechanism being real and owner-observed, but it explains only a narrow opt-in slice of a report that is explicitly ongoing and "as far back as I can remember" — it is not the standing cause.
- Severity: Magnitude: σ pinned at the old 0.8 floor scales only the fresh horizontal, so a fresh sprint hit drops 0.90→0.72 b/t (~0.18 b/t, ~20% of fresh; less as a fraction of shipped velocity because the residual-half is unscaled) ≈ 0.3–0.6 block shorter settle. Bounded — it can never reach "little to no" or true non-sprint (0.40) magnitude because the clamp floor is 0.8. Frequency: WITHIN the trigger config it fires on essentially every landed mid-combo hit, weighted toward close range (where residual pins σ* to the floor) — a good spatial match. BUT the trigger requires (a) the default-OFF COMBO_HOLD feature manually enabled AND (b) running 2.4.2–2.4.5 (a ~5-day window, fixed in 2.4.6+/current tree). In default config or on the current build: zero occurrences. Net expected frequency in real close-range PvP: high for the owner's own opt-in playtests in that window, nil for a stock server and nil today.

## `wtap-registration-off-stale-view-verdict` — merged as config-dependent, sources: desk-obligations

**Mechanism:** With the wtap-registration knob off (wtapConsultWire=false) the registration verdict falls back to the attacker's PUBLISHED view sprinting flag — up to a tick stale. A sub-tick w-tap (START then ATTACK inside one tick — the whole reason the wire view exists) reads the pre-START snapshot: sprinting=false, and the hit ships plain. The same fallback (fresh=null) applies to any packetless attacker.

**Trigger:** hit-registration wtap-registration off (default is ON) + attacker re-pressing W and clicking within ~50ms: every such hit loses the sprint extra.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:523-535 (peek wire only when wtapConsultWire, else view fallback with fresh=null); .claude/skills/netty-fast-path/SKILL.md ('the tick-frozen PlayerView is up to a tick OLDER than that contract').

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'w-tapping ... non-sprinting knockback' only on deployments with the feature toggled off — a config check, not the default-path cause.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Verified the cited code directly. The mechanism is accurate as a code fact: with wtapConsultWire=false, sprintVerdict() (HitRegistrationUnit.java:533-534) returns SprintVerdict(view.sprinting(), null, clock.current()) — the published PlayerView sprint flag (end of previous tick, up to a tick stale) with fresh=null, and fresh=null forces freshSprint=false at line 365. That is the documented pre-module fallback (WtapRegistrationUnit doc lines 17-18). So the wire's sub-tick accuracy is genuinely lost on the off path, and a sub-tick START→ATTACK w-tap that lands after the last published boundary reads pre-START state. Could not refute the core code claim.

However the finding is correctly self-limiting and I confirmed the scoping: WTAP_REGISTRATION defaults enabled=true (Feature.java:47) and wtapConsultWire is initialized true (MentalPluginV5.java:168), so the DEFAULT path uses the era-accurate wire. The user's bug is described as present on (presumably default) config 'as far back as I can remember' — this finding explicitly does NOT match the default path and admits it ('a config check, not the default-path cause').

Two overstatements to correct: (1) 'every such hit loses the sprint extra' is too strong. verdict.sprinting() still flows into preAttackerState (line 462), so a continuously-sprinting attacker whose end-of-tick published view reads sprinting=true STILL gets the ordinary vanilla sprint knockback bonus off-wire. Only the narrow sub-tick w-tap window (view momentarily false, or the freshness-gated behavior) loses the bonus. The finding's own trigger phrasing (re-press W + click within ~50ms) is the defensible scope; the 'every' claim is not. (2) The off-path is only reachable when an operator deliberately disables the default-ON feature via the GUI, opting into the documented pre-module behavior.

era_call: the off-path (tick-frozen sprint read) is actually LESS accurate than vanilla, where inbound packets are processed in arrival order within the tick so isSprinting() is current at attack time — the WIRE (default ON) replicates that. So the off-path is a divergence-from-era, but it only manifests behind a non-default operator toggle, making config-dependent the apt label the finding chose.
- Corrections: Code claim stands: off-wire, sprintVerdict falls back to the published (up-to-a-tick-stale) view with fresh=null, losing sub-tick w-tap accuracy and the freshness-gated bonus. But 'every such hit loses the sprint extra' is overstated — verdict.sprinting() still feeds preAttackerState (line 462), so an attacker whose end-of-tick published view reads sprinting=true still receives the ordinary sprint knockback bonus; only the momentary sub-tick w-tap window (view reads false / freshness matters) loses it. Scope to the finding's own trigger (re-press W + click within ~50ms), not 'every hit'. Critically, this requires an operator to have manually disabled a default-ON, era-accurate feature, so it does not explain the user's default-config report.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss when it does trigger: up to the full vanilla sprint-hit extra (roughly one block of additional pushback lost on an affected w-tap hit) plus loss of freshness. Expected frequency in real close-range PvP on DEFAULT config: zero — the feature defaults ON, so the era-accurate wire path is used and this code path is never reached. Non-zero only on deployments that manually toggled wtap-registration OFF (a deliberate opt-in to pre-module behavior), where affected sub-tick w-taps are a minority of engagement hits. Net practical severity for the reported (default-config) bug: negligible.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Mechanism confirmed exactly as described. sprintVerdict() (HitRegistrationUnit.java:523-535) falls back to the tick-frozen published PlayerView sprint flag when wtapConsultWire.get()==false, with fresh=null. That flag is up to a tick stale, so a sub-tick w-tap (START then ATTACK inside one tick) reads the pre-START snapshot sprinting=false and the kernel (KnockbackEngine:214, sprintLevels = sprinting?sprintFactor:0) drops the entire sprint extra. With LEGACY_17 numbers (extra=Push(0.5,0.1), sprintFactor=1.0, base=Push(0.4,0.4)) the hit loses ~0.5 b/t horizontal + 0.1 vertical — a ~55% horizontal reduction, shipping the exact base/non-sprint value. This is the single tightest match to the report's wording ('w-tapping ... it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback').\n\nBUT it is config-gated. Default is ON: config.yml:33 wtap-registration:true, MentalPluginV5:168 AtomicBoolean default true, WtapRegistrationUnit sets true on assemble. On any default deployment a real close-range player always has a SprintWire, so the wire verdict (arrival-ordered, sub-tick) is used and the sprint is registered correctly, distance-independent — the fallback never fires for real PvP (the fresh=null branch only reaches packetless synthetic/bot attackers). So on default it produces the symptom ZERO times. It fires on every sub-tick w-tap sprint hit ONLY when the feature is toggled off, or on the pre-1.7.0 builds where memory records the frozen-view path was the sole pipeline ('byte-identical to the pre-module pipeline') — consistent with the owner's 'as far back as I can remember,' since historically this WAS the universal behavior before the wtap-registration module existed.\n\nNot refuted: the mechanism plausibly and precisely produces the reported experience (indeed it is the archetypal producer of that exact wording) on off-config or pre-module deployments. But it is not the default-path cause, and it does not explain the 'especially when players are close together' clustering on a default-ON deployment (the wire fixes it regardless of range). Config-dependent, exactly as the finding classifies.
- Corrections: Finding is accurate. Two refinements: (1) It is the tightest verbatim match among candidates to the report's 'w-tapping ... non-sprinting knockback' phrasing, because a sub-tick w-tap reading the pre-START stale view is the precise textbook failure the wire was built to prevent. (2) Historically relevant: memory records the wtap-registration module was added ~1.7.0 and the off-path is 'byte-identical to the pre-module pipeline' — so pre-module builds ALWAYS took this frozen-view path, meaning 'as far back as I can remember' is fully consistent with this being the true historical cause even though the current default (ON) masks it in real PvP. Caveat: on a default-ON deployment it cannot explain the close-range clustering (the wire is distance-independent), so that facet of the report needs another mechanism. The verifier must check the OWNER'S DEPLOYED wtap-registration toggle before ruling this in or out.
- Severity: Per-hit magnitude when it fires: HIGH — loses ~0.5 b/t horizontal (sprintFactor 1.0 x extra.horizontal 0.5) x freshFactor plus 0.1 vertical; base push stays 0.4, so shipped horizontal drops from ~0.9 to ~0.4 (~55% cut), i.e. exactly the non-sprint value. Frequency: BIMODAL. Default (wtap-registration ON): 0% in real close-range PvP — every real attacker has a SprintWire, so the sub-tick w-tap uses the fresh arrival-ordered verdict regardless of range; only packetless bots hit the fallback. Feature OFF (or pre-1.7.0 builds): fires on EVERY sub-tick w-tap/re-sprint hit (~50ms START-then-click), i.e. very frequently and pervasively, which would read as a constant, subtle 'sprint hits feel weak / like non-sprint KB' exactly as reported. Net: catastrophic-when-off / absent-when-on; verdict hinges entirely on the deployed toggle, which is not in the repo.

## Merged findings capped out of round-1 verification (unverified as of this round)

### `valve-arm-lifecycle-races` — config-dependent

**Mechanism:** Two stale-arm valve races that can eat or smear knocks. (1) Third-party plugins: DeskRouter resolves and arms at PlayerVelocityEvent priority HIGH; a HIGHEST/MONITOR listener cancelling (or modifying) the event means vanilla never sends the matching duplicate — the arm persists up to one session tick, and because the valve key carries NO hit identity (recipient, entityId, 3 quantized shorts) and stationary close trades produce byte-identical stamps, the NEXT hit's pre-send burst (which traverses the full pipeline and the ValveListener) is consumed against the dead arm; that hit's own tracker duplicate is then eaten by its own arm — the second hit reaches the client with ZERO velocity copies. (2) Blocked-path redeliveries: deliverBlockedKnock arms during the task phase but its duplicate only emits at the end-of-tick tracker; the victim's session-tick clearStale (unconditional, no age check) can wipe the arm first (duplicate ships uncancelled = doubled stamp), or in the !wirePreSent branch the arm can beat the just-flushed burst on the event loop and eat Mental's OWN burst (knock arrives a tick late — mushy).
