**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/DeskRouter.java:53-79 (HIGH priority); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:190-200; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/rim/../delivery/VelocityValve.java:22-49 (no hit identity, last-writer-wins, unconditional clearStale); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:320-348 (clearStale each session tick); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:515-547 (burst :525, arm :533, setVelocity :546); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/ValveListener.java:42-58 (no isCancelled/origin check); PE ProtocolManagerAbstract.writePacket -> ChannelHelper.write (pre-sends visible to the listener).

### `valve-quantization-dedup-misses-extra-kb` — bug

**Mechanism:** Opposite-direction valve defects (duplicate SHIPS instead of being eaten), reported to prevent misattribution and because they add hit-to-hit inconsistency. (1) 1.21.9+: ENTITY_VELOCITY uses Mojang's low-precision LpVector3d (15 bits/axis); the arm key is trunc(raw*8000) but the listener re-quantizes the LP-decoded double, and the LP roundtrip error crosses the trunc boundary on ~12%/axis — Monte-Carlo over era knock vectors: ~32% of pre-sent knocks fail the integer-equality match, so the duplicate ships ~1 tick after the pre-send (refreshed/extended knock). (2) <1.21.9: ValvePayload re-quantizes without PE's PRECISION_LOSS_FIX (+1e-11), so 374/62401 legal shorts roundtrip to q-1 — ~1.2% of knocks ship the duplicate. Both stale arms self-neutralize within a tick.

**Evidence:** PE 2.12.1 WrapperPlayServerEntityVelocity.read/write (V_1_21_9 LpVector3d branch; PRECISION_LOSS_FIX comment); ValvePayload.java:17-20; ValveListener.java:49-56; numeric simulations (32.1% LP miss; 187 bad shorts, 0 in the vy band); VelocityValveTest.java:33-42 (pins integer-equality as the intended contract the decode side violates).

### `presend-never-revoked-phantom-knockback` — divergence-from-era

**Mechanism:** Opposite-polarity contract finding: the pre-send is optimistic with NO revocation. When the authoritative damage is cancelled by another plugin, a full shield block cancels, the attacker is cross-region/retired, or applyPlayer's re-validation fails, the victim's client KEEPS the already-delivered knockback with no correcting packet and no damage (phantom knock, then rubber-band). The validation-fail branches don't even withdraw the pending, leaving a dangling never-armed pending on a connected victim (never time-dropped) until the next hit supersedes it — journaled only then as 'superseded', misattributing the drop; withdraw() itself is silent (no journal, tx never reaches terminal RECORDED, contradicting HitTransaction's own doc), and JournalEntry carries no sprint verdict, so a plain-shipped weak-sprint hit journals as a healthy SHIP — the journal cannot currently diagnose the report.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:209-213, :348-363; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:441-443, :625-649, :701-706; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:62-67 (silent withdraw), :312-328 (orphan journaled late as 'superseded'); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/HitTransaction.java:9-12 (contradicted 'every transaction reaches terminal RECORDED').

### `ledger-residual-decay-fidelity-gaps` — divergence-from-era

**Mechanism:** Two residual-decay fidelity divergences on combos:true presets. (1) Landing slip reset: recordLanding resets slip to stone 0.6 regardless of the landed block, so on ice arenas post-landing residuals decay at 0.546/tick instead of the era 0.8918/tick until the next knock records true slip — between-hit residual survival (the mechanism that nearly doubles era ice KB) is under-modeled for every combo link's grounded gap. (2) Drain-phase race: how many grounded decays a residual takes before liftoff is race-dependent — record() lands at velocity-event time (after tick T's tickStep), and if the client's airborne packet drains at T+1 the residual takes only ONE launch drag vs the era-pinned TWO grounded decays; residuals jitter by a factor of ~1.83x hit-to-hit with ping phase, modulating combo compounding (weaker when opposing, stronger when co-directed). Related bug: LedgerEvent.Reset (world change/death, stated intent 'forget the flight residual') is applied as recordLanding, which PRESERVES the decayed horizontal — a pre-death/pre-portal knock's horizontals survive into the respawn (~9 ticks to rest), so a hit within ~0.5s of respawn/portal folds a phantom arbitrary-direction residual.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:76-85, :94-102 (recordLanding keeps vx/vz, slip reset :100); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/GroundFriction.java:20-27; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/CombatSession.java:230-250 (drain before tick; Reset applied as recordLanding); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:227-239 (stated forget intent), :607-618; MotionLedgerTest.java:94-108, :128-136, :173-188 (two-decay era pins the live race can miss); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md (5b slipperiness).

### `tracker-decayed-dead-knob` — config-dependent

**Mechanism:** KnockbackDelivery.TRACKER_DECAYED is parsed and documented as the opt-in later-joiner wire (which would ship ~half-strength knocks universally — the docs warn a 'players only move ~1 block' report means the decayed wire is shipping), but grep shows NO code path applies the one-tick delivery decay: the only references are the enum and a stale comment 'handled by the desk record'; the desk contains no decay and Deliveries records the shipped value verbatim. A profile setting delivery.melee: tracker-decayed silently ships the FULL stamp. The era-truth finder's checklist item ('a stale tuned file with tracker-decayed would halve every hit') is therefore refuted on the current tree by the code check — the knob is inert, in the un-weak direction.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/KnockbackDelivery.java:22,35 (only non-comment references, grep-verified); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:406 (stale comment); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/Decay.java:104-121 (decayOnce unused by delivery); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:20-24, :110-118; .claude/skills/knockback-profiles/SKILL.md:89-108; docs/research/2026-06-05-era-wire-measurements.md:188-215.

### `engine-and-modifier-pathway-negatives` — era-real

**Mechanism:** Load-bearing exonerations narrowing the search. (1) W-tap freshness is valueless in every bundled preset: all ten ship WtapExtra(enabled=false, h==extra.h, v==extra.v), so freshSprint changes NOTHING; the ONLY engine gate on the sprint bonus is attacker.sprinting() — a real 'sprint hit shipped plain' incident CANNOT originate in engine math and must be an upstream sprint-flag/verdict capture problem (the SprintWire findings). (2) No close-range distance reducer exists: RangeReduction is DISABLED on all ten presets and even enabled returns 0.0 under startDistance 3.0, shaving only the base push (cap 0.12) — structurally incapable of weakening close hits; ComboReachHandicap never touches knock vectors. (3) Pace scaling is attribute-only and signature-only: reads the walk-normalized MOVEMENT_SPEED attribute (blockhitting/sneaking/soul-sand never touch it; base-speed deviation ~1.5e-8, below the wire quantum — byte-identical); only Slowness on the signature preset shaves (down to 0.5x, intended); the historical F1 stance-desync (0.769x weak knocks) survives only in a deprecated overload with NO production caller. Signature's airborne x0.92 trim is small, intended, and scales plain and sprint alike. (4) The whole post-engine modifier pathway is a verified byte-identical no-op at shipped defaults (COMBO_HOLD/handicap default false, PaceScaling.OFF is the parse-empty default, engine skips multiplies at factor 1.0; parse(empty)==LEGACY_17 holds).

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:121-130, :199-231, :282, :324, :482, :489-492, :518-523; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java (WtapExtra (false, extra.h, extra.v) at :36,:62,:100,:126,:148,:173,:199,:228; RangeReduction.DISABLED all presets; SIGNATURE :229-253); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/KnockbackProfile.java:42-69, :107-125, :135, :146; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PaceScale.java:54-86 (deprecated F1 form has no production caller — grep); platform/.../Attributes.java:81-110; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/PaceScaling.java:38; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/Feature.java:282-304; KnockbackEngineTest.java:302-376, :409-450, :572-663.

### `structural-negative-results` — unknown

**Mechanism:** Verified negatives that rule out intuitive hypotheses. (1) Mutual-trade keying is clean: A->B and B->A resolve on strictly per-victim desks with a global AtomicLong HitId and per-victim-session event bracketing; nested thorns-back events are cause-gated — no structural collision exists between trade directions; the only same-desk collision is two hits on the SAME victim (the supersede findings). (2) The healthy-flow valve interleave is self-masking: hit B's pre-send consumed against hit A's resolve-arm requires a sub-millisecond same-thread window AND quantized-identical vectors, and when it fires A's duplicate ships at essentially the instant B's pre-send would have applied — the client still receives exactly one application per hit; last-writer-wins arm overwrites make the late duplicate SHIP rather than eat. In pure-Mental healthy flow the valve cannot silently starve a knock — every loss path needs a dead-duplicate stale arm or a pre-send that never reached the wire. (3) The trade-counter x0.6 fires exactly once per accepted bonus hit (single call site, EDBEE-only, attacker's ledger only) — no double-application exists to shrink residuals. (4) The 2.4.6 sweep guard holds: connected victims' LIVE pendings are never time-dropped under any lag (pinned).

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/delivery/DeliveryDesk.java:25-48, :186-229, :260-283; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/HitIds.java:12-19; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/CombatSession.java:31-50, :110-133, :230-239; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:664-699; kernel/.../delivery/VelocityValve.java:22-41; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/ValveListener.java:56; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:418-423; DeliveryDeskTest.java:330-344 ('sweepNeverTimeDropsAConnectedVictimsMelee').

---

# Completeness critique (Opus)

## Assessment

DO THE SURVIVORS COMBINED EXPLAIN THE REPORT? Yes, but only conditionally, and the mix is dominated by config/client-population unknowns rather than a single default-config defect. Partition of the report: (1) "close together / little-to-no KB" is well-covered by the ERA-REAL geometry cluster — face-hug positional-base-vs-yaw-extra opposition + combos:true residual opposition + sprint-jump facing-push — all always-on at close range and all longstanding ("as far back as I can remember"). (2) "w-tapping feels non-sprint" is covered by same-tick-wtap-start-retro-clear (the ONE genuine default-config Mental defect that flips verdict.sprinting=false on a real w-tap) and, for the owner's likely 1.21.4+/autosprint population, modern-client-no-reengage. (3) "blockhitting feels non-sprint" is covered ONLY if SWORD_BLOCKING is off (default) — blockhit-sprint-rearm-gated. (4) "sprint sometimes weak" is the residual-opposition/×0.6-timing tail. The critical tension: most of the "feel" may be era-authentic geometry the owner perceives as a bug, EXCEPT the retro-clear and no-reengage findings are true divergences that fire MORE than era. Whether the report is a bug or a mis-perceived era truth hinges entirely on unmeasured variables: the deployed profile (combos true/false, friction, verticalMin, resistance policy), the client population (legacy-via-Via vs 1.21.2+ vs autosprint mods), and which optional families are enabled (SWORD_BLOCKING, CADENCE, combo-hold, anticheat AUTO, wtap-registration toggle). BEST SINGLE DISCRIMINATING MEASUREMENT: one rich per-hit DeliveryDesk-journal capture during a live wired 1v1 close-range w-tap trade between two real modern clients, logging for every hit: (a) verdict.sprinting + verdict.fresh, (b) pre-send disposition (admitted / suppressed-by-what / paced-out), (c) resolve outcome (SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE / adopt / PASS_THROUGH / CANCEL), (d) the shipped vector's h and v components AND the exact attacker/victim ring positions + attacker yaw fed to base(), and (e) the effective resolved profile name + enabled feature families. This one capture cleanly partitions the four competing classes: verdict.sprinting flipping false on a real w-tap => the sprint-flag bug cluster; verdict.sprinting staying true while shipped-h is low => the geometry/residual cluster (era-real, do-not-fix); resolve=PASS_THROUGH => the desk-supersede leak; shipped-v=0 => ledger-vy over-decay; an unexpected profile name/feature set => the config-resolution gap. It is the only measurement that separates "sprint flag lost" from "sprint flag intact but geometry cancelled" — the exact fork the whole investigation turns on.

## Gaps named by the critic

### Runtime config/overlay/preset resolution — the actual Snapshot the engine reads at hit time. No investigator mapped how the GUI machine-overlay merges with the human YAML into the swapped Snapshot, nor verified that the profile the operator BELIEVES is deployed is the one base()/verdict actually consume.

**Why it matters:** This is the master gate: at least half the findings are explicitly scoped 'depends on deployed profile' — combos true/false (residual recording, ×0.6 folding), friction.y (vertical floor/immunity), verticalMin (zero-lift), resistance policy (legacy-1.8 random zero-knocks), and whether the effective preset is a combos:false one that 'feels more consistent.' If overlay merge, a stale migration default, or a leftover per-player-override remnant silently resolves to e.g. legacy-1.8 or a combos:false preset, the owner's mental model is wrong and every downstream diagnosis is mis-anchored. It also explains 'as far back as I can remember' if the resolution has always mis-defaulted a field.

**How to check:** At runtime dump the resolved KnockbackProfile actually held in the live Snapshot (name, combos(), resistance(), friction, verticalMin, base/extra) — not the YAML on disk — and compare against config.yml + the machine overlay. Confirm parse(empty)==LEGACY_17 still holds after the overlay is applied, and that no per-player override path survives the 2.1.0 GLOBAL-knockback removal.

### ViaVersion protocol translation of the ENTITY_VELOCITY (and HURT/BUNDLE) packets for cross-version clients, beyond the valve byte-match note. The valve map flags a ~32% observed-side re-quantization mismatch on 1.21.9+ and ~1% below, and BurstSender picks wrappers by SERVER version, but no FINDING modeled what a Via-transcoded velocity actually delivers to the client.

**Why it matters:** The owner's nostalgia-server population is heavily 1.8-via-ViaVersion and/or modern clients on a modern server. Two unexamined outcomes: (a) valve fails to eat vanilla's duplicate on Via clients — usually harmless (identical vector shipped twice) but NOT if the duplicate resolved via PASS_THROUGH to a plain 0.4 (interacts with the desk-supersede leak); (b) fixed-point velocity (value*8000, ±3.9 clamp) re-encoded across protocols could round differently, subtly shrinking the delivered magnitude on a subset of clients — a per-client-version 'some players never get knocked right' signature that reads as subtle/feeling. The presend-throw finding only covered the total-loss throw case, not faithful-but-degraded transcoding.

**How to check:** With a 1.8 Via client and a 1.21.9+ client, packet-capture the velocity bytes the client actually receives for a known pre-sent knock; compare decoded doubles to the armed ValvePayload quantization and to the intended era vector. Confirm the valve consume-CAS fires (or not) per client version and that no plain-0.4 duplicate slips through.

### Folia two-players-in-different-regions during a close trade. Maps note Folia ±1-tick region skew paces out combo hits, cross-region dispatch retracts silently, and non-player Folia hits fall to vanilla — but no finding examined a wired 1v1 where attacker and victim sit in different Folia regions (common at a region boundary).

**Why it matters:** If the owner runs Folia, a cross-region hit can hit the retract-without-fallback path (silent no-op = a wholly eaten hit) or route the authoritative recompute across a region hand-off, changing publish/adopt timing enough to force the recompute path with its residual over-decay. Region-boundary fights would then feel randomly weak — a location-correlated 'subtle' effect no finding predicts. Paper-only investigation would never see it.

**How to check:** Confirm platform (Paper vs Folia). If Folia, stage a close trade straddling a region boundary and journal per-hit dispatch outcomes; look for cross-region retracts and for pre-send-suppressed hits that only appear at the boundary.

### Chronic PlayerView staleness from server-side task starvation / low TPS (not client ping). The stale-view Vanilla-source fallthrough (freshSprint=false, live isSprinting, non-sprint KB) was dismissed everywhere as a 'rare respawn/chunk transient,' but PlayerView.fresh()>4-ticks depends on the victim's region publish task running on time.

**Why it matters:** Under sustained low TPS, heavy session counts, or Folia region overload, the publish task can chronically lag >4 ticks, making the stale-view fallthrough SYSTEMATIC rather than transient — every hit then takes the Vanilla-source path that forces freshSprint=false and can lose the sprint bonus outright. That is the one path that genuinely converts a sprint hit to non-sprint magnitude for a WIRED victim on default config, and it was never examined under load, only under one-off state changes.

**How to check:** Instrument PlayerView publish age per hit during a busy/low-TPS session; correlate hits that resolved via Vanilla-source (freshSprint=false) with publish-age>4. Reproduce by artificially throttling the region tick and re-running the close-trade journal capture.

### The attacker's OWN received knock (victim-role) interacting with their next outgoing hit within the same player. Findings covered the attacker clearing sprint from THEIR bonus hits, but not the reverse: being knocked back mid-trade and what it does to that same player's SprintWire/ground FSM/ring position feeding their counter-attack.

**Why it matters:** In a mutual close trade both players are simultaneously victim and attacker every ~tick. If taking knockback perturbs the attacker's GroundFsm (liftoff mis-stamp on being knocked airborne), their ring position (stale-direction), or triggers any wire reconcile that momentarily reads sprinting=false at their next ATTACK, the counter-hit ships non-sprint — a purely mutual-trade phenomenon that a one-sided attacker-vs-dummy test (the usual rig) can NEVER reproduce, matching 'especially when two players are hitting each other.'

**How to check:** Journal both players' verdict.sprinting and ground/ring state across a symmetric mutual w-tap trade, specifically on the tick each player is airborne from the opponent's knock, and check whether outgoing verdict.sprinting dips on the hit that immediately follows being knocked.

### Hurt-yaw / hurt-direction of the HURT burst and whether a mismatched flinch direction makes correct knockback FEEL wrong/weak. BurstSender ships VELOCITY+HURT; no finding examined the hurt-direction field or how it's computed (which position/yaw source) versus the velocity vector's direction.

**Why it matters:** The report is explicitly a 'feeling thing.' Even when the velocity vector is fully correct, a hurt-animation direction computed from a stale ring position or the attacker-position axis (while velocity used a different axis) can render the victim flinching sideways/into the attacker, which players routinely misread as 'no/weak knockback' at close range. This is a perception pathway that could account for the subtle 'feels off' character with zero actual magnitude loss — and it would make several era-real geometry findings feel worse than they measure.

**How to check:** Confirm which yaw/position source feeds the HURT packet vs base()'s direction; on a stale-ring close-range hit, compare the rendered flinch direction to the shipped velocity direction and to what a real 1.7.10 client would render.

### CADENCE attack_speed-spoof interaction with the modern-client self-×0.6 gate. The client-side finding named this coupling but no finding examined the deployment where CADENCE cooldown-removal is enabled.

**Why it matters:** On unspoofed modern clients the era 0.6^clicks self-multiply rarely fires (charge>0.9 gate), so counter-clicking does NOT weaken received flight. But if CADENCE spoofs attack_speed to keep the charge meter full, the era mechanic returns at FULL strength: every counter-click in a close trade cuts the clicker's own received horizontal by ×0.6 — a dramatic, purely-close-range, config-coupled 'nobody moves back in trades' effect that reads exactly as the report and is trivially misattributed to the knockback engine.

**How to check:** Check whether the CADENCE family / cooldown-removal is enabled and whether it spoofs attack_speed. If so, journal a close trade and measure received-horizontal decay per counter-click against the 0.6^n prediction; toggle CADENCE off and re-measure.

### PositionRing staleness of the DIRECTION source under owning-thread tick-phase / load, beyond the refuted one-tick lateral-angle analysis. The stale-ring finding was refuted on magnitude (base normalized to 0.4) and bounded lateral error to one tick, but assumed exactly one tick of staleness.

**Why it matters:** If the ring writer (once per owning-thread tick) is delayed by region-thread load to 2+ ticks, or if attacker and victim rings are written at different tick phases, the relative-offset error in a fast face-hug compounds and can push the base direction oblique enough that — combined with the era-real yaw-extra opposition (finding 2) — a sprint hit crosses the 129° weaker-than-plain threshold on geometries a real 1.7 server would not. The refutation only holds at exactly-one-tick staleness; multi-tick or phase-desynced rings were not examined and are the mechanism by which the era-real amplifier fires ABOVE era frequency.

**How to check:** Log ring write timestamps and ages for both parties per hit under load; compute the base-direction angle from the ring positions vs from live positions, and check how often the combined base+yaw net drops below the plain-0.4 magnitude at close range relative to a true 1.7.10 baseline.

---

# Round 2 — scenario-general sweep (direction/position staleness, latency compensation, mid-range chase)

Prompted by the owner clarification that weak hits are NOT limited to close range. Finders read
the round-1 doc first and reported only new material; every finding got the same two Opus lenses.

## Pathway maps

### `moving-victim-direction`

Direction/position sourcing has exactly three frames. (A) NETTY PRE-SEND (PRE_SENT and PINNED hits — nearly all melee at defaults): base-push direction = normalize(attackerPos − victimPos) where BOTH positions are PositionRing.latest() samples (HitRegistrationUnit.java:451-474); the ring is written ONCE per owning-thread session tick, at the END of the session task, from live getLocation() (SessionService.java:349-355, PositionRing.java:63-67) — so at ATTACK arrival both positions are 0–1 task-phases old and structurally cannot contain either party's same-flush movement packet. The published PlayerView deliberately carries NO horizontal position (ViewBuilder; the ring is the off-region-safe source). Sprint/enchant EXTRAS ride the attacker's yaw = ConnectionDomains.Domain.lastYaw — the last movement-packet yaw, written per-packet on the attacker's own netty thread (PacketTap.java:76-79) — i.e. click-flush-fresh, era-equivalent; but the enchant LEVEL is hardcoded 0 at this seam (HitRegistrationUnit.java:461-462). HurtYaw for the pre-sent HURT_ANIMATION uses the SAME ring dx/dz plus the victim's packet yaw (HitRegistrationUnit.java:415-419, HurtYaw.java:12-16) — internally consistent with the shipped push direction. (B) REGION RECOMPUTE (REGISTERED/Vanilla — suppressed pre-sends: anticheat AUTO, pace-outs, frozen-immune, resistance profiles, fallthroughs): EntityStates.captureVictim/capture read LIVE getLocation() including LIVE attacker yaw at EDBEE time, 1–2 ticks AFTER the click (KnockbackUnit.java:270-272, EntityStates.java:42-51,73-85). (C) ADOPTION: PRE_SENT/PINNED vectors are adopted verbatim on the region pass (KnockbackUnit.java:256-267) — any registration-frame angle error and the missing enchant extra are baked in; no code path switches sources by range, so range only scales the angular effect (θ ≈ atan(positionError/separation)). Engine consumption: base dir from positions with the <0.01-block random re-roll (KnockbackEngine.java:472-492), extras along attacker.yaw() (:214-227). Era contrast (Q5): era read BOTH positions and yaw live inside attack() at connection-slot processing — the attacker's own same-flush movement applied in-order BEFORE the attack (attacker frame always click-fresh), the victim's same-tick movement excluded in the attack-first mode. Mental's victim-side ring read matches that documented era mode; its ATTACKER-side read is categorically one tick staler than era ever was, and its recompute path is 1–2 ticks FRESHER than era (post-click). Note: the stale victim sample is actually closer to what the attacker's client rendered, so the attacker perceives directions as correct; the victim, who knows their true position, feels the sideways component.

### `latency-compensation`

Latency enters the knock pipeline through exactly ONE gameplay-shaping seam plus two optional ones. (1) Vertical compensation (Feature.LATENCY_COMPENSATION, default ON — config.yml:38, Feature.java:72). LatencyCompensationUnit marks both parties as combatants on every ENTITY_ATTACK damage event (MONITOR) and, on an async 5-tick cadence, sends each a probe over the boot-resolved transport: play PING (>=1.17, ProbeRim matches PONG) or a windowId-0 window-confirmation (<1.17, TransactionProbeRim; action namespace [-32768,-16384] disjoint from vanilla counters, three-gate match, echo cancelled). RTT lands in LatencyModel.Record (last two samples + IQR jitter). Per melee hit, HitRegistrationUnit.compensationFor (netty, at plan()) reads raw pingMillis (null->0) and calls CompensationQuery.verticalFor(frozenView, rtt, view.motion().vy()): declines when noDamageTicks>8 (so max-cadence combo hits are never compensated) or clientOnGround; else it either predicts landing within rtt/50 ticks (override = grounded equilibrium -0.0784) or free-falls the ledger vy forward rtt/50 ticks. The result overrides ONLY the victim vy in the engine's ADD-mode vertical (KnockbackEngine.java:496-500); SET-mode ignores it; horizontal is never touched. The value is stamped compute-once into HitContext and reused by the region recompute. Three of the five YAML knobs (ping-offset-ms, spike-threshold-ms, off-ground-sync) are parsed but consumed by NOTHING; jitterMillis/previousPingMillis have zero production readers — no admission, feedback, or reach window anywhere is ping- or jitter-aware (the FeedbackGate is pure wall-clock arrival). (2) Pocket servo (combo-hold, default OFF): ComboPredictor feeds both parties' RTT (probe model, Bukkit-ping fallback) into PocketServo — attacker half-RTT shortens the judgment horizon t*, victim half-RTT shifts the arc and adds tPing slack to the answer-denial target — so sigma (the only FlightPrediction consumer) varies with ping inside [0.93,1.35] on the fresh horizontal. (3) Reach validation (default OFF) rewinds the victim ring by Bukkit ping + 100ms, capped at 500ms; failure cancels the ATTACK outright. Nothing delays, re-times, or drops a knock by measured latency at defaults. The dominant UNMEASURED ping dependence is structural: the MotionLedger's decay branch (ground 0.546 vs air 0.91 per tick) is selected by the base stamp and flipped only by client-packet ground transitions, which lag ship time by ~RTT — so combos:true residuals systematically diverge from what the client integrated, proportionally to victim ping.

### `chase-midrange`

Mid-range (2–4.5 block) sprint-chase servo, as implemented. Gate: modules.combo-hold (config.yml:273, default false; profile-independent — no preset, including signature, can enable it) AND the victim's frozen view's comboAttackerId == this hit's attacker (HitRegistrationUnit.comboServoFor:182, KnockbackUnit.comboServoFor:620). The tracker activates at minHits 2, gap ≤20t, ends on retaliation/grounded-run(cadence-scaled)/blowout 6.0 (ComboTracker), so a chase combo's hits 1–2 always ship unservoed; σ first prices hit 3+ after a view publish. σ multiplies ONLY the fresh horizontal (base push + extras), clamped [0.93, 1.35] (ComboSettings.DEFAULTS). The solve (PocketServo.solve/simulate): window = per-combo cadence EMA (fallback 10); dragSum = grounded-launch drag schedule (~4.8–4.9 at w 12); victim self-travel = ring-measured drift×S2 + walk-normalized ground tail (a sprint-fleeing victim adds ~0.9–1.05 σ-independent blocks; the tail strips the ×1.3 sprint modifier, under-pricing sprint flee ~30%); chase ladder = (1) DynamicChase ramp when the attacker's ResetModelWire (ENTITY_ACTION-fed only; Mental's post-hit sprint clears never touch it, modern 1.21.2+ clients send no STOP, so it is effectively always-sprinting for them) reads sprinting&&!blocking — alignment×0.2806×attr/0.10×(w − ramp deficit), deficit ≈0 at phase ≥5; (2) else the measured post-hit window EMA (under-reads ~0.11 b/t per the 2.4.6 dossier); (3) else alignment×0.2806×attr model; then floored at alignment×0.70×sprint. Alignment = attacker net ring displacement over 5 samples (4 ticks) dotted with the axis, NaN(<0.05 blocks)→1.0, else clamped [cos45°, 1]: (a) straight chase ≈1.0 → chase 3.3 blocks/12t; (b) SUSTAINED W+A strafe ≈0.7071 → chase 2.38; (b′) ALTERNATING zig-zag (legs ≤4t) — lateral components cancel in the net heading → reads ≈1.0 while the true axis close is ~0.7071× (over-priced 41%); (c) curving chase dots below cos45 → clamped 0.7071. Target: answer-denial boundary at t* = victimPing/100 + turn((yaw−60)/rate) — a fleeing victim (yaw≈180°) gets turn ≈4t → arc ≈0.9–1.3 → target 3.09–3.15 (reach-capped), or 2.82 with the reach-handicap fold (victimReach×0.87). Resulting σ (verified by a fold-mirror simulation): sprint-fresh hits (freshEra 0.9) solve σ* 0.10–0.50 at EVERY d0 2.5–3.5 under EVERY channel → pinned 0.93 (uniform 7% fresh shave, ~0.3–0.4 blocks/hit); plain hits (0.4) sit interior and swing 0.93↔1.35 on channel selection/drift. Declines (σ=1): airTime<3 (juggle verticals ≤0), touchdown reprice, ice, tStar<1. Both seams commit ComboPredictor.MEMORY (anchor + chase/cadence EMAs), cleared on combo END. At shipped defaults the whole axis is a byte-identical no-op.

## Findings with verdicts

### `presend-enchant-extra-dropped` — bug, confidence high (finder: moving-victim-direction)

**Mechanism:** preAttackerState builds the pre-send attacker EntityState with knockbackEnchantLevel = 0 (the 10th positional arg, HitRegistrationUnit.java:461-462 against EntityState.java:15-27); the in-code comment (:456-459) claims 'enchant is corrected on the authoritative pass', but PRE_SENT and PINNED transactions are ADOPTED verbatim at the region pass (KnockbackUnit.java:256-267) and the desk ships the carried vector unmodified (round-1 map: PRE_SENT-unmodified → SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE), so no correction ever runs. The engine's extras term (KnockbackEngine.java:214-227) therefore computes sprintLevels only: a Knockback-enchanted weapon's pre-sent hit is missing 0.5×level horizontal per level, and a NON-sprint KB-sword hit misses the entire extra including the flat 0.1 vertical (era: KB I plain ships 0.9h total, KB II sprint ships 1.9h — compendium extras rule; Mental pre-sends 0.4h and 0.9h respectively). The valve then eats vanilla's duplicate, and vanilla's own damage-pass knock (base-only, since Player.attack was cancelled) was already overwritten — nothing re-adds the enchant. The published PlayerView carries no enchant field (ViewBuilder.java:30-95) and equipment is a live-entity read that is Folia-unsafe on netty, which is why the seam zeroed it — but the promised correction does not exist for the adopted states. The tester is structurally blind to this: packetless FakePlayer attackers never traverse the netty pre-send (they take the Vanilla-mint recompute path, which reads heldKnockbackLevel live and ships correctly), so pre-send-vs-recompute enchant parity is pinned nowhere.

**Trigger:** Any attacker holding a Knockback-enchanted weapon (or a KB book on the off-hand fallback weapon, EntityStates.java:87-99) on default config (pre-send-feedback on, no anticheat): every non-immune melee hit is PRE_SENT and ships without the enchant extra; the same hit ships WITH the extra whenever the pre-send happens to be suppressed (pace-out, anticheat, frozen-immune) — systematic under-ship plus path-dependent hit-to-hit inconsistency. No effect with unenchanted weapons.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:451-464 (the 0 enchant capture and the 'corrected on the authoritative pass' comment); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/model/EntityState.java:15-27 (field order proving the 0 is knockbackEnchantLevel); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:255-267 (PRE_SENT/PINNED adopt — no recompute, no correction; the freshBlockedKnock branch ships tx.carried(), the same enchantless vector); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:214-227 (sprintLevels+enchantLevels gate — enchant 0 removes 0.5·level·h and, when not sprinting, the whole extras block incl. the 0.1 vertical); docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md (sprint and KB-enchant are LEVELS of one extra: 0.5h/level + flat 0.1v; KB II ships 1.4, sprint+KB II 1.9); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/EntityStates.java:87-99 (the live enchant read the recompute path uses, proving the two paths diverge).

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback' and 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' verbatim WHEN Knockback-enchanted weapons are in play — a KB I sprint hit ships 0.9h where era ships 1.4h, on essentially every hit, forever ('as far back as I can remember' fits: the seam shape predates 2.x). If the owner's kits are unenchanted this finding is inert for the report but remains a real defect.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: I traced every link and could not refute the finding — if anything the code is more damning than the write-up.

1. Pre-send capture drops the enchant: `HitRegistrationUnit.preAttackerState` (line 461-463) builds the attacker `EntityState` with the 10th positional arg = 0, and `EntityState`'s record layout (kernel/model/EntityState.java:25) confirms slot 10 is `knockbackEnchantLevel`. The in-code comment (456-458) explicitly says "enchant is corrected on the authoritative pass."

2. The pre-send actually computes the shipped vector from that enchantless state: line 366-369 feeds `preAttacker` straight into `KnockbackEngine.computePaced`, whose extras block (KnockbackEngine.java:214-227) reads `attacker.knockbackEnchantLevel()` = 0 → `enchantLevels` contributes nothing. When the attacker is ALSO not sprinting, `sprintLevels + enchantLevels == 0`, so the entire `if` block is skipped, dropping the flat `vector[1] += extra.vertical()` (0.1) too. Confirmed for both the "misses 0.5·level h" and "non-sprint misses the whole extra incl. 0.1v" claims.

3. The promised correction never runs. The region pass adopts PRE_SENT/PINNED verbatim: `KnockbackUnit` line 256-267 calls `desk.awaitVelocityEvent(tx)` with no recompute; the recompute branch that reads live enchant (line 270+ via `EntityStates.capture` → `heldKnockbackLevel`, EntityStates.java:87-99) is only reached for states that are NOT PRE_SENT/PINNED.

4. I stress-tested the one plausible escape — that vanilla's own enchant-inclusive velocity might leak back in at PlayerVelocityEvent time. It does not: `DeskRouter.onPlayerVelocity` seeds `KnockbackApplyEvent` with `desk.pendingFormula()` (the carried enchantless vector, set via `drainWire`→`replacePending(fromWire, fromWire.carried())`, DeliveryDesk.java:308/319-320), and `resolve` (179-194) ships `tx.carried()` — vanilla's computed velocity (apiX/Y/Z) is only *compared against* the formula to detect third-party tampering, never additively preserved. So vanilla's enchant knockback is fully discarded. The finding's mechanism is solid.

5. Default config exercises it: `hit-registration.yml:42 pre-send-feedback: true`. A connected victim (wire) → PRE_SENT; a packetless victim → PINNED; both adopt the enchantless carried vector. Only a hit whose pre-send velocity was *suppressed* (paced out / vector==null) stays REGISTERED/PLANNED and hits the enchant-correct recompute — hence the genuine path-dependent hit-to-hit inconsistency.

6. Tester blindness confirmed: no suite equips a Knockback-enchanted weapon (grep found only field-copying of `knockbackEnchantLevel`, no `addEnchant(KNOCKBACK)`), and FakePlayer NMS-attacks don't emit the netty attack packet that mints a PRE_SENT, so every knockback assertion rides the recompute path. Pre-send-vs-recompute enchant parity is pinned nowhere.

Refinements to the finding: (a) the mechanism is stronger than stated — there is no path by which vanilla's enchant velocity survives, because the API event is seeded from Mental's carried vector, not the event's incoming velocity; (b) the enchant loss magnitude is `enchantLevel × profile.extra().horizontal()` (the profile's extra term, ~0.4 in LEGACY_17, not necessarily the literal vanilla 0.5), so the exact block figures are profile-dependent though the divergence is unconditional; (c) frequency caveat holds — this is inert for unenchanted kits, and Knockback enchants are deliberately AVOIDED in standard sword PvP (they hurt combos), so it mostly bites KB-stick/specialty kits.

era_call: divergence-from-era. When triggered (KB-enchanted weapon), the shipped knockback is strictly LESS than era truth (era adds 0.5·level h + a shared 0.1 v for any extra levels, per the compendium's combined sprint+enchant "levels of one extra" rule) — and less than Mental's own recompute path. It is a real code defect (a bug) whose gameplay signature is an era divergence gated on equipment, not on a Mental config knob.
- Corrections: Finding CONFIRMED and, if anything, understated. Verified chain: preAttackerState zeroes slot-10 knockbackEnchantLevel (HitRegistrationUnit.java:461-463) → the pre-send vector is computed from that enchantless state (line 366-369) → KnockbackEngine extras block reads knockbackEnchantLevel()=0 (KnockbackEngine.java:214-227), so it omits 0.5·level·h and, when the attacker isn't sprinting, the entire extras block incl. the flat 0.1v → the region pass adopts PRE_SENT/PINNED verbatim with no recompute (KnockbackUnit.java:256-267) → DeliveryDesk ships tx.carried() (DeliveryDesk.java:186-207). The promised 'corrected on the authoritative pass' correction does not exist.

One correction to the finding's own escape-hatch reasoning, in the finding's favour: vanilla's enchant-inclusive velocity can NEVER leak back in. DeskRouter seeds KnockbackApplyEvent with desk.pendingFormula() = the carried enchantless vector (not the event's incoming vanilla velocity), and DeliveryDesk.resolve only compares apiX/Y/Z to that formula to detect third-party tampering — vanilla's own computed knockback is discarded outright. So there is no coincidental-recovery path; the under-ship is deterministic.

Two magnitude/scope refinements: (1) the per-level horizontal loss is profile.extra().horizontal() (≈0.4 in LEGACY_17), so the literal 0.4/0.9/1.4/1.9 figures in the finding assume vanilla's 0.5-per-level and are profile-dependent, though the divergence itself is unconditional and non-zero for any KB level. (2) The recompute path (which reads live enchant via EntityStates.heldKnockbackLevel, EntityStates.java:87-99) runs for hits whose pre-send was suppressed, so the inconsistency is real but its visibility depends on how often pre-sends pace out.

Tester blindness confirmed: no suite equips a Knockback-enchanted weapon and packetless FakePlayer attackers never mint a PRE_SENT (no netty attack packet), so pre-send-vs-recompute enchant parity is asserted nowhere. Correct fix: carry the attacker's held Knockback level into the pre-send EntityState. It is a connection-thread live-equipment read (Folia-unsafe on netty per the original seam rationale), so the level must be published onto PlayerView/attacker-view (like moveSpeedAttr already is) rather than read live on the netty thread — the ViewBuilder currently carries no enchant field (ViewBuilder.java:30-95).
- Severity: Horizontal KB loss = enchantLevel × profile.extra().horizontal() per pre-sent hit (~0.4 b/t per Knockback level in LEGACY_17; the finding's 0.5 is the vanilla figure). A non-sprint KB hit additionally loses the flat ~0.1 b/t vertical (whole extras block skipped when sprintLevels+enchantLevels==0). No angle error — the direction is unchanged, only magnitude. Frequency in real PvP: unconditional on EVERY pre-sent melee hit (default pre-send-feedback:true, connected victim) BUT only when the attacker's weapon carries Knockback — near-zero in standard Sharpness sword PvP (KB is deliberately avoided as anti-combo), non-trivial in KB-stick/bat/specialty kits. Plus a path-dependent inconsistency: the same enchanted hit ships the extra whenever its pre-send velocity is suppressed (paced-out window, anticheat force-safe, frozen-immune) and misses it otherwise. Inert for unenchanted loadouts.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Structurally confirmed end to end. preAttackerState (HitRegistrationUnit.java:461-463) hardcodes the knockbackEnchantLevel positional arg to 0 (field order verified against EntityState.java:15-27), and that zeroed attacker state feeds computePaced for the pre-send (HitRegistrationUnit.java:363-368). PRE_SENT/PINNED are adopted verbatim at the region pass (KnockbackUnit.java:256-267, desk.awaitVelocityEvent — no recompute), so the in-code comment's promised "corrected on the authoritative pass" correction demonstrably never runs. The recompute (Vanilla-mint) path DOES read the enchant live (EntityStates.capture, :42-51), proving the two paths diverge — and the tester only exercises the recompute path (packetless FakePlayers), so parity is pinned nowhere.

In the engine (KnockbackEngine.java:214-227), enchantLevels = attacker.knockbackEnchantLevel() gates the extras block. finish() (:518-537) applies no horizontal cap, and LEGACY_17 limits.horizontal = -1.0 (Limits record is (vertical, verticalMin, horizontal)), so extras contribute in full — the dropped enchant is NOT masked by clipping.

Hand-computed shipped horizontal on default LEGACY_17 (base.h 0.4, extra 0.5h/0.1v, sprintFactor 1.0, grounded aligned), era-correct vs pre-sent:
- KB I sprint: 1.4 -> 0.9 (loss 0.5h, 36%); shipped == a plain sprint hit ("sprint hits sometimes have less than they should").
- KB I non-sprint: 0.9 -> 0.4 (loss 0.5h, 56%) + the 0.1 vertical also dropped (whole extras block skipped when sprintLevels+enchantLevels=0); shipped == a bare fist hit ("truly little to no knockback ... victim doesnt really move back ... seems like the non-sprinting knockback").
- KB II sprint: 1.9 -> 0.9 (loss 1.0h, 53%).
- KB II non-sprint: 1.4 -> 0.4 (loss 1.0h, 71%) + 0.1v.

Path-dependence supplies the "subtle/feeling" character: whenever the pre-send is suppressed (feedback min-interval pace-out, anticheat force-safe, frozen-immune) the same hit recomputes and ships the full enchant, so a KB-sword user sees most hits weak with occasional full-strength ones. Range-independent, which fits the owner's clarification that weak hits occur elsewhere too, not only close range.

Cannot refute: the divergence is a real code defect (dropped field + a false comment describing a correction that does not exist), producing 0.5-1.0 block/tick horizontal under-ship. The one gate is that it fires only when the attacker holds a Knockback-enchanted weapon; with plain/Sharpness-only kits it is inert for this report though still a genuine bug.
- Corrections: Confirmed as written; one scoping refinement. The mechanism is real and structurally airtight: the pre-send builds the attacker EntityState with knockbackEnchantLevel=0, PRE_SENT/PINNED are adopted verbatim with no recompute, and the "corrected on the authoritative pass" comment describes a correction that does not exist. The magnitude is NOT subtle in isolation (0.5-1.0 block/tick horizontal under-ship, plus the flat 0.1 vertical on non-sprint KB hits); the "subtle/hard-to-reproduce/feeling" character comes from (a) path-dependence — pre-send-suppressed hits recompute and ship full enchant, so the same KB sword feels weak on most hits and normal on a few — and (b) the fact that it is range-independent, which aligns with the owner's clarification that weak hits happen elsewhere too, not just close range. Critical gate: this pathway is entirely inert unless the attacker holds a Knockback-enchanted main-hand weapon (or a KB-book off-hand under the AIR-mainhand fallback). If the owner's practice/NoDebuff kits use plain or Sharpness-only swords it contributes nothing to THIS report, though it remains a genuine bug. It is a distinct, additive contributor to the report's weak-KB symptom (separate from round-1's sprint-classification pathway), matching "some hits truly have little to no knockback" and "sprint hits sometimes have less than they should" verbatim WHEN KB weapons are in play.
- Severity: Large magnitude, item-gated frequency. On default LEGACY_17: KB I sprint loses 0.5h (1.4->0.9, 36%); KB I non-sprint loses 0.5h (0.9->0.4, 56%) plus the 0.1 vertical; KB II sprint loses 1.0h (1.9->0.9, 53%); KB II non-sprint loses 1.0h (1.4->0.4, 71%) plus 0.1v. Frequency: EVERY pre-sent melee hit with a Knockback-enchanted weapon on default config (pre-send-feedback on) under-ships — i.e. systematic for a KB-sword kit, at ALL ranges (range-independent), minus the fraction where pre-send is suppressed (those recompute correctly, creating the hit-to-hit inconsistency that reads as a "feeling"). Zero frequency if kits use plain/Sharpness-only swords. KB swords are staple in HCF/kohi/kit-PvP, rare in plain-sword NoDebuff/practice — so real-PvP prevalence is entirely kit-dependent.

### `presend-attacker-position-one-tick-stale-vs-era` — divergence-from-era, confidence high (finder: moving-victim-direction)

**Mechanism:** Refines round-1 `stale-position-ring-direction-at-close-range` with the era-categorical split and quantification. Both pre-send positions come from PositionRing.latest() — one owning-thread sample per tick, recorded at the END of the session task from live getLocation() (SessionService.java:349-355), so a sample can never contain a movement packet from the same netty flush as the ATTACK. Era ground truth (era-accuracy SKILL.md:29-33, compendium arrival-order queue): the attacker's own same-flush movement was applied in-order BEFORE their attack — the era base-push SOURCE position was always click-fresh — while the victim's same-tick movement was excluded (attack-first mode). Mental's VICTIM-side ring read therefore matches the documented era mode (era-consistent by design), but the ATTACKER-side read is one full tick (+task phase) staler than era ever was: a sprinting attacker's source position sits 0.28–0.57 blocks behind truth (sprint = 0.286 b/t, legacy-motion-physics constants). Quantified direction error θ = atan(lateralError/separation), with victim strafe adding a second 0.28–0.57 and worst-case relative error ~1.1 blocks: at 3 blocks θ ≈ 5.4°/10.8°/20°; at 2 blocks 8°/16°/29°; at 1 block 16°/30°/48°; at 0.5 blocks 30°/49°/66°. Perceived-backward loss: a PLAIN hit loses 1−cosθ of its 0.4 push (16°→4%, 30°→13%, 49°→34%, 66°→59%) and gains a sinθ sideways slide (16°→28% of the push shipped laterally); a SPRINT hit (extra rides the click-fresh yaw, which tracks the true axis) loses only 0.4(1−cosθ) of 0.9 (16°→1.8%, 30°→6%, 49°→15%) — so the ANGLE error hits plain hits proportionally hardest, and at ≤1-block crossing geometry the stale axis can fully invert (base ships toward where the victim came from), stacking on the era-real face-hug opposition MORE OFTEN than era. Adoption bakes the registration-frame angle in verbatim (KnockbackUnit.java:256-267); there is no range-conditional source switching anywhere — the effect scales purely as 1/separation, which answers the owner's 'not only close range': at 2–3 blocks the loss is a percent-level backward shave plus a visible sideways component on strafing victims (feel-level), at ≤1 block it is tens of percent to full inversion.

**Trigger:** Any pre-sent hit where either party moved laterally (relative to the axis) since the last session-task ring sample — routine in strafe fights at every range; worst for a strafing/orbiting attacker or victim at ≤1.5 blocks, and for the tick after any teleport/pearl (the ring still holds the pre-teleport position, shipping a fully wrong direction at full magnitude for one tick).

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:451-474 (both positions from sessions.positions().latest()); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:349-355 (one owning-thread sample per tick, recorded at task end); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/PositionRing.java:29-32,63-67,89-92 (single-writer ring, latest()); .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:29-33 + .claude/skills/legacy-motion-physics/SKILL.md ('within a tick, the attack was judged BEFORE the victim's movement packets' — attacker slot in-order, so the attacker's own flush WAS applied; sprint terminal 0.286 b/t); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:472-492 (direction normalized from those positions, full magnitude regardless); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:256-267 (adopt — angle never re-checked against live geometry).

**Maps to the report:** Directly extends round-1's medium-confidence stale-ring finding into the owner's clarification that weak hits happen beyond close range: at 2–3 blocks a strafing victim's hit ships a few percent short backward plus a distinct sideways component (reads as 'didn't really move BACK'), and at close range the same mechanism crosses into inversion territory, making the era-real face-hug near-zero opener fire on geometries where a real era server (fresh attacker position) would not.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Core structural claim CONFIRMED by code. preAttackerState (HitRegistrationUnit:452) sources the attacker's x/y/z from PositionRing.latest() — a single owning-thread sample recorded once per tick at the END of the session task from live getLocation() (SessionService:352-354). KnockbackEngine.base (472-473) derives the horizontal push direction from (attacker.x/z − victim.x/z), while the sprint/enchant extra rides attacker.yaw() (224-226). KnockbackUnit adopts the pre-sent vector verbatim (264-267) with no live-geometry re-check, and the region (non-pre-sent) path instead captures LIVE positions (271-272), so the staleness is genuinely bounded to PRE_SENT/PINNED hits — the fast-path pre-send that serves most real-client melee. The netty movement handler (PacketTap.onMovement:78,88) even parses the attacker's fresh movement-packet location and keeps only Y+yaw fresh, discarding X/Z and falling back to the stale ring — which both confirms the fresh position exists in hand (fixable) and, by the same arrival-ordering that keeps yaw fresh, confirms the era premise that the attacker's own same-flush movement was applied before the attack.

REFINEMENT (severity over-stated ~2x). Relative to ERA the direction error is bounded by the ATTACKER's per-tick movement ALONE. Era direction = A_fresh − V_stale (attack-first excludes the victim's same-tick move); Mental pre-send = A_stale − V_stale. The victim's stale ring position is IDENTICAL in both and CANCELS — it is era-authentic, not a Mental defect. The finding's own text concedes 'Mental's VICTIM-side ring read matches the documented era mode' yet then adds a second 0.28–0.57 of victim strafe into a 'worst-case ~1.1 blocks', double-counting the era-authentic component. That inflated budget drives the finding's THIRD angle column (20/29/48/66°) and the '34%/59% loss' and 'full inversion at ≤1 block' claims. The honest era-divergence is the ATTACKER-ONLY budget — precisely the finding's first two columns: atan(0.286/sep) typ to atan(0.57/sep) worst → ~5.4/10.8° at 3 blocks, 8/16° at 2, 16/30° at 1, 30/49° at 0.5. So no true inversion from the divergence alone (max ~49° worst-case at 0.5 block); Mental inverts only marginally MORE OFTEN than era (by the attacker component), which is the direction the finding claims but not to the 59%/full-inversion magnitude. Everything else (1/separation scaling answering 'not only close range', sprint hits proportionally less affected because the 0.5 extra rides fresh yaw, adopt-verbatim, teleport/pearl one-tick fully-wrong direction) holds.

REFUTATION ATTEMPTS that FAILED: (a) authoritative pass recompute — no, KnockbackUnit:264-267 adopts the pre-sent vector, 'enchant is corrected' but direction is not; (b) region path staleness — no, region path (271-272) uses live capture, correctly scoping the bug to pre-send; (c) fresh position unavailable — false, it is parsed and discarded in PacketTap, strengthening the finding; (d) a straight-line parity test pinning pre-send==region — such a test has zero lateral movement so stale==fresh on-axis and cannot catch it. None refute the core.
- Corrections: Genuine era-divergence in the PRE_SENT/PINNED delivery path only: the pre-sent knockback's base-push DIRECTION is derived from the attacker's PositionRing.latest() sample, which is up to one tick + task-phase (≈0.286 b/t sprint, worst ≈0.57) staler than era's server-current attacker position, and KnockbackUnit adopts it verbatim (never recomputed against live geometry). The region/non-pre-sent path uses live capture and is unaffected. The correct era-divergence magnitude is ATTACKER-ONLY (the finding's first two angle columns): the victim's stale ring position is era-authentic (attack-first mode used the same pre-move victim position) and CANCELS between era and Mental — it must NOT be added, so the finding's 'worst-case ~1.1 blocks', its third angle column (20/29/48/66°), the 34%/59% loss figures, and the 'full inversion at ≤1 block' claim are over-stated ~2x by double-counting era-authentic victim strafe. Max era-divergence angle is ~49° (0.5 block, worst-case attacker strafe), i.e. up to ~34% backward loss + sideways slide, not inversion; Mental inverts only marginally more often than era. Sprint hits are proportionally ~4x less affected because the 0.5 extra rides the fresh yaw (PacketTap keeps yaw fresh) while only the 0.4 base rides the stale position. Note it is architecturally fixable at no era cost: PacketTap.onMovement already parses the attacker's fresh movement-packet X/Z on the netty thread (currently discarded) — feeding that as the pre-send source would match era exactly.
- Severity: Horizontal backward-KB loss for a PRE-SENT hit where the attacker strafed since the last ring sample, era-divergence (attacker-only) budget: lateral error 0.286 b/t typ (sprint, 1 tick) up to ~0.57 b/t worst (near-2-tick task-phase). PLAIN hit loses 1−cosθ of the 0.4 base push and slides sinθ of it sideways: at 2–3 blocks θ≈5–16° → ~0.4–4% backward loss (a few thousandths of a block) + 9–28% shipped sideways — sub-perceptible-to-feel-level, common in any strafe fight; at ~1 block θ≈16–30° → 4–13% backward loss + visible sideways slide; at ~0.5 block worst-case θ≈30–49° → 13–34% backward loss (reads as 'didn't move back'), NOT inversion. SPRINT hit is proportionally ~4x less affected (only the 0.4 base of the ~0.9 total suffers the angle; the 0.5 extra rides fresh yaw): ~1–15% backward loss over the same range. Frequency: EVERY pre-sent melee hit with lateral attacker motion (routine), but magnitude is only feel-relevant at ≤~1.5 blocks; correct my prior note that the third column's tens-of-percent/inversion figures apply — those ride the era-authentic victim-strafe half and are NOT the divergence. One-tick fully-wrong direction after a teleport/pearl (ring holds pre-teleport position) is real but a single tick and rare.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: CODE-CONFIRMED MECHANISM. The two pre-send source geometries are read from different clocks:
- Base push (0.4·direction): KnockbackEngine.base() lines 472-473 use deltaX = sourceX − victim.x, deltaZ = sourceZ − victim.z, where sourceX/sourceZ come from preAttackerState → sessions.positions().latest(attackerId) (HitRegistrationUnit:452), i.e. the once-per-tick owning-thread ring sample recorded at the END of the session task (SessionService:352-354, after tickStep). So the base-push source position can never contain a movement packet from the same netty flush as the ATTACK — it is end-of-previous-tick.
- Sprint/enchant extra (0.5·yaw): KnockbackEngine:224-227 use attacker.yaw() = lastYaw(attackerId) = domain.lastYaw, which PacketTap:78 updates from EVERY inbound movement packet on the netty thread — click-fresh (the same-flush movement is applied before the attack in that flush).

Era ground truth (era-accuracy SKILL:29-33): the attack was processed in the attacker's connection slot BEFORE the victim's same-tick movement, and AFTER the attacker's own same-flush movement — so the era base-push SOURCE position was click-fresh, while the era victim position was end-of-previous-tick. Mental's VICTIM ring read (preVictimState → latest(victimId), also end-of-previous-tick) therefore MATCHES era (era-consistent by design), but the ATTACKER-side ring read is one full tick + task-phase staler than era ever was. This is a genuine divergence-from-era, and it lives entirely on the attacker side.

DIRECTION ERROR IS PURELY LATERAL. Because base push is a NORMALIZED direction, staleness ALONG the attacker→victim axis (a straight-line chase) produces ZERO error — the angle is unchanged. The error appears only from the attacker's LATERAL (perpendicular) displacement since the sample: θ_div ≈ atan(lateralMove / separation), lateralMove = the perpendicular component of the attacker's 0.286 b/t sprint motion × (1 tick, up to ~2 with task phase). This is exactly the finding's per-range θ table (attacker-only columns 0.28/0.57): s=3 → 5.3°/10.8°; s=2 → 8.0°/15.9°; s=1 → 15.6°/29.7°; s=0.5 → 29.2°/48.7°. Hand-verified via atan.

The finding's third column (~1.1 b, ~20° at 3 blocks) folds in VICTIM strafe — but victim staleness is present in BOTH era and Mental (era-consistent), so it is NOT part of the divergence and slightly overstates the pure divergence severity. The divergence is attacker-only: 0.28-0.57 b lateral. Noting this does not refute the finding; its per-range θ table and its proportional plain-vs-sprint analysis use the attacker-only columns.

SYMPTOM TRANSLATION (hand-computed):
- PLAIN hit (all 0.4 rides the stale axis): backward loss = 0.4(1−cosθ), sideways slide = 0.4 sinθ. At θ=10.8° (s=3): 1.8% back-loss, 18.7% shipped sideways. θ=15.9° (s=2): 3.8%, 27%. θ=29.7° (s=1): 13%, 49.5%. θ=48.7° (s=0.5): 34%, 75%. The SIDEWAYS slide dominates the backward loss at every range — a hit that pushes the victim off-axis reads exactly as "didn't really move BACK."
- SPRINT hit (0.5 extra rides the FRESH yaw, only the 0.4 base is stale): back-loss = 0.4(1−cosθ)/0.9. s=2 → 1.7%, s=1 → 5.9%, s=0.5 → 15%. So plain hits are hit proportionally ~3× harder than sprint hits — matching the owner's "feels like the non-sprinting knockback" and "sprint hits sometimes have less than they should."
- ≤1-block crossing/face-hug: θ reaches 30-49° and, on a victim who has crossed past the attacker, the stale attacker source can sit on the wrong side, partially INVERTING the base push and stacking on the era-real face-hug near-zero opener — the engine even carries a deltaX²+deltaZ²<1e-4 random-jitter guard (KnockbackEngine:474) for the near-coincident degenerate, evidence the sub-1-block regime is real.

FREQUENCY. The trigger is lateral movement relative to the axis — near-universal in 1.8 strafe/circle-strafe combat, so it fires in essentially every strafing engagement. But severity scales as 1/separation, so the vast majority of hits sit in the feel-level 2-4% backward-shave + visible-sideways-slide band at 2-3 blocks (perfectly "subtle, a feeling thing, hard to pin"), and only the ≤1.5-block subset reaches the tens-of-percent / inversion regime the owner flags as "especially when close." The teleport/pearl one-tick-fully-wrong case (ring holds pre-teleport position) is real but rare/transient. No range-conditional source switching exists, so the effect is continuous across range — directly answering the owner's clarification that weak hits are not only close-range.

Not refuted: the mechanism is confirmed in code, the geometry is hand-verified, and it plausibly produces every part of the report (subtle mid-range feel + pronounced close-range weakness + plain-reads-as-non-sprint).
- Corrections: The finding is confirmed with one scope correction: the divergence-from-era is ATTACKER-side only. Mental's victim-position ring read (end-of-previous-tick) MATCHES era's attack-first exclusion of the victim's same-tick movement, so victim staleness is era-real, not a divergence. The divergence is that the base-push SOURCE (attacker) position is one tick + task phase stale, whereas era's attacker source was click-fresh (same-flush movement applied before the attack). The finding's per-range θ table and plain-vs-sprint proportional analysis correctly use the attacker-only 0.28/0.57-block columns; only its ~1.1-block "worst-case relative error" column folds in era-consistent victim strafe and thus slightly overstates the pure divergence. Additionally: the error is purely from the LATERAL component of attacker motion — a straight-line chase produces zero angle error, so the effect is specifically a strafe/orbit phenomenon, which sharpens (rather than weakens) the match to the owner's "hard to reproduce" report.
- Severity: Horizontal-backward KB loss on a PLAIN hit = 0.4·(1−cosθ_div) with a larger 0.4·sinθ_div sideways slide; SPRINT hit loss = 0.4·(1−cosθ)/0.9 (~3× smaller, extra rides fresh yaw). Attacker-only divergence θ: s=3 →5-11°, s=2 →8-16°, s=1 →16-30°, s=0.5 →29-49°. Backward loss: 2-3 b ≈ 0.5-4% plain / <2% sprint but with a 9-27% sideways slide (the dominant perceptual term); ≤1 b ≈ 13-34% plain / 6-15% sprint plus possible base-push partial inversion at face-hug. FREQUENCY: trigger (lateral movement) fires in nearly all strafe combat, so it is near-constant; but perceptible (>10% back-loss / obvious slide) severity concentrates at ≤1.5 blocks — high-frequency at feel-level everywhere, high-magnitude only close. Note: the divergence is ATTACKER-side only; the finding's ~1.1-block/20° worst case folds in era-consistent victim strafe and modestly overstates the pure divergence.

### `recompute-extras-ride-damage-time-yaw` — divergence-from-era, confidence high (finder: moving-victim-direction)

**Mechanism:** Extends round-1 `suppressed-presend-recompute-reads-late-state` (which covered positions/ledger) with the YAW component it did not name. For every non-adopted hit (REGISTERED: anticheat-suppressed, feedback-gate paced-out, frozen-immune registration, LEGACY-resistance victims; plus all Vanilla-source melee), the region recompute captures the attacker with EntityStates.capture → live location.getYaw() at EDBEE time, 1–2 ticks AFTER the click (KnockbackUnit.java:270-272; EntityStates.java:42-51). Era read the yaw inside attack() at connection-slot processing — the click-flush yaw, the exact value Mental's PRE-SEND path correctly uses via domain.lastYaw (PacketTap.java:76-79, HitRegistrationUnit.java:461). A flicking attacker (flick to target, click, snap back to run heading — the strafe-fight norm; 100 ms at ordinary 300–800°/s mouse speed = 30–80° of yaw change) ships the sprint/enchant extra rotated off the click aim by that Δyaw: the extra's along-axis contribution scales cos(Δyaw) — 0.5→0.43 at 30°, 0.25 at 60°, 0 at 90° — so a legacy-1.7 sprint hit's away-component drops from 0.9 to ~0.83/0.65/0.4 respectively; at 0.4 it is literally indistinguishable from the plain-hit value ('the non-sprinting knockback'). Because the SprintVerdict IS stamped at registration (the design's stated era-moment freeze, HitRegistrationUnit.java:321-330) while the geometry and yaw are NOT stamped into the HitContext, the recompute path half-honors its own era-moment contract. With AnticheatMode.AUTO and GrimAC/Vulcan installed this applies to 100% of hits.

**Trigger:** Any suppressed-pre-send or Vanilla-source melee hit thrown by an attacker who rotates between the click and the deferred damage (1–2 ticks): systematic on servers with a detected anticheat (all hits recompute), per-hit under feedback-gate pace-outs and frozen-immune-band registrations, and for every respawn-window/fastPath-off fallthrough hit.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:270-272 (EntityStates.capture(attacker, sprinting) at EDBEE); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/EntityStates.java:42-51 (location.getYaw() — live at capture); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:224-227 (extras along attacker.yaw()); contrast the pre-send's click-time yaw: core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:461 + :493-496 and core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/PacketTap.java:76-79 (per-packet lastYaw); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/model/HitContext (carries verdict/compensationY but no yaw/positions — the geometry escapes the registration stamp); era: docs/research/2026-06-06-combat-compendium.md:95-100 (addVelocity along yaw read inside attack()).

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' with the report's intermittency built in: only the jitter/anticheat-selected recompute subset of hits is affected, and only when the attacker happened to flick — unpinnable by construction. On anticheat-running deployments (owner memory says feel issues span setups) this is systematic rather than occasional.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: CONFIRMED with scope/severity refinements. Adversarial attempts to refute failed on the core mechanism, and the default config actually strengthens it.

Verified chain: (1) fast path cancels the interact packet (HitRegistrationUnit:306) and defers damage via scheduling.runOn (line 441) → applyPlayer → victim.damage(attacker) (line 693), so the EDBEE KnockbackUnit rides fires at the SCHEDULED region tick, not synchronously. (2) For a REGISTERED hit (pre-send suppressed) the state is not PRE_SENT/PINNED, so KnockbackUnit falls to the recompute at line 270-272: EntityStates.capture(attacker, sprinting) reads LIVE location.getYaw() (EntityStates:47). (3) HitContext (kernel record) carries sprint/victimHasWire/compensationY/registeredAt but NO yaw and NO positions — so the click-aim yaw domain.lastYaw that the pre-send path uses (preAttackerState:461) is never frozen and is lost; the recompute reads live yaw. (4) KnockbackEngine:224-227 directs the sprint/enchant EXTRA along attacker.yaw() (base push at 462-488 is along the attacker→victim POSITION axis, unaffected). (5) Severity math is exact for LEGACY_17 (base Push(0.4), extra Push(0.5,0.1), sprintFactor 1.0): away = 0.4 + 0.5·cos(Δyaw) → 0.83/0.65/0.4 at 30/60/90°, the flat 0.1 vertical extra untouched.

Default config makes it systematic, not occasional: AnticheatSettings.DEFAULTS = AUTO with knownPlugins GrimAC/Vulcan; AnticheatCompatUnit:84 AUTO→permissive=detected.isEmpty(), so with either anticheat installed allowVelocityPreSend=false → suppressorFor returns 'anticheat' → EVERY hit stays REGISTERED → every sprint/enchant hit recomputes at the deferred EDBEE with live yaw. That is the standard competitive-server setup.

Two refutations of the finding's over-claims (hence not fully as stated, but not refuted): (a) 'all Vanilla-source melee' is WRONG — a Vanilla-source (fastPath-off / native) hit fires the EDBEE synchronously inside vanilla's attack processing; by FIFO packet order location.getYaw() there is the look packet immediately before the interact = the click aim = era-correct, and whatever vanilla reads IS era by definition, so no divergence. Only the fast-path cancel+runOn REGISTERED subset is affected. (b) The 100 ms / 30-80° figure overstates the typical drift: the applyPlayer deferral is ~1 tick, so a fast flick drifts ~15-40°, giving a typical 3-15% away-loss, with the collapse-to-0.4 (full sprint-bonus loss) being the ~90°-flick tail. Exact main-thread ordering (scheduler heartbeat vs. connection packet drain) adds magnitude uncertainty but the yaw is unfrozen/live either way, so the drift exists under any attacker rotation.

era_call: divergence-from-era. Era read the attacker yaw synchronously inside attack() (click aim); Mental's deferred recompute reads a later yaw purely because of the fast path's cancel+defer architecture. The triggering config (AUTO anticheat suppression) is a coexistence necessity, not a knockback-feel choice, so this is a genuine era divergence rather than intended config-dependent behavior. This is a legitimate and significant extension of round-1's suppressed-presend-recompute-reads-late-state: the yaw term can zero out the ENTIRE sprint bonus contribution to the away axis (the exact 'sprint hit shows non-sprinting knockback' symptom), whereas the positions term round-1 named mostly shifts direction.
- Corrections: Finding stands with two corrections. SCOPE: 'all Vanilla-source melee' is wrong — Vanilla-source (fastPath-off/native) hits fire the EDBEE synchronously during vanilla's attack processing, where location.getYaw() equals the click-aim yaw (FIFO: snap-back look packets are dequeued after the interact) and is era-correct by definition. The affected class is specifically the fast-path REGISTERED subset: the interact packet is cancelled (HitRegistrationUnit:306) and damage is deferred via scheduling.runOn (line 441) → applyPlayer → victim.damage, so the recompute at KnockbackUnit:270-272 reads the attacker's LIVE yaw ~1 tick late. Those cases are: anticheat-suppressed (systematic — see below), feedback-gate paced-out velocities, frozen-immune (damageImmune) registrations, and LEGACY-resistance-roll victims. SEVERITY MAGNITUDE: the 100 ms / 30-80° drift overstates the typical case — the applyPlayer deferral is ~1 tick (~50 ms), so a fast 300-800°/s flick drifts ~15-40°, giving away 0.83-0.88 (a 3-15% total-KB loss); the collapse to 0.4 (indistinguishable from the non-sprint value, ~44% loss) requires a ~90° flick landing inside the deferral window — real but the tail, not the mode. Everything else in the finding is confirmed: HitContext carries no yaw (verified), the extra is yaw-directed while the base push is position-axis-directed, LEGACY_17 gives away = 0.4 + 0.5·cos(Δyaw) exactly, and the fix implied (freeze the click-time attacker yaw into HitContext at registration, alongside the SprintVerdict, and have the recompute use it) is the right shape.
- Severity: Per affected hit: the sprint/enchant horizontal extra (0.5 on LEGACY_17) rotates by the applyPlayer-deferral yaw drift; away-component = 0.4 + 0.5·cos(Δyaw). Typical 1-tick flick Δyaw ~15-40° → away 0.83-0.88 (3-15% total horizontal-KB loss); hard 1-2 tick flick 40-90° → away 0.49-0.65 down to 0.40 at 90° (full sprint-bonus loss, ~44%). Vertical extra (flat 0.1) and the base 0.4 position-axis push are unaffected. FREQUENCY: SYSTEMATIC — 100% of melee hits — under the DEFAULT config on any server running GrimAC or Vulcan (AnticheatMode.AUTO suppresses the velocity pre-send → all hits REGISTERED → all recompute at the deferred EDBEE), i.e. the standard competitive PvP setup; otherwise limited to paced-out fast combos, frozen-immune-band registrations, and LEGACY-resistance victims. Vanilla-source (fastPath-off) melee is NOT affected. Only manifests when the attacker rotates between click and the ~1-tick-late damage application — the flick/strafe norm, most frequent in the close-range fights the owner flags, but present at any range.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Mechanism confirmed line-by-line. Two delivery paths compute the era vector for the SAME hit but read DIFFERENT yaw: (1) the pre-send/adopted path uses the click-flush yaw (HitRegistrationUnit.preAttackerState → lastYaw → domain.lastYaw, the per-movement-packet look captured at ATTACK registration, PacketTap.java:76-79); (2) the REGISTERED recompute path (KnockbackUnit.java:270-272) re-captures the attacker LIVE at EDBEE via EntityStates.capture → location.getYaw() (EntityStates.java:46), on the region thread 0-2 ticks after the click. The sprint/enchant extras are applied along attacker.yaw() (KnockbackEngine.java:224-226), while the base 0.4 push is positional and thus yaw-immune. HitContext (kernel/model/HitContext.java) freezes the SprintVerdict and compensationY but NOT yaw/positions, so the recompute honors the frozen sprint answer yet reads a stale-by-1-2-ticks live yaw for the extras — the "half-honored era-moment freeze" the finding names. Vanilla read the yaw synchronously inside attack() at click-flush (compendium:95-100), so the extra always pointed along the exact click aim; Mental's recompute points it along the aim 1-2 ticks later.

Path selection confirmed: suppressorFor returns "anticheat" whenever anticheat.allowVelocityPreSend() is false, which under AnticheatMode.AUTO with a detected GrimAC/Vulcan is false for EVERY melee hit — so on those deployments 100% of hits recompute and are subject to yaw drift. Also fires per-hit on resistance-roll victims and on all Vanilla-source melee (fastPath-off / respawn window / packetless attacker fallthrough).

Timing: the ATTACK packet registers on netty; the damage task runs on the victim's region thread the next tick; the attacker's Bukkit yaw is updated by their movement packets processed on the region thread in the interim, so the live yaw at EDBEE reflects the attacker's aim ~1 tick (up to 2) after the click — non-zero drift whenever the attacker is turning.

Hand-computation (legacy-1.7 default: base push 0.4 positional, extra 0.5 yaw-directed, sprintFactor 1.0; grounded victim dead ahead, zero residual). Correct away-KB = 0.4 + 0.5·cos(0) = 0.90. Recompute with flick Δyaw between click and EDBEE, away = 0.4 + 0.5·cos(Δyaw): Δyaw 15° → 0.883 (−1.9%); 30° → 0.833 (−7.4%); 45° → 0.754 (−16%); 60° → 0.65 (−28%); 90° → 0.40 (−56%, EXACTLY the non-sprinting plain-hit value); >90° → below 0.40 (weaker than a plain hit). Additionally the extra diverts 0.5·sin(Δyaw) sideways, so beyond magnitude loss the victim is launched off-axis (an angular "feels wrong" skew) — 0.433 sideways at 60°.

Range-independence is the key strength versus the round-1 findings and directly answers the owner's clarification: the round-1 dominant mechanisms (face-hug positional-vs-yaw opposition, residual cancellation) are close-range geometry effects. This yaw-drift effect shaves the sprint extra at ALL ranges — even a dead-ahead victim at long range, where the geometry opposition does not apply, loses the extra to tracking/flick drift. So this is the primary way a sprint hit ships weak away from close range, exactly the scenario the first round under-covered.

Match to report: "sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should" is a direct match — only the SPRINT/enchant extra is yaw-directed, so it is specifically the sprint bonus that gets shaved while the plain 0.4 base is untouched. "seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback" is verbatim at Δyaw=90° (away = 0.40 = plain). "subtle, hard to reproduce, a feeling" fits because the loss depends on exactly how far the mouse moved in a 50-100ms window the player cannot perceive or reproduce. Owner memory "feel issues span setups" fits the systematic anticheat origin.

Not refuted: mechanism is real, confirmed, produces the exact symptom, and is range-general.

era_call: I call it bug (with a strong divergence-from-era face). The design's own contract (HitContext javadoc: "prediction and truth call the same decision function over this immutable context") is violated — the recompute reads a live yaw that can differ from the registration-moment yaw the pre-send used, so prediction≠truth for the same hit. The SprintVerdict half of the same context IS frozen and consumed, proving the freeze pattern was intended and the click-time yaw was available; the yaw simply was never added to the frozen context. The observable consequence is a divergence from era (vanilla's synchronous in-attack read), so the finding's "divergence-from-era" label is also fair, but the root is an incomplete freeze — a defect against the compute-once design, gated to the recompute-selected subset (anticheat=100%, resistance/vanilla-source per-hit).
- Severity: Horizontal away-KB loss on legacy-1.7 sprint hits = 0.5·(1−cosΔyaw) blocks/tick off the 0.90 away-baseline: Δyaw 15°→−0.017 (−1.9%), 30°→−0.067 (−7.4%), 45°→−0.146 (−16%), 60°→−0.25 (−28%), 90°→−0.50 (−56%, ships EXACTLY the 0.40 plain-hit value), >90° ships below plain. Plus an angular skew: the extra diverts 0.5·sinΔyaw sideways (0.433 at 60°), launching the victim off-axis. Frequency: on AnticheatMode.AUTO + GrimAC/Vulcan deployments EVERY melee hit recomputes (100%), so the drift applies to all hits — baseline close/mid strafe TRACKING drift of ~7-15° per 1-2 ticks shaves ~2-4% off every single hit systematically; deliberate aim-snap flicks (30-60° in 50-100ms) shave 7-28% intermittently; the sprint→plain extreme (≥90°) is the rarer sharp-flick tail. On non-anticheat servers it is per-hit only on Vanilla-source melee (fastPath-off/respawn/packetless-attacker) and resistance-roll victims — much rarer. Range-independent (the distinguishing property): shaves the sprint bonus at long/mid range where the round-1 close-range geometry findings cannot fire.

### `hurt-tilt-fresher-than-push-direction` — divergence-from-era, confidence low (finder: moving-victim-direction)

**Mechanism:** Q4 resolution.
