The pre-sent burst's flinch and its velocity are internally consistent: HurtYaw.hurtYaw uses the SAME ring dx/dz as the shipped push direction plus the victim's packet-fresh lastYaw (HitRegistrationUnit.java:415-419; HurtYaw.java:12-16 — vanilla's exact atan2 extraction, unit-pinned in HurtYawTest), so the pre-send tilt and pre-send push agree bit-for-bit; below 1.19.4 the hurt degrades to directionless entity-status 2 and the question is moot. The divergence: the authoritative victim.damage() then runs vanilla's full pipeline, which broadcasts its OWN hurt/damage feedback computed from LIVE damage-time positions 1–2 ticks fresher; the ValveListener consumes only the duplicate ENTITY_VELOCITY, never the duplicate hurt (by design — BurstSender.java:26-30 'duplicates are fine'). The client applies last-write-wins on the tilt, so the FELT flinch direction is the fresh geometry while the SHIPPED push is the registration-frozen geometry — they disagree by exactly the staleness angle θ of finding presend-attacker-position-one-tick-stale-vs-era (up to ~30-50° at ≤1 block with strafing). Era sent ONE hurt and ONE velocity from the same processing instant — tilt and push always agreed. A tilt that says 'hit from your left' while the push goes 'backward' reads as wrong/mushy knockback even at full magnitude.

**Trigger:** Any pre-sent hit on 1.19.4+ where either party moved laterally between the ring sample and the deferred damage — the same strafe-fight population as the position-staleness finding; imperceptible for stationary pairs (both frames agree).

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:415-419 (hurtYaw from the same ring reads as the vector); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/HurtYaw.java:12-16; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/BurstSender.java:26-30,84-93 (HURT_ANIMATION 1.19.4+/status-2 below; duplicates-by-design note); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/ValveListener (velocity-only consumption, per round-1 valve map); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:581-585 (the blocked-knock redelivery computes hurtYawFor from LIVE locations — a third frame, consistent with its own live-computed vector).

**Maps to the report:** Contributes to the 'more like a feeling thing' texture: hits whose magnitude is correct still FEEL misdirected because the victim's flinch tilt (fresh) and their actual displacement (stale-frame) disagree; not a magnitude loss, so it cannot alone explain 'doesn't move back', but it plausibly shapes the owner's inability to pin the sensation.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Traced the full chain and could not refute it. (1) Pre-send push direction and hurtYaw both derive from the same PositionRing.latest() frame (HitRegistrationUnit vector build 352-369/452-467 vs hurtYaw 415-419) — internally consistent, as claimed. (2) BurstSender degrades to directionless ENTITY_STATUS 2 below 1.19.4 (lines 90-92) — moot there, correct. (3) The authoritative pass calls victim.damage(...) on the region thread ~1 tick later (applyPlayer→damageWithSlot line 693), running vanilla's pipeline which broadcasts the modern ClientboundHurtAnimationPacket from LIVE damage-time positions. This hurt is NOT suppressed: ValveListener cancels only ENTITY_VELOCITY (line 42) and is the sole outbound suppressor; nothing eats the duplicate hurt. So last-write-wins gives the client the fresh-frame tilt. (4) I specifically tried to refute via 'the authoritative velocity is also fresh and would override the frozen push, re-converging tilt and push' — this fails: DeliveryDesk.resolve case 3 (189-194) ships the CARRIED frozen pre-sent vector and arms the valve, so the authoritative velocity is byte-identical and cancelled; the client keeps the frozen ring-frame push. Push stays frozen while tilt ships fresh — the divergence is real code behavior. Era nuance: real 1.7/1.8 hurt was directionless (entity status 2), so the finding's 'era always agreed' is vacuous for the era itself; the correct baseline is vanilla-modern, where one damage() emits one velocity + one hurt from the same live frame that agree. Mental's pre-send/re-deliver split is what desyncs them — a divergence from vanilla-modern and from era feel alike. The finding is accurate but self-limiting (low confidence, explicitly a visual-tilt-only texture contributor, zero magnitude loss).
- Corrections: Confirmed as a real code-level divergence; not refuted. Refinements: (a) The finding's 'era sent ONE hurt and ONE velocity that always agreed' is imprecise about the ERA specifically — 1.7/1.8 hurt was DIRECTIONLESS (entity status 2), so there was no directional tilt to agree/disagree. The accurate baseline for the tilt/push agreement is vanilla-MODERN (1.19.4+ without Mental): a single victim.damage() emits one velocity and one hurt from the same live frame, so they agree. Mental's pre-send-then-authoritative-redeliver architecture is what desynchronizes them — the divergence is from vanilla-modern (and, trivially, era had no directional tilt at all). (b) The push-stays-frozen half is load-bearing and verified: DeliveryDesk.resolve case 3 (kernel/.../DeliveryDesk.java:189-194) ships the CARRIED frozen pre-sent vector and arms the valve, so the byte-identical authoritative velocity is cancelled and the client keeps the ring-frame push; the fresh authoritative velocity never reaches the client, so tilt and push cannot re-converge. (c) KnockbackUnit.hurtYawFor (581-585) is a THIRD, self-consistent live frame used only on the blocked-knock redelivery path — it computes both its hurt and its own vector from the same live locations, so it is NOT a divergence source itself (consistent with its own push); it only matters for blocked hits, a narrower population than the main melee path. (d) Scope: 1.19.4+ only; strafing/lateral-motion pairs only; visual-only, zero magnitude loss — a 'feeling' texture contributor, not an explanation for 'doesn't move back'.
- Severity: Zero horizontal-KB magnitude loss — this is a pure hurt-tilt direction mismatch (visual/proprioceptive), not a push weakening, so it cannot by itself produce the owner's 'doesn't move back'. Angle error bounded by the sibling position-staleness angle theta (finding cites up to ~30-50 deg at <=1 block with strafing; typically a few deg to ~20 deg for a 0.2-0.3 block lateral drift at sub-block range). Gated to 1.19.4+ clients only (directionless below). Frequency: same population as the position-staleness finding — common in close-range strafe fights where either party moves laterally between the ring sample and deferred damage; imperceptible for stationary/co-linear pairs (both frames agree). Net: a subtle 'mushy/misdirected but full-strength' feel contributor on modern clients, well below the threshold of a magnitude complaint.

**SYMPTOM lens: REFUTED** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: The mechanism is real as coded. Pre-send: HitRegistrationUnit.java:415-419 computes hurtYaw from the SAME frozen ring geometry (positionX/Z of attacker & victim, lastYaw) that produces the shipped push vector `shipped`, so the pre-sent HURT_ANIMATION tilt and the pre-sent ENTITY_VELOCITY push agree bit-for-bit. BurstSender.java:26-30 confirms the authoritative vanilla path re-emits its own hurt animation ("duplicates are fine by design"), and per the round-1 valve map ValveListener eats only the duplicate ENTITY_VELOCITY, never the duplicate hurt. Vanilla's LivingEntity hurt path recomputes hurtDir = atan2(dz,dx)*180/pi - yRot from LIVE damage-time positions 1-2 ticks fresher, so on 1.19.4+ the client's last-write-wins tilt ends up on the fresh geometry while the displacement it applied is the frozen-registration geometry. They disagree by the same staleness angle theta as the position-staleness finding.\n\nBUT this is a symptom-reproduction check, and the reported symptom is entirely a MAGNITUDE symptom: "little to no knockback," "the victim just doesnt really move back," "the non-sprinting knockback," "less knockback than they should." This mechanism produces exactly ZERO change in displacement magnitude AND zero change in displacement direction — the velocity that actually moves the victim is the (full-magnitude, frozen-geometry) pre-sent burst; the valve consumes vanilla's duplicate. The ONLY thing that diverges is the red hurt-tilt camera animation direction. A hit that still flings the victim the full distance, merely with a flinch tilt pointing up to ~30-50 deg off, reads as a strong hit that landed weird — never as "the victim didn't move back" or "non-sprinting knockback." The owner never describes a misdirected flinch; every phrase in the report is about how far the victim travels. The finding's own matches_report concedes "not a magnitude loss, so it cannot alone explain 'doesn't move back'." Below 1.19.4 the hurt is directionless entity-status 2 and the effect is null entirely.\n\nThe finding is a genuine era divergence (era sent one hurt + one velocity from one processing instant; Mental ships tilt-fresh/push-stale), but it cannot reproduce the reported weak/absent-knockback sensation — that is a distinct, unreported symptom (visual flinch mismatch, not reduced displacement). Refuted for symptom reproduction.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss: 0.00 blocks (displacement magnitude AND direction are the full frozen-registration push — unchanged by this mechanism). Sole effect: hurt-tilt ANIMATION direction error, magnitude = the position-staleness angle theta, up to ~30-50 deg at <=1 block with lateral movement, ~0 for stationary pairs. Frequency: same strafe-fight, 1.19.4+ population as the position-staleness finding (imperceptible below 1.19.4 — directionless status-2 hurt). But the produced symptom is a mis-pointed flinch on a full-strength shove, which does not present as weak/absent/non-sprinting knockback; it is not the reported symptom at any frequency.

### `ring-origin-fallback-first-tick` — bug, confidence low (finder: moving-victim-direction)

**Mechanism:** positionX/positionZ and preAttackerState/preVictimState fall back to 0.0 when PositionRing.latest() returns null (HitRegistrationUnit.java:452-455,467-470,476-484). The ring's first sample for a player is recorded at the END of their first session tick, AFTER the view is published inside the same task (SessionService.tick: buildView/tickStep at :335-347 precede positions.record at :352-354), so there exists a sub-tick window per session creation where viewOf() returns a fresh view (registration proceeds) but latest() is still null — the pre-send then computes the base-push direction from coordinates (0,0,0), i.e. normalize(attacker−origin) or normalize(origin−victim): a full-magnitude knock toward/away from the world origin, an arbitrary compass direction at any arena location. HurtYaw takes the same corrupt frame. The same fallback shape exists for the servo inputs (:352-353). Frequency is bounded by the region-thread/netty interleave inside one task invocation per player per join (positions.forget runs only on the honest quit-time forget, SessionService.java:309, not on respawn re-arm), so this is a micro-window race, not a steady-state leak — reported because it is the one place the direction source can be WHOLLY fabricated rather than stale, and no test pins the null-sample path (only ReachClampTest touches the ring in tests).

**Trigger:** An ATTACK packet registered against (or thrown by) a player whose first session-tick view publish has happened but whose first ring record has not — a microseconds-wide window once per session creation; requires the hit to land essentially at join time.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:452-455,467-470,476-484 (0.0 fallbacks feeding the engine's direction); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:335-354 (publish precedes the first record within one task), :309 (ring forgotten only at quit); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:472-492 (a (0,0,0) source still normalizes to a full-magnitude push).

**Maps to the report:** Marginal: too rare to be the owner's felt pattern, but a hit affected ships full knockback in a compass-arbitrary direction — at most an occasional inexplicable one-off; included to complete the direction-sourcing audit rather than as a report explanation.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Could not refute the core mechanism. Verified each link: (1) Publish-before-record ordering is real — CombatSession.tickStep calls published.set(freshlyBuilt) at line 237, invoked from SessionService.tick at :347, while positions.record runs later at :353, so during the FIRST session tick there is a genuine instruction-width window where viewOf() is non-null but positions.latest() is null. (2) The freshness gate (HitRegistrationUnit:270) does NOT close it — PlayerView.fresh() is recentAt(now,4) and the first published view carries the current stamp, so it is fresh on tick 1. (3) passesReach (:557-593) fails OPEN on a null ring (line 569-570: `if (attackerPos==null||victimPos==null) return true;`) and returns true even earlier if reach validation is disabled — so it never cancels the null-ring hit. (4) plan() requires only attackerView!=null && victimView!=null (published), not ring samples, so the pre-send proceeds; preAttackerState/preVictimState (:451-474) and positionX/Z (:476-484) then feed 0.0 into KnockbackEngine.base (:472-488), which normalizes sourceX-victim.x() to a FULL-magnitude push — an arbitrary compass direction fixed by the arena's absolute coordinates; HurtYaw (:415-419) takes the same corrupt frame. So the finding's mechanism is code-accurate and not refuted.

However, I sharpened reachability and impact. Realistically only ONE sub-case fires: the VICTIM just genuinely joined (its ring is null in the window) while the ATTACKER is established — the attacker is the party sending the ATTACK packet, so it has ticked many times and its ring is populated, making the attacker-null case effectively unreachable. Also confirmed the window is join-ONLY, not respawn: onDeath (SessionService:238) only enqueues a Reset and retire keeps the session; positions.forget runs solely in forget() at quit (:309), so the ring survives death/respawn — the finding's own "once per session creation" bound is correct and even narrower than a respawn-inclusive read. Net: this is a real but astronomically rare latent defect that produces a full-magnitude WRONG-direction knock (plus wrong hurt-animation yaw), which is the opposite shape of the owner's "weak / non-sprinting knockback" report. The finding itself correctly labels it marginal and not a report explanation.
- Corrections: Mechanism confirmed with two refinements. (1) Only the victim-just-joined sub-case is realistically reachable: the attacker sends the ATTACK packet, so its session has ticked and its ring is populated; the attacker-null path is effectively unreachable. So the practical corruption is preVictimState reading (0,0,0) while preAttackerState reads real attacker coords, giving deltaX/Z = attackerCoord - 0 -> a full-magnitude push whose direction is the arena's absolute compass bearing, not the local attacker->victim geometry. (2) Scope is genuine-join-only, NOT respawn: the ring is forgotten solely in forget() (quit), and onDeath keeps the session alive (Reset only), so a respawned player's ring is still populated — the window recurs strictly once per fresh join. It is not config-gated in any meaningful way (DELIVERY/pre-send is always-on family), but reach validation being enabled is irrelevant since that gate fails open on null. Result is a full-magnitude wrong-direction knock + corrupt HurtYaw, never weak knockback.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB magnitude: NO loss (full magnitude); the defect is a directional/angle error up to ~180deg, fixed by the arena's absolute coordinates rather than local geometry. Expected frequency in real PvP: effectively zero — requires a genuine fresh join (not respawn) AND the joining player being attacked within an instruction-width window (the ~5-6 statements between published.set at SessionService:347 and positions.record at :353) of that player's very first session tick. Realistically fires zero times over a server's lifetime; wholly disjoint from the owner's felt weak-KB pattern (wrong-direction full knock, not a soft/non-sprint knock).

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Verified against source. HitRegistrationUnit:452-484 do fall back to 0.0 when PositionRing.latest() returns null, and SessionService.tick publishes the view (buildView, :335) before recording the first ring sample (:352-354) within one region task — so a genuine sub-tick null-ring window exists exactly once per session creation (positions.forget runs only in remove()/quit at :309, not on respawn). Registration gates on a non-null/fresh victim view (:269-273), which a just-published first-tick view satisfies, so the window is reachable in principle.

But the SYMPTOM produced is NOT weak knockback. In KnockbackEngine.base (:472-492) the fabricated (0,0,0) source is normalized and multiplied by the FULL push = profile.base().horizontal(); the <1e-4 degenerate guard (:474-480) only randomizes the DIRECTION, preserving full magnitude. Single-sided fallback (attacker null→0, victim real) gives deltaX = 0 − victim.x(), a large radial-from-origin vector — again full magnitude, compass-arbitrary direction. So the bug yields a full-strength knock in the WRONG direction, never the reduced 'non-sprinting' magnitude the owner describes.

A radially-directed full-magnitude push has an uncorrelated projection onto the true attacker→victim (backward) axis, so a single fluke hit CAN read as 'victim didn't really move back' — a plausible fragment of one phrasing in the report. That is why this is not fully refutable. But it is a once-per-join, microseconds-wide netty/region interleave race against/by a player at their literal join instant — it cannot correlate with close range, w-tap, blockhit, or the reduced-magnitude sprint-vs-non-sprint feel, and it is not a recurring steady pattern. This matches the finder's own low-confidence, audit-completeness framing.
- Severity: Per-affected-hit: horizontal magnitude is UNCHANGED (full push shipped), but direction is corrupted to radial-from-origin, so the backward (attacker→victim axis) component is uniformly random in ~[−push, +push]; expected backward loss ≈ full push with high variance (a hit can even point forward, i.e. victim pulled toward attacker). At the canonical signature push this is on the order of a full ~0.4 b/t horizontal component misdirected. Frequency in real PvP: effectively nil — at most once per join, and only if an attack packet lands in the ~microsecond gap between buildView (:335) and positions.record (:352) of a player's very first session tick, against/by a player at their join instant; no respawn re-arm. Not close-range-, w-tap-, or blockhit-correlated. Does not reproduce the owner's recurring subtle-weak-KB pattern; at most an isolated inexplicable wrong-direction one-off.

### `latency-comp-vertical-only-no-horizontal-path` — unknown, confidence high (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** Q1 negative, load-bearing for the synthesizer: latency compensation cannot scale, delay, re-time, or drop the HORIZONTAL knock. CompensationQuery.verticalFor returns a y-override consumed solely as the victim-vy substitute in the engine's ADD-mode vertical (y = vyOverride*friction.y + base.vertical); SET-mode profiles ignore it entirely, and base()/extras/finish never read it for x/z. It also never gates the pre-send, the FeedbackGate, the desk, or the valve. The feature is default ON (modules.latency-compensation: true; Feature defaultEnabled true) and preset-agnostic (all ten presets are VerticalMode.ADD). At high ping it ships LESS VERTICAL on airborne falling victims (deeper simulated fall) and the grounded 0.3608-equivalent when landing is predicted — never less horizontal. Any real 'high ping ships less horizontal' effect must come from the ledger ground-transition lag or the optional servo/reach paths (separate findings).

**Trigger:** N/A — scope determination. Every hit on every preset with the feature on: vertical-only, and only when frozen noDamageTicks<=8 and the victim is client-airborne.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/CompensationQuery.java:22-44 (returns a y override only); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:494-500 (victimYOverride consumed only in the ADD vertical; SET ignores), 497-501 (x/z never read it); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:326,537-544 (computed per hit, stamped into HitContext); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:373-388 (region reuse); core/src/main/resources/config.yml:38; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/Feature.java:72-81; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/Presets.java:34,60,98,124,145 (ADD everywhere)

**Maps to the report:** Rules the compensation feature out as a direct source of 'the victim just doesnt really move back' horizontally; its ping-dependent effects are confined to the vertical pop (see the amplification and dead-band findings).

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Verified against the cited code. The finding's core premises hold: CompensationQuery.verticalFor (kernel/.../wire/CompensationQuery.java:22-44) returns a nullable y-override gated on noDamageTicks>8 and clientOnGround; the feature is default ON (config.yml latency-compensation:true, Feature enum defaultEnabled=true); base()'s x/z (KnockbackEngine.java:497,501) read victim.vx()/vz() directly and never the override; SET mode ignores it; the shown presets are all VerticalMode.ADD. So on the DIRECT vector path (base/extras/finish), compensation is vertical-only and cannot scale/delay/drop the horizontal knock, and it never gates the pre-send/FeedbackGate/desk/valve. That conclusion — compensation is not a standalone DIRECT source of weak horizontal knockback — could not be refuted and stands.\n\nHOWEVER the finding is OVERSTATED and factually wrong on one point it treats as load-bearing: it claims victimYOverride is 'consumed SOLELY as the victim-vy substitute in the ADD-mode vertical' and that latency comp 'cannot scale the HORIZONTAL knock.' In fact victimYOverride is ALSO read in shippedVertical (KnockbackEngine.java:346 call, :365 use) inside servoFactor. When the pocket servo is active (computePaced line 206-208), that compensation-modified verticalStamp feeds PocketServo.solve, producing σ (combo), and freshFactor = pace * combo (line 210) scales the fresh horizontal push and extras (lines 212, 221-226). Therefore the compensation vertical IS an input to the horizontal σ whenever the combo-hold servo is active — compensation is coupled to horizontal, not orthogonal to it. The finding mischaracterizes the servo as a compensation-independent 'separate finding' when it actually consumes compensation's output. A deeper simulated fall (more-negative override) changes the servo's flight-time bound and can nudge σ, and thus horizontal, in either direction. This is a genuine (narrow, servo-gated) coupling the finding denies in absolute terms.\n\nNet: the conclusion (not the primary/direct horizontal-weakener) survives; the mechanism's absolutes ('solely', 'cannot ... horizontal') are false and need correction. Not a full refutation — refuted=false with a mandatory correction.
- Corrections: The finding's conclusion stands: latency compensation does not DIRECTLY weaken horizontal knockback — on the base()/extras/finish vector path the override is read only for the ADD-mode vertical (KnockbackEngine.java:496-501), x reads victim.vx(), z reads victim.vz(), SET ignores it, and it never gates pre-send/FeedbackGate/desk/valve. Default ON and presets all ADD confirmed. BUT two of the finding's absolutes are FALSE and must be struck: (1) victimYOverride is NOT 'consumed solely as the victim-vy substitute in the ADD-mode vertical' — it is also read in shippedVertical (KnockbackEngine.java:346,365); (2) latency compensation therefore CAN influence the horizontal knock, indirectly, when the pocket servo is active: shippedVertical's compensation-modified verticalStamp feeds PocketServo.solve, yielding sigma (combo), and freshFactor=pace*combo (line 210) scales the fresh horizontal push and extras. The servo is thus NOT a compensation-independent 'separate finding' — it consumes compensation's output, so any servo horizontal weakening at high ping is partly compensation-driven. Restate the mechanism as: 'compensation has no DIRECT horizontal effect on the base vector; its vertical override couples into horizontal ONLY through the combo-hold pocket servo (a narrow, default-behavior-gated path), never through base/extras/finish/pre-send/valve.'
- Severity: Direct horizontal-KB loss attributable to latency compensation: ZERO — base()/extras/finish never read the override for x/z, so the finding correctly rules it out as a direct cause of 'the victim doesnt move back' horizontally. Vertical effect: fires on every client-airborne victim hit with noDamageTicks<=8 at any ping (rtt>=50ms), shipping less vertical pop (deeper fall) or the grounded equilibrium when landing is predicted — common in real PvP but horizontal-neutral on the direct path. The ONLY horizontal coupling is second-order: via shippedVertical->servoFactor->sigma->freshFactor, active ONLY when the combo-hold pocket servo is active for that hit (attacker holds victim's active combo), a narrow subset of close-range combo hits; magnitude is a small sigma nudge, not a systematic loss, and can go either direction. Not a plausible primary source of the owner's broad-range weak-KB feel.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: This is a Q1-negative scope-determination finding; I am CONFIRMING it, not refuting it. Code trace verifies every claim. In KnockbackEngine.base() (496-501) the shipped x/z are `victim.vx()*friction.x - pushX` and `victim.vz()*friction.z - pushZ`; both read the victim's own live horizontal velocity, and pushX/pushZ come only from profile.base().horizontal(), pushReduction, and paceFactor. The latency-compensation override (`victimYOverride`, from CompensationQuery.verticalFor) is consumed at exactly two sites — base() line 496-500 and shippedVertical() line 365-368 — and in both it substitutes only the vertical seed `victimVy` for the ADD-mode `y = victimVy*friction.y + base.vertical`; SET mode ignores it outright (498-500). It never scales, delays, drops, or gates x/z, and it never touches the pre-send, FeedbackGate, desk, or valve. CompensationQuery returns a single Double y-override gated to client-airborne victims with noDamageTicks<=8. Feature is default ON (config.yml latency-compensation: true; Feature.LATENCY_COMPENSATION defaultEnabled true) and preset-agnostic — all ten Presets are VerticalMode.ADD. Therefore latency compensation cannot be the source of the owner's horizontal 'victim just doesnt really move back' / 'non-sprinting knockback' symptom: it produces exactly zero horizontal-velocity change at every range on every bundled preset. The only residual coupling is that servoFactor (346) reads the vertical stamp to bound the pocket-servo flight window, so on the OPTIONAL, default-INACTIVE servo path a comp-reduced vertical could re-price horizontal chase — but the compute() path passes PocketServoConfig.INACTIVE (129), and the finding explicitly delegates the servo/reach paths and the vertical-pop magnitude to sibling findings. Its own scope (base/finish) is horizontal-clean. The finding's factual assertions are all correct, so refuted=false (the scope determination stands).
- Corrections: Confirmed: latency compensation is strictly vertical. The horizontal knockback Mental ships is byte-identical whether the feature is on or off — the override (a single y-value from CompensationQuery.verticalFor) is read only as the ADD-mode vertical seed in base() (496-500) and shippedVertical() (365-368); x and z always use victim.vx()/victim.vz() and the profile-derived pushX/pushZ. It cannot scale, delay, re-time, drop, or gate the horizontal knock, and does not touch the pre-send, FeedbackGate, desk, or valve. So it is correctly ruled OUT as a direct cause of the horizontal 'doesn't move back / non-sprinting knockback' report. Two precisions to carry forward, both already scoped to sibling findings: (1) SET-mode profiles ignore the override entirely, but this is moot for bundled play since all ten presets are ADD; (2) on the OPTIONAL pocket-servo path, servoFactor (346) reads the comp-reduced vertical stamp to bound the flight window, so a lower vertical can indirectly under-price the horizontal chase — but that path is default-INACTIVE on compute() and is the servo finding's concern, not latency comp's. Any genuine 'high ping ships less horizontal' effect must come from the ledger ground-transition lag or the servo/reach paths, exactly as the finding states.

Frequency of a horizontal effect in real PvP: never (0%). What latency comp DOES change is the vertical stamp on airborne victims with noDamageTicks<=8 at nonzero ping: on high-friction.y presets (legacy/kohi/mmc/minehq/badlion, friction.y=0.5) a deeper simulated fall of e.g. victimVy -0.5→-0.9 over ~4 ticks drops the vertical seed by ~0.2 (0.25→0.05 shipped y); on velt/signature (friction.y=0.1) the same swing is only ~0.04. That is a vertical/air-time (and thus indirect horizontal-DISTANCE) effect, not a horizontal-velocity effect, and it belongs to the amplification/dead-band sibling findings — it does NOT reproduce the 'non-sprinting knockback at close range' signature the owner flags.

### `ping-offset-knob-never-subtracted` — bug, confidence high (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** latency-compensation.yml documents ping-offset-ms (default 25) as 'Subtracted from each measured round trip before compensation (tournament-derived constant)'. The knob is parsed into CompensationSettings and consumed by NOTHING: both compensation call sites use the raw pingMillis (rtt = round(ping)) with no subtraction, and grep shows pingOffsetMillis has zero readers outside the settings record and the parser. Consequence: every compensated hit simulates rtt/50 ticks off the UN-offset RTT — 0-1 extra fall tick per hit (25ms is half a tick; integer division makes it phase-dependent), i.e. up to ~0.04 lower shipped vertical on airborne victims, systematically, and the operator cannot correct it because the documented lever is inert.

**Trigger:** Any compensated hit (feature on — the default — victim client-airborne, frozen noDamageTicks<=8, RTT probe present). Editing ping-offset-ms changes nothing.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/resources/latency-compensation.yml:13-15 (documented contract); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/CompensationSettings.java:10-19 (field exists); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/SnapshotParser.java:173 (parsed); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:541-543 and core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:385-387 (raw ping used, no offset); grep: no other pingOffsetMillis reader in core/kernel/platform main trees

**Maps to the report:** Weak direct match (vertical-only, <=1 tick), but it biases every compensated hit toward LESS vertical — part of the 'hits feel dead' texture — and violates the feature's own config contract.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Could not refute the core claim; it is a confirmed code fact. Verified: (1) `ping-offset-ms` is documented as "Subtracted from each measured round trip before compensation" (latency-compensation.yml:13-15); (2) it is parsed into CompensationSettings.pingOffsetMillis (SnapshotParser.java:173, record field CompensationSettings.java:12); (3) grep across core/kernel/platform main trees shows `pingOffsetMillis` has exactly two occurrences — the record field and the parser — i.e. ZERO consumers. Every compensation call site uses the raw ping: HitRegistrationUnit.java:542-543 and KnockbackUnit.java:386-387 both do `int rtt = round(ping); CompensationQuery.verticalFor(view, rtt, vy)`, and the third consumer ComboPredictor.rttMillis (line 324) is likewise raw. CompensationQuery.verticalFor takes rttMillis directly and does `int ticks = rttMillis / 50` with no offset. The kernel LatencyModel stores raw RTT (rttNanos/1e6) and never applies an offset. No subtraction of 25/settings anywhere. The feature is ON by default (config.yml:38 `latency-compensation: true`; line 543 `compensation: false` is only a debug category). So the documented operator lever is genuinely inert — editing ping-offset-ms changes nothing.

Adversarial checks that failed to refute: no test pins the offset behavior (CompensationQueryTest passes rtt directly); no alternate compensation implementation exists; no projectile/combo path applies it either.

Direction of the mechanism is real: an unsubtracted 25 ms means the effective RTT is half a tick too high, so `rttMillis/50` is up to 1 tick too high (phase-dependent on RTT mod 50 ms). More simulated fall ticks make an airborne victim's predicted vy more negative (falling) or less positive (rising), and more readily trip the `ticksToLand <= ticks` → groundedEquilibrium branch — all of which lower the shipped vertical. Subtracting the offset (the intended behavior) would RAISE vertical, so the inert knob costs vertical launch, consistent with the "dead hit" texture. But this is vertical-only and airborne-only.

Severity is honestly low and a weak match to the report. The user's complaint is primarily HORIZONTAL ("victim doesn't move back," "non-sprinting knockback"); this bug has ZERO horizontal-KB effect. In close-range grounded exchanges the victim is client-on-ground, so verticalFor returns null and the bug never fires. It only bites airborne victims (jump-reset/combo air phases) with compensation engaged, and only on the fraction of hits where the 25 ms tips the integer tick boundary.

era_call = bug: this is a plain config-contract/implementation defect (a documented knob wired to nothing). Latency compensation is a modern feature, not an era mechanic, so it is not an era-authenticity divergence.
- Corrections: Finding stands as a confirmed code defect but is over-attributed to the user's symptom. Precise statement: pingOffsetMillis (default 25) is parsed and stored but has zero consumers — all three compensation consumers (HitRegistrationUnit:542, KnockbackUnit:386, ComboPredictor:324) use the raw round-trip; CompensationQuery.verticalFor computes `ticks = rttMillis/50` with no offset; kernel LatencyModel stores raw RTT. The documented "subtracted from each measured round trip" contract is inert; the operator lever does nothing. Effect is confined to VERTICAL knockback on client-airborne victims when LATENCY_COMPENSATION is enabled (default) and noDamageTicks<=8: the un-offset RTT over-counts fall ticks by at most 1 (phase-dependent, only when raw RTT mod 50 falls in the top 25 ms of a bucket), biasing shipped vertical DOWN by ~0.04-0.08 vy or occasionally into groundedEquilibrium. It does NOT affect horizontal knockback, sprint-vs-non-sprint horizontal magnitude, or grounded close-range exchanges (grounded victims short-circuit to null), so it is essentially orthogonal to the primary "victim doesn't move back / feels like non-sprint KB" complaint. Classify as a low-severity config-contract bug, not a driver of the reported weak-horizontal-KB feel.
- Severity: Vertical-only, airborne-only. On a compensated airborne hit, the missing 25 ms (half a tick) tips `rttMillis/50` up by 1 tick on roughly the ~50% of hits whose raw RTT falls in the 25 ms band above each 50 ms boundary; each extra fall tick costs ~0.04-0.08 of vy vertical launch, or (less often) tips the landed-branch into groundedEquilibrium for a larger discrete vertical loss. ZERO horizontal-KB or angle effect. Expected frequency in real PvP: near-zero at the reported close/grounded range (grounded victim → verticalFor returns null); only airborne exchanges see it. Weak match to the (horizontal) reported symptom; genuine but minor inert-knob bug.

**SYMPTOM lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap)

### `spike-filter-documented-but-unimplemented` — bug, confidence high (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** latency-compensation.yml documents spike-threshold-ms (default 20): 'A ping jump larger than this is treated as a one-off spike and the previous reading is used instead.' The machinery half-exists — LatencyModel.Record keeps previousPingMillis explicitly 'spike detection' per its javadoc — but NO production code reads previousPingMillis or spikeThresholdMillis (grep: only tests and the parser). compensationFor always consumes the latest single sample. Consequence: one delayed probe echo (GC pause, wifi burst, bufferbloat — e.g. 240ms on a true-40ms link) poisons pingMillis for up to probe-interval (5 ticks, 250ms); hits in that window simulate 4 extra fall ticks instead of ~1, shipping the grounded-equilibrium override or a deeply-fallen vy (floored at 0 lift). Under sustained ±30ms wifi jitter the per-hit vertical wanders hit-to-hit with the raw sample stream — exactly the un-pinnable inconsistency the filter was designed (and documented) to remove.

**Trigger:** Feature on (default) + any RTT sample spike or jitter; compensated hits (client-airborne victim, noDamageTicks<=8) within 5 ticks of the bad sample ship a mispredicted vertical.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/resources/latency-compensation.yml:16-18 (documented contract); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/LatencyModel.java:8-9,51-52,68-69,78-80 (previousPingMillis kept 'spike detection', never consulted); grep: previousPingMillis/spikeThreshold readers exist only in kernel/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/LatencyModelTest.java and SnapshotParser.java:174; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:541-542 (latest sample used raw)

**Maps to the report:** Matches the 'more like a feeling thing' character: jitter-selected hits ship visibly flatter verticals with no reproducible trigger; ping-spike-proportional, any range.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Verified every code claim; none refutable. spike-threshold-ms is documented as behavioral in latency-compensation.yml:16-18 and parsed into CompensationSettings.spikeThresholdMillis (SnapshotParser.java:174), but grep finds NO production reader for spikeThresholdMillis (only parser + record field) and NO production reader for LatencyModel.Record.previousPingMillis (getter called only by LatencyModelTest). onResponse (LatencyModel.java:68-69) sets pingMillis unconditionally from the newest RTT with no spike gate; jitterMillis() is also defined but unconsumed, so there is zero smoothing on the sample stream. Both compensation consumers (HitRegistrationUnit.java:541, KnockbackUnit.java:385) read the raw latest pingMillis. CompensationQuery.verticalFor maps rtt to ticks=rttMillis/50, so a spike (e.g. 240ms on a true-40ms link → 4 ticks vs 0) inflates the forward fall simulation, deepening predicted vy or flipping to Decay.groundedEquilibrium — mispredicting the airborne victim's vertical for up to a probe interval (5 ticks / 250ms). Feature is default ON (config.yml:38, Feature enum flag true). - Corrections: Confirmed defect: the documented spike filter (spike-threshold-ms, default 20) and the previousPingMillis 'spike detection' machinery are parsed/maintained but never consulted by production code (grep: readers are tests + SnapshotParser only). LatencyModel.onResponse sets pingMillis unconditionally from the newest RTT with no filter and no jitter smoothing (jitterMillis() also unconsumed), and both compensation consumers (HitRegistrationUnit.java:541, KnockbackUnit.java:385) feed that raw sample into CompensationQuery.verticalFor, where ticks=rttMillis/50. A delayed probe echo therefore poisons the vertical prediction for up to a probe interval (5 ticks/250ms). Feature default ON (config.yml:38). SCOPE CORRECTION: compensationY overrides ONLY vertical launch, not horizontal knockback, so this is at most a secondary contributor to the vertical feel of weak hits and cannot be the horizontal 'victim doesn't move back' mechanism the owner primarily describes. Fix direction: implement the documented spike rejection in onResponse (if |rtt - previousPing| > spikeThresholdMillis, retain previous reading) and/or thread spikeThresholdMillis to the consumers — currently a wholly dead knob.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss: 0 — this path overrides only the vertical component, so it does NOT explain the owner's primary horizontal 'doesn't move back' symptom. Vertical error: under common ±30ms wifi jitter straddling a 50ms tick boundary (e.g. 40ms↔70ms), the per-hit vy override wanders by ~1 tick ≈ 0.08 b/t hit-to-hit; a larger 200ms+ spike inflates by ~4 ticks, pushing a near-apex baseVy≈0 to a ~-0.30 b/t predicted vy (flatter/weaker upward launch) or flipping to a grounded-equilibrium override on a legitimately-airborne victim. Gated to airborne victims with noDamageTicks<=8, feature default ON. Frequency: moderate on jittery/wifi links (subtle 1-tick vertical wobble), rare/large on stable LAN; matches the 'more a feeling thing' character but only for the vertical dimension of hits, not the horizontal complaint.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Code state confirmed: spike-threshold-ms (default 20) and Record.previousPingMillis are documented and kept but consulted ONLY by SnapshotParser and tests — no production reader (grep clean). Both compensationFor sites (HitRegistrationUnit:541-543, KnockbackUnit:385-387) consume latency.forPlayer(id).pingMillis(), the raw latest RTT sample, unfiltered. LATENCY_COMPENSATION defaults ON (Feature.java:74). A single delayed probe echo therefore poisons pingMillis for up to probe-interval (5 ticks) and CompensationQuery.verticalFor simulates rtt/50 forward fall-ticks off the bad sample.

BUT the override is vertical-only. In KnockbackEngine.base() (496-501) victimYOverride feeds only y; horizontal x/z derive from victim.vx/vz and pushX/pushZ, and finish()'s air multiplier keys off victim.grounded() (a distinct field the override never sets). So the spike cannot directly weaken the horizontal push that the report describes as 'victim doesn't move back' / 'non-sprinting knockback' — those are horizontal-magnitude perceptions.

Hand-computed (LEGACY_17 default: friction.y=0.5, base.vertical=0.4, cap 0.4, verticalMin 0.0, ADD): true 40ms link → ticks=0 → no distortion. A 200ms one-off spike → ticks=4; a near-apex victim (baseVy≈0) yields override −0.304, final vertical 0.248 vs the true 0.40 — a ~37% flatter launch (~0.15 vy). Effect only bites on a FALLING victim (vy<0, so y falls below the 0.4 cap); a rising victim clamps at 0.4 either way (no effect). A flatter vertical shortens total airtime/travel and can drop a victim out of a juggle, which reads as 'weak', but it is not the horizontal symptom.

An indirect horizontal pathway exists only with COMBO_HOLD enabled (default OFF, Feature.java:284): servoFactor feeds the mispredicted verticalStamp into PocketServo.solve, whose σ scales the fresh horizontal knock — so a combo user running Solve Horizontal KB could see a small horizontal wander from vertical misprediction.

Jitter driver partly overstated: rtt/50 integer division rounds away sub-tick ±30ms jitter; only genuine ≥50ms spikes (GC/bufferbloat) shift a whole simulated fall-tick.

Verdict: not refuted — it plausibly produces the subtle, unpinnable, network-driven, range-independent per-hit vertical inconsistency that matches the report's 'more like a feeling thing' character (and aligns with the owner's clarification that weak hits are not only close-range, since compensation is range-blind). It does NOT reproduce the core horizontal 'non-sprinting knockback' mechanism on default config.
- Corrections: The finding's code claim is correct and confirmed, but its symptom scope is overstated. compensationY (spiked or not) distorts the VERTICAL knockback component ONLY — in KnockbackEngine.base() the override feeds y alone; horizontal x/z come from victim.vx/vz and the away-push, and finish()'s air branch keys off victim.grounded(), a separate field the override never sets. So an unfiltered ping spike CANNOT directly produce the report's core horizontal symptom ('victim doesn't move back', 'seems like the non-sprinting knockback', 'sprint hits with less horizontal KB'). What it genuinely produces is per-hit VERTICAL launch variance on client-airborne, descending victims: e.g. a 200ms one-off spike on a 40ms link flattens a near-apex hit from 0.40 to ~0.25 vy (~37%), floored at 0. That is a real, subtle, network-driven, range-independent inconsistency that matches the report's 'more like a feeling thing than something I can pin down' and the owner's 'not only close range' clarification (a flatter vertical shortens travel and can break a juggle, reading as 'weak'). The horizontal 'non-sprinting knockback' perception is a DIFFERENT mechanism (belongs to a separate finding). One caveat: with COMBO_HOLD ('Solve Horizontal KB', default OFF but plausibly on for this owner) the mispredicted verticalStamp perturbs the pocket-servo σ that scales the FRESH horizontal knock, giving a small indirect horizontal wander — the one path by which this spike gap can touch horizontal KB. Also note the jitter framing: rtt/50 integer division rounds away sub-tick ±30ms jitter, so real ≥50ms spikes (GC/bufferbloat), not steady low jitter, are the actual trigger. (Separately observed while tracing this: ping-offset-ms=25 is likewise parsed into CompensationSettings but never consumed in the compensation path — the raw RTT is used directly — which slightly enlarges every spike's tick count; out of scope for this finding but worth a follow-up.)

Zero DIRECT horizontal-KB loss (compensationY feeds only KnockbackEngine.base()'s y; horizontal push and the grounded flag are untouched). ### `off-ground-sync-knob-inert` — bug, confidence high (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** latency-compensation.yml documents off-ground-sync (default true): 'Also rewrite the victim's vertical motion while airborne (full client-side simulation), not just the on-ground case.' The flag is parsed into CompensationSettings.offGroundSync and consumed by NOTHING: CompensationQuery.verticalFor unconditionally runs the airborne simulateVerticalVelocity branch whenever the landing fold does not fire; no caller passes or checks the setting (grep: zero readers outside the record and parser). An operator who sets off-ground-sync: false — e.g. to stop high-ping airborne victims' verticals being shaved, the natural reaction to dead-feeling juggle hits — changes nothing; the airborne rewrite cannot be disabled without turning the whole feature off.

**Trigger:** Any non-default off-ground-sync: false config; the airborne vy rewrite keeps firing on every compensated hit regardless.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/resources/latency-compensation.yml:23-25 (documented semantics); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/CompensationSettings.java:16 (field), core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/SnapshotParser.java:177 (parsed); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/CompensationQuery.java:42-43 (airborne branch unconditional); grep: no offGroundSync reader in any main tree

**Maps to the report:** Indirect: makes the ping-proportional airborne vertical shave un-opt-out-able, so a server owner diagnosing weak airborne hits cannot mitigate via the documented knob.

**CODE lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap)

**SYMPTOM lens: REFUTED** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: The mechanism is real and code-confirmed: off-ground-sync is parsed but has zero readers, so CompensationQuery.verticalFor runs the airborne simulateVerticalVelocity branch unconditionally. However, this is a config-plumbing / documentation-mismatch bug, not a knockback-strength bug, and it cannot produce the owner's reported symptom for three independent reasons:

(1) Vertical-only. verticalFor returns a Double y-override that overwrites the victim's residual vy only. The horizontal knockback (base 0.4 + sprint bonus 0.4, the attacker/speed scaling) is never touched by this code path. The owner's core complaint — "the victim just doesn't really move back," "it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback," "sprint hits with less knockback than they should" — is horizontal. A vertical shave cannot make horizontal pushback read as non-sprinting.

(2) No behavioral delta on the owner's config. The default is off-ground-sync: true, and true's intended behavior IS "run the airborne rewrite." The dead knob means the airborne rewrite fires — exactly what true is supposed to do. So on the default config (the owner's config; the report says "as far back as I can remember," i.e. stock behavior) the bug changes nothing that ships. There is no run-to-run velocity difference attributable to this finding.

(3) The bug only manifests as a divergence-from-expectation when an operator explicitly sets off-ground-sync: false and expects the airborne vy shave to stop. Even then, no gameplay changes — the shave keeps firing — so the knob fails to FIX a feel problem; it does not CAUSE one. The owner never reports toggling this knob. The finding's own matches_report concedes the link is "indirect: makes the shave un-opt-out-able."

The airborne rewrite itself does have real magnitude — at ping 100ms (2 ticks) a vy of 0.42 simulates to 0.248 (Δ −0.17 vertical), at 200ms to ~0.08 (Δ −0.34), going negative past ~300ms — a genuine ping-proportional "dead juggle" effect. But that is the intended latency-compensation FEATURE working on default config, a separate tuning question, not something the dead knob causes. This finding, narrowly "the knob is inert," produces zero horizontal loss and zero default-config change, so it cannot reproduce any part of the reported symptom.
- Corrections: off-ground-sync is a genuinely dead config knob (real code-hygiene / documentation bug worth fixing — either wire CompensationQuery.verticalFor to short-circuit the airborne branch when the setting is false, or delete the flag and its doc line). But it is NOT a reproducer of the owner's weak-knockback report: the compensation path overrides vertical vy only (horizontal pushback, including the sprint bonus, is never affected), and on the default config (off-ground-sync: true) the dead knob produces byte-identical behavior to intent, so it cannot cause a default-config, primarily-horizontal, long-standing weak-KB feeling. Refuted as a symptom cause; retain only as a low-priority config-plumbing cleanup.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss attributable to this finding: 0.00 b/t (the code path overrides vertical vy only; horizontal is untouched). Default-config behavioral delta: 0.00 (default true == the always-on branch, so the dead knob ships identical velocity to intent). The only quantifiable effect is the airborne vertical shave that this knob fails to disable — Δvy ≈ −0.17 at 100ms ping, −0.34 at 200ms, sign-flip past ~300ms on a rising (0.42) victim — but that fires on default config as the intended feature, not because the knob is dead. Frequency of the finding actually biting: effectively never in real PvP, since it requires an operator to set off-ground-sync:false AND expect a change; and even then gameplay is unchanged. It matches neither the horizontal "doesn't move back" symptom nor the default-config persistence of the report.

### `combo-residual-ground-transition-lag-ping-proportional` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** Q2 answer. For evenly-spaced hits with no ground transition, the ledger residual is ping-INVARIANT (both hits shift +RTT/2 on the client, so client decay ticks == server decay ticks — clean). The divergence is entirely at ground-state transitions, and it scales with victim RTT: Deliveries.recordDelivered stamps grounded/slip from the published view (grounded=true for the standard standing knock), MotionLedger decays ALL ticks of a segment at that one branch (ground 0.546/tick vs air 0.91/tick), and the branch flips only when the client's own movement packet crosses the wire (GroundFsm liftoff/landing -> inbox -> drain). The client applies the pre-sent knock RTT/2 after ship, goes airborne a tick later, and its onGround=false packet takes another RTT/2 — so the ledger applies ~RTT/50 EXTRA ground decays (x0.546 each) where the client applied air decays (x0.91), an under-read factor of 0.6^(RTT/50) on top of the fixed 1-2-tick jitter round 1 found. Quantified for a 0.9 sprint stamp read 10 ticks later (era chain 0.9*0.546^2*0.91^8≈0.126): 50ms -> ≈0.076 (-40%), 100ms -> ≈0.045 (-64%), 150ms -> ≈0.027 (-78%) vs what the client actually integrated. On combos:true presets (legacy-1.7 default, kohi, minehq, badlion) the next hit's base = residual*0.5 - push, so max-cadence combo hits on high-ping victims systematically lose ~0.02-0.05 b/t of horizontal compounding — at ANY range. The mirror case (victim landed several ticks before the next hit) OVER-reads by 1.67^(RTT/50) (air drag applied where the client was grounded) — inflated knocks on slower-cadence chase hits; the two never cancel within one max-cadence window because the victim is still airborne at the next hit. Era 1.7.10 flipped its fields on the server's OWN physics one tick after the knock, ping-blind — Mental's packet-fed transitions are as-designed but era-divergent, ping-proportionally. Extends round-1 grounded-decay-count-jitter (fixed +/-1 tick) and refines toward-attacker-residual-cancellation's upstream caveat; combos:false presets immune (no melee residual).

**Trigger:** combos:true preset; victim ping 50ms+; attacker chains hits at the legal ~10-tick cadence starting from a grounded victim: every hit N+1 reads a residual with RTT/50 too many ground decays. Worse on stone (0.546) than ice; worst at 150ms+ wifi.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/delivery/Deliveries.java:41-44 (grounded/slip stamped from the view at ship); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:60-67 (branch fixed per segment), 76-85 (liftoff re-bases from the already-over-decayed current()), 94-102 (landing mirror), 126-133; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/Decay.java:79-101 (single drag for all segment ticks; grounded vy discarded to equilibrium); kernel/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedgerTest.java (pins assume record->liftoff = 1 tick); round-1 doc lines 594-598 (packet-fed transitions), 652-660 (the fixed-jitter subset)

**Maps to the report:** Directly matches 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' as a subtle, ping-proportional, any-range effect on the default legacy-1.7 preset — invisible at LAN/0-ping testing, present for real players, 'ever since versions as far back as I can remember'.

**CODE lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap)

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Code confirms the mechanism end to end. Deliveries.recordDelivered (core delivery/Deliveries.java:42-43) stamps the knock into the ledger with view.grounded()/view.slipperiness(); for a standing knock that is grounded=true, slip=0.6. MotionLedger.current() calls Decay.decay (kernel math/Decay.java:79-101), which applies ONE drag for ALL segment ticks: grounded uses slip*0.91 = 0.546, airborne uses 0.91. The branch only flips when a client movement packet (GroundFsm liftoff via the D1 to D2 inbox) re-bases via recordLiftoff (MotionLedger.java:76-85). That packet is RTT-gated: the knock reaches the client about RTT/2 after ship, the client lifts off a tick later, and its onGround=false packet returns about RTT/2 later, so the ledger holds the ground branch about RTT/50 ticks too long, decaying the horizontal residual at 0.546 where the era server (which flipped on its own physics one tick after the knock, ping-blind) applied 0.91. Each swapped tick multiplies the residual by 0.546/0.91 = 0.6. That under-read residual feeds the next combo hit. KnockbackEngine.base() line 497 computes x = victim.vx()*friction.x() - pushX; the residual (pointing away from the attacker) and the fresh push ADD in magnitude, so a smaller residual means a weaker total knock, matching the reported weak-hit direction. The default preset LEGACY_17 is combos=true with friction 0.5 (KnockbackProfile.java:128+), so the residual contributes 0.5*residual to every combo hit. combos=true presets: legacy-1.7 (DEFAULT), kohi, minehq, badlion. Hand computation matches the finding to three significant figures: a 0.9 sprint stamp read 10 ticks later, era chain 0.9*0.546^2*0.91^8 = 0.1262; +1 ground-swap (50ms RTT) gives 0.0757 (-40 percent), +2 (100ms) gives 0.0454 (-64 percent), +3 (150ms) gives 0.0273 (-78 percent). Through friction 0.5 the next hit's shipped horizontal loses 0.025 / 0.040 / 0.049 b/t. Matches report: reproduces sprint hits sometimes having less knockback than they should as a subtle ping-proportional effect on the DEFAULT preset, invisible on LAN/0-ping tests (zero extra ground ticks) and present for every real online victim at ping >=50ms, exactly the subtle, hard-to-reproduce, feeling-thing and as-far-back-as-I-can-remember description. Most pronounced in rapid max-cadence combos (close range, matching especially close) but range-agnostic, matching the owner clarification. It covers PART of the report (the sprint-hit clause), which satisfies refuted=false. Classification divergence-from-era is correct: the packet-fed ground transition is the intended D1/D2 design; the era divergence is real, ping-proportional, and inherent to reconstructing ground state from client packets rather than server physics. Not a coding bug, and not exculpatory-config-dependent since the shipped default is affected.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss on the residual-compounding term of combo hit N+1, hand-verified: ~0.025 b/t at 50ms RTT, ~0.040 at 100ms, ~0.049 at 150ms (the residual itself drops 40-78 percent; roughly 2-5 percent of a ~0.9 sprint combo hit). Frequency HIGH: affects the DEFAULT preset legacy-1.7 (combos=true) plus kohi/minehq/badlion, on every online combo exchange against a victim at ping >=50ms; strictly zero on LAN/0-ping test servers, which is why it reads as unreproducible. Worst in rapid combos (close range), on stone vs ice, at wifi-tier ping.

### `compensation-dead-band-probe-lifecycle` — bug, confidence medium (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** The feature's two gates are near-complementary, leaving it structurally OFF for the hits it exists for. (a) Probes start only AFTER combat is marked by a damage event and ride a 5-tick async cadence, so the FIRST hit of every engagement runs with pingMillis==null -> rtt=0 -> verticalFor simulates 0 ticks (exact no-op); RTT becomes available ~5-10 ticks + RTT after the opener. (b) tickProbes on a 30-tick (1.5s) hit lull removes the combatant AND calls latency.forget(id), wiping the measured RTT entirely (not just stopping probes) — every re-engagement opener after a chase gap is uncompensated again. (c) The noDamageTicks>8 guard declines all legal max-cadence combo hits (frozen 9-11 at the boundary). Net operative band: hits arriving 12-30 ticks after the previous hit in sustained combat — openers and cadence hits, the common cases, silently skip compensation. Side effects: hit-to-hit vertical inconsistency (compensated vs not alternates with cadence phase); rod/projectile hits never mark combat (cause!=ENTITY_ATTACK filter), so the KnockbackUnit non-melee compensation path effectively always sees rtt=0 in rod-only exchanges; and because the landing-prediction branch is the one thing that RESCUES the over-decayed ledger vy to the grounded 0.3608 (instead of a floored 0.0 lift), the narrow band means that rescue almost never fires where the ledger-vy bug bites.

**Trigger:** Every fresh engagement's first hits and every re-engagement after a 1.5s+ gap (feature on, the default): compensation contributes nothing. Mid-fight 12-30-tick-gap hits: compensation active — the inconsistency is the symptom.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/LatencyCompensationUnit.java:90-102 (combat marked only on damage), 108-121 (30-tick timeout -> combatants.remove + latency.forget), 74-76 (5-tick cadence); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:541-542 (null ping -> rtt 0); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/CompensationQuery.java:25-27 (noDamageTicks>8 guard), 33 (rtt/50=0 -> no-op), 38-41 (the landing rescue); core/src/main/resources/latency-compensation.yml:2-6 (stated purpose)

**Maps to the report:** Contributes the unreproducible vertical inconsistency ('a feeling thing'): identical-looking hits alternate between corrected and uncorrected verticals by cadence phase and lull history, and the correction is absent exactly on opener hits where a falling-on-their-screen victim ships an over-tall stale vertical or (post-2.4.8 floor) a dead one.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The finding's code descriptions are factually accurate: the compensation feature marks combatants only on ENTITY_ATTACK damage (LatencyCompensationUnit:90-102), probes on a 5-tick async cadence, so openers run with pingMillis==null -> rtt=0 -> verticalFor no-ops (HitRegistrationUnit:541-542, CompensationQuery:33); tickProbes calls latency.forget on the 30-tick lull wiping RTT (114-117, LatencyModel:39-41); the noDamageTicks>8 guard declines recently-hit combo victims (CompensationQuery:25); feature is default ON (config.yml:38). All verified. BUT the finding fails as a diagnosis of the reported bug on four grounds. (1) The compensation is STRICTLY VERTICAL: compensationY feeds only victimYOverride -> victimVy -> the y component (KnockbackEngine:365, 496-500). The horizontal knockback x/z (lines 481-501) derives from base().horizontal(), pace factor, sprint bonus, and the victim's own vx/vz — it never reads victimYOverride. The owner's report is explicitly horizontal ("doesn't move back", "non-sprinting knockback", "sprint hits with less knockback" — sprint-vs-non-sprint is a horizontal bonus/extra distinction). The feature cannot touch it. The finding only matches the report by re-labeling the symptom as "vertical inconsistency", which is not what was reported. (2) The dead-band is by-design graceful degradation: when RTT is unavailable or a guard declines, verticalFor returns the raw ledger vertical = era-exact-no-op. Compensation is a refinement layered on era-correct behavior; its absence yields era-baseline vertical, not weakened knockback. "Structurally OFF" = correct no-op. (3) The noDamageTicks>8 guard is the documented double-hit guard (comment: "the ledger already carries the flight residual") — a deliberate hand-off to the D2 ledger, not an over-decline defect; any ledger over-decay is the separately-tracked 2.4.8 ledger-vy divergence, not this feature. (4) The rod/ENTITY_ATTACK observation is vertical-only AND rods never knocked players per the compendium.
- Corrections: The finding's mechanical claims about the code hold, but its bug classification and symptom-match do not. Reclassify: this is not a weak-knockback bug and does not match the owner's report. The latency-compensation query is strictly a per-hit VERTICAL y-override (CompensationQuery.verticalFor -> victimYOverride -> victimVy -> y in KnockbackEngine:496-500); the horizontal knockback (push from base horizontal + pace + sprint bonus, and the victim's own vx/vz friction residual, KnockbackEngine:481-501) is entirely independent of it. Therefore no branch of the described "dead band" can produce weak horizontal knockback, the "non-sprinting knockback feel", or weaker sprint hits — all of which are horizontal-plane symptoms. Every no-op branch the finding flags (rtt=0 opener, forget-on-lull, noDamageTicks>8) reverts to the era-exact-no-op vertical (the raw ledger vy), which is correct era-baseline behavior; the noDamageTicks>8 guard is the intentional double-hit hand-off to the D2 ledger (its comment states the ledger carries the flight residual). The genuine residual observation — that the vertical compensation activates phase-dependently and can make combo verticals feel inconsistent — is a subtle vertical-pop feel, is separable from the tracked ledger-vy over-decay issue, and is NOT the reported horizontal weakness. Investigators pursuing the owner's symptom should look at the horizontal path: sprint verdict resolution (sprintVerdict / SprintWire freshness at close range), the base().horizontal() / push computation, pace/servo horizontal scaling, and resistance/suppressor rolls — none of which this feature touches.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss from this feature: exactly ZERO at all ranges — compensationY feeds only the y component (KnockbackEngine:496-500); horizontal x/z never read it, so it cannot weaken the "moves back" distance or the sprint-vs-non-sprint horizontal bonus the owner describes. Vertical effect where the dead-band no-ops on a falling-victim opener: the compensated grounded-equilibrium (~0.3608) vs stale ledger vy could differ by up to ~0.3-0.4 in vy, i.e. a vertical-feel/pop-height difference only, on opener and post-1.5s-gap first hits (common in real PvP). No angle error and no horizontal-distance loss in any scenario. Does not explain the reported horizontal weak-knockback symptom.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: MECHANISM VERIFIED AT SOURCE. All three gates are real and the operative band is genuinely narrow:
(a) LatencyCompensationUnit.onDamage (line 92) marks combat only on ENTITY_ATTACK; probes ride a 5-tick repeatAsync (line 74-76). compensationFor (HitRegistrationUnit:542, KnockbackUnit:386) reads latency.forPlayer(id).pingMillis(), which is null until a probe round-trips. Null→rtt=0→CompensationQuery does simulateVerticalVelocity(baseVy,g,0)=baseVy (0 iterations), an exact no-op. Probes only start ~5 ticks after the opener marks combat and reply ~RTT later, so the opener AND the first 1-2 post-opener hits run with rtt=0.
(b) tickProbes (line 114-116) at the 30-tick (1.5s) timeout does combatants.remove(id) AND latency.forget(id) — LatencyModel.forget removes the whole Record, wiping pingMillis to null. Every re-engagement after a chase gap is a fresh dead-band opener.
(c) CompensationQuery:25 `noDamageTicks()>8` declines hits landing within ~12 ticks of the last — the fast-combo cadence hits land at the half-immunity boundary (frozen noDamageTicks ~9-11), declined. Net operative band ~12-30 ticks; openers and max-cadence combo hits skip compensation.

HOW IT REACHES THE SYMPTOM. Compensation is PURELY VERTICAL (KnockbackEngine:494-500: `y = victimVy·friction.y + base.vertical`, override replaces victimVy; horizontal untouched, SET-mode comment says the hint is "irrelevant by definition"). It bites only in ADD vertical mode — which every era preset uses. On the default LEGACY_17 (friction.y 0.5, base.vertical 0.4, verticalMin floored to 0.0 in 2.4.8), an AIRBORNE falling victim carrying the separately-diagnosed over-decayed ledger vy (~−1.5) ships y=−1.5·0.5+0.4=−0.35 → clamped to 0.0 = a DEAD vertical. Compensation's landing branch would have rescued it to groundedEquilibrium −0.0784·0.5+0.4 = 0.3608 (matches the finding's cited value). A 0.0-vertical hit leaves the victim grounded, so ground-drag (×0.6 slipperiness) eats the horizontal push and the victim "doesn't really move back" — a real pathway to the HORIZONTAL symptom, even though the mechanism only writes vertical. Without the ledger bug (real vy ~−0.2), the dead-band still produces a ~0.06 b/tick vertical inconsistency vs the 0.3608 rescue — the "feeling thing."

FREQUENCY. Raw dead-band coverage is high: every engagement opener, the first 1-2 hits after it (ping not yet measured), every re-engagement after a 1.5s gap, and max-cadence combo hits. BUT the symptom is only VISIBLE when the victim is airborne with a negative/over-decayed vy — grounded openers hit the clientOnGround early-return (CompensationQuery:30) and carry equilibrium vy anyway, so they ship full pop unaffected. The symptom-producing subset is exactly the close-range jumping/w-tap exchange the owner names ("especially when two players are quite close and hitting each other," victim airborne). High raw frequency, narrower visible subset → recurring but unreproducible-on-demand.

RELATION TO REPORT. This finding is best read as the SAFETY-NET-WITH-HOLES enabler of the ledger-vy over-decay symptom: the one branch that rescues an over-decayed vertical to 0.3608 almost never fires where the bug bites (openers, re-engagements, fast combos all in the dead-band). It also independently contributes the hit-to-hit vertical inconsistency by cadence phase. It does NOT independently create horizontal weak-KB (mechanism is vertical-only), but dead-vertical → grounded → ground-drag is a plausible route to reduced backward travel, so it plausibly produces PART of the report. Not refutable. Config note: default-ON (config.yml:38), so this is the default experience. Rod/projectile-only exchanges (KnockbackUnit non-melee path) never mark combat (ENTITY_ATTACK filter) so always see rtt=0 — confirmed but minor. Classification: a code defect in Mental's own corrector (near-complementary gates), not an era mechanic — bug.
- Severity: Vertical-only mechanism (horizontal never touched). On the default LEGACY_17 and the floored practice presets (friction.y 0.5, verticalMin 0.0): a dead-band hit on an airborne, over-decayed-ledger-vy victim (~−1.5) ships vertical clamped to 0.0 vs the compensated rescue 0.3608 — a full ~0.36 b/tick vertical launch lost; the victim stays grounded and ground-drag (×0.6) eats the horizontal push → "doesn't really move back." Without the co-occurring ledger-vy bug (real vy ~−0.2): ~0.06 b/tick vertical inconsistency vs 0.3608 (subtle "feeling"). On signature/velt (friction.y 0.1, unfloored): only ~0.14 b/tick inconsistency, never a dead zero. FREQUENCY: dead-band covers every engagement opener, the first 1-2 post-opener hits (ping not yet measured), every re-engagement after a 1.5s gap, and max-cadence combo hits — high raw frequency, but the visible weak-KB subset is airborne-victim close exchanges (jumping/w-tap), since grounded openers early-return and pop normally. This finding is the enabler that lets the ledger-vy symptom through, not an independent horizontal-KB cause; matches "subtle, hard to reproduce, more a feeling" and "especially when two players are quite close and hitting each other."

### `compensation-amplifies-overdecayed-ledger-vy` — bug, confidence medium (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** CompensationQuery's baseVy input is view.motion().vy() — the LEDGER vy, which the 2.4.8 round measured diverging badly for juggled victims (ledger free-falls to -1.5 while the real client hovers -0.05..-0.34; round-1 ledger-vy-overdecay-and-nonrising-liftoff-misstamp). When compensation fires on such a victim (12+-tick gap, client-airborne, RTT present), the airborne branch simulates that ALREADY-too-deep vy a further rtt/50 ticks downward before it enters y = vy*0.5 + 0.4 — compounding the known error proportionally to victim ping (150ms adds 3 gravity steps ≈ -0.23 more vy ≈ -0.12 more vertical) and pushing more hits into the verticalMin 0.0 floor (zero-lift 'dead' hits). The landing branch partially counteracts: ticksToFall computed from the too-deep vy predicts touchdown EARLY, so some of these hits are rescued to the grounded equilibrium (0.3608 vertical) — meaning the net per-hit outcome flips between 'rescued-normal' and 'floored-dead' depending on distanceToGround, RTT, and the error magnitude: high-variance verticals concentrated on juggled victims, worse at higher ping.

**Trigger:** Feature on (default) + combos gap >=12 ticks with the victim still airborne (juggle/knock-away chase) + RTT probe present: the compensated vertical is computed from garbage vy and made ping-proportionally worse, or snapped to grounded by a mispredicted early landing.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:543 (baseVy = view.motion().vy() — the ledger); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/CompensationQuery.java:33-44 (simulate/land off that vy); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/MotionMath.java:35-41,86-99; docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-ledger-vy-divergence.md (measured divergence); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:527-529 (verticalMin floor). Refines round-1 ledger-vy-overdecay-and-nonrising-liftoff-misstamp with the ping-scaling propagation.

**Maps to the report:** Extends the strongest round-1 vertical finding to explain why it feels PING- and phase-dependent: the same juggle hit ships a normal pop, a flat 0-lift shove, or a grounded-equivalent stamp depending on RTT and the mispredicted landing — unpinnable by construction.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: All literal code claims verify: baseVy is the over-decayed ledger vy (HitRegistrationUnit:543; SessionService:533 feeds session.ledger().current()); LEGACY_17 default uses VerticalMode.ADD with Friction.y=0.5 and Limits(0.4, verticalMin=0.0) (KnockbackProfile:133-144), so compensation's vertical IS consumed (the SET short-circuit at KnockbackEngine:494-495 does not apply); LATENCY_COMPENSATION is default-ON (Feature.java:74); the airborne branch simulates ping-proportionally more negative (MotionMath:35-41); the 0.0 floor exists (KnockbackEngine:527). So the mechanism is code-real in a NARROW regime.

But the finding's causal/severity story is refuted on three grounds:

(1) Vertical-only. computeVector (KnockbackEngine:496-501) routes victimYOverride ONLY into y; x/z are victim.vx/vz*friction - pushX/Z, independent of compensation. The owner's report is horizontal ('doesn't move back', 'non-sprinting knockback'). This mechanism cannot reduce horizontal push; only a secondary grounded-friction feel effect from staying grounded.

(2) The finding's HEADLINE scenario (juggled victim, measured ledger −1.5 vs real −0.2) actually hits the LANDING branch → RESCUE, not amplify. distanceToGround and clientOnGround are built from the LIVE player location (SessionService:508-509), i.e. the REAL near-ground position, while baseVy is the diverged ledger. ticksToFall(−1.5, small-real-distance, g)=1 ≤ rtt/50 → returns groundedEquilibrium(−0.0784) → y = −0.0784·0.5+0.4 = 0.3608 healthy pop. Compensation rescues the exact scenario the finding says it harms.

(3) Where the airborne branch does fire (large real distanceToGround) with the deeply-negative measured baseVy≈−1.5, the raw no-comp value −1.5·0.5+0.4=−0.35 ALREADY floors to 0.0; the compensated ≈−0.465 also floors. Identical outcome — the floor decides, not compensation. Compensation is only the marginal cause of a floored hit in a thin band (baseVy≈−0.57..−0.8, large distanceToGround, ≥~150ms ping), which is neither 'concentrated on juggled victims' nor a plausible driver of the owner's complaint.

Guard checks (noDamageTicks>8 double-hit guard, clientOnGround→null) are consistent with the finding's stated trigger but do not save it. CompensationQueryTest pins exactly the landing→groundedEquilibrium and airborne→simulate behaviors I relied on.
- Corrections: Residual real behavior (not the finding's claim): CompensationQuery's airborne branch (kernel/.../CompensationQuery.java:43) does simulate the ledger baseVy ping-proportionally more negative, and in a narrow regime — client genuinely airborne with a LARGE real distanceToGround, a ledger vy only mildly over-decayed (≈−0.57..−0.8), and ≥~150ms ping — it can flip a small positive vertical pop into the verticalMin 0.0 floor (KnockbackEngine:527), where the raw value would not have floored. This is vertical-only, config-gated (only ADD-mode profiles like the default LEGACY_17; a SET-vertical profile discards it per KnockbackEngine:494-495), and feature-gated (LATENCY_COMPENSATION on). The finding's stated headline — 'compensation amplifies the over-decayed vy on JUGGLED victims, pushing MORE hits into the floor' — is backwards for that scenario: distanceToGround/clientOnGround come from the REAL live location (SessionService:508-509), so the measured juggle divergence (real client near ground) drives ticksToFall to land in 1 tick → LANDING branch → groundedEquilibrium → 0.3608 pop (a RESCUE), and in deep over-decay the raw value already floors so compensation is outcome-neutral. If a fix is wanted, the correct lever is the planned baseVy source (clamp toward the position-ring-derived real vy, per the 2.4.8 max(ledgerVy, ringVy−0.15) plan), which fixes both this narrow-band case and the raw ledger-vy floor at its source; touching CompensationQuery alone would not address the dominant (rescue / floor-regardless) behaviors.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss: ZERO — compensation writes only y (KnockbackEngine:496-501); the owner's horizontal 'doesn't move back' report is untouchable by this path (only an indirect grounded-friction feel effect). Vertical: in the genuine but narrow amplification window (airborne AND real distanceToGround >~3 blocks AND over-decayed ledger baseVy in ≈[−0.57,−0.8] AND ping ≥~150ms), a small positive pop (0.0–0.36 lift) is flipped to a floored 0.0 — at most ~0.36 vertical lift lost, ping-proportional. Expected real-PvP frequency: LOW/rare. The common measured juggle divergence (real client near ground, small distanceToGround) hits the LANDING branch and is RESCUED to 0.3608, and the deep-over-decay airborne case floors identically with or without compensation, so compensation is the marginal cause only in the thin band above — not a meaningful contributor to felt weak knockback at the ranges in the report.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: MECHANISM VERIFIED IN CODE, with important scope corrections.

Vertical pipeline (LEGACY_17 default, the parse-empty profile): friction.y=0.5, base.vertical=0.4, verticalMode=ADD, verticalMin=0.0 (2.4.8 owner floor now covers legacy too), vertical cap=0.4, air=(1.0,1.0), add=(0,0). - Floor threshold: y hits 0.0 when victimVy < -0.8.
- Standing grounded eq (-0.0784) → y=0.3608 (the canonical era standing pop).
