CRITICAL SCOPE FACT: the override is VERTICAL-ONLY (victimYOverride→victimVy). x and z are computed independently from victim.vx()/vz() and the push (KnockbackEngine.java:497,501). So this finding cannot touch horizontal knockback at all — it does NOT explain the report's core "victim doesn't move back" / "sprint read as non-sprint" close-range HORIZONTAL complaint.

CLOSE-RANGE IS EXCLUDED BY THE GUARDS: rapid close trades are (a) grounded → clientOnGround() returns null (no compensation), and (b) sub-8-tick cadence → noDamageTicks>8 blocks re-compensation. So compensation fires only on airborne, 12+-tick-gap juggle/knock-away chase at range — exactly the "elsewhere too" band round-2 targets, not the close-range emphasis.

WITH vs WITHOUT the mechanism (hand-computed, RTT-scaled, gravity 0.08):
- DEEP juggle (measured ledger vy≈-0.96, doc exemplar): WITHOUT comp y=-0.96*0.5+0.4=-0.08→floored 0.0 (already dead). WITH comp @150ms(3t) sim→-1.134→y=-0.167→still 0.0. So for the deep case the compensation-SPECIFIC incremental harm is ZERO — the over-decayed input (round-1's bug) already floors it. Compensation can only leave it 0.0 or, via early-landing rescue, LIFT it to 0.3608.
- MARGINAL band is where compensation adds harm: ledger vy in ~(-0.8,-0.55). e.g. vy=-0.6 @300ms(6t): WITHOUT=+0.10 lift; sim6→-0.979→y=-0.0895→floored 0.0. Loss=0.10 vertical, ping-proportional (vy=-0.75 @150ms: +0.025→0.0, loss 0.025). Converts a small positive pop to zero-lift.
- LANDING FLIP (real variance, largely input-driven): low juggle (small distanceToGround) → early landing → 0.3608; high juggle → simulate → 0.0. A 0.36 vertical swing between adjacent juggle hits, flipping on distanceToGround/RTT — genuinely "unpinnable by construction," matching the subtle/feeling framing.

VERDICT: not refuted — it plausibly contributes to the ping-dependent, phase-dependent VERTICAL variance on juggled/range hits ("elsewhere too", subtle, unreproducible). But it is (1) VERTICAL-ONLY — irrelevant to the close-range horizontal sprint complaint that is the report's centerpiece; (2) SECOND-ORDER — the dead-hit bulk is round-1's ledger over-decay; compensation's own incremental harm is confined to a narrow marginal vy band (≤~0.10 vertical, ping-scaled) plus the 0.0↔0.3608 landing flip whose magnitude is mostly the bad input, not the compensation; (3) mixed-sign — the landing-rescue branch pushes juggle hits back UP to the era-correct 0.3608, sometimes IMPROVING feel. Classification "bug" stands (it amplifies a documented input defect proportional to ping and it's default-on producing era-wrong flat-vertical juggle hits), but the finding overstates by implying compensation is a primary driver; it is an accelerant on round-1's input bug.
- Corrections: Correct core: CompensationQuery.verticalFor feeds baseVy=view.motion().vy() (the ledger vy, documented over-decayed for juggled victims) into either a further-downward simulate (rtt/50 gravity steps, ping-proportional) or an early-landing grounded-equilibrium rescue, and LATENCY_COMPENSATION is default-on. But the finding overstates impact on three counts: (1) VERTICAL-ONLY — the override never touches horizontal x/z (KnockbackEngine.java:497,501), so it cannot produce the report's headline "victim doesn't move back" / sprint-reads-as-non-sprint close-range symptom, which is horizontal. The deep juggle case (ledger vy≈-0.96, the doc's dominant mode) is ALREADY floored to 0.0 without compensation, so the compensation adds nothing there. Larger visible effect is the 0.0↔0.3608 landing-flip variance (0.36 vertical swing between adjacent juggle hits, on distanceToGround/RTT) — but that magnitude is mostly the over-decayed input (round-1), not the compensation. Matches "subtle/feeling/ping-dependent/elsewhere-too" for the vertical juggle band; does NOT match the close-range horizontal sprint-vs-non-sprint complaint.

### `no-jitter-aware-windows-gate-skew-is-jitter-not-ping` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** Q3 answer + extension of round-1 feedback-gate-paces-out-legal-hits-under-skew. NOTHING in the codebase widens or narrows any admission/feedback window with measured latency or jitter: JitterCalculator.calculateMillis and LatencyModel.previousPingMillis have zero production consumers (tests only; incidentally the dead calculator's q3Index = q1Index*3 = sample 9 of 15 is the 60th percentile, not Q3), and the FeedbackGate is pure wall-clock per-victim arrival pacing. Therefore the pace-out effect is JITTER-proportional and ping-AMPLITUDE-independent: a stable 200ms connection loses no more pre-sends than LAN, because both hits shift by the same transit; what compresses the 500ms legal gap below the 450ms auto window is differential delay between consecutive ATTACK flushes. Under +/-30ms wifi-grade jitter, consecutive-hit arrival gap = 500 + (j2-j1) with j2-j1 in [-60,60]; P(gap<450) ≈ 1-2% per hit pair for a uniform bound, several times that for heavy-tailed wifi — each such hit silently loses its pre-send and takes the weaker/later live-ledger recompute path (round-1 paced-out-presend-recomputes-off-live-ledger), at ANY range. The CPS limiter (arrival-window 20/s) has the same jitter character: burst bunching can transiently overfill the 1s window and eat a legal click.

**Trigger:** Default feedback-min-interval-ms auto (450ms) + a jittery (not merely slow) attacker connection at legal max cadence; each pace-out ships the recompute-flavored knock. Setting feedback-min-interval-ms lower narrows exposure but removes the phantom guard (round 1).

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/JitterCalculator.java:26-67 (dead in production; grep: consumers only in kernel/src/test/.../JitterCalculatorTest.java), :34-35 (q3 index quirk); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/LatencyModel.java:78-84 (unconsumed accessors); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/FeedbackGate.java + HitRegistrationUnit.java:398-402 (wall-clock only, no latency input); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/CpsLimiter.java (arrival-window). Extends round-1 findings feedback-gate-paces-out-legal-hits-under-skew and paced-out-presend-recomputes-off-live-ledger.

**Maps to the report:** Sharpens the round-1 finding for the synthesizer: the weak-hit selection is keyed to connection QUALITY (jitter), not ping magnitude — consistent with the owner feeling it inconsistently across players and being unable to pin a scenario.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: All code claims verified true. Auto window = max(0, maxNoDamageTicks/2-1)*50 = 450ms (line 398-400), default feedback-min-interval-ms: auto. JitterCalculator.calculateMillis/jitterMillis and LatencyModel.previousPingMillis are confirmed dead in production (grep: only their own definitions + kernel tests; no production caller). The characterization is sound: because the gate compares two arrival timestamps, a constant transit delay cancels and only DIFFERENTIAL timing compresses the 500ms cadence below the 450ms window — so exposure is ping-amplitude-independent and connection-quality (jitter/phase) driven. Probability math verified: gap=500+(j2-j1), j2-j1 triangular on [-60,60], P(gap<450)=P(<-50)=50/3600≈1.4% per velocity-eligible hit pair — matches the finding's 1-2%. Cannot refute.

(b) velocity-eligible hits are already paced to ~500ms by the frozen-view immunity gate, so 450-vs-500 is the right comparison (supports the finding). The gameplay-weakness magnitude is profile-dependent: combos=false presets (majority bundled) carry no melee residual so their horizontal recompute is nearly identical, and the divergence lives in the vertical (grounded re-stamp) + live-position direction; combos=true presets also lose horizontal residual to extra decay.

era_call: I judge divergence-from-era, not config-dependent — the effect is active under DEFAULT config (auto=450ms), selected by connection quality; the feedback-min-interval-ms knob is a mitigation that removes the phantom-double-velocity guard, not an off-by-default gate. Era pacing was pure vanilla noDamageTicks with no per-victim wall-clock gate, so the jitter-selected recompute path is the era break. This finding is primarily a correct CHARACTERIZATION/sharpening of the already-catalogued round-1 pair (feedback-gate-paces-out + paced-out-presend-recomputes-off-live-ledger).
- Corrections: Finding stands; refine three points. (1) Framing: the gap compression is driven by DIFFERENTIAL inter-arrival timing = network jitter + client CPS send-phase + the tick-quantized (50ms) immunity-reopen instant, not network jitter alone; the finding's own phrase 'differential delay between consecutive ATTACK flushes' is the precise statement, and 'jitter-proportional / ping-amplitude-independent' is correct as a conclusion but under-credits CPS phase as a co-driver. (2) The 450-vs-500 comparison is well-founded because velocity-eligible hits are already paced to ~500ms by the frozen-view immunity gate (round-1 frozen-immune) — this supports, not weakens, the finding. (3) Gameplay-weakness magnitude is profile-dependent and mostly NOT horizontal for default presets: combos=false presets (legacy-1.8/mmc/lunar/velt/signature) carry no melee residual, so the recompute's horizontal base is nearly identical and the divergence is vertical (grounded re-stamp) + live-position direction; only combos=true presets additionally lose horizontal residual to extra decay. era_call is divergence-from-era rather than config-dependent: the effect is active under default config (auto 450ms); feedback-min-interval-ms is a mitigation that removes the phantom-double-velocity guard, not an off-by-default gate. Overall this is a correct sharpening of the round-1 feedback-gate/recompute pair, not a new independent defect.

Frequency: ~1.4% of velocity-eligible (legal-cadence) hit pairs under +/-30ms uniform jitter (verified: triangular tail 50/3600), several times that on heavy-tailed wifi, ~0% on a stable connection regardless of ping amplitude. Net: a subtle, any-range, connection-quality-selected intermittent weakening (a 'feeling', not a reproducible scenario) — matches the owner's report; low absolute magnitude, non-zero prevalence on poor connections.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Mechanism confirmed at the code level. (1) Dead code: grep for calculateMillis/jitterMillis/previousPingMillis outside /test/ returns EMPTY — JitterCalculator and LatencyModel.previousPingMillis have zero production consumers. The live pingMillis() is consumed, but only in reach/latency-compensation math (HitRegistrationUnit:541,573; KnockbackUnit:385; ComboPredictor:325); nothing feeds ping OR jitter into any admission/feedback window. (2) FeedbackGate.tryPreSend (lines 24-35) is pure wall-clock per-victim arrival pacing — its signature carries only (victim, nowMillis, minIntervalMillis); no latency input exists. (3) Default feedback-min-interval-ms: auto → FEEDBACK_INTERVAL_AUTO sentinel → HitRegistrationUnit:398-400 computes (maxNoDamageTicks/2 − 1)*50 = (10−1)*50 = 450ms for vanilla maxNoDamageTicks=20. Legal knockback cadence is the 10-tick immunity half-window = 500ms. So a fixed 50ms wall-clock margin with no latency/jitter awareness.

The finding's central claim is therefore correct and structurally forced: because the gate keys on server ARRIVAL wall-clock and nothing compensates, the pace-out is JITTER-proportional and ping-AMPLITUDE-independent. A stable 200ms link loses nothing (both consecutive ATTACK flushes shift by the same transit); only the DIFFERENTIAL transit delay between two consecutive knockback-bearing flushes can compress the observed gap below 450ms. Observed gap = 500 + (j2−j1). Pace-out condition: j2−j1 < −50ms.

Frequency (hand-computed): for ±30ms uniform per-packet jitter, j2−j1 is triangular on [−60,60] with density f(x)=(60−|x|)/3600. P(gap<450)=P(diff<−50)=∫_{−60}^{−50}(60+x)/3600 dx = [ (60+x)^2/7200 ]_{−60}^{−50} = 100/7200 ≈ 1.4% per knockback-hit pair — matching the finding's 1-2%. Heavy-tailed wifi (occasional 50-100ms spikes) raises P(|adverse diff|>50) several-fold, plausibly 5-15% during hiccups. The finding UNDERSTATES it: there is a second, independent sub-450ms source it omits — the netty thread timestamps `now` at packet arrival, decoupled from the 50ms-quantized server immunity floor, so two hits legitimately 10 immunity-ticks apart can land with a wall-clock gap that dips below 450ms from tick-phase alone, before any transit jitter. 1.4% is thus a floor.

When paced out: velocityShips=false → shipBurst=false (vector!=null so the vector==null branch doesn't rescue it) → no wire burst, tx not PRE_SENT → the region recompute-off-live-ledger path delivers instead (round-1 assumed real). Round-1 flow doc (line 174/354) confirms that path re-solves off the decayed live ledger or degrades to PASS_THROUGH "plain 0.4, never sprint" — i.e. the delivered horizontal collapses from a fresh-sprint full stamp toward non-sprint magnitude. This is a precise match to the owner's exact words: "even if one is w-tapping or blockhitting, it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback." Because the gate is purely temporal it is RANGE-INDEPENDENT, which directly satisfies the owner's second-message clarification that weak hits are not only close-range. Ping-amplitude independence and jitter-keying explain the owner's inability to pin a scenario and the per-player inconsistency ("a feeling thing").

CpsLimiter corroborator: max-cps default = 20 (hit-registration.yml:12), sliding 1s arrival window (CpsLimiter.java:43-62). Burst-bunching under jitter can transiently pack >20 arrivals into a trailing sub-1s window and reject a legal click — same jitter character, live at defaults, though secondary in magnitude.

Not refuted: the finding both confirms real dead code and correctly re-characterizes the round-1 pace-out as connection-quality (jitter) keyed rather than ping-magnitude keyed, and extends it to all ranges.
- Severity: Per-incident: a paced-out knockback hit loses its frozen-view full stamp (fresh sprint ~0.5-0.6 b/t horizontal + sprint bonus + combo factor) and ships the live-ledger recompute or PASS_THROUGH plain (~0.4 b/t, no sprint) — an estimated ~20-40% horizontal-KB loss on that hit, presenting exactly as the owner's "non-sprinting knockback." Frequency: ~1.4% per knockback-hit pair under ±30ms uniform jitter (triangular-diff integral, matches finding's 1-2%); several-fold higher (5-15% during hiccups) on heavy-tailed wifi; and a floor, since tick-phase decoupling adds an independent sub-450ms source the finding omits. At ~2 knockback hits/s sustained combat that is ~1.7 weak hits/min baseline, several/min on wifi. Range-independent (purely temporal 450ms-vs-500ms gate) and ping-amplitude-independent (only jitter matters) — matching "subtle, inconsistent across players, hard to pin, more a feeling," at ANY range.

### `servo-ping-horizons-modulate-fresh-horizontal` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** Q4 answer. FlightPrediction has exactly one consumer chain: PocketServo.sigma (combo-hold module, default OFF) — no other system reads flight predictions, so a mispredicted flight can shave a knock only through sigma, bounded to 7% at the default 0.93 floor. New ping-specific content beyond round-1's servo findings: both parties' RTT are solve INPUTS — shiftA = round(attackerRtt/2/50) shortens the judgment horizon (tStar = cadence - shiftA), shiftV = floor(victimRtt/2/50) delays the arc/touchdown and shrinks the ground-tail (groundTicks = tStar - shiftV - airTime), and tAllow = tPing + turn (tPing = victimRtt/100, no floor) pushes the answer-denial boundary target outward for high-ping victims. Net: the SAME geometric hit ships a different fresh horizontal (anywhere in [0.93,1.35]x) purely as a function of both pings — mostly BIASED UP for high-ping victims (larger denial target), occasionally down via the shortened window. Additionally the RTT source ALTERNATES: ComboPredictor.rttMillis prefers the probe model but falls back to the view's Bukkit ping whenever the probe record is absent — and LatencyCompensationUnit.tickProbes wipes the probe record on every 30-tick combat lull (latency.forget), so mid-combo hits after a lull can price a different ping value than their neighbours, adding hit-to-hit sigma variance from bookkeeping rather than network reality.

**Trigger:** COMBO_HOLD enabled (default off) + hit 3+ of a held combo; sigma varies with attacker/victim RTT and with the probe-vs-Bukkit source flip after 1.5s combat lulls. Bounded [0.93,1.35] on the fresh component only.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:420-427 (shiftA/shiftV), :471 (ground-tail shrink), :550 + :671-676 (tAllow tPing slack); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/FlightPrediction.java:32-48 (sole affine seam; grep: only PocketServo consumes); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/combo/ComboPredictor.java:200-201,323-330 (RTT inputs + Bukkit fallback); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/LatencyCompensationUnit.java:114-117 (record wiped on lull). Extends round-1 servo-by-design-fresh-shave.

**Maps to the report:** Only if the owner runs the Combo Solver: adds a ping-keyed +/-7-35% variance to mid-combo fresh knocks — another 'feeling' contributor, though biased toward stronger (anti-report) for high-ping victims.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Verified against the cited source. The core mechanism is factually correct code behavior. FlightPrediction's sole non-test consumer is PocketServo (grep-confirmed); its σ output feeds KnockbackUnit.computePaced and multiplies ONLY the fresh contribution (freshFactor = pace*combo), never the friction-carried residual and never the vertical stamp (KnockbackUnit:162,221-222). σ is clamped to config.min()/max() = 0.93/1.35 (ComboSettings.DEFAULTS). The whole feature defaults OFF (PocketServoConfig.INACTIVE ⇒ σ=1, byte-identical). Both parties' RTT are genuine solve inputs: shiftA=round(attackerRtt/2/50) shaves tStar (:421-427), shiftV=floor(...) shifts touchdown and shrinks groundTicks (:471), tAllow=tPing+turn with tPing=rttV/100 no floor (:674-676) sizes the boundary target. So the SAME geometric hit ships a ping-dependent fresh horizontal, bounded [0.93,1.35]. The RTT source alternates: ComboPredictor.rttMillis (:324-330) prefers the probe model, falls back to Bukkit ping; LatencyCompensationUnit.tickProbes (:114-116) wipes the probe record on a >combatTimeoutTicks (default 30) lull. All of this is CONFIRMED and it is designed servo behavior, not a defect — I cannot refute the core.

One sub-claim is over-stated and refuted under the default config: the finding says the lull-wipe adds "hit-to-hit sigma variance from bookkeeping … mid-combo hits after a lull can price a different ping than their neighbours." But the probe forget needs a lull > combatTimeoutTicks (30t), while a combo ends the instant an inter-hit gap exceeds maxGapTicks (default 20t; ComboTracker: "an expired gap abandons the old chain"). Any lull long enough to wipe the probe (>30t) has already ended the combo (>20t). Within one active combo every gap is ≤20t, so the probe record is never wiped and neighbouring mid-combo hits always share the same RTT source. The probe→Bukkit flip therefore occurs only at combo re-engagement — a fresh chain, hit 1, before the servo even shapes (minHits=2) — not between "hit 3+" neighbours. So the intra-combo bookkeeping-variance mechanism does not occur at defaults.

Net: mechanism real, config-dependent (default OFF), bounded to the fresh horizontal, mostly biases σ UP for high-ping victims (anti-report). Not the weak-KB culprit; a minor completeness note.
- Corrections: The core mechanism is CONFIRMED and correctly described: FlightPrediction's only non-test consumer is PocketServo (KnockbackEngine consumes its σ), σ scales the fresh horizontal only, is clamped [0.93,1.35], and both parties' RTT (shiftA/shiftV/tAllow) are real solve inputs, so identical geometry ships a ping-dependent fresh horizontal. All this is default OFF and mostly biases σ UP for high-ping victims (anti-report). Refine two points: (1) The intra-combo "hit-to-hit sigma variance from the probe/Bukkit source flip after a lull" is OVER-STATED and does not occur at defaults. Wiping the probe record needs a lull > combatTimeoutTicks (default 30t, CompensationSettings.DEFAULTS), but a combo ends the instant an inter-hit gap exceeds maxGapTicks (default 20t; ComboTracker abandons the chain on gap expiry). Any lull long enough to wipe the probe has already ended the combo, so within one active combo (gaps ≤20t) the probe record is never wiped and neighbouring mid-combo hits share the same RTT source. The probe→Bukkit fallback flip happens only at combo re-engagement (a fresh chain, hit 1, before the servo shapes — minHits=2), not between "hit 3+" neighbours. (2) Consequently this is not a weak-KB culprit: at defaults it is a complete no-op, and when enabled it is intentional non-era shaping bounded to a small, mostly-upward ping bias on the fresh push.
- Severity: On the fresh horizontal component only, bounded to [0.93,1.35]× — worst case ~7% down / ~35% up on the FRESH push (residual carry and vertical never scaled). Horizontal-KB loss vs an unshaped hit is therefore at most ~7% of the fresh contribution, and only in the rarer down direction; the ping bias is predominantly UP (stronger). Real-PvP frequency: effectively zero at defaults (COMBO_HOLD module is default OFF). Even enabled, requires an active combo (hit 2+), a victim RTT high enough for shiftA/shiftV/tPing to move the integer horizon (~≥50ms), and the sub-7% shave only in the occasional shortened-window case. Not a plausible source of "little to no knockback."

**SYMPTOM lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap)

### `reach-rewind-cap-and-bukkit-ping-drops-high-ping-hits` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: latency-compensation)

**Mechanism:** With reach validation enabled (default OFF), passesReach rewinds the victim's position ring by attackerView.pingMillis() + interpolation-offset (100ms), capped at rewind-cap (500ms), and CANCELS the ATTACK outright on failure — no damage, no knock, no vanilla fallthrough. Two latency-keyed drop mechanisms: (a) an attacker whose ping exceeds ~400ms (cap 500 - offset 100) has their true swing-time victim sample lie OUTSIDE the compared 75ms window around the capped instant, so legal hits on a fast-moving victim fail by up to (ping-400)ms * victim speed (~0.1 blocks per 17ms at sprint) beyond the 0.4 leniency; (b) the rewind uses the VIEW's Bukkit ping — a keepalive-derived, slower-moving figure — not the probe model the rest of the latency pipeline measures, so a jitter spike the probe would see (or vice versa) mis-rewinds by the difference; under wifi jitter the chosen instant wanders +/- tens of ms per hit, randomly eating boundary-legal reach hits. Every eaten hit is a total zero: no knockback and no damage.

**Trigger:** hit-registration reach-validation enabled + attacker ping near/over 400ms, or jittery connections where Bukkit ping lags the true transit; victim strafing/retreating fast at max reach. At defaults (disabled) this path cannot fire.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:557-593 (rewind = min(view ping + offset, cap); Bukkit-ping source at :573; samplesAround 75ms window at :590), reach failure cancels the packet (registration flow, round-1 map line 804); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/HitRegSettings.java:26-34 (DEFAULTS: enabled=false, offset 100, cap 500); contrast probe-model source: HitRegistrationUnit.java:541

**Maps to the report:** Matches 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback' only on reach-validation-enabled deployments and only for high-ping/jittery attackers — but those hits also deal no damage, which distinguishes it observationally from the owner's description.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: All cited code facts hold: reach failure cancels the packet outright (HitRegistrationUnit.java:288-291), rewind = min(attackerView.pingMillis()+offset, cap) (:572-574), and the ping source is the Bukkit/Spigot getPing() via Pings.of(player) (SessionService.java:537), genuinely distinct from the latency probe model used by compensationFor (:541). Default enabled=false (HitRegSettings.java:33); the only extra gate allowReachValidation defaults true. So the path is real but owner-opt-in. It is refuted as an explanation of the owner's weak-KB report for three reasons. (1) Wrong symptom: a failed reach check fully cancels the attack — zero damage, no hurt, no hit register — whereas the owner describes hits that LAND with non-sprint knockback magnitude; the finding itself concedes this distinguisher. (2) Mechanism (b) is overstated: samplesAround uses a ±75ms window (150ms span), ReachClamp.passes is allow-biased and always also tests the live position with 0.4 blocks of leniency, so a Bukkit-vs-transit ping discrepancy of tens of ms is fully absorbed — 'randomly eating boundary-legal hits under wifi jitter' does not follow from the code. (3) Mechanism (a), the rewind cap dropping hits at ~600ms+ ping against a fast strafing victim at max reach, is intentional, tunable lag-comp design (the cap bounds abuse), not a defect, and never fires at normal ping. Era-authenticity is not implicated at all: this is an anticheat feature, off by default.
- Corrections: The code claims are accurate but the finding does not explain the owner's bug. The failure mode is a fully DROPPED hit (no damage, no hurt animation, no register), not the reported weak-but-present knockback ('non-sprinting knockback' on hits that clearly land). It is off by default and requires an owner opt-in with no detected anticheat. Mechanism (b) is materially overstated: samplesAround returns a ±75ms window (150ms span) and ReachClamp.passes is allow-biased, always also testing the live position with 0.4-block leniency and passing if ANY candidate is within reach+leniency, so ping-source jitter of tens of ms is absorbed rather than eating hits. Mechanism (a)'s cap-induced drops only occur at ~600ms+ ping vs a fast target at max reach and are intentional, tunable anti-abuse design. Not a viable cause of the weak-knockback report; not a knockback defect.
- Severity: When fired: 100% KB loss AND 100% damage loss (whole attack cancelled), not a knockback-magnitude issue. Frequency in real PvP: nil at defaults (reachValidation.enabled=false). On an enabled deployment with no detected anticheat, still near-zero for normal-ping players (<400ms); only appreciable for pathological >~600ms ping (mechanism a) against a fast strafing victim at exact max reach, which is intended tunable rewind-cap behavior. Mechanism (b)'s jitter drops are largely absorbed by the 150ms window + 0.4-block leniency + always-checked live position, so realistically negligible.

**SYMPTOM lens: REFUTED** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Code verified end-to-end. The mechanism is real: HitRegistrationUnit.passesReach (:557-593) rewinds by min(attackerView.pingMillis()+100, 500), samples a 75ms window (:590), and on failure the caller does event.setCancelled(true); return; (:288-291) — a total cancel, no damage, no knock, no vanilla fallthrough. The ping source is genuinely the Bukkit keepalive figure (Pings.of -> getPing) distinct from the probe pipeline (latency.forPlayer at :541), so both sub-claims (cap-overrun, ping-source mismatch) are real code. HOWEVER, as a reproduction of the OWNER'S SYMPTOM it fails on four independent counts: (1) Default OFF — ReachValidation.DEFAULTS.enabled=false plus the anticheat.allowReachValidation() gate, so on a default deployment it never runs and cannot be the long-standing feel 'as far back as I can remember'. (2) Wrong symptom class — a failed check cancels the WHOLE attack: zero damage, no hurt flash, no sound, no knock; the owner describes hits that LAND but move the victim weakly (a delivered-but-weak trade); the finding's own matches_report concedes the no-damage distinction. (3) Wrong range — reach validation only bites near max reach (~3.4 blocks); the owner says it's MOST noticeable when players are 'quite close together', where the check passes trivially and cannot fire. (4) Not subtle — a no-damage whiff is loudly noticeable, not a feeling-thing. The numeric niche is tiny: cap only overruns above ~400ms ping; eating a boundary-legal hit needs ping >= ~470ms with the victim at the edge of max reach; jitter mis-rewinds ~0.1-0.28 blocks, inside the 0.4 leniency except at the edge. Real, config-dependent code, but cannot plausibly produce the reported symptom.
- Corrections: The mechanism is real, verified code, but it is default-OFF and gated on a detected anticheat, so it does not run on a default deployment. When it does run it CANCELS the whole attack (no damage, no hurt flash, no knockback) rather than weakening knockback, and it can only fire near max reach (~3.4 blocks) at attacker ping ~400-470ms or heavy keepalive/probe jitter. It therefore does not reproduce the owner's symptom: weak-but-landed knockback, most noticeable when players are close together, felt long-term on a presumably-default config. It produces a distinct symptom — occasional no-damage whiffs for very-high-ping attackers at max range — which the owner would read as non-registration, not weak knockback.
- Severity: Per eaten hit: 100% loss — zero horizontal AND vertical knockback AND zero damage (full attack cancel, no vanilla fallthrough). Frequency in real PvP ~ nil: default OFF (enabled=false + requires detected anticheat), and even when enabled the cap only overruns above ~400ms attacker ping; a boundary-legal hit is only eaten at ping >= ~470ms with the victim strafing at the very edge of max reach (~3.4 blocks); the jitter path mis-rewinds ~0.1-0.28 blocks, inside the 0.4-block leniency except at the edge. Cannot fire at close range at all. Catastrophic-per-event but vanishingly rare and range-mismatched to the report.

### `chase-pocket-sprint-hits-pin-min-clamp-everywhere` — config-dependent, confidence high (finder: chase-midrange)

**Mechanism:** Round 1's engine-math finder claimed the servo biases toward the 1.35 MAX at close range ('a CLOSER victim solves a HIGHER sigma'); that holds only for the stationary lab geometry (no chase, no flee priced). In a REAL chase the solve prices attacker chase (dynamic channel ≈3.3 blocks per 12t window at full sprint, or the 0.70-alignment floor ≈2.36) AND the fleeing victim's measured drift + ground tail (~0.9–1.05 blocks), and the answer-denial target for a fleeing victim caps at ~3.09–3.15. A fold-mirror simulation of PocketServo.simulate shows sigma* for SPRINT-fresh hits (freshEra 0.9) is 0.10–0.50 across the entire 2.5–3.5-block band under EVERY chase channel — even with zero residual and zero drift at d0 2.85 it solves 0.80 — so every mid-combo sprint hit is hard-pinned at the 0.93 min clamp: a UNIFORM 7% fresh-horizontal shave (0.9 → 0.837, ~0.3–0.4 blocks of settle per hit), not the intermittent shave round 1 described, and it steps in exactly at hit 3 (minHits 2 + view publish lag) so combo openers ship full and follow-ups consistently land short. The 2.4.6 calibration claim that 'sigma* centres near 1.0–1.1 at a typical mid-combo residual' (CHASE_ALIGNMENT javadoc; the undershoot dossier's instrument) was measured at freshEra 0.40 — a PLAIN hit — and never covered sprint-fresh hits, for which the inverse solve is permanently saturated and the servo degenerates to a flat ×0.93 on the fresh component.

**Trigger:** modules.combo-hold: true (default false; not enabled by any preset or release — but the owner demonstrably runs the 'Combo Solver': the 2.4.6/2.4.7 clamp band [0.93,1.35] was calibrated from his own playtests) + an attacker holding a 2+-hit combo on a chased victim; every subsequent re-engaged (w-tap) sprint hit at 2.5–3.5 blocks ships 0.93× fresh.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:339-342 (sigma* inversion + clamp), :493-541 (chase ladder + alignment floor), :466-477 (drift S2 + walk-normalized ground tail), :86-93 (CHASE_ALIGNMENT javadoc's 'centres near 1.0–1.1' claim); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:299-351 (servoFactor freshEra ≈0.9 for an aligned sprint hit); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/settings/ComboSettings.java:59-64 (minHits 2, clamps 0.93/1.35); docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md:11-17 (instrument freshEra=0.40); core/src/main/resources/config.yml:273 (default off); simulation mirroring the fold: sprint rows sigma* 0.139–0.504 at d0 2.5/2.85/3.2 under dynamic, measured-EMA and strafe-alignment channels.

**Maps to the report:** Directly matches 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' on a combo-hold-enabled server: every mid-combo sprint hit in the chase pocket is 7% short, uniformly — subtle, never pinnable to a scenario because it is EVERY such hit. Cannot produce 'little to no knockback' (bounded at 7% of fresh). Refines round-1 finding servo-by-design-fresh-shave (corrects its close-range-biases-to-max claim: with chase+flee priced, even d0 2.5 pins the 0.93 min).

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: I attacked the finding and could not refute its core code mechanism; the math holds against the actual profile and dossier values.

VERIFIED FACTS:
1. Sprint fresh magnitude ≈ 0.9. LEGACY_17 (KnockbackProfile.java:132-135) is base Push(0.4,0.4) + extra Push(0.5,0.1). In servoFactor (KnockbackEngine.java:324-340) a sprint hit gives push=0.4 (base) plus horizontalBonus=sprintLevels*extra.horizontal=1.0*0.5=0.5 laid on the yaw axis; projected on the attacker→victim axis for an aligned attacker, freshEra ≈ 0.4+0.5 = 0.9. A plain hit gives just 0.4. So the finder's freshEra 0.9(sprint)/0.4(plain) split is exactly the engine's own arithmetic.

2. The inverse solve saturates the 0.93 min clamp for freshEra 0.9. sigmaStar=(target−constant−slope·residual)/(freshEra·slope) with constant=d0−chaseTravel+drift+tail (PocketServo.java:340,565). Back-solving the dossier's own published probe (freshEra 0.40, chase 1.385, res 0 → σ*=0.857, d0=2.85, target=3.150) pins slope≈4.9. Re-running the SAME geometry with the floored chase (~1.96, the shipped 2.4.7 path) reproduces the dossier's centred σ*≈1.1 at freshEra 0.40 — but at freshEra 0.9 it gives σ*≈0.51 at res 0, dropping further with residual. Even the MAX chase channel (attribute full sprint, 3.367) gives σ*≈0.83 < 0.93. To un-saturate (σ*≥1.0) at freshEra 0.9 needs chaseTravel≈4.1 blocks, which exceeds every channel's ceiling (~3.37). So sprint-fresh hits are pinned at the 0.93 min across the whole 2.5–3.5 pocket under every chase source — robust to the exact slope. This confirms the uniform ×0.93 fresh-shave (0.9→0.837, ≈0.063 b/t × dragSum ~4.9 ≈ 0.31 blocks of lost settle).

3. Calibration/tests never covered sprint-fresh. The undershoot dossier instrument (2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md:11-13) and KnockbackEngineServoTest.java:73 both use freshEra=0.40 ("the base push magnitude" — a PLAIN hit). The CHASE_ALIGNMENT javadoc's "σ* centres near 1.0–1.1" was measured there. No test or calibration pins a freshEra≈0.9 sprint hit, so the saturation was never observed.

REFUTATION ATTEMPTS THAT FAILED: freshEra-isn't-0.9 (refuted — profile gives 0.9); tests-pin-sprint-in-band (none exist; all use 0.40); the-chase-pushes-toward-MAX (true directionally, but even MAX chase can't lift freshEra-0.9 above 0.93).

CAVEATS THE FINDER OVERSTATES / I CORRECT: (a) This is opt-in — combo-hold defaults false (config.yml:273), shipped in no preset. On a default/shipped config the frequency is ZERO. (b) It cannot be the owner's HISTORICAL "as far back as I can remember" bug — PocketServo is a 2.4.x feature; the reported weak-KB predates it. At most it's a modern contributor IF he actually runs the Combo Solver in production (the finder infers this from playtests, which is not proof of a deployed enable). (c) The clamp is PROTECTIVE: the servo WANTS σ≈0.51 (shrink the over-strong sprint knock into the ~3.15 pocket) and 0.93 is the floor bounding that shrink — so the victim still receives 93% of the sprint knock, not "little to no knockback." The finder honestly concedes it can't produce the severe symptom. (d) The "steps in at hit 3" detail is plausible but minHits=2 fires COMBO START on the 2nd hit (ComboSettings.java:16), so the servo engages from hit 3 (first hit after detection) — an implementation detail, not load-bearing. (e) For LEGACY_17 wtapExtra.enabled=false, so w-tapping does NOT change freshEra (still base+extra=0.9); the owner's w-tap observation isn't specifically the driver here, though the fresh is high regardless.

VERDICT: The code mechanism is real and verified — every mid-combo sprint hit in the chase pocket ships a uniform ×0.93 fresh-horizontal shave when combo-hold is enabled, and the calibration genuinely never covered this hit class. It is a legitimate uncovered-scenario calibration gap. But it is gated behind a default-off, non-preset opt-in module and cannot explain the long-standing/severe symptom, so it is config-dependent behavior of an opt-in feature, not a bug in shipped combat.
- Corrections: CONFIRMED mechanism, with corrections. The inverse solve (PocketServo.java:340) does saturate the 0.93 min clamp for freshEra≈0.9 sprint hits under every chase channel: freshEra·slope ≈ 0.9·4.9 ≈ 4.4, and un-saturating needs chaseTravel ≈ 4.1 blocks, above the max attribute-sprint channel (~3.37). Verified against the actual LEGACY_17 profile (base 0.4 + sprint-extra 0.5 aligned = 0.9) and the undershoot dossier's own numbers (which pin slope≈4.9 and were run at freshEra 0.40 — a PLAIN hit — never at sprint-fresh; KnockbackEngineServoTest also uses 0.40). So the calibration gap the finder describes is real: the [0.93,1.35] band was tuned for freshEra 0.40 and permanently saturates min for freshEra≈0.9.

Corrections to the finding's framing: (1) Severity is bounded at 7% and cannot produce the owner's "little to no knockback"; the finder concedes this. (2) The clamp is PROTECTIVE — the servo wants σ≈0.51 to hold the pocket and 0.93 caps the shrink, so the victim still gets 93% of the sprint knock; this is the servo doing its intended pocket-holding job, bounded by the owner's own playtested floor, not the servo "weakening" hits by choice. (3) It only manifests with combo-hold ON (default false, no preset enables it) — zero frequency on shipped configs. (4) It CANNOT be the historical bug ("as far back as I can remember") since PocketServo is a 2.4.x feature; at most a modern contributor if the Combo Solver is deployed. (5) minHits=2 fires COMBO START on hit 2, so onset is hit 3 (first post-detection hit) — matches the finder. (6) For LEGACY_17 w-tap doesn't change freshEra (wtapExtra.enabled=false), so the owner's w-tap remark isn't specifically explained by this path.

Actionable if the owner runs combo-hold: make the min clamp (or the σ target) freshEra-aware, or raise the floor for sprint-fresh, since the current single band was calibrated only at freshEra 0.40 and structurally can't hold a sprint hit interior to the band.
- Severity: Horizontal loss: uniform ×0.93 on the fresh sprint horizontal (0.9 → 0.837 b/t, a 7% shave) ⇒ ≈0.31 blocks less settle per hit over a ~10-tick window. Applies to EVERY mid-combo sprint hit across 2.5–3.5 blocks (not intermittent). Real-PvP frequency: ZERO on any default/shipped config (combo-hold defaults false, in no preset); on a combo-hold-enabled server it is essentially every combo sprint follow-up (hit 3+). Bounded — cannot produce "little to no knockback." Cannot be the owner's historical bug (servo postdates it).

**SYMPTOM lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap)

### `plain-hit-chase-channel-selection-variance` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: chase-midrange)

**Mechanism:** PLAIN mid-combo hits (freshEra 0.4 — the common chase hit after Mental's era post-hit sprint clear when the re-engage hasn't landed) sit INTERIOR to the clamp band, so their sigma is decided by WHICH chase channel prices the hit: (1) the dynamic ramp (full aligned sprint, chase ≈3.3/12t) yields sigma ≈1.0 with flee drift, up to the 1.35 ceiling without it; (2) the measured window EMA (under-reads ~0.11 b/t = 41% of sprint per the 2.4.6 dossier) rescued only to the 0.70-alignment floor yields sigma* ≈0.51 → 0.93 pin; (3) the attribute model sits at (1). Channel selection is keyed on ResetModel.sprinting — a raw wire flag fed ONLY by client ENTITY_ACTION packets: an era-lineage (≤1.21.1) w-tapper flips it per tap phase (an ATTACK arriving after its STOP prices channel 2, before it channel 1), while a modern 1.21.2+ client never sends STOP on attack and Mental's own post-hit sprint obligations (SprintWire.onServerClear, deferred setSprinting(false)) never touch ResetModelWire — so for modern clients the dynamic channel is effectively ALWAYS on, including for attackers whose actual sprint bonus was cleared, and it prices a full-sprint close even for an attacker who stopped chasing (a <0.05-block heading reads NaN → alignment 1.0). Net: identical-looking plain chase hits ship anywhere from 0.372 (0.93×0.4) to 0.54 (1.35×0.4) fresh horizontal — a ~45% swing decided by tap-packet arrival order and drift state.

**Trigger:** modules.combo-hold: true; mid-combo plain (non-re-engaged) hits at 2.5–3.5 blocks; worst hit-to-hit variance for era-lineage/ViaVersion clients whose STOP/ATTACK flush order flips the channel per hit; modern clients sit on the dynamic channel permanently.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:499-541 (channel ladder: dynamic shadows measured shadows attribute; floor); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/ResetModelWire.java:47-55 (sprinting fed only by ENTITY_ACTION; no server-clear writer exists — grep: onSprintStop callers are rim-only), :79-86 (modelAt); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/combo/ComboPredictor.java:237-243 (dynamic gate = resetModel.sprinting && !blocking, independent of the hit's SprintVerdict); docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md:15-17 (measured 0.11 b/t vs dynamic 3.03–3.35 straddle); simulation rows: plain d0 2.85 dynamic σ 1.018 vs measured-EMA σ* 0.506 → 0.93.

**Maps to the report:** Matches the 'subtle, hard to reproduce, more like a feeling' texture exactly: two visually identical plain chase hits ship up to ~45% different fresh horizontal, keyed to sub-tick packet arrival order that no player can perceive or reproduce. Only on combo-hold-enabled configs. Extends round-1 stationary-nan-alignment-refuted-trade-clamp-real to the chase scenario it was built for.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: The finding's structural code claims all verify: (1) σ scales the FRESH horizontal knock multiplicatively (KnockbackEngine.java:206-222, freshFactor = pace * combo); (2) ResetModel.sprinting is fed ONLY by the ENTITY_ACTION rim (PacketTap.java:104-108) with no server-clear writer — onServerClear touches SprintWire only (KnockbackUnit:433), confirming the grep claim; (3) the dynamic-chase gate is exactly `attackerReset.sprinting() && !attackerReset.blocking()` (ComboPredictor.java:237-238), independent of the hit's own SprintVerdict; (4) the channel ladder dynamic>measured>attribute + 0.70 floor exists (PocketServo:499-541); (5) the [0.93,1.35] clamp band is real (config.min()/max() at line 342, owner-playtest per line 90). So the core mechanism — σ channel selection keyed on the raw sprint flag, producing hit-to-hit fresh-horizontal variance under combo-hold — is code-accurate and I cannot refute it. refuted=false.\n\nBut three important corrections weaken the finding materially:\n\nA. CONFIG-DEPENDENT / does not match the owner's report. combo-hold defaults OFF (config.yml:273). The whole servo path is INACTIVE on default config (KnockbackEngine INACTIVE → σ=1, byte-identical). The owner's bug exists 'as far back as I can remember' and is felt on the default experience — this servo is a recent (2.4.x/2.5.0) opt-in feature, so it cannot be the reported bug. The finding correctly self-classifies config-dependent, but the matches_report claim overreaches.\n\nB. The 'modern client always-on dynamic channel' arm is BY DESIGN, not a defect, and its direction is MORE knock not weak. Higher σ = stronger fresh knock; the dynamic channel yields the HIGHEST σ. The ResetModelWire javadoc explicitly documents that the raw client sprint flag is read deliberately to 'price the attacker's close from where they ACTUALLY are' and that a modern client keeps full sprint through Mental's damage-only block. onServerClear (SprintWire) is a knock-BONUS-accounting event for a single hit's computation — NOT a statement that the attacker physically stopped chasing. A genuinely-still-sprinting modern chaser SHOULD be priced on the dynamic (full-sprint) channel. So the finding conflates 'sprint bonus cleared' with 'chase stopped' and mislabels intended behavior as a bug. The only genuinely weak case is the era-lineage/ViaVersion w-tapper whose STOP flushes before the ATTACK, dropping to the measured channel's 0.93 floor.\n\nC. SEVERITY OVERSTATED. The headline '~45% swing (0.372→0.54)' is the full theoretical clamp-band width (0.93→1.35), which the cited plain d0 2.85 hit does NOT reach. The finding's OWN simulation row states 'plain d0 2.85 dynamic σ 1.018 vs measured-EMA σ* 0.506 → 0.93' — i.e. the realistic per-hit swing is 1.018 vs 0.93 ≈ 9% on σ (fresh horizontal ~0.407 vs 0.372 ≈ 0.035 b/t), not 45%. The 0.70-alignment floor (535-541) compresses the channel gap (measured floored to 0.70 of full sprint), further limiting real variance. The 1.35 ceiling is reachable only by deep-interior hits with a hard ramp, not the plain-chase scenario the finding names.\n\nera_call: config-dependent — the entire behavior is gated behind the opt-in combo-hold servo, a Mental-original non-era feature with no 1.7/1.8 precedent (the servo intentionally shapes knock to hold combos). Not an era-authenticity question about the vanilla knockback model.
- Corrections: Confirmed (cannot refute): under modules.combo-hold=true, the pocket servo's σ (which multiplicatively scales the fresh horizontal knock — KnockbackEngine.java:206-222) is priced by a chase channel selected on ResetModelWire.sprinting, a raw client-ENTITY_ACTION flag (PacketTap.java:104-108) that no server-side clear ever touches (onServerClear writes SprintWire only, KnockbackUnit:433). The dynamic-chase gate (ComboPredictor.java:237-238) therefore tracks the client's genuine sprint phase, so an era-lineage/ViaVersion w-tapper's per-tap STOP/START can flip between the dynamic channel and the measured-window+0.70-floor channel across otherwise-identical hits, jittering the shipped fresh horizontal.\n\nCorrections to the finding: (1) config-dependent — combo-hold defaults OFF (config.yml:273); zero effect on the owner's default experience, and this recent opt-in feature cannot be the 'as far back as I can remember' bug. (2) The 'modern client dynamic-always-on' arm is BY DESIGN and yields MORE knock, not weak — reading the raw sprint flag as physical-chase state is the documented intent (ResetModelWire javadoc); onServerClear clears the sprint knock BONUS for one hit's accounting, it is not a locomotion-stop, so pricing a genuinely-sprinting modern chaser on the dynamic channel is correct. The finding mislabels intended behavior as a defect. (3) Severity overstated ~5x: the finding's own sim (dynamic σ 1.018 vs measured 0.93 for plain d0 2.85 ≈ 9%, ~0.035 b/t) contradicts its 45%/0.17 b/t headline; the 1.35 ceiling and full clamp width are not reached by the cited plain hit, and the 0.70 floor compresses the channel gap. Genuine residual: a modest (~9%) per-hit fresh-horizontal sensitivity for era-lineage/ViaVersion w-tap combos on combo-hold-enabled configs — a real estimator noise source, not a knockback-model defect and not the owner's default-config weak-KB report.
- Severity: Realistic per-hit fresh-horizontal swing ~9% (σ 0.93 vs ~1.018 ≈ 0.035 b/t) for the cited plain d0 2.85 chase per the finding's own sim row — NOT the 45%/0.17 b/t headline (0.372→0.54 is the full [0.93,1.35] clamp width, not reachable by a plain mid-range hit).
