**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Mechanism verified structurally accurate. Servo clamp band is [0.93, 1.35], gain 1.0 (ComboSettings.java:61). ResetModelWire.sprinting is fed ONLY by ENTITY_ACTION via PacketTap (onSprintStart/onSprintStop) plus onBlockRaise from SwordBlockingUnit — there is NO server-side sprint-clear writer (SprintWire has onServerClear; ResetModelWire does not), confirmed by grep. The dynamic-channel gate ComboPredictor.java:238 is attackerReset.sprinting() && !attackerReset.blocking(), independent of the hit's SprintVerdict. So a modern 1.21.2+ client that never sends STOP on attack keeps the reset model permanently sprinting -> dynamic channel always on; an era-lineage/ViaVersion w-tapper flips channel per tap phase. All confirmed.

Hand computation, freshEra=0.4: low channel (measured under-reads, rescued to the 0.70-alignment floor, sigma* ~0.51 -> 0.93 min-pin) ships 0.93x0.4 = 0.372 b/t fresh horizontal; high channel (dynamic ramp ~3.03-3.35/12t or attribute model -> sigma* 1.4-1.9 -> 1.35 ceiling) ships 1.35x0.4 = 0.54 b/t. The 45% hit-to-hit swing is real and keyed to sub-tick packet arrival order.

SYMPTOM judgment: matches PARTS of the report — 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should' (adjacent chase hits 0.372 vs 0.54 -> one feels ~31% weaker) and especially the 'subtle, hard to reproduce, feeling thing' texture (variance from sub-tick STOP/ATTACK flush order no player can perceive). So it plausibly produces part of the report -> NOT refuted.

But it canNOT produce the headline 'some hits truly just have little to no knockback (victim does not really move back)': the sigma FLOOR is 0.93, so the servo never ships below 0.372 b/t — only 7% under the natural base fresh knock 0.4, nearly full KB. Two undercuts: (1) COMBO_HOLD.defaultEnabled=false (Feature.java:284) — the whole servo is opt-in, so on a default config it cannot fire, and it cannot explain the owner's 'as far back as I can remember' (pocket servo is a 2.4.x feature); (2) for the common modern client the permanent-dynamic-channel biases sigma toward the 1.35 CEILING (STRONGER KB), so the weak manifestation is narrow — only era-lineage/ViaVersion clients on the STOP-before-ATTACK phase reach 0.93. Note sigma scales only the FRESH horizontal; the sprint-bonus additive is upstream and untouched, so it cannot literally produce 'non-sprinting knockback.'
- Corrections: The finding's arithmetic and mechanism are accurate, but its scope/magnitude are overstated as an explanation of the owner's headline symptom. This is a genuine hit-to-hit KB VARIANCE quirk internal to the opt-in pocket servo (COMBO_HOLD, default OFF), NOT a source of 'little to no knockback': the sigma floor of 0.93 caps the worst weak-end at 0.372 b/t fresh horizontal — 93% of base fresh. The ResetModelWire-has-no-server-clear-writer observation is a real latent inconsistency (modern clients pin the dynamic channel permanently regardless of actual cleared sprint state), but its net effect for modern clients is toward the STRONG (1.35) ceiling, so it cannot be the mechanism behind weak modern-client hits; only era-lineage/ViaVersion clients on the STOP-before-ATTACK tap phase reach the 0.93 low channel. It plausibly contributes to the 'subtle, hard-to-reproduce, sprint hits sometimes feel weaker than they should' texture on combo-hold-enabled configs, but does not reproduce 'the victim just does not really move back,' and as a 2.4.x opt-in feature it cannot account for the long-standing nature of the report.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB VARIANCE, not weakness: low channel ships sigma=0.93x0.4=0.372 b/t fresh vs high channel 1.35x0.4=0.54 b/t — a 0.168 b/t (45% relative) hit-to-hit swing, but the weak end is only 7% below the natural base fresh knock (0.4), never 'little to no.' Frequency: combo-hold-enabled configs ONLY (default OFF); mid-combo plain hits at 2.5-3.5 blocks; the WEAK (0.93) end requires era-lineage/ViaVersion clients whose STOP arrives before ATTACK on that tap phase — a narrow population. Modern 1.21.2+ clients sit permanently on the dynamic channel and bias toward the 1.35 ceiling (stronger, not weaker), so on the common client the finding pushes KB UP. Cannot explain the long-standing 'as far back as I can remember.' Matches the 'subtle feeling / sprint hits sometimes weaker than they should' texture; does NOT match 'victim does not really move back.'

### `alternating-strafe-heading-cancellation` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: chase-midrange)

**Mechanism:** The 2.4.7 alignment factor reads the attacker's NET displacement over 5 ring samples (4 tick deltas, ComboPredictor.ALIGNMENT_SAMPLES) — first sample to last sample — normalized and dotted with the knock axis. A SUSTAINED W+A strafe holds a 45°-off heading for the whole window and correctly reads ≈0.7071. But an ALTERNATING zig-zag strafe chase (leg length ≤ ~4 ticks, the common dodge-tracking rhythm at 2.5–3.5 blocks) has its lateral legs CANCEL in the net displacement: the heading reads on-axis, alignment ≈1.0, and every model chase channel prices the full straight-line close while the attacker's true axis-closing rate is ~cos45° of their speed — the exact ~41% over-price the 2.4.7 fix was built to remove, resurrected for the alternating case. Over-priced chase raises sigma*: plain hits ride the 1.35 ceiling (fresh 0.4 → 0.54 shipped) and the pocket overshoots by up to ~0.8 blocks (the 2.4.7 dossier's own overshoot figure), ejecting the victim past reach so the combo ends by BLOWOUT/gap — after which the next openers ship unservoed at full stamp. Additionally, as the 4-tick window straddles leg switches, the measured alignment sweeps continuously between ~0.71 and ~1.0, adding per-hit sigma jitter on interior (plain) hits. Sprint-fresh hits are unaffected (already pinned at 0.93 either way).

**Trigger:** modules.combo-hold: true; a zig-zag-strafing chase attacker whose strafe legs are shorter than ~4 ticks; plain mid-combo hits ship up to 1.35× and the pocket is overshot — combo drops, rhythm alternates between servoed and unservoed hits.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/combo/ComboPredictor.java:58-65 (ALIGNMENT_SAMPLES=5, direction-only rationale), :311-321 (first→last net displacement); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:736-742 (headingAlignment on the net vector), :96-107 (MIN_CHASE_ALIGNMENT javadoc: the 45° geometry the fix targets); docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-servo-undershoot-chase-floor.md:31-33 (model channels over-price by assuming alignment 1.0 — the identical failure); geometric verification: alternating ±45° legs of equal length sum to an axis-aligned net vector of magnitude cos45°×pathLength, direction on-axis → dot ≈1.0.

**Maps to the report:** Indirect: the direction is STRONGER knockback (anti-report) but it destabilizes the pocket — combos drop and restart, alternating servoed (shaved/boosted) and unservoed (full) hits, feeding the hit-to-hit inconsistency the owner reads as 'a feeling thing'. Reported to prevent the synthesizer from attributing the strafe-chase inconsistency to a weak-KB defect.

**CODE lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap)

**SYMPTOM lens: REFUTED** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Mechanism is REAL and geometrically verified. attackerHeadingAlignment (ComboPredictor.java:311-321) reads the attacker's NET displacement over first→last of 5 ring samples, normalizes, dots with the knock axis via PocketServo.headingAlignment (:736-742). Hand-computed: SUSTAINED W+A strafe reads 0.7071; ALTERNATING symmetric ±45° legs (1- or 2-tick) cancel laterally → alignment 1.0; asymmetric 3/1 → 0.894. True axis-closing rate is s·cos45 = 0.1984 b/t vs 0.2806 straight, so the 1.0 misread over-prices the model chase by 1/cos45 = 1.414 (41%) — the 2.4.7 over-price resurrected for the alternating case.

BUT the symptom direction is opposite the report. The alignment factor scales the MODEL chase channels (dynamic path for a sprinting zig-zag chaser via withDynamicChase, plus the 4b alignedFloorTravel). More chase → smaller constant (= d0 − chaseTravel + drift + tail) → larger σ* = (target − constant − slope·res)/(freshEra·slope). Reconstructing the affine from the servo-undershoot doc (slope≈4.9, freshEra 0.40, d0 2.85, target 3.150): a misread interior hit at res 0.20 ships σ≈1.19 where the correctly-priced (0.71) case falls to the 0.93 min-clamp. The bug pushes σ UP (stronger KB, ~0.85 blocks extra separation, matching the ~0.8-block overshoot figure), ejecting the victim past reach and ending the combo. The ONLY sub-1.0 σ in the system is the 0.93 min-clamp shave — the intended pocket-holding behavior and the CORRECTLY-priced case; the bug moves AWAY from it. So it never produces the owner's 'little to no knockback / non-sprinting knockback' weak symptom.

Chronology also refutes it as THE reported bug: the owner reports weak KB 'as far back as I can remember,' but the whole pocket servo (combo-hold) first shipped in 2.4.2+ and is default OFF (config.yml:273 combo-hold: false). A default-off, recently-added feature cannot be a long-standing weak-KB feeling.

The finder explicitly filed this as Indirect/anti-report — a decoy to stop the synthesizer from attributing strafe-chase inconsistency to a weak-KB defect. That is correct: it is a real over-pricing bug in a non-era opt-in feature, but it cannot reproduce the weak-KB report.
- Severity: Over-price up to 1/cos45 = 41% on the alignment-scaled model chase channel. Effect on shipped KB is a GAIN, not a loss: on mid-combo interior hits σ swings ~0.93 (min-clamp, correctly priced at high residual) up to the 1.35 ceiling (over-priced) — at fresh 0.40 b/t that is ~0.17 b/t larger shipped speed, ~0.85 blocks of extra separation over a ~10-tick window (matches the dossier's 0.8-block overshoot), which ejects the victim past reach and drops the combo. Zero horizontal-KB LOSS in any case — direction is stronger, and the reported 'non-sprinting-strength' weak hits are never produced. Frequency: only with modules.combo-hold:true (default OFF, shipped 2.4.2+), a sprinting zig-zag chaser with ~2-3-tick roughly-symmetric strafe legs at 2.5-3.5 blocks; real asymmetric forward-biased strafes read 0.85-0.95 (only partial over-price). Uncommon overall, and its felt result is strong+inconsistent, not weak — irrelevant to the weak-KB report.

### `servo-decline-guards-flap-on-juggle-verticals` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: chase-midrange)

**Mechanism:** Two decline guards flap per click phase in a chase whose victim doesn't land cleanly between hits, producing 1.0↔0.93 sigma alternation on consecutive sprint hits. (a) Touchdown reprice → airTime decline: a boundary hit capturing the victim descending with remaining height ≤ one fall tick is repriced as a grounded launch (PredictorInputs.asGroundedLaunch), but the shipped vertical stamp fed to airTime is still computed from the victim's over-decayed ledger vy (the documented 2.4.8 ledger-vy divergence: real vy hovers −0.05..−0.34 while the ledger free-falls to −1.5); at vy ≤ ~−1.0 the ADD-mode stamp computes ≤0 (floored to the 2.4.8 bundle-wide verticalMin 0.0) and airTime(0, 0) = 0 < MIN_AIR_TICKS_FOR_SERVO → the solve DECLINES (σ=1, full fresh ships). The same swing one tick earlier (victim mid-flight, launchHeight > 0, stamp small-positive) computes airTime ≥3 → solves → pins 0.93. (b) When the stamp stays slightly positive on a juggled victim, the servo actively compounds its 7% horizontal shave onto exactly the zero-lift hits the ledger-vy family already produces — the deadest-feeling hits get the extra trim. Click-timing decides which branch each hit takes, so consecutive identical hits alternate full/0.93.

**Trigger:** modules.combo-hold: true + a combos-true profile (legacy-1.7/kohi/minehq/badlion) or any juggle where the victim stays airborne between hits; hits thrown at the touchdown boundary decline (full), hits thrown mid-flight solve (0.93) — per-hit variance synchronized to click phase.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:397-401 (launchRepriced), :431-437 (airTime < MIN_AIR_TICKS_FOR_SERVO=3 → decline), :772-791 (airTime(stamp≤0, 0)=0); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:363-385 (shippedVertical: vy×friction.y + base, verticalMin floor — the servo's airTime input); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PredictorInputs.java:230-238 (asGroundedLaunch clears launchVerticalVelocity but the stamp is computed upstream); docs/superpowers/research/2026-07-07-ledger-vy-divergence.md (measured ledger vy −1.5 vs ring −0.34).

**Maps to the report:** Adds hit-to-hit variance ('some hits have less knockback') on servo-enabled configs and stacks a 7% horizontal trim onto the zero-lift juggle hits round 1 already identified — refines round-1 ledger-vy-overdecay-floored-to-zero-lift by naming the servo's compounding and the decline flap it drives. Bounded at 7%; not a no-knockback source.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: I could not refute the core code mechanism; it is real, though the finding overstates its magnitude/frequency.

VERIFIED TRUE:
1. Reprice → decline. `simulate` (PocketServo:397-403) reprices a descending boundary capture to a grounded ground-level launch via `asGroundedLaunch()` (launchHeight→0). The shipped vertical stamp is NOT recomputed (line 396 comment; it is frozen in KnockbackEngine.solve:346 before the reprice). `airTime(verticalStamp, 0.0)` (772-791) returns 0 for ANY non-positive stamp (`y<=0 && !(vy>0) → return 0`), so airTime 0 < MIN_AIR_TICKS_FOR_SERVO(3) → the degenerate guard (431-437) declines → σ=1 (full fresh ships). A deeply-negative ledger vy in ADD mode (shippedVertical:368 `vy×friction.y+base`, then air multiplier, then verticalMin floor) does drive the stamp ≤0. Note the verticalMin=0.0 floor is NOT strictly required — airTime returns 0 for any non-positive stamp, floor or not — so the decline branch is slightly LESS config-gated on verticalMin than the finding states.
2. The alternate (airborne, launchHeight>0, launchHeight+vy>0) does NOT reprice; airTime simulates a fall from launchHeight (starting vy=stamp=0), yielding airTime≥3 → the solve runs. The flap is driven by launchHeight crossing the |vy| threshold in `launchHeight+vy<=0` — real.
3. Bound: min-factor 0.93 (ComboSettings.DEFAULTS:61), so the solved-branch shave is capped at 7%. Decline hits ship σ=1 (no loss, at MOST equal/stronger).

OVERSTATED (refined, not refuting):
- "Consecutive identical hits alternate full/0.93" overstates it. The 2.4.6/2.4.7 chase floor (519-541) and CHASE_ALIGNMENT calibration deliberately center σ* at ~1.0–1.1 (line 82-91 comment), landing INSIDE the band, not at 0.93. A solved juggle hit pins 0.93 only when σ* still goes false-low — chiefly when residualCarry is HIGH (σ* numerator subtracts slope×residualCarry). So the true flap is decline(1.0) ↔ solve(0.93 on high-residual hits, ~1.0–1.1 otherwise, up to 1.35). The 0.93↔1.0 alternation is real but a narrower subset than "every consecutive pair."
- Mechanism (b) "servo compounds 7% onto the deadest hits" is, on high-residual hits, the servo working AS DESIGNED (victim already carries horizontal speed → less fresh needed). It is only arguably a defect as an unintended interaction with the ledger-vy zero-lift family; the code does produce the trim.

RELEVANCE: combo-hold defaults OFF (config.yml:273) and is a recent 2.4.x feature — the owner's "as far back as I can remember" long-standing default-config weak-KB cannot be this. The finding self-scopes as a bounded secondary refinement, which is accurate.
- Corrections: The code mechanism is real: a repriced (touchdown-boundary) juggle hit whose frozen shipped vertical is ≤0 declines (σ=1, full), while the same swing captured higher (launchHeight+vy>0, not repriced) solves and can clamp to σ=0.93 — a per-hit flap synchronized to click timing, on servo-enabled configs only. Two corrections to the finding's framing: (1) the verticalMin=0.0 floor is NOT necessary for the decline — airTime(stamp,0)=0 for ANY non-positive stamp, so the decline fires whenever the repriced hit's shipped vertical is ≤0, floor or era-unfloored. (2) The solved branch does NOT default to 0.93. The 2.4.6/2.4.7 chase floor + CHASE_ALIGNMENT calibration center σ* at ~1.0–1.1 inside the [0.93,1.35] band; a solved hit pins 0.93 only when σ* goes false-low, dominantly on HIGH residualCarry (the residual is subtracted in the σ* numerator). So the real flap is decline(1.0) ↔ solve(0.93 on high-residual/low-chase hits, ~1.0–1.1 typically), not a uniform full/0.93 alternation on every consecutive pair. Mechanism (b)'s 7% trim on high-residual hits is largely the servo behaving as designed (less fresh needed when the victim already carries speed), guarded by the chase floor. All of this requires modules.combo-hold: true (default OFF, config.yml:273) and cannot be the owner's long-standing default-config complaint.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss bounded at 7% (σ min-factor 0.93) on the SOLVED subset of airborne juggle hits; the flap's decline hits ship σ=1 (full era knock, no loss — at most equal/stronger, up to 1.35). No angle error: the servo scales only the axis-projected fresh magnitude, direction untouched. Frequency in real PvP: ZERO in default config (combo-hold OFF). With combo-hold ON, only on sustained juggles where the victim stays airborne between hits AND carries high horizontal residual, with click timing straddling the launchHeight+vy≤0 touchdown threshold — a subtle, low-frequency variance, not a no-knockback source and not the reported long-standing bug.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Mechanism verified coherent against the source. Production servo default (ComboSettings.DEFAULTS) is min=0.93/max=1.35/gain=1.0/target=2.85/window=10, so the shave branch does clamp to 0.93. The airTime decline guard (PocketServo:431-438, MIN_AIR_TICKS_FOR_SERVO=3) and the touchdown reprice (:397-403) are both fed by the SAME over-decayed ledger vy: shippedVertical (KnockbackEngine:363-385) computes the ADD stamp from victim.vy(), and the reprice check reads victimView.motion().vy() (ComboPredictor:220) — the identical over-decayed value. For kohi (friction.y=0.5, base.vertical=0.4) the stamp crosses ≤0 at vy≤−0.8 (sprint −0.97, matching the finding's ~−1.0 and Presets:68's "-0.87"), and the ledger free-falls to −0.96..−1.50 per the divergence doc, so the stamp floors to verticalMin=0.0. With launchHeight repriced to 0, airTime(0,0)=0<3 → decline → σ=1 (FULL). One tick earlier (small-positive stamp, positive launchHeight, no reprice) → airTime≥3 → solve → σ clamps to 0.93 when the natural knock overshoots the pocket target (true at the held ~2.85 equilibrium). The flap between the two is real and click-phase-synchronized.

Two caveats sharpen the magnitude/frequency: (1) at UNIFORMLY deep decay (vy≈−1.5) the reprice fires on essentially every airborne hit and every stamp floors to 0 → all σ=1 (full), no flap; the flap only lives in the transitional band where the ledger vy hovers near the kohi threshold (~−0.8..−1.0), which cadence-vs-decay phase tips across — making it even more intermittent. (2) On the solve branch σ clamps to 0.93 (weak) only when the natural knock overshoots target; in a fast close-in chase σ* can instead clamp to MAX (1.35, extra KB), the opposite of weak. So the weak-producing subset is real but a fraction of servo hits.

Weak side = branch (b): σ=0.93 shaves the FRESH era horizontal (kohi sprint ≈0.35+0.425=0.775 b/t aligned) by 7% ≈ 0.054 b/t, and it lands on exactly the zero-lift (stamp≈0) hits, compounding a flat trajectory with a 7% horizontal trim. As landing separation the shave is ~0.30 blocks over the window; as a fraction of total shipped horizontal (residual+fresh) it is ~4-6%. Branch (a) produces σ=1 = FULL knockback (not weak).

Not refuted: it plausibly produces the "some sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should" + "very subtle, hard to reproduce, more a feeling" phenomenology, which is a strong qualitative match. It does NOT match "little to no knockback" on its own (7% is not near-zero) and cannot match "as far back as I can remember" (combo-hold is a recent 2.4.x opt-in feature). It is a refinement/contributor to round-1's ledger-vy zero-lift family for servo-enabled configs, not a root cause.

era_call = config-dependent: the manifestation strictly requires modules.combo-hold: true (default OFF). Within that opt-in feature there is a genuine discontinuity artifact (the airTime<3 decline guard flapping, fed by the documented ledger-vy over-decay bug), but with the module off it is byte-identical no-op, so config-dependent is the honest classification.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB variance of up to 7% of the fresh era horizontal on the weak (solve→0.93) branch: kohi sprint fresh ≈0.775 b/t → ~0.054 b/t shave (~0.30 blocks of landing separation, ~4-6% of total shipped horizontal incl. residual). The flap is 0.93↔1.0 between consecutive hits, click-phase-synchronized. No angle/vertical loss added by this finding itself (the zero-lift is round-1's ledger-vy issue; this only compounds the 7% horizontal trim onto those flat hits). Frequency: LOW/config-gated — requires modules.combo-hold=true (default OFF) AND a sustained juggle with no clean landing between hits (open-arena is faithful per the divergence doc) AND the ledger vy sitting in the narrow transitional band near the preset's stamp-zero threshold, at pocket range (~2.85 blocks / close). In real PvP on a servo-enabled server this is occasional-in-corners, negligible in open field; on default (module-off) configs it is impossible. Matches the report's 'subtle/feeling/some sprint hits weaker' phenomenology strongly, its 'little to no knockback' magnitude weakly, and its 'as far back as I can remember' span not at all (servo is a recent feature).

### `reach-handicap-knock-semantics-target-fold-only` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: chase-midrange)

**Mechanism:** Q3 resolution — exact distance semantics of ComboReachHandicap + ReachClamp, and the one place they alter a hit's KNOCK. ReachClamp itself only gates hit ADMISSION, and only on the ATTACKER'S OWN swings while a combo is held AGAINST THEM (the juggled victim answering back), only when reach-validation is enabled (default OFF): plain shape eye-to-box ≤ maxReach+leniency (3.4); handicap shape accepts on eye-to-CENTRE ≤ scale×3.4 = 2.958 OR eye-to-box ≤ scale×3.0 = 2.61 — no knock magnitude is ever touched, and a mid-range chase ATTACKER holding the combo is never handicapped. The ONLY knock-magnitude effect in the pair is the servo-target fold: effectiveVictimReach multiplies the servo config's victimReach by handicap.scale (3.0 → 2.61 at 0.87) whenever COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP is enabled AND the server is 1.20.5+, which lowers sepDeny and drops the boundary target from ~3.09–3.15 to ~2.82 at chase arc heights — pushing plain-hit sigma* down ~0.2 (simulation: 0.85 → deeper into the 0.93 pin) and keeping sprint hits pinned. One composition gap: the fold keys on server-side lever support only, never on whether the VICTIM'S client honors the synced attribute — a ViaVersion legacy client ignores it (documented in ComboReachHandicap's own javadoc), so for such victims the servo steers to a denial boundary that is not actually enforced (the victim can answer at the steered separation) while their knocks are shaved as if it were.

**Trigger:** modules.combo-hold + modules.combo-reach-handicap both true on 1.20.5+ (both default false): mid-combo targets drop ~0.27–0.3 blocks → more 0.93 pinning on plain hits; the Via-legacy-victim mismatch needs such a client in the combo.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/ReachClamp.java:105-150 (admission-only, both shapes); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:557-615 (handicap scale applies only when a combo is held AGAINST the attacker; reach-validation default off per settings), :204-212 + core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:643-651 (effectiveVictimReach fold, lever-supported gate only); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:582-646 (sepDeny/boundaryTarget); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/combo/ComboReachHandicap.java:38-41 ('ViaVersion legacy clients ignore the synced attribute'); simulation row H1 (vreach 2.61 → target 2.818, sigma* 0.846).

**Maps to the report:** Weak match: answers the assigned question — there is NO hidden mid-range band where the handicap/clamp pair reduces knock magnitude; the servo-target fold is the only knock-touching semantic and is bounded by the 0.93 clamp. Extends round-1 no-close-range-distance-reducer to the mid-range band with the Via-legacy composition caveat.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: I tried to refute the finding and could not — every load-bearing code claim checks out:

1. ReachClamp touches only hit ADMISSION. `grep` confirms `ReachClamp.passes(...)` is called from exactly one site, `HitRegistrationUnit.passesReach` (line 588). It returns a boolean and no caller uses it to scale a velocity. So ReachClamp never touches knock magnitude — confirmed.

2. The reach-validation gate defaults OFF: `HitRegSettings.ReachValidation.DEFAULTS = new ReachValidation(false, 3.0, 0.4, 100, 500)` (first field `enabled=false`), and `passesReach` early-returns `true` when `!reach.enabled()`. Confirmed default-off.

3. The handicap admission branch (`handicapScale != null`) only fires on the ATTACKER'S OWN swing when a combo is held against them: `comboReachHandicapScale(attackerView)` returns null unless `attackerView.comboAttackerId() != null` AND `COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP` enabled AND `ComboReachHandicap.leverSupported()`. Confirmed. Shapes: centre threshold `scale*(maxReach+leniency)`, box floor `scale*maxReach` — matches finding's 2.958 / 2.61 at scale 0.87.

4. The ONLY knock-magnitude effect is the servo-target fold: `effectiveVictimReach(settings)` (HitRegistrationUnit:204-212 and KnockbackUnit:643-651) multiplies `settings.victimReach()` by `handicap.scale()` only when `COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP` enabled AND `leverSupported()`. It feeds ONLY `settings.servo(...)` via `comboServoFor`, which is INACTIVE unless `COMBO_HOLD` is enabled AND the attacker holds the combo. So the fold matters only when BOTH modules are on. Confirmed.

5. The effect is bounded: `ComboSettings.DEFAULTS` has `minFactor 0.93, maxFactor 1.35` — the servo sigma is clamped to [0.93, 1.35], so the folded target can shave at most ~7% off the fresh horizontal knock. The lowered `sepDeny`/`boundaryTarget` (PocketServo:582-646) drops the target, pushing sigma* toward the 0.93 pin — matches the finding's simulation (target ~2.82, sigma* ~0.85 clamped to 0.93). Confirmed bounded.

6. Both modules default OFF: `Feature.COMBO_HOLD` and `Feature.COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP` both pass `false` (default-enabled flag) in Feature.java:284/295. Confirmed.

7. The Via-legacy composition gap is real: `ComboReachHandicap.leverSupported()` checks ONLY `Attributes.entityInteractionRange() != null && AttributeModifiers.supported()` — both server-side class-load probes, never the victim's client version. The class javadoc (and the enable() warning) explicitly note "ViaVersion legacy clients ignore the synced attribute." So on a 1.20.5+ server, the servo folds the target down (shaving the victim's knock toward the 0.93 pin) while a Via-legacy victim can still answer at the steered separation — the denial premise fails but the knock is still shaved. Confirmed real, but bounded to the same ~7% and needs such a client mid-combo.

I could not find any hidden mid-range distance-reducer in the handicap/clamp pair beyond this bounded, config-gated servo fold. The finding's negative claim holds.

Minor refinement worth noting: the mechanism sentence phrases the fold as applying "whenever COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP is enabled AND the server is 1.20.5+," but the fold is inert unless COMBO_HOLD is ALSO enabled (the servo it feeds is INACTIVE otherwise). The finding's trigger already states both must be true, so this is a phrasing tightening, not a correction of substance.
- Corrections: The finding is accurate and survives adversarial verification. Every code claim was confirmed: ReachClamp is admission-only (single call site in passesReach, never scales velocity); reach-validation defaults OFF (ReachValidation.DEFAULTS enabled=false); the handicap admission branch fires only on the combo-victim's own answer swing; the servo-target fold in effectiveVictimReach is the sole knock-magnitude path and feeds only comboServoFor, which is INACTIVE unless COMBO_HOLD is enabled and the attacker holds the combo; the sigma effect is clamped to [0.93, 1.35] (ComboSettings minFactor 0.93 → at most ~7% horizontal shave); both COMBO_HOLD and COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP default OFF; and the Via-legacy gap is real (leverSupported() is a server-side-only probe, documented in ComboReachHandicap's javadoc). One phrasing tightening: the servo fold is inert unless COMBO_HOLD is ALSO enabled (the finding's trigger already states both modules must be true, so this is not a substantive correction). Classification config-dependent is correct — this is intended combo-solver behavior, gated behind two opt-in modules on 1.20.5+, not a default-config weak-KB bug and thus an unlikely explanation for the owner's "since forever, default-feel" complaint.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss: bounded at ~7% on the folded plain hits (servo sigma floored at 0.93; the ~0.27–0.3-block target drop pushes sigma* from ~0.85 into the 0.93 pin). No angle/vertical effect (R_a never handicapped, vertical never scaled). Frequency in real PvP: effectively zero in default config — requires BOTH combo-hold AND combo-reach-handicap enabled on a 1.20.5+ server, and only during an actively held combo; the Via-legacy sub-caveat further needs a ViaVersion legacy client in that combo. On opted-in servers it recurs every combo but stays capped at ~7%. Not a plausible driver of the owner's default-feel, cross-version, close-range weak-KB complaint.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Hand-computation confirms the finding's resolution. Verified: servo sigma clamped to [0.93, 1.35] (ComboSettings.DEFAULTS minFactor 0.93), gain 1.0; the handicap fold multiplies servo victimReach 3.0->2.61 at scale 0.87 (KnockbackUnit.java:643-651 == HitRegistrationUnit.java:204-212), gated on COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP enabled AND leverSupported() (1.20.5+). ReachClamp.passes (105-150) is admission-only for both shapes (no knock magnitude), only reached when reach-validation is enabled (default OFF) and a combo is held AGAINST the attacker. So the sole knock-magnitude path is the servo-target fold; its sign is toward weaker knock (lower victimReach -> lower sepDeny -> lower boundaryTarget -> lower sigma*).

Reproduction: attacker A holds a combo (minHits=2) against victim V on 1.20.5+ with BOTH modules.combo-hold and modules.combo-reach-handicap = true (both default FALSE). At a chase arc height victimReach 3.0 folds to 2.61, dropping boundaryTarget ~3.09 -> ~2.82, pushing plain-hit sigma* ~0.85 -> ~0.846, which clamps to 0.93. Delivered plain-hit fresh horizontal knock (era base ~0.4) scaled by 0.93 = 0.372 b/t, i.e. ~0.028 b/t (~7%) weaker, ~0.2-0.3 blocks less total pushback. Sprint fresh (~0.85) sigma* stays above the clamp so sprint hits are untouched.

Crucially the fold's MARGINAL effect over COMBO_HOLD-alone is often ZERO: whenever un-handicapped sigma* already sits <=0.93 (most chase geometry), both clamp to the same 0.93 floor -> identical delivered knock. Nonzero only in the narrow band where un-handicapped sigma* in (0.93, ~1.0) drops below 0.93. This pathway can never reach the report's headline magnitude ('victim just doesnt really move back', 'feels like non-sprint') which needs a ~40%+ deficit; the 0.93 clamp caps it at 7%, only on plain non-sprint answering hits during an established combo, only with two opt-in modules on. It does not match the owner's emphasized close-range FIRST-hit scenario (the servo needs a held combo). The Via-legacy gap (ComboReachHandicap.java:38-41 — legacy clients ignore the synced ENTITY_INTERACTION_RANGE) is real: the servo steers to a deny boundary the Via victim can actually answer from while the attacker's fresh knock is shaved via the folded 2.61 — but that shave is still capped at the same 0.93 floor.

Not fully refuted because the servo-target fold is a genuine knock-touching semantic that, when configured, subtly shaves plain combo hits (matches the 'subtle feeling' descriptor for the mid-combo case). But it is a config-gated, bounded, non-primary contributor that cannot be the reported bug's cause — consistent with the finding's own 'weak match' verdict.
- Corrections: The finding is accurate as a resolution: within the ComboReachHandicap + ReachClamp pair there is NO hidden mid-range distance-reducer — ReachClamp is admission-only (both shapes, only when reach-validation is enabled/default OFF, only on the attacker's own swings while a combo is held against them), and the sole knock-magnitude path is the servo-target fold (effectiveVictimReach: victimReach 3.0 x 0.87 = 2.61 when COMBO_REACH_HANDICAP is on and the server is 1.20.5+). That fold lowers sepDeny/boundaryTarget and drives plain-hit sigma* deeper into the 0.93 clamp, shaving delivered plain-hit horizontal knock by AT MOST 7% (sigma floor 0.93 x fresh ~0.4 -> ~0.372 b/t), only during an established combo, only on non-sprint answering hits, only with both opt-in modules enabled (both default false). Its marginal delta over COMBO_HOLD-alone is frequently zero because the un-handicapped sigma* already pins at 0.93 in most chase geometry. This cannot be the primary cause of the owner's report: off by default, combo-gated (never the close-range first hit), bounded to 7% (never 'little to no knockback' or a 'non-sprint feel'), sprint-hit-neutral. The Via-legacy caveat is real but equally capped by the 0.93 floor. Net: a genuine but minor, config-dependent, mid-combo-only contributor to the 'subtle feeling' — not the mechanism behind the reported weak-knockback bug.
- Severity: Horizontal-KB loss bounded by the 0.93 servo floor = at most 7% of the fresh horizontal component (~0.028 b/t on a non-sprint ~0.4 fresh knock, ~0.2-0.3 blocks less total pushback), applied ONLY to plain non-sprint answering hits during a held combo; sprint hits stay above the clamp and are untouched. The handicap fold's MARGINAL loss over COMBO_HOLD-alone is 0 in most chase geometry (both clamp to 0.93), nonzero only in the narrow band where un-handicapped sigma* in (0.93, ~1.0). Expected real-PvP frequency in DEFAULT config: zero (both modules default false, requires 1.20.5+). With both modules deliberately on: occasional, mid-combo only, never a first/close-range hit, never sprint — cannot produce 'little to no knockback' or a 'non-sprint feel' (needs ~40%+ deficit; this caps at 7%).

### `attacker-motion-enters-victim-knock-only-via-servo-channels` — unknown, confidence high (finder: chase-midrange)

**Mechanism:** Q5 negative result. Complete inventory of attacker-MOTION reads feeding a victim's knock: (1) PaceScale — the walk-normalized MOVEMENT_SPEED attribute only, never measured velocity, signature-preset only (round-1 covered). (2) The servo's chase channels, all combo-hold-gated: the measured post-hit window EMA (attacker ring displacement over the inter-hit gap), the heading alignment (attacker ring net displacement over 4 ticks), and ResetModelWire (attacker ENTITY_ACTION packets). Nothing else — the engine's attacker terms are position, yaw, sprint flag, enchant level. A chasing attacker who gets counter-hit carries their received knock in their RING, not into the victim's formula: the alignment reads their knock-dominated heading as ≤0 → clamped to cos45° (round-1's trade-clamp), and a counter-knock spanning a measured window can drive windowChaseRate near zero or negative → the chase EMA sinks and persists ~3 windows (α 0.3) — but the alignment-scaled 0.70 floor re-prices every such hit at ≥0.49×sprint, and the [0.93, 1.35] clamps bound the shipped effect to ±7/35% of the fresh component on interior hits. The era attack() ×0.6 bites only the ATTACKER'S own ledger (their next RECEIVED knock) and never enters the victim's compute. At shipped defaults (combo-hold off) no attacker-motion signal exists in the victim's knock at all.

**Trigger:** N/A — verification result bounding the axis: with combo-hold off, mid-range weak sprint hits cannot originate from any attacker-momentum interplay; with it on, every such interplay is floor/clamp-bounded.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:212-231 + :299-351 (attacker terms: x/z, yaw, sprinting, enchant, moveSpeedAttr only); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/combo/ComboPredictor.java:166, :187-198, :237-243 (the three chase-channel reads); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/PocketServo.java:535-541 (floor bounds a sunk EMA), :679-684 (chase EMA α 0.3 persistence), :755-760 (cos45 clamp); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:418-424 (×0.6 is attacker-ledger-only).

**Maps to the report:** Load-bearing negative for the synthesizer: the mid-range 'sprint hits sometimes weaker' report cannot be an attacker-momentum artifact on default configs, and on servo-enabled configs every attacker-motion pathway is bounded — pointing residual unexplained weakness at the sprint-verdict and delivery pathways round 1 owns.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Verified every cited claim against source. (1) Engine attacker reads are exactly position/yaw/sprint-flag/enchant-level/moveSpeedAttr — EntityState carries attacker vx/vy/vz but the formula never consumes them; residualCarry reads victim.vx()/vz() (KnockbackEngine:341-343), not attacker motion. (2) COMBO_HOLD.defaultEnabled=false (Feature.java:284) and comboServoFor gates on snapshot.enabled(COMBO_HOLD) returning PocketServoConfig.INACTIVE otherwise (KnockbackUnit:620-630), so at shipped defaults combo=1.0 (KnockbackEngine:206-209) and PredictorInputs is not even built with the chase channels (KnockbackUnit:287) — no attacker-motion signal enters the victim's knock at all. (3) With servo ON, default min/max=0.93/1.35 (ComboSettings:61) bounds the σ-scaled fresh horizontal to at most a 7% reduction; σ multiplies only fresh horizontal via freshFactor (KnockbackEngine:210,221-223), flat vertical never. (4) The era ×0.6 is attackerSession.ledger().scaleHorizontal(0.6) (KnockbackUnit:423) — the attacker's OWN ledger (their next received knock), never the current victim's compute. (5) The alignment-scaled 0.70 floor and cos45 clamp exist as cited (PocketServo:535-541, :93, :107). PaceScale is attribute-based (moveSpeedAttr, not measured velocity) and returns exactly 1.0 when inactive (PaceScale.factor). I could not find any additional attacker-motion pathway into the victim's knock, nor any way for the servo to weaken beyond the σ-min. The finding's bounding negative holds. One minor over-precision: the finding calls PaceScale 'signature-preset only' — that is a config/preset detail (pace is applied unconditionally whenever paceScaling.active(), and returns 1.0 otherwise), but since it reads an attribute not velocity and yields ~1.0 at base speed, it is not a weak-KB source and the inventory correctly captures it; this does not affect the finding's conclusion.
- Corrections: Finding stands as written. Two clarifications that tighten (not overturn) it: (a) PaceScale is applied on ANY preset whose paceScaling.active() is true, not strictly 'signature-only' — but it reads the walk-normalized MOVEMENT_SPEED attribute (never measured velocity) and returns exactly 1.0 both when inactive and at base speed, so it is not an attacker-MOTION weak-KB source regardless of preset; the inventory's intent is correct. (b) The [0.93,1.35] bound means the servo's maximum WEAKENING is 7% of the fresh horizontal (σ_min=0.93), confirming the axis cannot produce 'little to no knockback' even when combo-hold is on. Core negative — 'at shipped defaults no attacker-motion signal exists in the victim's knock, and with the servo on every attacker-motion pathway is floor/clamp-bounded' — is fully confirmed against KnockbackEngine, KnockbackUnit, ComboPredictor, PocketServo, ComboSettings, and Feature.
- Severity: As a bug source: none. At shipped defaults (COMBO_HOLD off) the attacker-momentum axis contributes exactly 0 horizontal-KB loss to a victim's knock — no attacker-velocity term exists in the compute at any range. With COMBO_HOLD enabled, the servo can weaken the fresh horizontal by at most 7% (σ min 0.93) on interior hits, and every chase channel is alignment-floored (≥0.49×sprint) — far too bounded to read as 'little to no knockback.' Expected real-PvP frequency of this axis producing the reported weakness: effectively nil; it rules the axis out rather than explaining the report.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: This is a NEGATIVE (bounding) finding, and every structural claim it makes is verified against source. (1) The victim's knock formula reads only attacker position, yaw, sprint flag, enchant level, and walk-normalized move-speed attribute (KnockbackEngine.java:212-231, servoFactor :309-337) — no attacker velocity/RING term exists in compute. (2) The era attack() ×0.6 is applied to the ATTACKER's OWN session ledger (KnockbackUnit.java:423 `attackerSession.ledger().scaleHorizontal(0.6)`), shaping the attacker's next RECEIVED knock, and never the victim's compute — confirmed. (3) The only pathway by which any attacker MOTION (ring displacement) reaches the victim's knock is the pocket servo's three chase channels (window-chase EMA ComboPredictor:193-197, heading alignment :166, dynamic/reset chase :237-243), and all are gated behind servo.active() (KnockbackEngine:206-209), i.e. modules.combo-hold, default false (config.yml:273). At default config combo==1.0 and there is literally no attacker-motion signal in the victim's knock. (4) When combo-hold IS on, σ is hard-clamped to [0.93,1.35] (PocketServo:342; ComboSettings.DEFAULTS min 0.93/max 1.35) and multiplies ONLY the fresh horizontal (base push + sprint/enchant extras), never the residual, never the vertical (KnockbackEngine:210,221-222). The alignment factor (clamped [cos45≈0.707, 1.0], PocketServo:755-760) and the 0.70 straight-line chase floor scaled by it, plus the α=0.3 chase-EMA persistence (:680-683), all feed the σ* solve, but the terminal [0.93,1.35] clamp is the hard bound: even a counter-knocked chaser whose alignment reads ≤0 and whose window-chase EMA sinks negative cannot drive shipped σ below 0.93. So the entire attacker-motion axis is bounded to a 7% fresh-horizontal shave at worst, and only on the opt-in servo. Concrete worst case (combo-hold on, legacy-1.7, dead-ahead mid-combo sprint): fresh = push 0.4 + extra 0.5 = 0.9h at σ=1; a full-sprint stamp overshoots the pocket so σ* solves ~0.7, floored to 0.93, ships 0.837h — a ~0.063h (7%) loss, sub-perceptual, never 'little to no KB'. The finding therefore stands as a valid, verified negative: it correctly bounds this axis and correctly points the real weak-KB symptom at the sprint-verdict and delivery pathways round-1 owns. It is not refuted — its claim is that this axis is NOT a meaningful source, and that claim is confirmed. The one caveat: it matches the very mildest fringe of 'sprint hits sometimes weaker' (the 7% floor shave, already covered by round-1's pocket-servo-min-clamp finding) but only on non-default configs, and it cannot explain the owner's historical 'as far back as I can remember' report because the servo is a 2.5.0-era opt-in.
- Severity: Default config (combo-hold OFF): exactly 0 horizontal-KB loss — no attacker-motion term exists in the victim's knock formula; frequency 0. Combo-hold ON (opt-in, non-default): worst-case σ floor 0.93 → 7% shave of the FRESH horizontal only (residual + vertical untouched). E.g. legacy-1.7 dead-ahead mid-combo sprint 0.9h → 0.837h (loss ~0.063h); sub-perceptual (~fraction of a pixel of settle distance). Frequency on a servo-enabled server: most mid-combo full-sprint stamps ride the 0.93 floor, but the magnitude is below the 'feeling' threshold and cannot produce 'little to no knockback'. Angular contribution: none — the servo scales magnitude along the existing away-axis, it does not rotate the knock.

# Standalone lens re-runs (round-2 missing verdicts)

## `combo-residual-ground-transition-lag-ping-proportional` — CODE lens: REFUTED as divergence, reclassified `era-real`

**Reasoning:** The code mechanism is real (Deliveries.java:41-44 stamps grounded/slip from the published view; MotionLedger decays each segment at one fixed branch; the branch flips only via GroundFsm packet events; no RTT rewind exists for the horizontal residual). But the era-divergence conclusion is refuted by the repo's own decompile-cited ground truth: compendium §1.6 (decomp-1.7.10/sv.java:905 + nh.java:185, both eras) shows onGround and the jump stamp were MOVEMENT-HANDLER packet-flag adoptions — era servers kept grounded friction until the victim's liftoff packet arrived, the same RTT-proportional lag. Mental replicates era, including the ping proportionality (adding at most ~1 tick of inbox-drain quantization).

**Corrected severity:** the factor hits the RESIDUAL, not the shipped knock — next hit = residual×0.5 + base, so at 100ms a 0.9-stamp gap-10 chain ships ~0.923 vs 0.963 ideal (~4% per hit; the residual contributes only ~6.5% at max cadence on stone). Near-nil on ice. Preset list should include lunar alongside legacy-1.7/kohi/minehq/badlion. Zero era-relative loss — real 1.7.10 behaved the same. A ring-fed clamp would be a feel improvement BEYOND era, not an era fix.

## `chase-pocket-sprint-hits-pin-min-clamp-everywhere` — SYMPTOM lens: STANDS, `config-dependent`

**Reasoning (hand-verified):** ComboSettings.DEFAULTS confirmed (min 0.93/max 1.35/gain 1.0/target 2.85/window 10/BOUNDARY). For a sprint-fresh hit (freshEra 0.9) on flat stone: drag schedule ΣΠ ≈ 4.47 (launch-tick ×0.546 then ×0.91 over ~10 air ticks; ~4.6 full-settle), constant = d0(~3.0) − chase(~1.96) + drift(~0.2) ≈ 1.24 → σ* ≈ 0.18, far below the 0.93 clamp — pinned, robust across slope/residual assumptions (even slope 3.3 → σ* ≈ 0.24). Settle difference ≈ 0.29 blocks less separation per hit vs era σ=1.

**Corrections:** (1) Δsettle ≈ 0.28–0.30 blocks, not 0.3–0.4. (2) Pinned at 0.93 means the servo UNDER-shrinks: the victim lands PAST the 2.85 pocket yet still ~0.3 blocks SHORT of full era — vs era it reads as weak AND the servo misses its own target on sprint hits (the 2.4.6 'σ* near 1.0–1.1' calibration was at freshEra 0.40; sprint-fresh was never covered). (3) Cannot produce 'little to no knockback' (bounded ~7% of fresh / ~10% of a ~2.9-block landing) — matches 'less than it should', not 'none'. (4) Deterministic on every hit-3+ chase sprint hit when combo-hold is ON; below clean conscious isolation → felt as 'sometimes weak, can't pin it'.
