# Round 3 — re-verification + critic-gap investigation

Re-runs of the lens-failed/capped round-1 items, plus the three critic-named gaps
(config resolution, mutual-trade self-perturbation, CADENCE spoof coupling). Verify lenses on Opus.

## Re-verification verdicts

### `modern-client-no-reengage-after-clear` — CODE lens: STANDS, era call `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Mechanism CONFIRMED in code, so I cannot cleanly refute the core: base sprint KB reads the wire flag (KnockbackEngine:214 `attacker.sprinting()`), the wire is captured at registration via verdictAt (HitRegistrationUnit:530, wtapConsultWire default true, WTAP_REGISTRATION default ON), and onServerClear unconditionally clears wire sprinting/armed on every accepted bonus melee hit for a connected attacker (KnockbackUnit:432-434). The only prompt re-arm is a client START_SPRINTING (PacketTap:104) or the sword-block reset — plain held-sprint has neither. So on a client that holds sprint without re-emitting START, hit 2 reads non-sprint. This produces reduced KB, matching the report. BUT the finding overstates two things: (1) 'reconcile cannot rescue' is wrong — a non-sprint follow-up hit skips onServerClear (bonus=false, KnockbackUnit:419), so lastWrite is not refreshed, the 3-tick quiet window elapses, and reconcile (PacketTap:85 -> SprintWire:167-174) restores the base sprinting flag from view.sprinting() as soon as the server flag reads true again (which it does on a still-sprinting modern client); only armed/freshness (the wtap-extra term, gated on profile.wtapExtra().enabled()) stays lost. So the effect is a recurring ~3-tick gap after each bonus hit, not a persistent RTT-long dropout. (2) The era framing hinges on an unverified client-version fact (1.21.2+ removing attack sprint interruption) and is in tension with the project's own w-tap-centric model. It also does not explain the owner's explicit w-tap/blockhit complaint: a w-tap emits START (re-arms, guarded by SprintWire:103) and blockhitting is reconstructed by SwordBlockingUnit. Net: real, modern-client-specific, but milder and narrower than stated.
- Corrections: Core mechanism holds and is verifiable in code: the base sprint KB bonus keys on the WIRE sprinting flag (KnockbackEngine.java:214 via HitRegistrationUnit.java:530), and onServerClear (KnockbackUnit.java:433) unconditionally clears that wire flag on every accepted bonus melee hit for a connected attacker. The only prompt re-arm is a client START_SPRINTING packet (PacketTap.java:104) or the SwordBlockingUnit reset; a client that holds sprint continuously without re-emitting START gets non-sprint KB on the hits following each bonus hit. This is a genuine, modern-client-specific reduction and a plausible contributor to the owner's 'some hits have non-sprinting knockback' feel.

CORRECTIONS to the finding: (1) 'The reconcile cannot rescue' is inaccurate. A non-sprint follow-up hit takes the bonus=false early return (KnockbackUnit.java:419) and therefore does NOT call onServerClear, so lastWrite is not refreshed; the 3-tick quiet window then elapses and reconcile (PacketTap.java:85 -> SprintWire.java:167-174) restores the base sprinting flag from player.isSprinting() as soon as the server flag reads true again — which it does for a client that is still sprinting server-side. Only armed/freshness (the wtap-extra pair, and only when profile.wtapExtra().enabled()) is not restored by reconcile. So the observable effect is a recurring gap of up to ~3 ticks after each bonus hit, not a persistent >=1 RTT dropout emitting nothing. (2) The era classification depends on an unverified client-version fact (1.21.2+ dropping the attack sprint interruption) and sits in tension with the project's own model where w-tap (STOP+START) is THE re-arm mechanism and held-sprint reduced KB is arguably era-authentic. (3) It does not explain the owner's explicit w-tap and blockhit complaints: a w-tap emits START and re-arms (guarded by SprintWire.java:103), and blockhitting is reconstructed by SwordBlockingUnit — both outside this finding's held-sprint-only scenario. Confidence should be lowered from medium and scope narrowed to continuous-hold, non-w-tapping attackers on clients that suppress the around-hit START.
- Severity: low-medium

### `presend-marked-before-ship-outcome-discarded-valve-eats-only-copy` — CODE lens: STANDS, era call `bug`

- Reasoning: Verified full chain. HitRegistrationUnit.plan() commits tx.preSent(shipped) at :409 before senders.ship() at :427 and discards ship()'s Outcome (grep: no Outcome ref in the unit); submitFromWire (:431) proceeds on PRE_SENT regardless of ship success. BurstSender.ship() (:63-82) catches all Throwables and null-user, returning UNSENDABLE having sent nothing; its javadoc (:22-23) requires the caller to pin, not account wire-delivered — honored only for the plan-time null check (:324-325), not a ship-time throw or user-null race between :325 and :427. On failure the phantom PRE_SENT tx resolves via DeliveryDesk.resolve (:186-194): apiVelocity==formula normally (DeskRouter builds the API event from formula) so unmodified=true, giving SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE. DirectiveExecutor (:27-29) sets event velocity to carried AND arms the valve; ValveListener (:56-57) cancels the byte-identical authoritative ENTITY_VELOCITY. Net: zero velocity packets, damage+flinch land, journaled healthy wireCarried=true. Defaults confirm path ON (hit-registration.yml fast-path.enabled=true, pre-send-feedback=true). No rescue: the 2.4.6 connected-victim sweep HOLDS the pending for the late velocity event, which the valve then eats. Could not refute the code defect. Caveats: yields a TOTAL zero-KB hit (matches 'doesn't really move back') but not the report's magnitude-reduction/non-sprint/close-range specifics; normal triggers are rare; the ViaVersion every-hit amplifier is plausible but unconfirmed from code.</parameter>
<parameter name="corrected">Real, default-enabled code defect. tx is PRE_SENT before the burst ships (HitRegistrationUnit:404-413), ship()'s UNSENDABLE Outcome is discarded (:427; no Outcome ref in unit), submitFromWire proceeds (:430-431). BurstSender's contract (pin on UNSENDABLE, javadoc :22-23) is honored only for the plan-time null-user check, not a runtime throw or the getUser() null-race at :427. resolve gives SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE (DeliveryDesk:186-194) which arms the valve (DirectiveExecutor:27-29) that cancels the byte-identical authoritative ENTITY_VELOCITY (ValveListener:56-57): a failed pre-send leaves the client with ZERO velocity packets while damage/flinch land, journaled as a healthy SHIP. The 2.4.6 connected-sweep does NOT rescue it (it holds the pending FOR that late event, whose resolution eats the copy). Refinements: (1) this is a TOTAL zero-KB hit — matches 'victim doesn't really move back' but does NOT explain the report's magnitude-reduction, non-sprint-looking, or close-range specifics (separate cause). (2) Normal-play triggers (1.20.2+ reconfigure during combat, transient encode throw, plan-to-ship user disappearance) are rare-per-hit — fits 'subtle/hard to reproduce' but unlikely the dominant driver. (3) The ViaVersion 'every hit on old clients' amplifier (BurstSender picks wrappers by SERVER version :42-44) is plausible but unproven — hinges on the PacketEvents-ViaVersion encode handoff, which normally succeeds. Fix: capture ship()'s Outcome and on UNSENDABLE pin instead of preSent, so no valve arms and the authoritative velocity survives.</parameter>
</invoke>
- Severity: medium

### `client-side-felt-kb-reduction-era-real` — SYM lens: STANDS, era call `era-real`

- Reasoning: Mechanism reproduces the report cleanly and strongly. Verified constants against the tree: LEGACY_18 base (0.4,0.4) + sprint extra (0.5,0.1) → non-sprint hit ships ~0.4 b/t horizontal, full sprint hit ~0.9 b/t; that 2.25x gap is the "sprint vs non-sprint" the owner describes. The era client contract (era-accuracy SKILL:57-66; compendium §0.6^clicks) is authentic and untouchable: an on-target sprint/KB-enchant click makes the clicking player's OWN client run motionX/Z*=0.6 + setSprinting(false) via local prediction. A victim who counter-clicks during their own flight cuts received velocity 0.6 per click: 0.9→0.54 (1), →0.324 (2), →0.194 (3). Two counter-clicks drop the full sprint knock (0.9) to 0.29 — BELOW the non-sprint 0.4 — i.e. "the knockback seems like the non-sprinting knockback," the exact wording. Held-W sprint air accel (0.026/tick, drag 0.91) reclaims further displacement, strongest on short face-hug flights = close range, where the owner says it's worst. Frequency: in mutual close trades at 8-12 CPS both players click through each other's flights, so the x0.6 fires nearly every trade — yet DeliveryDesk journals the correct full 0.9 stamp, so logs read "full KB delivered." Sub-tick click/packet interleaving makes it non-deterministic, invisible in logs, purely a feeling. Perfect fit to "very subtle, hard to reproduce, more a feeling." Config nuance: on unspoofed 1.9+ clients the self-x0.6 needs attack charge>0.9, so spam counter-clicks rarely fire it — but if CADENCE cooldown-removal spoofs attack_speed to keep the meter full, the era 0.6^clicks returns at full strength. Cannot refute: the mechanism plausibly produces the core of the report.
- Severity: Low as a Mental defect (server + journal ship the correct full stamp; the loss is an authentic, untouchable client-side era contract — "fixing" it = CPS-anti-reduce normalization, an explicit anti-feature). High as an EXPLANATION: it is the single strongest authentic account of the owner's exact "close-range feels like non-sprint KB" symptom.

### `stale-position-ring-direction-at-close-range` — SYM lens: STANDS, era call `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Verified against KnockbackEngine.base() (kernel:462-516) and LEGACY_18 preset. The finding's mechanism (pre-send reads PositionRing.latest() for both parties, HitRegistrationUnit:451-484; ring written once/tick, SessionService:349) is REAL, but its magnitude claim is wrong. The base push is NORMALIZED: pushX=(deltaX/magnitude)*0.4, so its magnitude is ALWAYS profile.base().horizontal() irrespective of separation — stale positions rotate the direction, they cannot collapse it to "near-zero." The horizontal cap (limits 0.4) bites only the already-0.4 base, a no-op. Hand-computed worst realistic face-hug strafe (live sep 0.6, victim strafe 0.25 b/t, ~1.3-tick stale ≈0.32 perpendicular): base rotates ~33°, magnitude preserved 0.4; total sprint knock (−0.217,0.836) mag 0.864 vs true 0.9 = ~4% loss plus a sideways skew. Typical 1-block strafe: ~14° rotation, mag 0.894 vs 0.9, <1%. Two hard immunities: (1) normalization preserves base magnitude, so no hit ever LOSES horizontal magnitude — it only skews sideways; (2) the sprint/wtap/enchant extra (the 0.5 that makes a sprint hit strong) is computed from attacker YAW (lastYaw), entirely position-independent, so this mechanism can NEVER make a sprint hit "feel like non-sprint." Full direction inversion (base opposing the yaw extra) needs the two player centers to cross within the staleness window — geometrically precluded, and pure radial closure along the sight-line doesn't rotate direction at all. So it fires on every close-range strafing hit (high frequency) but delivers only low-single-digit-% magnitude jitter + minor lateral skew: it CONTRIBUTES the "subtle, hard-to-reproduce, feeling-thing, worst-at-close-range" texture of the report, but does NOT produce the core "little to no knockback" or "feels like non-sprint" symptoms. Not refuted (it plausibly produces the subtle-variance part), but severity is low; the primary symptom belongs to the client-side x0.6/held-input era-real finding and the valve/registration bugs.
- Corrections: Stale PositionRing samples give the pre-send an up-to-~1-tick-old attacker/victim pair, so the base knock DIRECTION carries a small angular error that era (live positions at packet processing) never has. Because base() normalizes the push to a fixed 0.4 magnitude and the sprint/wtap extra rides YAW (not position), the effect is bounded to a few-percent reduction of the backward component plus a lateral skew — NOT a magnitude collapse and NOT a sprint→non-sprint downgrade. The finding's "base 0.4 push computes near-zero" is refuted by normalization; "oblique" is correct but geometrically small (perpendicular strafe only; radial closure doesn't rotate direction; inversion requires centers to cross, which is precluded). Real divergence from era, high frequency (every close moving hit), but low severity: it accounts only for the report's "subtle feeling/hard-to-reproduce, most noticeable at close range" hit-to-hit variance, not the primary weak/no-KB symptom.
- Severity: low

### `valve-arm-lifecycle-races` — CODE lens: STANDS, era call `bug`

- Reasoning: Tried hard to refute; could not. Verified every load-bearing link in the main tree + PE 2.12.1 source.

CLAIM (1) third-party stale arm — CONFIRMED code-valid. DeskRouter (DeskRouter.java:53) is @EventHandler HIGH with NO isCancelled check; a HIGHEST/MONITOR listener runs AFTER it. resolve() for an unmodified PRE_SENT returns SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE (DeliveryDesk.java:189-194): DirectiveExecutor.apply does sink.ship + valve.arm(victim,payload). If a downstream listener then cancels/modifies the event, vanilla emits no matching ENTITY_VELOCITY, so the arm is never consumed and persists until the next SessionService.tick clearStale (:348, unconditional, no age check). VelocityValve (core, not kernel as evidence says) keys ONLY (recipient,entityId,3 shorts) with no hit identity (VelocityValve.java:30-41) — stationary close trades produce byte-identical stamps. DECISIVE fact verified: the next hit's pre-send burst IS valve-visible — BurstSender uses user.writePacket (non-silent) → ProtocolManagerAbstract.writePacket → ChannelHelper.write → full outbound pipeline → PE encoder fires PacketSendEvent → ValveListener (HIGHEST, no origin check, ValveListener.java:42-58). So hit2's burst is consumed against hit1's dead arm (CAS clears it), then hit2 resolves SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE and its own tracker dup is eaten by its fresh arm → hit2 reaches client with ZERO velocity copies. In a rapid close exchange this cascades (hit1 lands via presend, hits2..n lost). Config-dependent: needs a plugin cancelling/modifying PlayerVelocityEvent at HIGHEST/MONITOR (anti-KB/anticheat/region-KB) — realistic and coexistable since Mental cannot block foreign listeners.

CLAIM (2) blocked-redelivery — CONFIRMED code-valid, and NOT gated on a foreign plugin (fires on ordinary shield/temp-shield/off-hand block-hitting, an always-on delivery path via freshBlockedKnock, KnockbackUnit.java:257/321). deliverBlockedKnock arms in the TASK phase (line 533) but its dup only emits at the end-of-tick tracker from the later setVelocity (:546), breaking the normal path's arm→dup same-thread adjacency. (A) session-tick clearStale can run between the arm and the tracker dup (damage-task vs session-task order within the tick is not guaranteed) → dup ships uncancelled = doubled/refreshed stamp. (B) in the !wirePreSent branch ship() (user.writePacket+flush) is issued from the owning thread; netty defers that write to the channel event loop, but arm() runs synchronously immediately after — so the arm is in place before the listener processes the burst → Mental's OWN burst is eaten (reliably, not just possibly) and the knock arrives only via the tracker dup ~1 tick late = mushy. Either way it's exactly one copy (consume-once), never a total loss for (2) — A=extra, B=late.

Refutation attempts that FAILED: no isCancelled guard on DeskRouter; writePacket (not Silently) confirmed pipeline-visible; clearStale has no age check; consume is the only other clear and it cascades correctly; the arm sites and line refs all match. Minor evidence defect only: the valve path is core/me.vexmc.mental.v5.VelocityValve, not the kernel path cited.

Matches the owner's report precisely: intermittent near-zero KB concentrated in close trades (1), and mushy/doubled block-hit KB (2), subtle and hard to reproduce (race + config gating).
- Corrections: Finding stands as two real, distinct valve-lifecycle races. Refinements after code verification:

(1) Third-party stale arm — the zero-KB path. Verified DECISIVE assumption in PacketEvents 2.12.1: BurstSender uses the NON-silent user.writePacket → ProtocolManagerAbstract.writePacket → ChannelHelper.write (full pipeline; only the *Silently variants use writeInContext(ENCODER_NAME) to bypass), so pre-send bursts genuinely fire PacketSendEvent and reach ValveListener. DeskRouter (HIGH) has no isCancelled guard, so a HIGHEST/MONITOR cancel or a HIGHEST modify (which makes vanilla's emit not match the arm) both strand the arm until the next unconditional clearStale (SessionService:348). Cascades across a run of quantized-identical close-range hits (hit1 lands via presend; hits2..n lose both their presend and their own tracker dup → zero copies). Strongest symptom-match but CONFIG-DEPENDENT: requires a plugin touching PlayerVelocityEvent at HIGHEST/MONITOR — confirm the server's plugin list before acting.

(2) Blocked-redelivery — always-on (no foreign plugin; any shield/temp-shield/off-hand block-hit). Real asymmetry: it arms in the task phase (KnockbackUnit:533) while the dup emits at the later tracker (setVelocity :546), unlike the normal path's arm→dup adjacency. (A) clearStale can wipe the arm before the tracker dup = doubled stamp — a genuine damage-task-vs-session-task ordering race. (B) in the !wirePreSent branch the owning-thread arm() runs before netty processes the just-issued writePacket, so it RELIABLY (not merely possibly) eats Mental's own burst → knock lands ~1 tick late (mushy). Consume-once bounds (2) to one copy — extra or late, never total loss.

Minor evidence defect: VelocityValve is core/me.vexmc.mental.v5.VelocityValve, not the kernel/rim path cited; line numbers otherwise correct.

Suggested fixes to consider: (i) give the valve arm a hit-identity or a bounded age so a stale arm cannot alias the next hit's presend, or make clearStale age-aware; (ii) in deliverBlockedKnock, arm AFTER (or from) the velocity-event resolution rather than in the task phase, restoring the arm→dup adjacency, and in the !wirePreSent branch arm on the netty thread after the burst (or use writePacketSilently for the burst) so the arm cannot eat its own presend.
- Severity: medium — directly matches the reported symptom (intermittent little/no KB in close trades, mushy blockhits). Sub-(1) yields genuine zero-KB hits but is gated on a third-party PlayerVelocityEvent-cancelling plugin; sub-(2) fires in ordinary block-hitting with no extra plugin but is only ±1-tick smear or a doubled stamp, never total loss.

### `valve-arm-lifecycle-races` — SYM lens: STANDS, era call `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Assuming the mechanism is real, I built the scenario. Mechanism 1 (stale arm via a 3rd-party velocity plugin): attacker A sprint-hits stationary victim B on SIGNATURE. Fresh sprint stamp = base.h 0.325 + extra.h 0.5 = 0.825 horizontal, base.v 0.365; q=axis*8000 so qy=q(0.365)=2920, horizontal ~6600 split across x/z by yaw. Fast path pre-sends the burst (client gets full KB for hit 1). At PlayerVelocityEvent, DeskRouter (HIGH) resolves SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE and arms VelocityValve[B]=(entityId,6600,2920). A HIGHEST/MONITOR anti-KB/anticheat listener then cancels or modifies the event, so vanilla's duplicate never matches and the arm stays live. Within the same 50ms window (before B's session-tick clearStale) hit 2 lands from the same stationary geometry with a byte-identical stamp. Hit 2's pre-send burst traverses ValveListener (BurstSender uses writePacket, not silent), matches the stale arm and is cancelled; hit 2's own arm then eats its vanilla duplicate, so B receives ZERO velocity copies. Shipped velocity WITH mechanism = 0 (hurt/flinch still land); WITHOUT = full 0.825h/0.365v. A literal total per-hit KB loss concentrated in close stationary trades, an exact match to 'little to no knockback, victim doesn't move back.' Mechanism 2b (blocked redelivery, !wirePreSent): ship() flushes the burst then arm() runs synchronously; writePacket schedules the encode on the netty loop, so the arm wins and ValveListener eats Mental's OWN burst; the knock reaches the client only via vanilla's end-of-tick tracker duplicate about 1 tick (50ms) late = mushy/weak, matching the 'blockhitting seems non-sprint' slice. Mechanism 2a is opposite polarity (doubled/stronger). So the finding plausibly produces parts of the report; refuted=false.
- Corrections: Not refuted; it plausibly reproduces two symptoms, but the strongest match (close-range total-loss on non-blocked hits) is config-gated. Mechanism 1 fires ONLY when a third-party plugin touches PlayerVelocityEvent at HIGHEST/MONITOR (cancel OR modify) after DeskRouter's HIGH arm, plus two byte-identical stamps on one victim inside a 50ms clearStale window (a 2-attacker gang or ~20cps single attacker). Without such a plugin this path is dead, so it cannot be the owner's 'as far back as I can remember, always present' non-blocked feel on a vanilla-ish stack, which is the finding's key weakness. Ask what anti-KB/anticheat/movement plugin is installed. Mechanism 2 needs no external config but is limited to blocked redeliveries (temp-shield/off-hand/BLOCKS_ATTACKS) and is polarity-ambiguous: 2a ships a DOUBLED (stronger) knock, only 2b yields the ~1-tick-late mushy weak read. Net: a genuine pair of valve races (per-victim arm carries no hit identity, unconditional clearStale, arm-after-async-writePacket ordering), medium severity, a secondary/config-dependent contributor rather than the primary always-present cause.
- Severity: medium

### `valve-quantization-dedup-misses-extra-kb` — CODE lens: STANDS, era call `bug`

- Reasoning: Code mechanism is genuinely NOT refutable. Verified against real sources: (1) PE 2.12.1 WrapperPlayServerEntityVelocity.read() has NO precision fix (lines 62-69); the +copySign(1e-11) fix exists only in write() (82-84). So the valve, reading packet.getVelocity(), sees raw xa/8000.0 (<1.21.9) or LpVector3d-decoded double (1.21.9+). (2) The <1.21.9 numeric claim reproduces EXACTLY: 374/62401 legal shorts (187 positive) satisfy trunc((xa/8000.0)*8000)==xa-1. (3) The arm-vs-observe asymmetry is real code: DeskRouter.sinkFor ships via event.setVelocity() (real PlayerVelocityEvent -> CraftBukkit re-emits NMS-quantized ENTITY_VELOCITY), while DeliveryDesk.resolve arms with ValvePayload.of(entityId, carried) on the RAW double. NMS (int)(clamp*8000)==q(carried)==armed; observe re-quantizes the decoded double -> lands on armed-1 for the 374 bad shorts, so consume() (all-3-axis integer equality) returns false and the duplicate ships. (4) VelocityValveTest builds observed shorts from the same ValvePayload.of, never exercising the decode roundtrip — the pinned-contract blind spot is real. The LP 32% figure I did not independently reproduce, but the LpVector3d ~15-bit-relative-to-max encoding confirms lossy decode and boundary-sensitive trunc, so the mechanism is sound and the order of magnitude plausible. HOWEVER: impact is overstated. A missed valve ships a duplicate ENTITY_VELOCITY carrying the SAME carried value; ENTITY_VELOCITY is a SET, so the client's end-state velocity is carried either way — a redundant double-SET, net-zero KB change, opposite-direction from the weak/no-KB report. The finding's own matches_report concedes this. So the code defect is real but low-severity and does NOT explain the owner's bug; cannot refute on code merits.
- Corrections: VERIFIED, code-accurate, but impact overstated. Confirmed against sources: PE 2.12.1 read() (lines 62-69) has no precision fix, only write() (82-84) does; the <1.21.9 roundtrip fails for exactly 374/62401 legal shorts (187 positive) where trunc((xa/8000)*8000)==xa-1; the arm side (DeliveryDesk.resolve -> ValvePayload.of on the raw carried double) matches NMS (int)(clamp*8000), while the observe side (ValveListener re-quantizing packet.getVelocity()) reads the decoded xa/8000.0, so consume()'s all-axis integer equality can miss by 1. DeskRouter.sinkFor ships via a real PlayerVelocityEvent.setVelocity, so CraftBukkit re-emits the NMS/LP-quantized packet the valve observes — premise holds. VelocityValveTest never exercises the decode roundtrip (builds observed from the same ValvePayload.of), so the blind spot is genuine. 1.21.9+ LpVector3d lossy decode is real (15-bit-relative-to-max, boundary-sensitive x8000 trunc); the ~32% Monte-Carlo figure I could NOT independently reproduce — treat as plausible, unverified. Downgrade impact: a missed valve ships a DUPLICATE ENTITY_VELOCITY carrying the same carried value; since ENTITY_VELOCITY is a SET (not add), the client's end velocity is carried either way — a redundant double-SET, net-zero KB, opposite-direction from the weak-KB report. Does NOT explain the owner's bug; it is a minor correctness gap violating the one-wire-stamp-per-knock contract with negligible gameplay effect.
- Severity: low

### `valve-quantization-dedup-misses-extra-kb` — SYM lens: STANDS, era call `bug`

- Reasoning: Verified against code. ValvePayload.q = trunc(clamp(axis,±3.9)·8000) as short; the arm key (ValvePayload.of, pre-send) is computed from the exact double, while ValveListener re-quantizes the ENTITY_VELOCITY the server re-emits (ValveListener.java:52-56). On 1.21.9+ that packet is LpVector3d (15-bit), so PE decodes a lossy double and trunc(lossy·8000) crosses the ×8000 boundary → integer-equality miss → duplicate NOT cancelled → it SHIPS ~1 tick after the pre-send. Below 1.21.9 the missing PRECISION_LOSS_FIX gives ~1.2% miss, horizontal-only per the finding's numeric note.\n\nHand-compute (1.21.9, signature, sprint hit, v=(0.80,0.36,0.20), arm qx=6400): tick T pre-send sets client motion; tick T authoritative LP-decodes 0.80→0.799987, listener trunc→6399≠6400, MISS; tick T+1 the un-suppressed duplicate REPLACES the by-then-decayed motion (~0.75,0.27,0.19) with the full fresh (0.80,0.36,0.20) — a re-launch. Net: ~1 restored tick of flight — horizontal +~5-9%, vertical re-lifted +~0.09 vy → floatier hang. A velocity packet REPLACES motion and the second copy is the full maximum, so it can only ADD flight, never subtract. Stale arm swept by clearStale next session tick → self-neutralizing, no cross-hit poisoning.\n\nFrequency: 32% on 1.21.9+/26.x; on the owner's actual 1.21.4 test clients only ~1.2% (horizontal-only, never vy). Genuine bug (breaks the one-wire-stamp-per-knock contract; VelocityValveTest pins integer-equality as the violated contract).\n\nBUT opposite polarity to the report: it makes hits floatier/slightly stronger and CANNOT make any hit weaker or read as non-sprint. Only overlap with the report is the generic 'subtle, feeling thing, hit-to-hit / version-to-version inconsistency' — which it does contribute, so not fully refuted — but that inconsistency points toward MORE knock, not the 'victim doesn't really move back' the owner describes. Not the owner's bug; included to prevent misattribution.
- Corrections: Real, code-confirmed dedup defect: the valve arm key is trunc(exactDouble·8000) but ValveListener re-quantizes the SERVER-re-emitted ENTITY_VELOCITY, whose LpVector3d (1.21.9+, 15-bit) roundtrip crosses the ×8000 trunc boundary ~32% of the time (and ~1.2% horizontal-only <1.21.9 without PE PRECISION_LOSS_FIX). A miss ships the tracker duplicate ~1 tick late; since a velocity packet REPLACES motion with the full fresh knock, the effect is a re-launch that RESTORES ~1 tick of decay — measurably floatier/slightly farther flight (~+0.09 vy re-lift, +5-9% horizontal), never weaker. Self-neutralizes via clearStale next session tick. It breaks the one-wire-stamp-per-knock contract and adds real version/hit inconsistency (the 'feeling thing' descriptor), so not fully refuted — but it is OPPOSITE polarity to the core symptom and cannot produce 'little to no knockback' or a sprint-reads-as-non-sprint hit. On the owner's own 1.21.4 test clients it is ~1% and horizontal-only. Not the owner's weak-KB bug; a genuine but low-severity modern-half correctness defect worth fixing (match on the LP-decoded quantum or widen the valve epsilon) for the inconsistency, not the weakness.
- Severity: low

### `presend-never-revoked-phantom-knockback` — CODE lens: STANDS, era call `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Could not refute; all five mechanistic claims verify. (1) The pre-send burst ships on the netty thread (HitRegistrationUnit.java:426-429) before dispatch schedules applyPlayer, and no reverse packet exists (the valve only consumes duplicates), so a hit later cancelled/blocked/failed leaves an un-revoked knock on the victim client. (2) applyPlayer validation-fail branches return WITHOUT retract (622-623 attacker-null, 633-635 offline/spectator, 636-640 victim dead/unreachable); only the cross-region branch and the runOn task-never-ran callback withdraw. (3) DeliveryDesk.sweep with victimConnected true never time-drops a LIVE pending (269-278), so a dangling pre-sent pending waits until replacePending journals it late as superseded (312-317). (4) withdraw calls clearDecision, which writes no journal and does not transition the tx, so it never reaches RECORDED, contradicting HitTransaction class doc (desk documents the silence as intentional for genuine cancels/yields). (5) JournalEntry has no sprint verdict field. Config is no escape: HitRegSettings.DEFAULTS has fastPath true and preSendFeedback true, so the path is live under shipped defaults. The finding itself notes this is opposite polarity to the weak/no-KB report and included to define the pre-send contract and journal diagnostic gaps. Minor overstatement: modern movement is client-authoritative, so the phantom knock likely lands as a real accepted displacement rather than always a rubber-band; the core holds either way.
- Corrections: Confirmed on mechanics; refine framing. TRUE: pre-send ships before applyPlayer validations and is never revoked; applyPlayer 622-623/633-635/636-640 return without withdraw; sweep never time-drops a connected victim LIVE pending (DeliveryDesk 269-278) so it lingers until superseded (312-317); withdraw is journal-silent and leaves the tx non-terminal, contradicting HitTransaction RECORDED doc; JournalEntry has no sprint verdict; path on by default. Refinements: (a) rubber-band is not certain, modern movement is client-authoritative so the phantom knock likely becomes a real accepted displacement rather than a snap-back; the un-revoked-knock defect stands regardless. (b) This is opposite polarity to the owner report and does not itself explain weak/no KB; the diagnostic-gap half (silent withdraw plus no sprint verdict) is the load-bearing takeaway because it explains why the real bug reads as a healthy SHIP in the journal.
- Severity: low-medium: real but rare-trigger latent edge, opposite polarity to the reported weak/no-KB bug (extra phantom movement, not missing knock); value is documenting the pre-send has-no-revocation contract and the journal gaps.

### `presend-never-revoked-phantom-knockback` — SYM lens: REFUTED, era call `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Mechanism confirmed real in code. Pre-send ships the FULL era knock to the victim's client on the netty thread BEFORE the authoritative pass. The authoritative pass can then: full-block-cancel (KnockbackUnit :209-213 desk.withdraw), protection-plugin cancel (:347-363 withdraw), cross-region retract (HitReg :626 retract), or silently return on re-validation fail (:636-640 — no withdraw, dangling pending confirmed). In EVERY case the server applies no velocity and sends NO correcting packet; withdraw()/clearDecision are server-side only (DeliveryDesk :62-67).

Hand-computed scenario (LEGACY_18 sprint, close range, ~4 CPS): base.h 0.4 + sprintExtra 0.5, friction.h 0.5 → the burst delivers a ~0.5–0.9 b/t horizontal impulse to the victim's client. WITH the mechanism after a cancel: client slid back the full knock; server never moved the entity. Outcome (a) no position correction → victim really moves back = EXTRA/phantom knock (opposite polarity); outcome (b) server position-authority correction → victim rubber-bands to net ~0. WITHOUT the mechanism a cancelled hit ships nothing and the victim stays put. So the mechanism's error is a phantom of the FULL knock in a ZERO-expected (no-damage) scenario, never a reduction of a legitimately-landing knock.

This does not reproduce the report's core: the owner describes hits that LAND and DEAL DAMAGE but under-knock (sprint reads as non-sprint) during two players trading blows at close range — a high-frequency, damage-dealing scenario in which this mechanism NEVER fires (no cancel/retract/revalidation-fail). The only overlap is a strained reading: a rubber-band-to-net-zero in a cancelled hit could read as 'victim didn't move back,' but that requires a zero-damage hit (opposite of the report), is low-frequency (needs a protection plugin, a full modern-shield block, cross-region attacker, or an out-of-reach-at-damage-time hit — the latter is a reach-EDGE event, not close range), and produces ~0 where ~0 is arguably correct. The finding's own author labels it 'opposite polarity, included to define the pre-send contract.' I could not construct any path where a damage-landing sprint hit ships reduced (non-sprint-magnitude) velocity via this mechanism: the dangling pending is cleanly superseded by the next hit's replacePending (DeliveryDesk :312-328) and the valve is armed only on SHIP_AND_ARM_VALVE at resolve, which never runs in the cancel path — so no subsequent legitimate knock is eaten or weakened. Real contract/journal gap, wrong symptom.
- Corrections: Symptom REFUTED for this report. The mechanism is real and is a genuine divergence-from-era (a cancelled hit should ship nothing, yet the client keeps the pre-sent knock with no revocation; the full-block-cancel branch itself diverges from era 'blocking knocks full'), but it produces the OPPOSITE polarity of the report — phantom/EXTRA knock (or a rubber-band net-zero) on hits that dealt NO damage, not reduced knock on hits that land. Frequency is confined to cancel/retract/re-validation-fail events, which are rare in and largely absent from the report's core scenario (two players trading damage at close range with vanilla rules). It cannot produce a sprint hit reading as non-sprint magnitude, and the dangling pending is cleanly superseded by the next hit (no valve arming, no subsequent-hit weakening). Keep it as a contract/journaling fix (add revocation packet + withdraw on the :636-640 return + a sprint verdict in JournalEntry so the real weak-KB bug becomes diagnosable), not as the cause of the owner's feel.
- Severity: As an explanation of the owner's weak/missing-KB report: none. As a standalone bug: low/edge — a cosmetic phantom-knock (or rubber-band) confined to rare cancel/retract/revalidation-fail hits, plus a real journal-diagnosis blind spot (silent withdraw, no sprint verdict) that matters for debuggability but not for the reported feel.

## Gap pathway maps

### `config-resolution`

Resolution chain (read in full): human YAMLs (config.yml, knockback.yml, hit-registration.yml, latency-compensation.yml, profiles/*.yml) are loaded per-file (ConfigStore.loadSources:173-195; a file that fails YAML parse becomes an EMPTY root, one console line); the machine overlay state/overrides.yml then sets its flat dotted keys onto the in-memory roots BEFORE parse (Overlay.apply:46-54, routed by first path segment; MentalPluginV5.parseSnapshot:717-719); SnapshotParser builds one immutable Snapshot swapped by a single volatile reference (MentalPluginV5.reloadAll:440-447). Profile selection: ProfileParser.parseSection lowercases stems/names, guarantees legacy-1.7 exists, warns+falls back on unknown selection (ProfileParser.java:151-160); Snapshot.profileFor(world) = perWorld override else server default else LEGACY_17 (Snapshot.java:64-68). The victim's profile is frozen per-tick into the PlayerView (SessionService.buildView:507, ViewBuilder) and the melee hit path prefers the frozen view over the live snapshot (KnockbackUnit.profileFor:604-606), so pre-send and authoritative pass share one profile per hit; PRE_SENT/PINNED adoption means a reload mid-hit cannot mix profiles — Q4 is CLEAN (only asymmetry: ProjectileKnockbackUnit:298/356 and FishingKnockbackUnit:217 read the live snapshot, a harmless ≤1-tick skew). Q5 CLEAN: an unmapped world gets the server default; unknown per-world entries are dropped with a warn. No per-player override remnant survives 2.1.0 (grep-verified). parse(empty)==LEGACY_17 holds through the overlay path (the overlay only sets explicitly-written keys; pinned in ProfileParserTest:39-44). Q3 shipped defaults: ON = hit-registration (max-cps 20, fast-path, pre-send, bundle, feedback auto, simulate-crits, legacy-tool-damage; reach-validation OFF), wtap-registration, knockback (profile legacy-1.7, per-world {}), latency-compensation, fishing-knockback, rod-velocity, projectile-knockback; anticheat mode AUTO with known [GrimAC, Vulcan]; everything else OFF — attack-cooldown, disable-attack-sounds, disable-sword-sweep, sword-blocking, old-hitboxes, all old-* rules, combo-hold, combo-reach-handicap, pot-fill, fast-pots (config.yml:22-307,523-527). Only legacy-1.8 ships armor-resistance: legacy; only signature ships pace scaling. The dirty layers are the overlay's permanence, the superseded-preset in-place upgrade, and whole-file parse degradation — findings below.

### `mutual-trade-self-perturbation`

Reverse coupling map (A = player as simultaneous victim+attacker). A's victim role mutates: (1) A's MotionLedger — recordDelivered of B's knock (combos:true only, DeskRouter), Liftoff/Landing from A's own movement packets (PacketTap→GroundFsm→inbox), and A's own attacker-role x0.6 (KnockbackUnit.java:423). (2) A's physical position (client integrates the knock; server sees it via A's movement packets; ring sampled once/owning-tick, SessionService.java:352-354). (3) A's measured ring heading (servo alignment, COMBO_HOLD only). A's victim role NEVER touches A's SprintWire, server sprint flag, ResetModel, CPS window, or FeedbackGate (grep-verified writer inventories). A's outgoing hit reads of A's own state: position x/z (ring at pre-send, HitRegistrationUnit.java:452-455; live Location at region recompute, EntityStates.java:43-46), yaw (domain.lastYaw, packet-fed, fresh), SprintVerdict (wire), knockbackEnchantLevel (0 at pre-send — see finding, live at region), moveSpeedAttr (view attr), view.grounded (captured but UNUSED — KnockbackEngine reads only victim.grounded()). A's own ledger, GroundFsm state, kinematics and measured velocity feed NOTHING on the outgoing vector (engine attacker terms: x,y,z,yaw,sprinting,enchant,attr only) except servo chase alignment, already covered by stationary-nan-alignment-refuted-trade-clamp-real. Q1: a knock-induced rising liftoff stamps A's ledger 0.42+push exactly like a jump — era-real (era movement handlers stamped any rising liftoff; the 1.8.9 combo-vy chain measures it); the non-rising body-block mis-stamp is already reported. Q2: the reconcile cannot resurrect a stale-TRUE view inside the deferred-clear window — quiet=3 exceeds the max 2-tick publish lag (PacketTap.java:39,85; clear at T+1/T+2, false view by T+2/T+3) — so the only weak-sprint interleavings are the two already merged (same-tick retro-clear; modern hold-sprint no-reengage). Q4: A's counter-attack x0.6 scales the SAME ledger holding B's knock residual — era-1.7-real (era attack() scaled fields holding the received knock); sole call site, bonus-gated, no double-apply; the 1-2-tick timing divergence is already merged (attacker-x06-residual-write-era-and-timing). New on this axis: the received-knock displacement invalidates the stale-ring refutation's 0.28 b/t lateral bound (refinement), the GroundFsm sprint-push reads the stale VIEW flag instead of the same-domain wire, and (found while tracing attacker reads) the pre-send stamps enchant level 0 and adoption never corrects it.

### `cadence-spoof-coupling`

CADENCE/ATTACK_COOLDOWN ("attack-cooldown", default OFF — Feature.java:166-174, config.yml:57) is one scoped unit (AttackCooldownUnit.assemble) with four halves: (a) AttackChargeReset raises the SERVER attack_speed BASE to CooldownSpoof.FULL_CHARGE_ATTACK_SPEED=1024.0 (attribute ceiling, never clamped) on enable→applyOnline, join, respawn, world-change (deferred via Scheduling.runOn); captured original is sanitized (>=16.0 treated as inflated → restore 4.0) and restored inline on quit (pre-NBT-save) and on scope close (disableAll). (b) CooldownSpoofListener rewrites/injects attack_speed=1024.0 in every outbound UPDATE_ATTRIBUTES for the receiver's OWN entity. (c) tooltip strip, (d) sweep re-disable (>=1.11 only). Scope.close unwinds in REVERSE order, so packet listeners unregister BEFORE disableAll's restore — restore packets ship unspoofed (no zombie).

Client coupling: attack_speed=1024 makes delay=20/1024≈0.02 ticks, so getAttackStrengthScale=1.0 on every click including same-tick re-clicks and post-miss resets. The client's local prediction runs the SAME shared attack() (SYNOPSIS:306-336, :382 — RemotePlayer.hurtClient→true; "sprint reset survives to 2026" at :336): kbAttack=isSprinting()&&scale>0.9 → with the spoof every sprint click fires the ×0.6 self-slow + local un-sprint → STOP crosses the wire after the ATTACK, START next client tick → SprintWire re-arms after Mental's post-hit clear. Without the spoof (DEFAULT), spam-CPS clicks never pass the 0.9 gate — no ×0.6, no STOP/START (legacy-combat.md:97-101).

Mental's own pipeline is fully charge-blind: zero attackStrength/cooldown references in the kernel; DamageShaper composes off the attribute base (legacy-combat.md:73); the KnockbackEngine's sprint term comes only from the SprintVerdict. AttackChargeReset does nothing when OFF (Reconciler assembles only on the disabled→enabled transition).

Q5 (reconciler/mixed populations) is CLEAN: the spoof is population-uniform — enable covers all online plus join/respawn/world-change listeners registered before the task; disable restores everyone captured; quit restores inline so a spoofed base can never persist to NBT. Only ~1-tick transients exist (deferred runOn after respawn), and the client-presentation packet half covers those windows. No mechanism leaves some players spoofed and others not. The real per-player asymmetry is client VERSION, not CADENCE state (finding 1).

## Gap findings with verdicts

### `overlay-shadow-hand-edits-permanent` — config-dependent, confidence high (finder: config-resolution)

**Mechanism:** Once the GUI writes any overlay key (FamilyMenu profile pick -> Management.setGlobalProfile -> overlaySet("knockback.profile"), module toggles -> "modules.<key>", CompatibilityMenu anticheat.mode, DebugMenu debug.*), that key wins over the human YAML on EVERY subsequent reload forever: Overlay.apply sets it onto the in-memory root before SnapshotParser runs (Overlay.java:46-54, MentalPluginV5.parseSnapshot:717-719). Overlay.remove (Overlay.java:75-78) has ZERO callers and Overlay.overrides() (the intended 'modified' marks) has zero production readers — there is no in-game or command path to clear an override, and reload emits no warning that a hand-edited file value is being shadowed. config.yml:16-17 explicitly promises 'Editing files by hand still works; reload to apply', which becomes false for any overlaid key. So an operator who ever touched the GUI profile picker and later hand-edits knockback.yml 'profile:' (or modules.knockback, anticheat.mode) plays under the overlay's value while believing the file's — the exact effective-profile-differs-from-belief gate the critic named; every profile-scoped finding (combos, friction, resistance, verticalMin, legacy-1.8 vs legacy-1.7) resolves through it.

**Trigger:** Any historical GUI write of knockback.profile / modules.* / anticheat.mode, followed by hand edits to the same key in the human YAML. Check: cat plugins/Mental/state/overrides.yml — any key present there overrides the file silently.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/Overlay.java:46-54,75-78 (remove: no callers, grep-verified); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/MentalPluginV5.java:717-719; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/manage/Management.java:58; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/gui/CompatibilityMenu.java:45, DebugMenu.java:62-73; core/src/main/resources/config.yml:16-17 (the now-false hand-edit promise)

**Maps to the report:** Master gate, not a direct KB mechanism: if the owner's deployment carries a stale knockback.profile or modules override, the profile every other finding is scoped on is not the one the files show — could sustain a years-long 'as far back as I can remember' mismatch across config edits that never actually applied.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: All cited code verified in the main tree: Overlay.apply mutates the in-memory config roots before SnapshotParser.parse (Overlay.java:46-54, MentalPluginV5.java:718-719); Overlay.remove has zero external callers (grep: only its own definition); overrides() has zero production readers; overlaySet writers are exactly Management.setGlobalProfile (knockback.profile), setModuleEnabled (modules.*), CompatibilityMenu (anticheat.mode), DebugMenu (debug.*); config.yml:17 makes the hand-edit promise. So the mechanism — a GUI-written overlay key permanently shadows the human YAML on every reload, with no in-game clear path and no shadow warning — is real and code-accurate; I cannot refute it as a config-resolution fact. But the finding overreaches on framing: (1) overlay-wins-over-file is intended, documented architecture (spec §10, effective = overlay ?? file ?? default), not a mechanism bug; the only defensible defect is the missing clear-path + missing reload warning + overpromising comment. (2) It does NOT match the owner's symptom: a stale overlay produces a deterministic, consistent effective profile (same value every hit), whereas the owner reports intermittent, subtle, 'sometimes weaker sprint KB,' hard-to-reproduce feel — a wrong global profile cannot produce 'sometimes.' (3) It requires specific operator history: setGlobalProfile no-writes when the picked profile already equals active, so an override exists only after a GUI change to a DIFFERENT profile then a same-key hand edit. Verdict: real mechanism, but a diagnostic caveat (check state/overrides.yml before trusting the YAML when scoping profile-dependent findings), not the direct cause of the reported knockback bug.
- Corrections: Mechanism confirmed and code-accurate: any GUI-written overlay key (knockback.profile, modules.*, anticheat.mode, debug.*) shadows the human YAML on every reload; Overlay.remove has no callers; overrides() has no production readers; config.yml:17 overpromises. Reframe: (a) overlay-wins-over-file is intended spec §10 design, not a mechanism bug — the real defect is only the missing in-game override-clear path + missing reload shadow-warning + the misleading config.yml comment; (b) this cannot be the DIRECT cause of the owner's bug — a stale overlay yields a deterministic, consistent effective profile (same value every hit), contradicting the owner's intermittent 'sometimes weaker sprint hit' feel; (c) it requires a specific history (setGlobalProfile no-writes when the picked profile already equals active, so an override exists only after a GUI change to a DIFFERENT profile then a same-key hand edit). Correct role: a diagnostic/measurement caveat — when scoping the profile-dependent findings, inspect state/overrides.yml, not just the human YAML — not a knockback-loss mechanism. Severity low.
- Severity: low

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Mechanism verified. Overlay.apply writes every override onto the in-memory config root BEFORE SnapshotParser.parse (parseSnapshot:717-719), so overlay wins over the human file. Overlay.remove has zero callers (grep: only its own def) and overrides() has zero production readers — there is genuinely no in-game/command path to clear an override, and reload emits no shadow warning. config.yml:17's "hand edits still work" promise is therefore false for any overlaid key. This is a real config-resolution defect. BUT it is a master GATE/confounder, not a direct KB producer: by itself it ships nothing weak — it only lets a stale knockback.profile / modules.knockback override silently keep a profile the files no longer show, so whichever downstream weak-KB finding (combos, friction, verticalMin, legacy-1.7-vs-1.8) is scoped on that profile stays active while the owner believes otherwise. A stale profile override produces UNIFORM behavior, not the report's "some hits, subtle, per-hit" close-range weakness — that per-hit character must come from a downstream mechanism, not this gate. Two caveats weaken it as THE root: (1) the overlay/GUI arrived in v2.1.0, yet the symptom is "as far back as I can remember," predating the system, so it cannot be the historical origin; (2) it only fires if the owner both used the GUI picker historically AND later hand-edited the same key. Where it DOES fit the report: it plausibly explains why "edits don't help" and why the mismatch persists across config changes. Not refuted — it plausibly explains part (persistence / effective-profile-≠-belief), even if not the subtle per-hit texture. Verify by: cat plugins/Mental/state/overrides.yml.
- Corrections: Real config-resolution defect (overlay permanently shadows hand-edits; no clear path; false doc promise), but it is a CONFOUNDING GATE, not a direct cause of subtle weak knockback. It cannot itself produce the "some hits, close-range, per-hit" texture — a stale override yields uniform behavior and only matters by keeping a downstream weak-KB finding's profile active. It also cannot be the historical root: the overlay/GUI shipped in v2.1.0, while the symptom predates it ("as far back as I can remember"). Its true value: check `cat plugins/Mental/state/overrides.yml` first — if a knockback.profile or modules.* key is present, every other profile-scoped finding is being evaluated against the wrong effective profile.
- Severity: Low as a direct producer of the subtle per-hit weak-KB symptom (it ships no velocity itself). Medium as a config-resolution defect and investigation master-gate: overrides.yml must be dumped before ANY profile-scoped finding is trusted, since a stale knockback.profile/modules.knockback override silently invalidates the file-based assumption. Genuine standalone bug regardless: no override-clear path + a now-false hand-edit promise (config.yml:17).

### `superseded-upgrade-reverts-owner-edit` — bug, confidence high (finder: config-resolution)

**Mechanism:** ConfigStore.upgradeSupersededPreset (ConfigStore.java:105-131) runs on EVERY boot AND every /mental reload (reloadAll -> ensureDefaultFiles, MentalPluginV5.java:441): it parses each preset file and, if the values+identity strings match ANY superseded revision (SupersededPresets.isSupersededVerbatim:403-412), overwrites the file with the current bundle. The heuristic cannot distinguish 'unedited old file' from 'owner edit that lands on an old revision' — and the bundled files THEMSELVES instruct exactly such an edit: 'Restore -3.9 to unfloor' (legacy-1.7.yml:37, legacy-1.8.yml:40, kohi.yml:52, mmc.yml:54, minehq.yml:43, badlion.yml:49; custom.yml:64 suggests the same). Since the 2.4.7/2.4.8 revisions differ from the current bundles ONLY in verticalMin (-3.9 vs 0.0), following that instruction produces a byte-value match with LEGACY17_2_4_7/LEGACY18_2_4_7/CUSTOM_2_4_7/KOHI_1_8/etc. and the edit is silently reverted to 0.0 on the next reload (one console line claims it was 'carried unedited'). Same trap on signature: deleting the speed-scaling block matches SIGNATURE_2_2_1 (pace re-enabled), setting exponent back to 1.0 matches SIGNATURE_2_4_0 — an owner trying to turn OFF signature's pace scaling by removing the block gets it re-enabled every reload. Violates the stated 'owner edits are sacred' contract (ConfigStore.java:26-29).

**Trigger:** Owner edits a preset file such that the parsed profile equals a SupersededPresets revision verbatim — most likely by following the file's own 'Restore -3.9 to unfloor' comment, or by deleting signature's speed-scaling block / setting its exponent to 1.0 — then any boot or /mental reload.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/ConfigStore.java:91-96,105-131; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/MentalPluginV5.java:440-441; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/SupersededPresets.java:253-304,313-389,403-412; core/src/main/resources/profiles/legacy-1.7.yml:32-38 and the parallel comments in the other five preset files

**Maps to the report:** Indirect: an owner's tuning attempt (unflooring, pace-off) silently un-applies, so 'I changed it and nothing changed' experiments mis-anchor the diagnosis; vertical-floor reverts affect downward knocks, pace-scaling revert affects signature's fresh-knock magnitude under Speed/Slowness.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Confirmed by direct reading; could not refute. reloadAll (MentalPluginV5.java:441) -> ensureDefaultFiles -> upgradeSupersededPreset per preset, on every boot and /mental reload. sameValues (KnockbackProfile.java:156-173) compares limits (verticalMin) and paceScaling, so unedited current bundles do NOT match their superseded twins (no self-overwrite), but an edit that lands verbatim on an old revision DOES. Core case is airtight: LEGACY17_2_4_7 differs from current legacy-1.7.yml ONLY in verticalMin (-3.9 vs 0.0), identity strings byte-identical; an owner following the file's OWN comment 'Restore -3.9 to unfloor' (legacy-1.7.yml:37) parses to exactly LEGACY17_2_4_7 -> isSupersededVerbatim true -> file overwritten back to 0.0 with a log line falsely claiming it was 'carried unedited'. Same for custom.yml (CUSTOM_2_4_7) and practice presets. Signature: deleting the speed-scaling block resets exponent to the LEGACY_17 default 1.0 -> PaceScaling.OFF -> matches SIGNATURE_2_2_1 (pace re-enabled); setting exponent to 1.0 with mode:attacker -> matches SIGNATURE_2_4_0 (reverted to 0.95). Nuance the finding gets right: setting mode:off while KEEPING exponent 0.95 does NOT match any revision, so that edit survives — only deleting the block reverts. Genuine config-handling correctness bug that contradicts the 'owner edits are sacred' doc AND the bundled file's own written instruction. Classification 'bug' is correct. era_call=bug: it is a plugin correctness defect, unrelated to era authenticity.
- Corrections: Finding CONFIRMED with one refinement to the signature sub-claim. The revert is guaranteed whenever an owner edit parses byte-for-byte to a SupersededPresets revision (values via sameValues incl. limits/paceScaling, plus display-name + description). The sharpest, most-reachable case is verticalMin: the current bundle differs from *_2_4_7/KOHI_1_8/etc. ONLY in verticalMin, and the bundle's OWN comment 'Restore -3.9 to unfloor' (legacy-1.7.yml:37, custom.yml:64-65, and the practice presets) instructs precisely the edit that upgradeSupersededPreset then reverts on the next boot or /mental reload — a self-contradiction with the 'owner edits are frozen' contract (ConfigStore.java:26-29,105-131). Signature nuance: only DELETING the speed-scaling block (which resets exponent to the LEGACY_17 default 1.0, matching SIGNATURE_2_2_1) or setting exponent=1.0 with mode:attacker (matching SIGNATURE_2_4_0) reverts; setting mode:off while keeping the shipped exponent 0.95 does NOT match any revision and survives — so the finding's 'delete the block' wording is necessary and correct. Relation to the user's weak-KB-at-close-range report is only indirect (owner's tuning experiments mis-anchor diagnosis); it does not itself produce the reported non-sprint-feeling horizontal knockback.
- Severity: low-to-medium: real and directly reachable (the bundled comment instructs the exact edit that gets reverted), but scope is narrow — an owner edit that lands verbatim on a superseded revision silently un-applies on the next boot/reload. Impact is confusion and wasted debugging plus a false 'carried unedited' log line, not gameplay breakage. Only marginally related to the user's weak-KB report: verticalMin governs downward knocks, and pace-scaling reverts only bite under Speed/Slowness — neither produces the sprint-reads-as-non-sprint horizontal symptom the owner describes. The finding's own matches_report labels this 'Indirect', which is accurate.

**SYMPTOM lens: MISSING** (structured-output retry cap)

### `profile-file-parse-degrades-to-legacy17-silently` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: config-resolution)

**Mechanism:** Two degradation layers make the EFFECTIVE profile drift from the file's intent without any GUI/selection change. (1) Whole-file: a profiles/<name>.yml with any YAML syntax error loads as an EMPTY root (ConfigStore.loadYaml:234-246, one console line 'could not be parsed — using defaults') and ProfileParser.parse of the empty section yields LEGACY_17's VALUES under the preset's name — the GUI still shows e.g. 'signature' selected, but every hit computes with legacy-1.7 numbers (friction 0.5 not 0.1, extra 0.5/0.1, combos true). (2) Per-key: every omitted key in an owner-edited preset falls back to the CURRENT KnockbackProfile.LEGACY_17 field (ProfileParser.parse:40-99), never to that preset's own bundled value — deleting a block from mmc.yml/lunar.yml splices legacy-1.7 values into an mmc-labeled profile. The fallback is also a MOVING target: 2.4.8 changed LEGACY_17.limits.verticalMin from -3.9 to 0.0 (KnockbackProfile.java:137-144), so any profile file omitting limits.vertical-min changed behavior across the upgrade with no file edit (the 2.4.8 memory's 'LEGACY_17 edits move the parse fallback' trap, now confirmed in-tree). Note parse(empty)==LEGACY_17 still literally holds (ProfileParserTest:39-44) — but since 2.4.8 LEGACY_17 itself is deliberately no longer the strict era no-op (the 0.0 floor trades away the era-authentic mid-fall negative, an owner directive).

**Trigger:** An owner-edited or corrupted profiles/<selected>.yml: any syntax error = full legacy-1.7 values under the preset's name; any omitted key = legacy-1.7's current value for that key. Check: reload console for 'could not be parsed', and diff the runtime profile dump against the file.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/ConfigStore.java:167-172,234-246; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/ProfileParser.java:37-99,140-151; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/profile/KnockbackProfile.java:127-153; core/src/test/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/ProfileParserTest.java:39-44

**Maps to the report:** A silently-degraded practice preset (velt/signature friction 0.1 -> legacy 0.5) changes residual carry-over in trades: with 0.5 survival the victim's toward-attacker counter-motion survives into the knock (the round-1 toward-attacker-residual-cancellation era-real mechanism bites HARDER than the wipe presets the owner thinks he is on) — a plausible chronic 'some hits barely move them' under a believed-wipe profile.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: All four code claims verified against the cited files. loadYaml (ConfigStore.java:234-246) returns an empty YamlConfiguration on parse failure with one log line; ProfileParser.parse (37-99) falls back per-key to KnockbackProfile.LEGACY_17 for every knob; the unit test emptyBlockParsesToLegacy17 pins parse(empty)==LEGACY_17; LEGACY_17.limits.verticalMin is 0.0 (line 144) with a comment documenting the 2.4.8 change from -3.9. velt/signature ship friction 0.1 vs LEGACY_17's 0.5. The mechanism is factually correct — I cannot refute the code facts, so refuted=false.

But severity is low and the matches_report is a stretch: (1) per-key fallback to LEGACY_17 is design-intended, documented in the class Javadoc, and unit-pinned — not a defect. (2) Whole-file degradation is NOT silent: it emits a console warning every load, and only triggers on an owner-introduced YAML syntax error in the selected file; bundled files extract as valid YAML so a fresh install never hits it. (3) Both modes are deterministic and global — a degraded selected profile makes EVERY hit use legacy values, a wholesale feel change, the opposite of the owner's SOME-hits/subtle/intermittent symptom. (4) The bridge to close-range weak-KB leans on a separate round-1 mechanism (toward-attacker-residual-cancellation) and does not itself explain close-range, w-tap/blockhit, or sprint-hit specificity. So it is a real config-hygiene observation, not the chronic intermittent pathway the owner reports.
- Corrections: Code facts confirmed exactly as stated (ConfigStore.java:234-246, ProfileParser.java:37-99, KnockbackProfile.java:144, test emptyBlockParsesToLegacy17). The two degradation layers are real. However this is a config-hygiene observation, not a code defect and not a strong match for the user's symptom: (a) per-key fallback to LEGACY_17 is design-intended, documented in the KnockbackProfile/ProfileParser Javadoc, and unit-pinned; (b) whole-file degradation is NOT silent — loadYaml logs a warning on every load, and it only fires when the OWNER introduced a YAML syntax error into the actively-selected file (bundled presets extract as valid YAML, so no fresh install triggers it); (c) both modes are deterministic and GLOBAL — a degraded selected profile makes ALL hits compute with legacy values, a consistent whole-feel change, which contradicts the owner's 'some hits, subtle, intermittent' description of a wholesale profile swap; (d) the matches_report link to close-range weak-KB borrows a separate round-1 mechanism and does not itself account for the close-range, w-tap/blockhit, or sprint-hit specificity. Verdict: an accurate config-resolution fact worth a diagnostic check (grep reload log for 'could not be parsed'; diff runtime profile dump vs file), but low severity and an unlikely explanation for the chronic intermittent report.
- Severity: low

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Both degradation paths are real in-tree. ConfigStore.loadYaml:234-246 turns any YAML syntax error into an empty YamlConfiguration (one console line); ProfileParser.parse of an empty section returns LEGACY_17 VALUES under the file's preset name, and every omitted key (ProfileParser:59-99) falls back to the CURRENT LEGACY_17 field, never the preset's bundled value. Swapping a wipe preset's friction 0.1 -> legacy 0.5 amplifies the round-1 toward-attacker-residual-cancellation. Matches "some hits barely move, especially close, feeling-thing": the degradation is a global constant but the unmasked symptom is state-dependent/intermittent (bites only on inward close trades), reproducing the subtle/hard-to-pin texture. <parameter name="corrected">Effective profile silently drifts to legacy-1.7 values under two GUI-invisible conditions: (1) any YAML syntax error in profiles/<selected>.yml loads empty -> full LEGACY_17 values under the preset name; (2) any omitted key falls back to the current LEGACY_17 field, not the preset's bundled value. - Severity: medium

### `per-world-map-masks-gui-selection` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: config-resolution)

**Mechanism:** Snapshot.profileFor resolves the VICTIM's world through knockback.per-world FIRST, server default second (Snapshot.java:64-68). Management.setGlobalProfile / the GUI picker write only the DEFAULT (knockback.profile overlay key, Management.java:49-62); no GUI surface shows or edits the per-world map, and DashboardMenu/FamilyMenu display only defaultProfile (DashboardMenu.java:150, FamilyMenu.java:134). So on a deployment with a per-world entry for the arena world, switching profiles in the GUI changes nothing for fights in that world — the operator A/B-tests presets and concludes 'the feel never changes'. Compounding the belief gap: knockback.yml's shipped comment still claims 'A per-player override (the API or /mental kb set) beats both' (knockback.yml:27-28) — that override was removed in 2.1.0 (grep-verified: no per-player profile path exists), so the documented precedence is wrong. Shipped default per-world is {} so this is inert on a fresh install.

**Trigger:** Any non-empty knockback.per-world entry covering the world where combat is judged, combined with GUI/default-profile switching. Check: knockback.yml per-world plus the world name players actually fight in (resolution is exact string match on World.getName()).

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/Snapshot.java:64-68; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/config/ProfileParser.java:162-177; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/manage/Management.java:49-62; core/src/main/resources/knockback.yml:26-31 (stale per-player-override comment)

**Maps to the report:** Gate-level: makes preset experiments inconclusive ('bug survives every profile'), reinforcing the 'ever since I can remember' framing while the tested knob was never the effective one.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Every code fact in the finding checks out, so I cannot refute it.

1. profileFor (Snapshot.java:64-68) does resolve perWorld.getOrDefault(worldName, defaultProfile) — per-world FIRST, default second. CONFIRMED.
2. Management.setGlobalProfile (Management.java:49-62) writes only the "knockback.profile" overlay key — the default. It never touches the per-world map. CONFIRMED.
3. No GUI surface edits or displays the per-world map: grep of gui/ finds zero perWorld references; DashboardMenu:150 and FamilyMenu:134 both read only snapshot().defaultProfile(). CONFIRMED — the GUI cannot override a per-world entry.
4. knockback.yml:27-28 comment "A per-player override (the API or /mental kb set) beats both" is stale: profileFor keys only on worldName, no per-player profile path exists anywhere (per-player override removed in 2.1.0). Genuine doc bug. CONFIRMED.
5. Shipped per-world is {} (line 29), so inert on a fresh install. CONFIRMED — the finding states this itself.

So the mechanism is real: on a deployment with a per-world entry for the arena world, GUI/default profile switching changes nothing for fights there, making A/B preset tests inconclusive.

BUT its explanatory power for the ACTUAL symptom is weak. A per-world override produces a CONSISTENTLY wrong-but-stable profile in that world, not the intermittent, close-range, per-hit "sometimes non-sprint knockback" the owner describes. It cannot produce sprint-hit-becomes-non-sprint variability. It is a testing-confound + doc-bug, not a cause of weak knockback. Requires a specific non-default config to manifest at all.

This is two distinct issues: (a) a real config/GUI gap where per-world entries silently mask GUI profile switches — a legitimate operator-confusion/testing-confound, and (b) a genuine stale documentation bug in knockback.yml worth a one-line fix.

Scope correction the finder already half-concedes: shipped per-world is {}, so this is inert on any fresh/unmodified install and only bites a deployment that (1) added a per-world entry for its combat world AND (2) A/B-tests via the GUI. Critically, it does NOT explain the reported symptom — a per-world override yields a stable wrong profile in that world, never the intermittent close-range "sprint hit reads as non-sprint" feel. It cannot cause per-hit knockback variability. Value is as a gate/testing caveat plus a doc fix, not as a root cause of the weak-knockback report. Severity low.

**SYMPTOM lens: REFUTED** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Mechanism is REAL and code-confirmed: profileFor (Snapshot.java:65) reads perWorld before defaultProfile; setGlobalProfile (Management.java:58) writes only knockback.profile; the stale per-player-override comment (knockback.yml:27-28) is verified. So a per-world entry for the arena world does mask GUI profile switches, and the docs mislead.

If the masked per-world profile were weaker, ALL hits in that world would be uniformly weak — not the subtle, hard-to-reproduce, distance/sprint-selective pattern the owner describes. Nothing in this pathway is distance-aware, close-pair-aware, or sprint-state-aware; it does not compute or attenuate per-hit velocity at all. Hand-computing 'with vs without' the mechanism yields identical per-hit shipped velocity for a given world/profile — the mechanism has zero per-hit variance to explain 'some hits.'

Its own matches_report concedes it is 'gate-level': it explains why preset A/B tests seem inconclusive ('bug survives every profile'), i.e. it obscures debugging, not why KB is weak. Requires a non-empty per-world entry (shipped {}, inert on fresh install). It cannot produce intermittent, close-range, sprint-selective weak knockback; at worst it makes ALL hits in one world uniformly reflect a masked profile, and its actual effect is to make preset A/B experiments inconclusive (a debugging-gate artifact). ### `attacker-self-state-isolation-clean` — unknown, confidence high (finder: mutual-trade-self-perturbation)

**Mechanism:** Complete negative for the axis's central hypothesis: the attacker's own received-knock state does NOT feed their outgoing knock values. KnockbackEngine consumes from the attacker EntityState only x/y/z (direction + disabled taper distance), yaw (extras), sprinting, knockbackEnchantLevel, moveSpeedAttr (KnockbackEngine.java:199-227, 309-337); attacker.vx/vy/vz and attacker.grounded() are never referenced (grounded reads are victim-only: :339, :375, :519). preAttackerState captures view.grounded() and zeros the velocity (HitRegistrationUnit.java:461-463) but both are engine-inert. A's ledger is read only when A is next a VICTIM. A's victim-role writes touch no attacker-role input: nothing on the delivery/desk path writes A's SprintWire, server sprint flag, ResetModel, CPS window or FeedbackGate (FeedbackGate keys on the OUTGOING hit's victim, HitRegistrationUnit.java:402,520). Yaw is packet-fed (PacketTap.java:77-79), unchanged by a knock. The only real victim-role->attacker-role couplings are: position displacement (see ring refinement), servo chase alignment (already merged), the reach-handicap fold when a combo is held AGAINST the attacker (comboReachHandicapScale, HitRegistrationUnit.java:587-615 — default-OFF, cancels the swing outright rather than weakening KB), and the x0.6 same-ledger write affecting only A's next RECEIVED knock (era-real).

**Trigger:** N/A — structural negative bounding the axis; any weak-KB explanation must route through position staleness, sprint verdict, or the already-merged servo/x06 couplings, not a hidden attacker-kinematics read.

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:212-230 (attacker terms), :462-516 (base uses source x/z only); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:451-464; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/EntityStates.java:42-51; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:404-449 (obligations write set); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/SprintWire.java (writers: packets, onServerClear, onBlockSprintReset, reconcile only).
