### `presend-attacker-enchant-level-zero-adopted` — bug, confidence high (finder: mutual-trade-self-perturbation)

**Mechanism:** Discovered while tracing every attacker-side read of the outgoing hit (Q1): the netty pre-send builds the attacker EntityState with knockbackEnchantLevel = 0 (the netty thread cannot read inventory) — HitRegistrationUnit.java:461-463, 10th arg literal 0 — and its comment claims 'enchant is corrected on the authoritative pass'. But a PRE_SENT/PINNED transaction is ADOPTED at the region EDBEE without recompute (KnockbackUnit.java:256-266 'the era stamped once'), the velocity event resolves to tx.carried() unchanged, and nothing in kernel/delivery or core/delivery reads enchant (grep-verified). So with a Knockback-enchanted weapon every pre-sent melee ships missing enchantLevels x extra.horizontal (0.5/level on legacy presets — KB II sprint should ship 1.9, ships 1.4-equivalent minus 1.0 of enchant push), and a NON-sprint KB-enchant hit loses the whole extras block including the flat +0.1 vertical (KnockbackEngine.java:216 gates on sprintLevels+enchantLevels>0, enchant=0 and sprint=false skips it): 0.4 h ships where era ships 0.9 h. Region-path hits (paced-out velocity, anticheat suppression, vanilla ENTITY_ATTACK) read the live held item (EntityStates.java:87-99) and ship FULL — so KB-sword knockback alternates weak/full hit-to-hit by which path fired. The obligations still gate bonus on the live enchant (KnockbackUnit.java:418), so sprint-clear/x0.6 fire for a hit whose shipped vector lacked the bonus.

**Trigger:** Attacker holds any Knockback-enchanted weapon; hit-registration fast path + pre-send-feedback on (shipped defaults) with a wired victim. Off-axis for the owner's report unless their tests involve KB swords; violates the code's own stated correction contract.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:456-463 (comment + literal 0); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:256-266 (adopt, no recompute), :418 (live enchant for obligations only); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:215-227; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/model/EntityState.java (field order confirms arg 10 = knockbackEnchantLevel); grep 'enchant' over kernel+core delivery packages: zero hits.

**Maps to the report:** Weak match: produces literal 'some hits have little knockback' inconsistency but only for KB-enchant loadouts, which the report does not mention; reported because it is a verified contract violation found on the mandated attacker-read trace.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Confirmed. Pre-send stamps enchant=0; region adopts verbatim; enchant bonus lost on pre-sent hits while region path ships full.
- Corrections: Off-axis for owner report but a real path-dependent bug.
- Severity: medium

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: MECHANISM VERIFIED. HitRegistrationUnit.java:461-463 constructs the pre-send attacker EntityState with arg 10 (knockbackEnchantLevel per EntityState.java:25 field order) as literal 0. KnockbackUnit.java:256-267 adopts tx.carried() for PRE_SENT/PINNED with no recompute. Region path (EntityStates.capture, line 42-50 / heldKnockbackLevel 87-99) reads the live held item's enchant. Obligations (KnockbackUnit:418) gate on live enchant. Default LEGACY_17: base (0.4,0.4), extra (0.5,0.1), sprintFactor 1.0 — finding's constants correct.

HAND-COMPUTE (σ=pace=taper=1, direct hit):
- NON-sprint, KB I: era horizontalBonus = 0 + 1×0.5 = 0.5 → ships base 0.4 + 0.5 = 0.9 h, +0.1 vertical. Pre-send enchant=0 AND sprint=false ⇒ sprintLevels+enchantLevels=0, the ENTIRE extras block (KnockbackEngine:216-228) is skipped ⇒ ships 0.4 h, no vertical bonus. 0.4 vs 0.9 = a >55% loss. Literally "little knockback."
- Sprint, KB II: era = base 0.4 + (1.0×0.5 + 2×0.5) = 1.9 h. Pre-send enchant=0: sprint keeps block alive, bonus = 0.5 only ⇒ 0.9 h. Loses 1.0 block. Matches "sprint hits with less knockback than they should."
- KB-sword hits alternate weak(pre-send)/full(region) hit-to-hit → the "some hits" inconsistency.

MAGNITUDE: large when it fires (halves h, drops +0.1 vy). FREQUENCY/APPLICABILITY: fires ONLY with a Knockback-enchanted weapon — with a plain sword enchant=0 in BOTH paths, zero divergence. Report never mentions KB swords and describes w-tap/blockhit plain PvP where the weak hit "seems like non-sprinting knockback"; that character is a SPRINT-flag symptom (Scenario B still ships sprint knockback, not non-sprint), orthogonal to this enchant bug. So off-axis/weak match.

Cannot refute: if the owner's play/tests involve KB swords it literally produces "some hits little/no knockback."
- Corrections: This is a real bug, not the reported symptom's likely cause. The pre-send fast path cannot read inventory so it stamps knockbackEnchantLevel=0 (HitRegistrationUnit.java:461-463), and PRE_SENT/PINNED transactions are adopted verbatim (KnockbackUnit.java:256-267) — no code in kernel/core delivery recomputes enchant. Era (and Mental's own region path via EntityStates.capture) ships the enchant extras: 0.5 h per level plus, for a non-sprint enchant hit, the whole extras block including +0.1 vertical. So every pre-sent KB-sword melee under-ships: a non-sprint KB I hit ships 0.4 h where era ships 0.9 h, and it alternates weak/full against the region path. FIX: the region adoption must recompute (or the obligations-side live enchant must correct) the horizontal/vertical enchant contribution, matching the comment's promise. HOWEVER this is off-axis for the owner's report, which describes plain w-tap/blockhit PvP with no KB enchant and a weak hit that "seems like non-sprinting knockback" — that is a sprint-flag symptom this bug does not explain (a sprint KB2 hit here still ships sprint-level knockback, not non-sprint). Fix it, but keep hunting for the sprint-flag pathway.
- Severity: medium — a genuine, code-confirmed high-magnitude bug (non-sprint KB hit ships base-only 0.4 vs era 0.9, a >55% loss; sprint KB2 loses a full block of push; also drops the flat +0.1 vertical), and it violates the code's own stated "corrected on the authoritative pass" contract. But it fires ONLY for Knockback-enchanted weapons, so for the plain-sword close-range w-tap/blockhit PvP the report centers on it produces zero divergence. Worth fixing on its own merits; low likelihood of being the reported symptom's cause.

### `stale-position-ring-direction-at-close-range` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium (finder: mutual-trade-self-perturbation)

**Mechanism:** REFINEMENT of the merged finding (CODE lens refuted it using a ~0.28 b/t strafe bound on lateral displacement). The unpriced displacement source is this axis's coupling: the ATTACKER'S OWN received knock. A player counter-attacking within ~1-3 ticks of being knocked moves at 0.4-0.9 b/t (decaying x0.91 air / x0.546 ground), 1.4-3x the strafe bound. The pre-send direction uses PositionRing.latest for BOTH parties (HitRegistrationUnit.java:452-455, 466-470), written once per owning tick (SessionService.java:352-354), so registration reads 0..1 tick (mean ~0.5) of missed displacement that era servers — reading the live in-order position at packet processing — would have seen. Geometry gates it: in a pure head-on trade B's knock on A is along the A->B axis and normalization discards it (refutation holds). But the knock A received = positional base + B's YAW-directed sprint extra; when B strafes/looks oblique (normal close circling) the extra is substantially perpendicular to the axis, giving A up to ~0.3-0.5 b of unpriced lateral displacement: at 1.5-block separation ~11-18 deg direction error, at 1.0 ~17-27 deg, sub-0.7 blocks 30-45 deg (partial inversion possible, contra the refutation's 'impossible'). Along-axis loss 5-12% typical, 15-30% sub-block, plus the hurtYaw flinch (same stale ring, HitRegistrationUnit.java:415-419) points wrong. Region recomputes use live Locations (EntityStates.java:43) and are immune — adding per-hit variance between the two paths.

**Trigger:** Pre-sent melee (default path) thrown by a player knocked in the previous 1-3 ticks in oblique/strafing close-range geometry (<1.5 blocks); worst when B's yaw was off-axis at the knock that displaced A. Head-on trades unaffected.

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/delivery/HitRegistrationUnit.java:452-470, :415-419; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:349-355; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/PositionRing.java:29-46 (one sample/tick, latest read); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/math/KnockbackEngine.java:472-492 (normalized direction — magnitude immune, direction not); knock speeds: .claude/skills/legacy-motion-physics/SKILL.md constants.

**Maps to the report:** Refines the refuted severity upward specifically for mutual close trades — exactly 'two players quite close together and hitting each other': glancing-direction knocks with mismatched flinch read as weak/no knockback, intermittent (tick-phase + geometry dependent), never at range. Still a feel-level (5-30%) effect, not the non-sprint-scale gap.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Code mechanism is real and un-refutable. Pre-send direction (HitRegistrationUnit.preAttackerState/preVictimState, :452-470) reads PositionRing.latest for both parties; the ring's ONLY writer is SessionService:353, once per owning tick, so it is a tick-boundary snapshot 0-1 tick stale (mean 0.5). Era servers process the attacker's movement packet in TCP order ahead of the attack on the main thread, so they knock from the freshest position. KnockbackEngine:472-488 normalizes the base push from the position delta, so staleness perturbs DIRECTION (magnitude is fixed by profile). A recently-knocked attacker moves 0.4-0.9 b/t (decaying x0.91), well above the ~0.28 b/t strafe bound the earlier refutation used, so its perpendicular component at close range is genuinely larger than that bound. EntityStates:43 region capture reads live Location, so the paths CAN differ. All the finding's cited facts are accurate. THREE corrections though: (1) sprint/enchant extras are yaw-directed (KnockbackEngine:224-226, 335-337, from lastYaw not position), so the direction error touches ONLY the base push, never the sprint bonus - consistent with the finding conceding it isn't the non-sprint-scale gap; (2) 'per-hit variance between the two paths' is overstated: for the dominant non-suppressed hit the pre-send is authoritative (valve consumes vanilla velocity), so the region recompute does NOT override it - the effect is a consistent stale-ring bias on pre-sends, not an A/B path race; (3) the 30-45deg high-end angles need sub-0.7-block separation (near hitbox overlap, 0.6 width) - realistic typical close trades give ~8-17deg / low-single-digit % along-axis loss. Net: a subtle, real, feel-level directional divergence.
- Corrections: Real but subtle directional divergence. The pre-send knock direction is computed from PositionRing.latest for both attacker and victim (HitRegistrationUnit.java:452-470); the ring is written only once per owning tick (SessionService.java:353, sole writer), so it is a tick-boundary snapshot 0-1 tick stale. An era server processes the attacker's movement packet in-order ahead of the attack and knocks from the fresher position; the base push is normalized from the position delta (KnockbackEngine.java:472-488), so the staleness perturbs the DIRECTION of the base horizontal push. A player attacking within 1-3 ticks of being knocked moves 0.4-0.9 b/t, whose off-axis component at close range exceeds the strafe bound the prior refutation relied on - so the earlier 'impossible' claim is too strong. Corrections to the finding: (1) the sprint/enchant EXTRA is yaw-directed (KnockbackEngine.java:224-226, 335-337, from lastYaw), NOT position-delta, so stale position never touches the sprint bonus - only the base push; this is why it cannot explain the 'non-sprinting-knockback' magnitude complaint the user described, and the finding correctly concedes that. (2) 'per-hit variance between the two paths' is overstated: for the dominant non-suppressed hit the pre-send value is authoritative and the region recompute does not override it, so the effect is a consistent stale-ring directional bias on pre-sends, not an intermittent two-path race. (3) The 30-45deg direction errors require sub-0.7-block separation (essentially hitbox overlap, width 0.6); realistic typical close trades yield ~8-17deg / low-single-digit % along-axis loss. Severity is feel-level and consistent with the user's 'very subtle, more a feeling' framing, but it is not the primary 'weak/non-sprint knockback' pathway.
- Severity: low

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Mechanism code-confirmed. Pre-send direction for both parties reads PositionRing.latest (HitRegistrationUnit:452-470), a once-per-owning-tick frozen sample (SessionService:353); the region path uses live getLocation (EntityStates:43), so the two paths genuinely diverge. KnockbackEngine:487-488 normalizes the base push, so a stale-position error rotates the shipped knock but never shrinks its magnitude. Hand-compute of the refined (self-perturbation) scenario: attacker A, knocked 1-3 ticks earlier, counter-attacks B while carrying residual velocity 0.4-0.9 b/t. Staleness 0..1 tick (mean 0.5) → missed displacement 0.2-0.45 b mean (up to 0.9 b worst-case tick phase). The along-axis part of A's received knock is discarded by normalization (the head-on refutation holds), but B's oblique/YAW-directed sprint extra leaves a perpendicular component δ_perp. Angular error = atan(δ_perp/d): d=1.5,δ0.3→~11°; d=1.0→~17°; d=0.7,δ0.4→~30°. Along-axis (separation) loss = 1-cos θ: ~2% at 11°, ~4% at 17°, 8-13% at 23-30°, up to ~29% sub-block; partial inversion only for the rare >45° sub-0.7-block near-full-staleness case. Same speed, wrong bearing → victim shoved partly sideways, separation rate down, reads as "weak." Intermittent because it needs (a) attacker mid-decay from a recent knock, (b) oblique geometry, (c) near-max tick-phase staleness, (d) close range simultaneously — exactly a mutual close trade, and exactly "hard to reproduce." NOT refuted: it plausibly produces the subtle close-range feel. But it CANNOT produce the literal "reads as non-sprinting knockback" scale — that requires a wrong magnitude, and magnitude is provably immune here; even the sub-block extreme (~29%) is far short of the ~2x sprint/non-sprint gap. So it matches the "subtle feeling" half of the report, not the dramatic half.
- Corrections: Refined finding survives as a low-severity, feel-level contributor confined to close mutual trades. Confirmed: both pre-send positions come from a once-per-tick frozen PositionRing sample while the region path uses live locations, and the base push is normalized so only DIRECTION (not magnitude) is corrupted. The dominant unpriced displacement is the attacker's own recently-received knock; normalization discards its along-axis part but keeps the perpendicular part from the victim's oblique yaw-directed sprint extra. Realistic close-trade geometry yields ~11-17 deg direction error (2-4% separation loss) typically, ~23-30 deg (8-13%) sub-block, with >45 deg partial inversion only in a rare confluence (sub-0.7-block + near-full tick-phase staleness + high perpendicular fraction). Correction to the finding's own numbers: "5-12% typical" is slightly optimistic — closer to 2-8% for d=1.0-1.5; "15-30% sub-block" is right for the worst geometry. The hurtYaw flinch reads the same stale ring, adding a cosmetic wrong-direction cue. This is a real divergence from era (era reads live in-order position at packet processing), adds genuine pre-send-vs-region per-hit variance, and matches the "subtle, especially close, hard to reproduce" report — but it does NOT and cannot reproduce the "non-sprinting knockback" magnitude claim, because magnitude is immune to this mechanism.
- Severity: low

### `knock-liftoff-facing-push-stale-view-sprint` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium (finder: mutual-trade-self-perturbation)

**Mechanism:** GroundFsm decides the era 0.2 sprint facing push (and Jump Boost) at a rising liftoff from view.sprinting — the PlayerView frozen at session-tick publish (PacketTap.java:112-119 builds ViewSlice from the view; GroundFsm.java:91-100 applies the push) — even though the arrival-order truth (SprintWire) sits on the SAME connection Domain and is never consulted. view.sprinting is the live server flag frozen >=1 tick ago (SessionService.java:535), and after A's own accepted bonus hit that flag itself lags era truth by Mental's deferred clear (EDBEE +1-2 ticks, KnockbackUnit.java:435-447) plus one publish tick. Era servers ran the jump bookkeeping in-order against the live flag, which attack() had already cleared synchronously. Divergent windows, both signs: (a) phantom push — A lands a bonus hit at T and jump-resets at T+1..T+3 without re-engaging (s-tap, dropped W, or a 1.21.2+ client that never re-sends START): era stamps NO push; Mental's still-true view stamps +0.2 along A's yaw (toward B in a trade) into A's ledger, so B's NEXT knock on A folds a ~0.2 x friction(0.5) = 0.1 h opposing residual — B's hit lands ~25% of base weaker than era. (b) missing push — A's re-engage START arrives in the same tick as the jump packet: wire is true instantly, view lags a tick, push omitted — B's next knock stronger than era. The knock-induced rising liftoff itself stamping 0.42+push is era-real (the measured 1.8.9 combo-vy chain IS that stamp) — only the flag SOURCE diverges.

**Trigger:** Mutual close trade on any preset with friction >= 0.5 (legacy-1.7/1.8, kohi, minehq, badlion, mmc, lunar — liftoffs write the ledger regardless of combos flag): the opponent's hits land within the ~10-tick residual life of a mis-stamped jump-reset. Fires at jump-reset cadence; negligible at friction 0.1 (velt/signature).

**Evidence:** kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/GroundFsm.java:91-100 (view.sprinting selects the push); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/PacketTap.java:112-119 (ViewSlice from view, wire ignored; domain.sprint() available on the same Domain at :85); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:531-541 (view.sprinting = live flag at publish); core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:435-447 (deferred clear extends stale-true); kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/ledger/MotionLedger.java:76-85 (push folded with launch drag); era ordering: .claude/skills/era-accuracy/SKILL.md:29-39, legacy-motion-physics:58-67.

**Maps to the report:** Contributes the 'hitting each other' texture: the phantom-push branch makes the OPPONENT'S next hit read ~0.1 h weak precisely in jump-reset-heavy close trades, intermittent by sprint-toggle phase — but capped at ~25% of base and sign-alternating, so a secondary contributor, not the headline.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: The finding's code claims check out: GroundFsm applies the +0.2 sprint-jump push from view.sprinting() (GroundFsm:96, ViewSlice at PacketTap:117-118), the SprintWire on the same domain is unconsulted for this decision, view.sprinting()==player.isSprinting() at publish (SessionService:535), and the attack defers setSprinting(false) (KnockbackUnit:435-447). The engine folds the victim residual (KnockbackEngine:32 base=victimMotion×friction−push), so A's ledger push can weaken B's next knock. BUT the finding misattributes the mechanism. The MotionLedger's contract (and legacy-motion-physics) is to MIRROR the real entity's actual motion so a later knock folds the physically-correct residual. Vanilla's EntityLivingBase.jump() applies the +0.2 push from the REAL player.isSprinting() flag. Because Mental DEFERS setSprinting(false), the REAL server flag stays stale-true, so vanilla's OWN jump() on Mental's server ALSO stamps the phantom push onto the real entity. view.sprinting() reads that same real flag — so GroundFsm keying the push on it correctly reproduces what the real body did; ledger and reality agree. The finding's proposed fix (consult the synchronously-cleared wire) would make the ledger record 'no push' while the real entity HAS one, desyncing the ledger from reality and making B's delivered knock physically wrong (failing to cancel A's real momentum toward B) — a regression, not a fix. Any genuine era-divergence is upstream: the deferred setSprinting(false) leaving the real flag stale so a phantom push occurs that a pristine synchronous-clear 1.8 server would deny — a different, intentional, wire-guarded location. So the cited GroundFsm/PacketTap source-choice is era-correct mirroring, not the defect.
- Corrections: The cited mechanism (GroundFsm keying the liftoff push on view.sprinting instead of the wire) is NOT a bug: view.sprinting()==player.isSprinting(), the same flag vanilla's jump() reads, so the ledger correctly mirrors the real entity's motion — which, on Mental's server, genuinely received the push because the deferred setSprinting(false) left the real flag stale-true and vanilla's own jump() stamped it. Switching the push to the SprintWire (as the finding proposes) would desync the ledger from reality and corrupt B's delivered knock. If a real, small era-divergence exists, it is the DIFFERENT, upstream, intentional decision: the deferred setSprinting(false) (KnockbackUnit:435-447) leaving the real player flag stale for a publish/execution window, causing the real entity to get a phantom sprint-jump push a pristine synchronous-clear 1.8 server would deny. That divergence is bounded (~0.2 push decaying to ~0.05–0.1 folded residual, ~10–12% not ~25% weaker), sign-alternating, and deliberately wire-guarded for re-engagement (the code re-consults the wire at execution time to honor F2 re-engage). It is not fixable at the finding's cited location. As written — locating the defect in GroundFsm/PacketTap and prescribing 'consult the wire' — the finding is refuted.
- Severity: low

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: All cited code verified. GroundFsm.java:96 gates the 0.2 sprint facing push on view.sprinting(); PacketTap.viewSlice (112-118) builds ViewSlice from the frozen view and never consults domain.sprint(), the SprintWire on the SAME Domain (present at :76/:85). SessionService:535 freezes player.isSprinting() into the view. KnockbackUnit:432-448 clears the wire synchronously but DEFERS the real setSprinting(false) via scheduling.runOn, so the Bukkit flag — and the view frozen from it — lags era's synchronous attack-time clear by the deferred-execution tick plus one publish tick. MotionLedger:76-85 folds the push into ledger horizontals (carried.vx()*launchDrag + facingPushX). Constants confirmed: SPRINT_JUMP_PUSH=0.2, slip=0.6, air drag=0.91.

Concrete scenario (mutual close trade, legacy-1.8/kohi/minehq/badlion/mmc/lunar, friction>=0.5): A lands a bonus hit (era clears sprint synchronously), jump-resets 1-3 ticks later without re-engaging W (dropped W / s-tap / 1.21.2+ client that never re-sends START). Mental's still-true frozen view stamps +0.2 along A's yaw = toward B into A's ledger. Airborne decay ×0.91: T=0.20, T+1=0.182, T+2=0.166. B's knock on A lands within the residual window and pushes A AWAY from B while the residual points TOWARD B — they oppose. Against a fresh ~0.4-0.5 h directional knock, a ~0.15 opposing residual removes ~25-30% of A's travel: "victim doesn't really move back."

Magnitude real but capped (~25%) and sign-alternating (branch b, same-tick re-engage, omits the push and strengthens). Frequency gated on a specific conjunction but jump-resets are dense in close trades and the 1.21.2+ no-re-START caveat makes the no-re-engage precondition common on modern clients. Cannot be refuted: the code path exists, the arithmetic is favorable, and it produces exactly the intermittent, phase-dependent weak-knockback texture in the report — as a secondary contributor.
- Severity: low-medium — a genuine, era-divergent contributor but capped at ~25% of the affected horizontal knock, sign-alternating, and firing only at the jump-reset/clear-lag conjunction; secondary to the headline weak-KB pathway, not the primary cause.

### `reconcile-clear-interleave-clean-beyond-known` — unknown, confidence high (finder: mutual-trade-self-perturbation)

**Mechanism:** Q2 negative result extending the two merged sprint findings: no ADDITIONAL weak-sprint interleaving exists between reconcile, the deferred clear, and START arrival. Traced full mutual w-tap timeline: A hits at T (verdict stamped); wire onServerClear(asOf=T) at EDBEE T+1/T+2; deferred setSprinting(false) same window (skip-guarded on wire re-arm, KnockbackUnit.java:442-446); view publishes the cleared flag at T+2/T+3. The dangerous inversions are both guarded: (a) a stale-TRUE view cannot resurrect the cleared wire, because reconcile requires now - lastWrite >= 3 quiet ticks (SPRINT_WIRE_QUIET_TICKS=3, PacketTap.java:39,85; SprintWire.java:172-174) and the clear stamps lastWrite=now (SprintWire.java:108), so the wire is quiet-locked past the <=2-tick stale-true window — no phantom sprint. (b) a stale-FALSE view cannot destroy a fresh re-engage: a START in [T+1, T+3] stamps lastWrite inside the quiet window, so reconcile no-ops until the view has caught up to the vanilla-applied true flag. Note reconcile's adopt/seed itself stamps lastWrite=now (SprintWire.java:170,174), so back-to-back movement packets cannot adopt twice inside a window. Being KNOCKED contributes nothing: no victim-role writer of the wire or the server flag exists. The residual per-hit weak-sprint probability at 10-14 CPS therefore remains exactly the two merged mechanisms: the same-tick retro-clear (per-hit dice, jitter-dependent, ~5-30% as verified) and the 1.21.2+ hold-sprint signal loss (deterministic until resync).

**Trigger:** N/A — clean negative; the quiet window (3) strictly exceeding the maximum view-publish lag (2) is the load-bearing margin. An operator cannot lower it (constant, not config).

**Evidence:** core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/rim/PacketTap.java:38-39, 80-86; kernel/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/kernel/wire/SprintWire.java:100-110, 167-178; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/knockback/KnockbackUnit.java:425-448; core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/session/SessionService.java:75-76 (same constant on the session side).

### `cadence-spoof-client-dichotomy-default-off` — config-dependent, confidence high (finder: cadence-spoof-coupling)

**Mechanism:** ATTACK_COOLDOWN spoofs attack_speed to 1024.0 both server-side (AttackChargeReset.applyNow, core/src/main/java/me/vexmc/mental/v5/feature/cadence/AttackChargeReset.java:85-98) and on the wire (CooldownSpoofListener.java:44; CooldownSpoof.java:58-76 rewrites/injects the receiver's own UPDATE_ATTRIBUTES). getAttackStrengthScale then reads 1.0 on every click, so the modern client's shared attack() prediction branch (SYNOPSIS.md:306-336, :382) fires on EVERY bonus click: (a) the clicker's own motion ×0.6 + local un-sprint — a counter-clicking victim erases their received horizontal 0.6^n, era-authentic close-trade 'nobody moves back'; (b) the un-sprint emits STOP (after the ATTACK) + next-tick START, constantly re-arming SprintWire after Mental's post-hit clear — sprint hits mostly KEEP the bonus. Spoof OFF (the DEFAULT — Feature.java:166-174 defaultEnabled=false, config.yml:57): at spam CPS neither runs (charge>0.9 gate, SYNOPSIS.md:309-310,:355; legacy-combat.md:97-101) — received KB reads FULLER than era, but no client START ever re-arms Mental's charge-blind post-hit clear (round-1 no-reengage divergence ACTIVE). Also: spoof OFF splits the population by client version — legacy/Via 1.7-1.8 clients still self-×0.6 and auto-re-arm every hit while modern clients do neither, so the same trade feels different per player.

**Trigger:** Which half fires is decided solely by modules.attack-cooldown. ON: mutual close trade, both sprint-clicking — each received knock cut 0.6 per counter-click (era-real feel, easily misread as engine weakness). OFF (default): modern-client attackers lose the sprint bonus on hits 2..n after Mental's clear (no STOP/START at spam CPS); legacy-client opponents in the same trade do not — per-player asymmetric feel.

**Evidence:** AttackCooldownUnit.java:20-92 (four halves, scope lifecycle); AttackChargeReset.java:44,85-98 (server base 1024 on enable/join/respawn/world-change); CooldownSpoof.java:37-43 (1024.0 = registered ceiling, delay ~0.02 ticks); CooldownSpoofListener.java:33-49; Feature.java:166-174 + core/src/main/resources/config.yml:57 (default false); SYNOPSIS.md:306-310 (kbAttack=isSprinting&&scale>0.9), :330-343 (×0.6 + setSprinting(false) inside amount>0), :382 (prediction reproduces slowdown+sprint-reset), :138 (legacy client unconditional); legacy-combat.md:97-101 ('modern clients only do the client-side part at >=90% charge'); compendium:249-263 (0.6^clicks; STOP same-flush after ATTACK, re-engage entity-action).

**Maps to the report:** Both halves map: spoof ON reproduces 'little to no knockback when close and hitting each other' at era-authentic full strength (victim's own counter-clicks erase the flight — server wire correct); spoof OFF (default) produces 'sprint hits sometimes have less knockback' via the never-re-armed clear, plus the per-client-version asymmetry that makes the feel inconsistent and unpinnable. Which half the owner lives in is one config key — must be checked on the DEPLOYED config before attributing close-trade weakness to the engine.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Both halves are code-confirmed and each reproduces part of the report; which fires is genuinely gated by modules.attack-cooldown (default OFF, verified Feature.java:166-174 + config.yml:57) and by client version.

DEFAULT config (spoof OFF) — the half the owner most likely lives in — reproduces the report almost verbatim. Mental's fast path clears the attacker's sprint flag after a bonus hit (mirroring vanilla setSprinting(false)) and then waits for a fresh client START to re-arm SprintWire. A modern client spam-clicking reads attack-charge <0.9, so its attack() NEVER runs the sprint-reset (SYNOPSIS:330-343; legacy-combat.md:97-101) and therefore never emits the STOP→START that would re-arm Mental. Result: hits 2..n read non-sprinting and Mental ships the 0.4 base knock instead of the 0.9 sprint knock. That is EXACTLY the owner's words "it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback" and "sprint hits sometimes have less knockback than they should." Magnitude: horizontal ~0.9→~0.4 (loses the +0.5 kbAttack bonus, roughly halved) — very visible "doesn't really move back," worst at close range where there is no residual to carry. Frequency: common in sprint-spam PvP for modern clients, intermittent because any incidental sprint re-toggle (collision, key release, w-tap) re-arms it — so it is a "feeling," hard to pin. Legacy/Via clients in the same server re-arm every hit (unconditional reset, SYNOPSIS:138), so they keep full sprint KB → per-player asymmetric feel that makes it unpinnable.

Spoof ON (non-default) reproduces the "close mutual trade, nobody moves back" via era-authentic 0.6^clicks counter-click erasure — real but era-correct, and not the default.

The mechanism plausibly produces multiple parts of the report; cannot refute.
- Corrections: Emphasis correction: the reproducing half on the DEFAULT config is (b), and it is a divergence-from-era (Mental clears sprint post-hit but the modern client's charge-gated re-engage never re-arms SprintWire at spam CPS, so non-sprint KB ships where era ships sprint KB). Half (a) requires attack-cooldown ON and is era-real, not a bug. So the owner's symptom on stock config is the modern-client no-reengage divergence surfacing as "non-sprinting knockback," amplified into a per-player asymmetry because legacy/Via clients re-arm every hit. Config key must be checked on the DEPLOYED config, but note the default OFF is the state that reproduces the report — this is not primarily an era-authentic counter-click effect. It overlaps the round-1 no-reengage divergence; the finding's added value is the client-version split and the config gate, not a new engine mechanism.
- Severity: medium

### `no-reengage-premise-corrected-spoof-cures-it` — divergence-from-era, confidence medium (finder: cadence-spoof-coupling)

**Mechanism:** Refines round-1 'modern-client-no-reengage-after-clear' (merged divergence-from-era). Its premise — '1.21.2+ clients REMOVED the attack sprint interruption' — is contradicted by the repo's own 26.1.2 decompile: SYNOPSIS.md:336 shows setSprinting(false) in Player.causeExtraKnockback with the note 'sprint reset survives to 2026', :382 states client prediction reproduces 'slowdown, sprint-reset', and :431 'client predicts the reset in all three'. The real gate is charge>0.9 (SYNOPSIS.md:309-310,:355) — the no-STOP/START observable is CPS-dependent, not version-removed: an unspoofed modern client at spam CPS never fires the un-sprint, but a slow full-charge clicker DOES re-arm era-style. Consequence: enabling ATTACK_COOLDOWN pins scale at 1.0 (CooldownSpoof.java:37-43), the prediction un-sprint fires every bonus click, STOP/START crosses the wire, SprintWire re-arms — the divergence is effectively CURED by the spoof; the shipped default-OFF is what leaves modern-client sprint hits plain after Mental's clear (KnockbackUnit.java:425-447). Caveat: an autosprint mod that re-sets the flag within the same client tick as the prediction's clear would still emit no delta, spoof or not.

**Trigger:** Modern-client attacker, W held, spam CPS, attack-cooldown OFF: hits 2..n plain (round-1 mechanism, stands). Same attacker with attack-cooldown ON: every bonus click cycles STOP/START and re-arms — sprint KB restored to era cadence. Slow (full-charge) clickers re-arm even unspoofed.

**Evidence:** SYNOPSIS.md:306-310, :330-343 (26.1.2 decompile: gate + reset both present), :354-355, :382, :431; CooldownSpoof.java:37-43 (delay ~0.02 ticks — scale 1.0 even at ticker=0, so the miss-penalty ticker reset can't drop it); legacy-combat.md:97-101; round-1 doc lines 1092-1116 (the finding and its verifier lenses — neither cited a client decompile for the 1.21.2-removal claim; evidence lines were Mental code only).

**Maps to the report:** Sharpens the round-1 finding's frequency profile: the plain-hit divergence is strictly a high-CPS phenomenon on ANY modern client (not a 1.21.2+ cliff), and it is config-coupled — deployments running attack-cooldown ON should NOT exhibit it at all. Gives the owner a live A/B: toggle attack-cooldown and re-test sprint-hit KB consistency; if weakness persists with it ON, the cause is elsewhere (retro-clear bug or engine).

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: I tried to refute this refinement and could not; the repo's own code and docs confirm every checkable claim.

1) Round-1's premise ("1.21.2+ clients REMOVED the attack sprint interruption") is demonstrably wrong. legacy-combat.md:97-101 states plainly: "All eras un-sprint the attacker after a bonus-knockback hit and the client re-sprints next tick with the key held; modern clients only do the client-side part of this at >=90% charge." SYNOPSIS.md:336 ("sprint reset survives to 2026"), :431 ("client predicts the reset in all three") corroborate. So the real gate is charge>0.9 (SYNOPSIS:309-310,:355), not a version cliff. The finding's central correction is CONFIRMED by the repo's own ground truth.

2) CPS-dependence is real: at spam CPS attackStrengthTicker resets every click (onAttack + miss, SYNOPSIS:354), so scale<0.9, so the client's causeExtraKnockback amount=0 (players have ATTACK_KNOCKBACK=0), so no client setSprinting(false), so no STOP/START crosses the wire, so SprintWire never re-arms (onSprintStart is the only re-arm; onServerClear drops sprinting/armed; reconcile re-seeds from Mental's own cleared flag). Hits 2..n read verdictAt=false -> plain. Confirmed in SprintWire.java:74-110,167-178 and KnockbackUnit.java:404-448.

3) CooldownSpoof pins client scale to 1.0 (attack_speed=1024 -> delay ~0.02 tick -> getAttackStrengthScale always 1.0, :37-43,:16-20). So with ATTACK_COOLDOWN ON the client fires setSprinting(false) every sprinting click -> STOP -> re-sprint-next-tick START (legacy-combat.md confirms "client re-sprints next tick with key held") -> onSprintStart -> wire re-arms -> era sprint KB restored. The cure mechanism is sound.

4) Default-OFF (CADENCE family) leaves it uncured -> shipped behavior exhibits the divergence. Correct.

The one unverifiable link (does the client actually emit a wire STOP+START delta around the prediction) is answered in Mental's favor by legacy-combat.md's own statement that the re-sprint crosses the wire, AND is honestly flagged for autosprint clients where no delta ever fires. Caveat is UNDERSTATED, not wrong: round-1 (doc:1110) calls autosprint "near-universal in modern PvP"; on those clients neither spoof nor default helps, so "effectively CURED" reaches only the non-autosprint population.

Classification divergence-from-era matches the round-1 merge and the underlying mechanic.
- Corrections: The finding stands: not refuted. Its correction of round-1 is confirmed by the repo's OWN ground truth — legacy-combat.md:97-101 ("modern clients only do the client-side part of [the sprint-reset re-arm] at >=90% charge") and SYNOPSIS.md:336/:431 — so the "1.21.2 removed the interruption" premise was wrong and the true gate is charge>0.9, making the plain-hit divergence a CPS phenomenon on any modern client, not a version cliff. The spoof-cure mechanism is mechanistically sound (CooldownSpoof.java:37-43 pins client scale to 1.0 -> setSprinting(false) fires every sprinting click -> STOP/START crosses the wire -> SprintWire.onSprintStart re-arms; SprintWire.java:74-110,192-198 back this).

Two refinements, both STRENGTHENING the finding, not refuting it:
(a) The autosprint caveat is UNDERSTATED. Round-1's own analysis (doc:1110) and legacy-combat context treat autosprint/toggle-sprint as near-universal in modern PvP; on those clients the sprint flag is re-set within the same client tick so NO wire delta fires regardless of charge — so the ATTACK_COOLDOWN spoof does NOT cure them. "Effectively CURED" is therefore true only for the non-autosprint sub-population. The A/B test the finding proposes remains valid but should expect residual weakness on autosprint clients even with the spoof ON.
(b) Classification: divergence-from-era is correct for the underlying mechanic; the cure being config-coupled makes the MITIGATION config-dependent, but the defect itself (unspoofed shipped default) is a genuine era divergence.

No code change is asserted or needed by this finding; it is a diagnostic sharpening of an already-merged divergence.
- Severity: Medium. The underlying per-hit KB loss is large (~0.5 b/t horizontal, ~56%, plus the +0.1 vertical pop lost — a full sprint->plain downgrade, per round-1 hand-computation on LEGACY_17 and all full-sprint presets), and frequency is HIGH-but-intermittent on the affected population (modern/autosprint clients holding W, spam-clicking at close range). But this is the SAME divergence already catalogued in round-1; the finding's own added value is diagnostic (corrected frequency profile + a live A/B), and its proposed mitigation (toggle ATTACK_COOLDOWN ON) is only PARTIAL — it cures non-autosprint attackers but autosprint/toggle-sprint clients (widespread in modern PvP) emit no STOP/START delta and stay divergent spoof-or-not.

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `config-dependent`

- Reasoning: Mechanism verified coherent against cited evidence. SYNOPSIS:309-310 confirms kbAttack (and thus the causeExtraKnockback amount>0 that fires setSprinting(false)) requires charge>0.9; :336/:382/:431 confirm the reset+client-prediction survive to 26.1.2. So a spam-CPS modern client, whose attackStrengthTicker resets every click, never reaches full charge, never predicts the un-sprint, and emits no STOP/START. SprintWire.onServerClear drops sprinting/armed after Mental's first sprint hit (KnockbackUnit:432-434), and since Mental also sets the server flag false (line 446), reconcile won't re-seed sprinting=true, and only an actual onSprintStart re-arms. Net: hits 2..n on a held-sprint spam-clicker ship the non-sprint knock. Hand-computed magnitude (SYNOPSIS:348-349, era profile Mental ships): sprint hit ~0.9 horizontal vs non-sprint ~0.4 — a ~2x drop, exactly "the non-sprinting knockback" the owner named verbatim. CooldownSpoof:43 pins client scale to 1.0, so with ATTACK_COOLDOWN ON every click is full-charge, the prediction fires the un-sprint+re-sprint, START crosses the wire, and the wire re-arms every hit — the divergence is cured. Default is OFF, so shipped deployments exhibit it. Frequency is intermittent: real combat is full of re-arm sources (w-taps=STOP+START, horizontal collisions, strafe restarts), which mask it; it bites only when sprint is held steady across several spam clicks — typical at close range where you stand and click rather than move. That intermittency + CPS/config dependence matches "subtle, hard to reproduce, a feeling." Cannot be refuted: it plausibly produces the "sprint hits sometimes have less KB than they should" and "non-sprinting knockback" parts of the report.
- Corrections: The finding's correction of the round-1 premise is sound: the sprint reset is NOT version-removed at 1.21.2 (SYNOPSIS:336) — the observable is gated on charge>0.9 (:309-310), so it is CPS-dependent. One era-nuance to flag on the classification: at spam CPS with continuous held sprint, shipping the non-sprint knock on hits 2..n is arguably ERA-FAITHFUL (1.8 also required a w-tap re-engage to re-arm sprint KB; continuous hold gave plain hits after the first). The genuine divergence is that a modern vanilla client AUTO re-arms at full charge via its own un-sprint+re-sprint prediction (no manual w-tap), which the owner's muscle memory expects; Mental honors that only when the client actually emits START, and at spam CPS it does not. So the symptom is best framed as config-dependent (ATTACK_COOLDOWN OFF exhibits, ON cures) layered over a real-but-subtle modern-vs-era re-arm-cadence difference — not a plain engine bug. The A/B the finding hands the owner (toggle attack-cooldown, re-test sprint-hit consistency) is the correct next diagnostic.
- Severity: moderate

### `cadence-spoof-amplifies-same-tick-retro-clear` — config-dependent, confidence medium (finder: cadence-spoof-coupling)

**Mechanism:** Refines round-1 'same-tick-reengage-retro-clear' (bug, confirmed): SprintWire.onServerClear no-ops only for STRICTLY newer writes (SprintWire.java:100-110), so a re-arm START landing in the same server tick as its ATTACK is retro-destroyed by the deferred desk clear (KnockbackUnit.java:404-448), leaving both wire and server flag false with no recovery signal. Round-1 bounded the exposure to '<=1.21.1 auto-cycle clients and fast w-taps'. With ATTACK_COOLDOWN ON the exposure widens to the ENTIRE modern-client population at every CPS: the spoof makes every bonus click emit the auto STOP(+next-tick START) cycle (SYNOPSIS.md:336,:382 with scale pinned 1.0), so every hit of every sprinting attacker rolls the network-bunching dice (two client-tick flushes delivered in one server tick), and once eaten the plain state persists until a genuine input change. The era-feel feature thus INCREASES the population-wide hit rate of a confirmed weak-KB bug — partially offsetting the cure in the sibling finding: spoof-ON trades a deterministic divergence (never re-arm at spam CPS) for a probabilistic bug (jitter-dependent retro-clear, every hit).

**Trigger:** attack-cooldown ON + any sprinting modern-client attacker landing repeated hits; network jitter bunches the auto-re-arm START into the ATTACK's server tick — subsequent hits ship plain KB until a real W-release/re-press. Higher CPS and unstable ping raise the roll count.

**Evidence:** SprintWire.java:100-110 (strictly-greater guard; kernel/src/main/java path per round-1 citations); KnockbackUnit.java:404-448 (deferred clear consults the poisoned wire); round-1 doc lines 120-128 (mechanism + '<=1.21.1 EVERY hit... rolls this dice' — the spoof extends this to all modern clients); SYNOPSIS.md:336,:382 (prediction un-sprint exists on 26.1.2, charge-gated); CooldownSpoof.java:37-43 (gate pinned open).

**Maps to the report:** Explains why the report says the bug exists 'as far back as I can remember' and stays feel-level on BOTH sides of the config: with the spoof off, the deterministic no-reengage divergence bites; with it on, this probabilistic race bites instead — no config state is fully clean until the retro-clear guard is fixed, which matches 'very subtle and hard to reproduce'.

**CODE lens: REFUTED** — era call: `divergence-from-era`

- Reasoning: Verified all cited files. CooldownSpoof.java only rewrites the attack_speed attribute (1024.0) in UPDATE_ATTRIBUTES; it never touches SprintWire and contains NO gate at lines 37-43 (that range is the FULL_CHARGE constant + javadoc). The real feature gate is Feature.ATTACK_COOLDOWN, default-OFF CADENCE family (AttackCooldownUnit:60-92). So the "gate pinned open" citation is wrong. The retro-clear the finding builds on IS real (SprintWire:103 strictly-greater guard eats a same-tick START) but that is round-1's own confirmed finding, not this one's contribution. The finding's NEW claim — that the spoof widens the retro-clear bug to "the ENTIRE modern-client population at every CPS" via an "auto STOP+START cycle" — is refuted by round-1's own premises: (a) the client-side attack un-sprint runs only at charge>0.9 (line 772), so the spoof's effect exists ONLY on <=1.21.1 clients where that interruption code is present; (b) 1.21.2+ clients REMOVED the attack sprint-interruption entirely (lines 132/1094/1110), so at ANY charge they emit no re-arm START — the spoof changes charge, not the removed client code, and thus creates nothing for the retro-clear to eat. The owner tests on 1.21.4+ (line 134/1096) — exactly the population where the spoof gives zero amplification. On <=1.21.1 the widening is only from full-charge hits (which already trigger the cycle WITHOUT the spoof) to extra spam-clicks: a modest frequency bump for one client tier, not a population-wide expansion. The finding is a re-narration of round-1's same-tick-reengage-retro-clear + modern-client-no-reengage findings with an overstated, internally self-contradictory coupling claim and a mis-cited gate.
- Corrections: Accurate scope: CooldownSpoof is a default-OFF, correctly-gated packet mutator (attack_speed->1024.0) with no defect and no link to SprintWire. When ATTACK_COOLDOWN is enabled, the spoof does make <=1.21.1 clients read every click as full charge, so their partial-charge spam-clicks now also trigger the client attack un-sprint (STOP + next-tick START), marginally increasing how often the real round-1 retro-clear race (SprintWire:103 same-tick clear) can be rolled FOR THAT CLIENT TIER. But it does NOT widen the bug to modern clients: 1.21.2+ clients (incl. the owner's 1.21.4+ test population and autosprint mods) emit no attack un-sprint cycle at any charge, so the spoof produces no re-arm START and cannot amplify the retro-clear there. The genuine underlying defect is round-1's same-tick-reengage-retro-clear (a divergence from era arrival-order ordering), independent of this feature; the CooldownSpoof-amplification thesis as stated ("entire modern-client population at every CPS") is refuted and its "gate pinned open at CooldownSpoof:37-43" citation points at a constant, not a gate.
- Severity: low

**SYMPTOM lens: STANDS** — era call: `bug`

- Reasoning: Mechanism verified in code. SprintWire.java:103 no-ops the deferred desk clear only for STRICTLY newer writes (`lastWrite.value() > asOf.value()`); a re-arm START whose stamp EQUALS the ATTACK's asOf (same server tick) fails the guard and falls through to the clear at :108, leaving sprinting=false/armed=false. Line 98's own comment concedes this same-tick residual is "accepted" as "physically implausible" — but network jitter bunching two client-tick flushes into one server tick makes it real. KnockbackUnit.java:432-434 feeds this poisoned wire via onServerClear(asOf).

CooldownSpoof.java pins client attack-strength scale to 1.0, so every spammed click renders as a full-charge sprint attack CLIENT-side and fires the client sprint-reset prediction (STOP then next-tick START) — the STOP/START cycle whose START can bunch. Without the spoof an under-charged spam click is not a client sprint-attack, emits no cycle, and the wire stays continuously sprinting (no roll). So the spoof genuinely broadens who rolls the dice, from w-tap/blockhit/auto-cycle clients to the whole modern population at every CPS.

Symptom match, hand-computed (SYNOPSIS.md:349): a poisoned next-hit ships non-sprint KB — modern h≈0.4 vs sprint 0.7; legacy 0.4 vs 0.9 (roughly half). This is verbatim the owner's "it seems like the knockback is the non-sprinting knockback." Frequency is per-hit, jitter-dependent, probabilistic → "very subtle, hard to reproduce, more a feeling." Owner's w-tap/blockhit/close-range emphasis fits: those techniques generate the STOP/START re-arm cycles, and close high-CPS trades raise the roll count. "As far back as I can remember" fits a structural strictly-greater guard (the deprecated onServerClear() retro-cleared unconditionally pre-2.4.1; the guarded form still leaves the same-tick hole). Cannot be refuted — it plausibly produces the exact reported symptom.

era_call=bug: the retro-clear ships non-era KB (the era applied packets in arrival order; a re-armed sprint would register), a genuine defect; the CADENCE spoof only modulates its exposure rate, so the config-coupling is real but the underlying wrongness is a bug, not era-truth.
- Corrections: The defect is a genuine bug (SprintWire.java:103 strictly-greater guard drops a same-tick re-arm START); CooldownSpoof (CADENCE, default-OFF) amplifies its exposure but is not the root cause. Fix direction: treat a same-tick re-arm START as surviving the deferred clear — change the guard to `>=` asOf, or track the last START stamp separately so a START at or after the ATTACK tick is never retro-cleared. Note the config-dependence is only in FREQUENCY of exposure; the base bug still bites w-tappers/blockhitters and <=1.21.1 auto-cycle clients with the spoof off.
- Severity: medium

### `charge-blind-pipeline-era-style-clean` — era-real, confidence high (finder: cadence-spoof-coupling)

**Mechanism:** Q4 negative result (clean): Mental's hit pipeline ignores attack charge entirely, era-style, regardless of the ATTACK_COOLDOWN toggle. The kernel contains zero attackStrength/cooldown/charge references (grep over kernel/src/main/java: no matches); DamageShaper composes the amount off the attribute base with no cooldown term (legacy-combat.md:73 — 'the 1.9 charge meter is never consulted, structurally'); the KnockbackEngine's sprint extra is driven only by the stamped SprintVerdict, never a charge scale. AttackChargeReset is inert when the feature is OFF (Reconciler.java:59-88 — assemble only on disabled→enabled). Divergence set vs modern vanilla: every partial-charge fast-path hit ships FULL era damage and the charge-blind sprint bonus where vanilla Player.attack would ramp damage 0.2+t^2*0.8 and withhold the sprint bonus at charge<=0.9 (SYNOPSIS.md:308-310) — direction is strictly MORE knockback/damage, so charge handling cannot produce the reported weakness. Residual nuance: hits that fall through to the vanilla damage path with the feature OFF (fast-path off, Folia non-player, round-1 fallthroughs) take vanilla's charge-SCALED damage (tiny amounts at spam CPS → more mid-invuln equal-or-weaker ignores), though Mental's EDBEE recompute still ships charge-blind KB when the hit is accepted.

**Trigger:** No trigger — this sub-area is clean for the fast path. The nuance arm needs fast-path OFF (non-default) plus spam CPS: fallthrough hits' vanilla-scaled damage amounts get eaten by the hurt-window difference rule slightly more often than era's full-damage clicks, an ignore (zero knock) either way.

**Evidence:** legacy-combat.md:73 (fast path bypasses Player#attack; amount off attribute base); AttackChargeReset.java:20-33 (docs: fast path 'structurally defeated'; vanilla path is the only charge-scaled one); kernel grep negative (no charge vocabulary anywhere in kernel/src/main/java); SYNOPSIS.md:304-326 (vanilla charge ramp + kbAttack gate that Mental never consults); Reconciler.java:59-88 (zero-touch when off).

**Maps to the report:** Does not match — reported to close the axis question: partial-charge modern-vanilla hits are never scaled down anywhere in Mental's own pipeline, so 'weak sprint hits' cannot come from charge scaling; the sprint-verdict machinery (round-1 findings) remains the live suspect.

**CODE lens: STANDS** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: Adversarial verification could not refute this negative-result finding; every citation holds. Kernel grep for charge/cooldown/attackStrength vocabulary returns zero matches (exit 1). DamageShaper.compose builds the amount off the legacy tool table or recovered attribute base with only crit/sharpness/potion terms — no cooldown/charge factor; its javadoc states the 1.9 charge scaling is 'never consulted, structurally.' KnockbackEngine.java:214 drives the sprint extra off attacker.sprinting()?profile.sprintFactor():0.0 — the stamped sprint flag, never a charge scale (the 'scale' terms present are pace/servo only). AttackChargeReset is inert when OFF because Reconciler.converge is idempotent (!desired&&!active: nothing to do), and its javadoc confirms the fast path (default ON, cancels the ATTACK packet so Player#attack never runs) structurally defeats the charge meter. legacy-combat.md:73 and SYNOPSIS.md:304-326 confirm the divergence direction vs modern vanilla is strictly MORE knockback/damage: era ships full damage plus the sprint bonus regardless of charge, where vanilla ramps 0.2+scale^2*0.8 and gates the sprint bonus behind scale>0.9. Charge-blindness therefore cannot manufacture the reported weakness. The residual fallthrough nuance (fast-path OFF -> vanilla charge-scaled damage more often eaten by the hurt-window difference rule) is correctly bounded as non-default and a zero-knock ignore either way. era_call=era-real: the charge-blindness is intentional 1.7/1.8 fidelity, a deliberate divergence from modern vanilla that only ever adds knockback.
- Corrections: Finding stands as written. Minor refinement: the 'nuance arm' requires BOTH fast-path OFF (non-default) AND the ATTACK_COOLDOWN/AttackChargeReset feature OFF — when AttackChargeReset is ON, the inflated attack_speed base makes getAttackStrengthScale clamp to 1.0 even on the vanilla Player#attack path, so no charge scaling occurs on either path. So the charge-scaled-weakness edge case is doubly gated behind non-default config, and even then produces a zero-knock ignore (via the hurt-window difference rule) rather than a merely-weaker knock. Nothing in Mental's own accepted-hit pipeline (fast-path damage or the EDBEE KB recompute) ever scales knockback or damage DOWN by attack charge; the sprint bonus is charge-blind and gated only by the SprintVerdict flag.
- Severity: none (informational negative result — closes the attack-charge axis; points back to the sprint-verdict machinery as the live weak-KB suspect)

**SYMPTOM lens: REFUTED** — era call: `era-real`

- Reasoning: Verified citations in the main tree. Kernel grep for charge, cooldown, and attackStrength is empty. AttackChargeReset documents the fast path as structurally charge-blind and the vanilla path as the only charge-scaled one. Every divergence from modern vanilla is toward more knockback and damage (vanilla would down-ramp partial-charge hits and withhold the sprint bonus below 0.9 charge).
